**Chapter 821: In the Wind and Snow**

When the old scholar was sent out of the Fifth World by Bai Ye with a single sword stroke, it was the third year of the Jiachun Era. 

By the time the old scholar visited Bai Ze and returned to the cultural temple in the Central Plains, it was the fourth year of Jiachun. When he arrived in the capital of the Great Li (Dali) on the central part of Baoping Continent and reunited with his former top disciple by the shores of the newly vibrant Qidu, it was already the early spring of the fifth year of Jiachun. The willows swayed gently, flowers bloomed amidst the trees, and the orioles chirped joyfully. Children got out of school early, and paper kites soared high in the wind.

This warm spring scene made the old scholar's frown ease, and he turned to Cui Qian beside him to ask if he had any thoughts on naming the Fifth World. 

Cui Qian replied that he had none.

However, Cui Dongshan, who followed behind them, had some ideas, but unfortunately, the old scholar did not inquire further. He merely mentioned that at the cultural temple, they initially considered naming it "Rules," but the Saint of Rites disagreed, saying that rules were like spring winds nourishing things, and did not need to be put on paper. Various philosophers had made suggestions, including several elders from the Yin-Yang School and the Agricultural School who collectively proposed "Peach Blossom Spring," which received more supporters. It symbolized a paradise beyond the mundane, implying beauty and allowing people to remember the Confucian contribution in creating a brand new world. Moreover, in the southeast of the new world, there was indeed a peach tree known for its extraordinary phenomena, blooming but never bearing fruit for many years. However, when Bai Ye split the heavens with his sword, it immediately bore fruit. Despite this, the sub-saint still rejected the suggestion.

Thus, the Fifth World still lacked a proper name. 

Cui Dongshan scoffed, "Is a pure land born from fleeing the calamities truly a paradise? I don’t believe there are many at ease in the Fifth World. After surviving disasters, people loosen their grip slightly and immediately start vying for territory, scheming, and causing chaos. Once the situation somewhat stabilizes, and they’ve enjoyed a few days of comfort, the folks from Tongye Continent will definitely settle scores, starting with their own people, cursing Yuguizong and Tongye Sect for being useless, unable to protect their homeland, and then cursing the cultural temple in the Central Plains, and finally cursing the Sword Qi Great Wall. They may not dare to speak out, but they’re surely thinking it. This is such a chaotic place; how can it be a paradise?”

The old scholar nodded, "The sub-saint seems to think similarly."

Cui Dongshan immediately changed his tune, "Then let's call it 'Peach Blossom Paradise.' I wholeheartedly support this idea. If that's not enough, I'll drag Gao Laodi over to back it up."

The old scholar treated it like a passing breeze. How strange, Cui Qian didn’t seem to have this temperament when he traveled to the alley years ago.

Before leaving, the old scholar handed over the character “Mountain,” which he had borrowed from the Grand Scholar of the Book of Rites, to Cui Qian.

Cui Qian did not refuse.

The old scholar implied that the matter of returning this character—how and when it would be returned—was entirely his business and had nothing to do with Cui Qian or the Great Li.

After Cui Qian departed, Cui Dongshan swaggered over to the old scholar and whispered, "If that old bastard doesn’t return the ‘Mountain’ character, are you planning to use that merit to make amends with the Saint of Rites?" 

Cui Dongshan had never doubted the old scholar's ability to clean up messes. In the past, the lineage of the Confucian Sage had always relied on the old scholar to patch things up, apologizing to students or providing support while arguing and flailing his sleeves around.

In Pei Qian’s eyes, her senior brother walked like a big white goose, his large sleeves flapping about. It was obvious who he learned that from.

There was an old gentleman who once guarded his chicks like a mother hen.

The old scholar eyed the youth in white with disdain. 

That little rascal was just so displeasing to look at.

Cui Dongshan shrank his neck and obediently called out, "Master Ancestor," acknowledging the teacher of his teacher, who was of a higher generation than himself.

Cui Dongshan sidled closer, holding his walking stick and lightly poking the ground, signaling to the old scholar that he was now your disciple, so even if he spoke up, it didn’t mean he’d be hit—teaching students was the teacher’s job, and it wasn't the place of a master ancestor.

Cui Dongshan huffed, "That Cui Qian fellow hardly spoke a word, utterly disrespectful! I’ll help you scold him more later."

The old scholar slowly replied, "You two are ultimately distinct individuals now. Cherish it. After all the rivers and mountains you’ve crossed together, you should understand that many rivers may vanish after they diverge from a single source. You must ensure that it flows far and wide."

Cui Dongshan nodded eagerly, "Besides being a constant flow, like the clear depths reflecting the heavens, one should also strive to be as upright and resilient as you, Master. If one can remain steadfast against the wind and rain, even if one feels a tinge of the passage of time, they can still face it without fear. Every bit of knowledge should serve as a resting point for future generations, allowing them to travel far and wide."

The old scholar smiled knowingly, "It seems that the ethos of Luopo Mountain has indeed been led astray by you."

However, after the notion of "clear depths reflecting the heavens," with tranquility and eloquence, it was indeed a beautiful way to put it. Among the direct disciples, Xiao Qi and Xiao Ping'an were both deserving of it.

Cui Dongshan looked dispirited, "If you say so, Master, then so be it."

The old scholar gently inquired, "What about over at Luopo Mountain?"

Although the question seemed a bit vague, Cui Dongshan immediately understood and hurried a few steps closer, replying softly, "Reporting to the Master Ancestor, we’re still short on money, but our assets are steadily increasing. The offerings to Zhou Fei are quite generous, and the status of the Lotus Root Blessed Land is not only not declining but improving. Moreover, the Master has brought back a long-lived friend from the Sword Qi Great Wall, an ancestor of gold and copper, who is a manifestation of fortune. She is in our Baoping Continent, and when she reaches Luopo Mountain, she will be in the right place. Additionally, there is a woman born from the confluence of literary energy in the Lotus Root Blessed Land. Now, we have both literary and financial prosperity at Luopo Mountain."

The old scholar raised his chin slightly.

Cui Dongshan added, "Brother Dazhong has already left, and pure martial artists at the Golden Body level cannot enter the new world. This rule is well established."

The old scholar nodded, "Scholars should not be ashamed to talk about money, nor should they feel embarrassed about making a profit. It’s not like earning a bit of money with ability means one loses their scholarly demeanor. The great divide between honor and disgrace—gentlemen love wealth, but those who prioritize righteousness over profit are honored. This is how one should acquire it rightly."

Cui Dongshan curiously asked, "So, is the Fifth World filled with blessings now?"

The old scholar hummed in agreement. "That peach tree, for instance, is a significant blessing, ranking within the top ten. Bai Ye hastily built a temporary hut there and left that celestial sword behind to repay the debt of borrowing a sword from Daoist Sun of the Great Xuandu. Bai Ye is waiting for a certain Daoist from the lineage of Sword Immortals to return the celestial sword. Once that is done, Bai Ye will return to the Haoran World. Thus, this hut is not something anyone would dare to take."

Cui Dongshan laughed, "If the Daoists of Bai Yujing were to charge in, that would be amusing."

The old scholar had indeed visited that place. The peculiar peach tree, with roots extending deep into the earth and blessed by heaven, did not appear remarkable at first glance; it looked no different from ordinary wild peach trees and seemed devoid of any auspicious signs.

However, the old scholar and Bai Ye could separate the heavens and earth, so their insight was naturally beyond that of ordinary immortals. Bai Ye had contributed immensely; let alone a single peach tree, even ten could be relocated at his whim.

Bai Ye sheathed his sword and immersed himself in study. The peach tree thrived in the hut, gradually bearing fruit. Among the branches, flowers and fruits intertwined, and at the foot of the tree lay the celestial sword.

Scholars occasionally travel afar, leaving behind a long sword to guard their home.

The old scholar gathered a large bag of peach blossoms from under the tree, intending to use them for brewing wine. He also asked Bai Zhi, the Blessed Land, to craft several dozen peach blossom stationery. Meanwhile, he secretly took a few handfuls of the famous "ten-thousand-year soil" from beside the tree, which was rare, for his closed-door disciples to use, so he took a bit more.

Of course, the old scholar had informed Bai Ye beforehand about his intentions, loudly inquiring if it was permissible. Since Bai Ye remained silent inside the hut, the old scholar took it as his brother’s tacit approval. In reality, it was only a few days after the old scholar left that Bai Ye returned from his travels. When the scholar saw the peach tree completely stripped, he looked up to check the branches, and that was when he received Bai Ye's parting sword.

Of course, the wording the old scholar used at the cultural temple implied that Bai Ye had sent him off with a gift.

At the dawn of creation, the first person at the jade purity realm, the first immortal, the first one to slay the "quirky" cultivators... all favored by the heavenly way.

The first pure martial artist to break through in that realm, the first to reach the distant travel realm, or the mountain pinnacle realm... all protected by martial fortune.

The first to establish the ancestral hall, burn incense, hang portraits, and branch out, the first to establish a sizable secular dynasty at the foot of the mountain, the first baby born in the new world, the first pair of immortal couples forming a covenant in that realm, all at the middle five realms... blessed by humanity.

In short, in this vast world, the three realms gather, and blessings abound.

Cui Dongshan suddenly looked worried, "My senior sister Pei Qian broke through to the sixth and seventh realms too quickly. She foolishly let go of her strongest realms in the North Julu Continent. If she ascends to the mountain pinnacle realm early in the Aiai Continent, she will definitely have to visit the Fuyun Continent. That place is much messier than the stagnant Tongye Continent, which makes me anxious."

The old scholar asked, "Have you been to the Qingming World?"

It was a leading question; he knew Cui Dongshan wasn't at the Ascended realm. Cui Dongshan replied with annoyance, "Have you been?"

Blame it on that old rascal who kept haunting him, making him accustomed to sparring with others. Realizing that this kind of conversation with his master ancestor wouldn’t yield good results, Cui Dongshan immediately covered his tracks, "Since the Master Ancestor hasn’t been, nor has the teacher, how could I dare to go first?"

The old scholar didn’t hold a grudge against Cui Dongshan’s disrespect; he wasn’t petty. He noted it down and planned to visit the Aiai Continent to consult with Pei Qian.

The old scholar looked up at the sky, observing that the Confucian sacrifices' sage, who stood guard here, was the final figure in the cultural temple, which is why Bai Yujing's third master Lu Chen had once teased him as "the seventy-two."

The old scholar walked slowly and said, "Not only in the Qingming World, but our Haoran World is pretty much the same. In every Daoist temple, the first great hall is the Hall of the Spirit Officials, and that great spirit official’s statue is indeed majestic. I remember the first time I traveled far, in a small temple in my hometown, this memory left a deep impression. Even after gaining some fame and titles, seeing other magnificent sights still doesn't compare to the shock I felt that year."

Cui Dongshan understood the old scholar's point and said, "So, Master Ancestor wants Pei Qian to stay by the teacher's side for this reason? To let her feel as though she is always in the Daoist temple, learning Dao through observation? As long as Pei Qian is beside the teacher, it will naturally lead her closer to that level of caution and independence?"

In the Qingming World, there are four great heavenly masters, each versed in profound Daoist methods and possessing unique abilities. Yet, they do not cultivate in Bai Yujing but are responsible for guarding the four corners of the world. One of them, associated with that great spirit official, has a well-known tale that has circulated widely. According to many Daoist texts, it is said that before that spirit official attained enlightenment, he committed numerous acts of violence and was punished by a passing great heavenly master. Afterward, the latter rang the heavenly drum, and Bai Yujing's grand master sent him to follow the great heavenly master on travels for three hundred years, promising that if he made even a single mistake, they would switch places. In the end, for three centuries, that great heavenly master made no errors in speech or action.

The old scholar chuckled silently, "Hasn't Pei Qian also turned towards goodness? Doesn’t that matter anymore? Do you think Pei Qian would be who she is today without the teachings of my closed-door disciples?"

The old scholar patted his chest, "If I am at peace, the world benefits; what could be better?"

The old scholar spoke earnestly, "Accomplishments and knowledge are good, but is it good enough? I doubt it. I’ll just mention three matters: Can we borrow the character from the Grand Scholar? Can we have Mr. Bai retrieve the Mountain Search Map? Can we have one more girl, who seeks goodness and avoids evil, enter the distant travel realm? Scholars cannot think they have done enough and rest easy, believing that the world should not demand more from them. If so, I will spit at the world and curse mankind for their ignorance and lack of conscience."

When the old scholar reached this point, he scratched his head, "Clearing my throat a few times, then spitting a heavy mouthful... damn it... still a bit disgusting."

He was referring to an incident involving smashing a statue, remembering that there was a scholar in the Shao Yuan Dynasty who was particularly enthusiastic about it.

In truth, the old scholar was talking about two different matters, but Cui Dongshan was clever enough to understand. One was about pursuing the original intentions of worldly affairs, and the other was just private grumbling among close acquaintances.

The old scholar continued, "Now that Pei Qian has reached a higher realm, she has become more cautious; this is a good thing. Because her fists are heavy but she is still young, she shouldn't think too early about changing the world."

"The world is the world; it’s merely the path of humanity."

The old scholar casually pointed, "On a misguided path crowded with errors, it may seem a shortcut, regardless of how many people there are or how easy it is to walk. Every teacher must tell every child learning to read and learn etiquette at the school that this is not the way. Once those children grow up and gain some strength, they may have to stand in the way, telling others that this is wrong. Wrong is wrong, and they might end up with a black eye from some worldly misfortune. If your studies can reduce the wrongdoings that fall upon good people, that is the greatest kindness."

Cui Dongshan said gloomily, "Why tell me this and not Cui Qian?"

The old scholar remained silent.

Only the great river flowing before them continued its slow journey.

Cui Dongshan muttered to himself, "To strive for virtue."

After a long silence, Cui Dongshan complained, "Let’s go; everyone has left anyway."

The old scholar said, "I’m going to see a certain predecessor."

That predecessor had once posed a question of great significance, starting with, "Who transmitted the Dao at the beginning of antiquity?" Just this question alone could bring tears to some lonely sages.

The old scholar had once been youthful and spirited, and during a rare drinking session, he had called out, "I will answer it; I can answer it..."

And on the Sword Qi Great Wall, his disciples had once made his junior brother Chen Ping'an respond to it.

Cui Dongshan hesitated and said, "Can we skip the heavenly question?"

It was still a question, yet it was not phrased as one.

Not answering, just lingering, once a teacher, you always remain in my heart.

The old scholar tugged at his beard and patted his belly lightly, "It’s been too long; I need to let it out."

Cui Dongshan curiously asked, "Did Qi Jingchun know that person was at the Shu Jian Lake from the beginning?"

The old scholar shook his head, "I only learned this secret after merging with the Dao. In the past, that old man kept it from me."

Suddenly, the old scholar slapped Cui Dongshan's head, "You little rascal, always cursing yourself as an old bastard, is it fun?"

Cui Dongshan looked at him with mournful eyes, "You said it yourself, after all, you are two people now."

The old scholar slapped him again, "How do you speak to your Master Ancestor, huh?"

Cui Dongshan shielded his head after receiving the slap, “That’s enough, isn't it?”

The old scholar suddenly said, "First, there were sages looking coldly upon the world from Shu Jian Lake. Spirit is the language of the gods. Equal means the tone and inflection of speech. The one who speaks of righteousness and balance is none other than heaven, nurturing all things in harmony, while the most central and harmonious is the earth. Thus, it is the most righteous and balanced. Later, Bai Ye wielded his sword to leave the nation and traveled the world. As for how to name the Fifth World, I have an idea now."

"To be truly pure and clear is to firmly uphold the teachings of the ancients."

Bai Ye's poetry is unmatched, drifting and thinking uncommonly. A truly pure person possesses a grand spirit, floating like clouds in the sky.

Cui Dongshan blinked, "Good."

The old scholar raised a hand, while Cui Dongshan waved his arms frantically to stop that slap.

The old scholar withdrew his hand, stroked his beard, and smiled contentedly, "A single word of goodness won’t suffice; it’s far from enough. So, when it comes to naming, your teacher has truly inherited the essence."

Cui Dongshan grinned, "What about finding a wife?"

The old scholar rubbed his chin thoughtfully, "I’ve never taught that either; it’s self-taught?"

Cui Dongshan chuckled, "If you had taught it, it probably wouldn’t work out." 

And with that, the old scholar walked away./n/nCui Dongshan soared through the clouds, reaching the sea of mist where the true form of Zhi Gui emerged, majestic and powerful as it traversed the grand river. Halfway through its journey, it bore numerous wounds, yet its momentum remained fierce, and the situation was under control.

The old scholar first visited the Book Scroll Lake, where he met an elderly man who was profoundly connected to the water, to the point of being drawn into it. Dressed in formal robes with a broad-brimmed hat, the elder had a lean face and a scholarly presence that transcended the confines of traditional Confucian teachings.

The old scholar performed a respectful bow. The elder returned the gesture with ancient propriety, though his demeanor was far from the rigid orthodoxy of Confucianism.

Afterwards, the elder took the old scholar to a mountain peak. It was here, some time ago, that he had finally managed to obtain some bamboo slips from a young man who appeared worn and haggard. Despite his youth, the young man was not easily deceived.

They had once engaged in a dreamlike exchange, not inquiring about the heavens and the earth, but rather probing the depths of one's heart.

After a long silence, the elder spoke, “I find myself a bit disappointed in my own efforts, feeling I could have done better, yet I’m not as disheartened with the world.”

The old scholar nodded with a smile, saying, “To walk alongside such esteemed gentlemen, even if I can’t match your strides, is still a source of pride for me. If I could enjoy the four large meat buns from Green Paulownia City, I would surely have the strength to reason with others and continue my journey.”

The elder replied, “A disciple can pave the way for the world; he can also close the door on the teachers. Not a bad deal at all.”

The old scholar laughed heartily, “Not bad, not bad at all.”

The elder sighed, “One need not inquire about the warmth or coldness of human feelings. Even without touching the scriptures, I still resent myself.”

The old scholar remarked, “As long as my eyes remain clear and my heart warm, the heavens will surely bless this old scholar.”

The elder chuckled, “Just like your disciple, you’re quite adept at conversation.”

The old scholar shook his head, “When it comes to ‘conversation,’ everyone in the world is younger than me.”

The elder said, “There’s no need to say much about the ‘Heavenly Questions.’ Take the other texts, ‘Mountain Spirits’ and ‘Crossing the River,’ without reservation.”

The old scholar hesitated for a moment.

The elder added, “As for ‘Eastern Lord’ and ‘Summoning the Soul,’ they are the same.”

The old scholar bowed again, this time in gratitude.

The first bow was a greeting; this one was a thanks.

With a sigh, the elder’s figure faded away, leaving four essays suspended in the air.

The old scholar tucked them into his sleeve, also letting out a sigh.

Afterwards, the old scholar entrusted the essays “Mountain Spirits” and “Crossing the River” to Cui Dongshan, who was stationed at the grand river, and instructed him to pass the “Eastern Lord” essay to the local apothecary. Following that, the old scholar carried only the “Summoning the Soul” essay, heading south to the Old Dragon City. He took advantage of the perilous terrain—not a complete quagmire—to make a brief visit to Paulownia Leaf Isle, assisting Taiping Mountain in stabilizing several formations.

Then he ventured to the Great Spring Dynasty, where even the emperor had quietly fled. Outside the Blue Dew Palace by the riverbank, the old scholar tugged at his sleeve, standing there for quite a while, yet no one paid him any mind.

Finally, the old scholar had to ask if the River Goddess of the Underworld was present.

A petite woman swaggered into view, one hand supporting the base of a large bowl and the other holding chopsticks. She sat on the threshold, frowning as she scrutinized the old Confucian scholar, who appeared to have no discernible depth of cultivation. She eventually inquired, “What brings you here, old sir? Don’t you know the world is in disarray? My Blue Dew Palace is but a small place, unable to protect anyone. I might end up in danger myself. It’s not that I’m stingy; you should hurry to the Great Fulu Academy, where things are more stable.”

The old scholar had no choice but to muster the courage to introduce himself, stating that he was the teacher of both Zuo and Chen Ping’an.

The River Goddess of the Underworld seemed struck by lightning, her mind a muddle, her face reddening as she struggled to find the words. She swayed as if drunk, lifting the large bowl above her head, implying that she wanted to treat the venerable Confucian to a late-night meal.

After that, she invited the venerable Confucian, who was too polite to refuse, to sit with her in the main hall of the Blue Dew Palace, where Chef Liu served them a small bowl of noodles as if it were a delicacy.

Ultimately, in a certain area of Paulownia Leaf Isle, outside the territory of the Paulownia Leaf Sect, Zuo, with his sword resting on his knees, sat above the sea of clouds, guarding the gate. Just beyond that door lay two worlds.

In the distance, the Golden Core sword cultivator Wang Shizi and a girl named Yu Xin were aiding a group of academy students and mountain cultivators in escorting displaced persons to safety, a daunting and chaotic task.

Even a dimwit like Wang Shizi could see Yu Xin’s feelings for Zuo. Otherwise, she wouldn’t have taken the risk to come here. Wang Shizi found himself at a critical juncture in his cultivation, much like the sword cultivator Cao Jun from South Posa Isle, needing to observe Zuo’s swordsmanship to break through his bottleneck. After all, Zuo was here, slaying demons with his sword. Even a distant glance could yield invaluable insights into the sword path.

Yet, upon learning that Yu Xin had accompanied him to this place, Zuo had patted Wang Shizi on the shoulder, his expression suggesting that he believed Wang Shizi had finally grasped something.

Today, when Yu Xin asked if he wanted to seek guidance on swordsmanship, Wang Shizi, no longer the naive fool he once was, nodded affirmatively, adding, “Actually, aside from his unrivaled sword skills, Zuo’s Daoist methods are also exceptional. After I consult him, don’t miss out.”

Yu Xin glanced at him, and although Wang Shizi displayed righteous resolve, she refrained from rolling her eyes at him again.

When they arrived at the sea of clouds, temporarily regarded as a place of cultivation by Zuo, Wang Shizi sincerely inquired about sword techniques before taking his leave. He didn’t forget to remind Zuo that Yu Xin had some questions about her cultivation path and wished to consult him.

Zuo shook his head, saying that aside from swordsmanship, he couldn’t teach others anything else. The secret techniques of the Paulownia Leaf Sect’s ancestral hall could directly lead to the upper five realms. As long as Yu Xin followed the steps diligently, she would undoubtedly succeed.

Just as Yu Xin approached, looking like a cloud drifting through the air, she overheard and immediately turned to leave. A few steps out, she suddenly descended, hastily returning to the mundane world.

Wang Shizi trailed after her, daring only to follow from a distance. A girl in sorrow likely preferred to hide her feelings from others, after all.

However, Yu Xin seemed to quickly compose herself, stopping in place as she hovered in the air, neither going to the sea of clouds nor returning to the ground. It was then that Wang Shizi felt safe enough to approach.

Yu Xin looked up at the sea of clouds and quietly asked, “Is Mr. Zuo unable to leave this place, yet longs to return to the Sword Qi Great Wall? Is that why he feels so… conflicted?”

Wang Shizi nodded, responding in thought, “The little junior brother of our esteemed senior, that hidden official, seems to have stayed behind. That’s why Zuo is eager to leave, but with the current situation on Paulownia Leaf Isle, it truly is challenging for him to depart.”

Yu Xin murmured, “He possesses such high sword skills, yet he’s always so troubled?”

Zuo was indeed troubled, unsure of when he could return to the Sword Qi Great Wall and bring his junior brother back.

Yu Xin felt pained. She didn’t want to imagine a day when she could no longer see that seemingly eternally lonely figure. She couldn’t bear the thought of him leaving for good one day.

In this world, there should be a Zuo who doesn’t have to feel conflicted.

Suddenly, an irate old scholar approached the sea of clouds, reaching Zuo’s back. Just as Zuo was about to rise, the old scholar didn’t need to jump; he slapped Zuo on the head, exclaiming, “Are you a fool?! Your teacher didn’t teach you how to find a wife, but neither did he teach you how to remain single for so long!”

Zuo received another slap from his teacher, utterly confused. But he was used to it by now.

Zheng Dafu had left his hometown early, with a clear destination in mind. However, it wasn’t until the fifth year of Jiachun that he obediently followed his master’s orders, no longer heading to the Lotus Root Paradise, but instead leisurely making his way into the Fifth Realm.

This quiet departure from his hometown and his intercontinental journey followed his master’s peculiar route. His first stop was North Julu Island, where he found his senior brother and sister-in-law at the foot of Lion Peak Mountain, enjoying several days of fine wine and food. Surprisingly, his sister-in-law didn’t scold him, even speaking softly to him, which made Zheng Dafu feel a pang of bitterness about his own situation. He hadn’t thought much of it before, but seeing his sister-in-law like that made him realize just how pitiful he truly was.

After feasting to his heart’s content, Zheng Dafu glanced outside at the empty courtyard and kindly offered to help his sister-in-law chop some bamboo on the mountain to make sturdy clotheslines.

Li Er was busy tidying up the dishes and paid him no mind. One day without being scolded, and he might as well not be a disciple anymore.

The woman had initially intended to scold him thoroughly but upon seeing the bearded, hunched man who seemed a head shorter than before, she acted unusually and said it wasn’t necessary. She quickly walked out of the house.

Zheng Dafu sighed deeply, turning to his senior brother and asking why his sister-in-law seemed to be bullied by outsiders, lacking the heroic spirit she had back home.

Li Er had just finished cleaning up the dishes when the woman returned, carrying two jugs of wine and a few plates of snacks, urging the brothers to have a good chat, as it had been so long since they last met, and they would soon part ways again. It wouldn’t hurt to drink a little more.

At that moment, the woman slightly regained her former demeanor, pointing at Zheng Dafu and scolding him for not staying home to guard the door. Even if he didn’t earn much, it was still a stable life. What was so appealing out there? With a face like his, standing at the door at night could ward off evil spirits, more effective than a door god. Without any real skills, how could he expect to entice women to bear his children?

Her scolding instantly refreshed Zheng Dafu’s spirit. He hurriedly invited his sister-in-law to sit down and drink, promising that if he got drunk today, he would sleep like a dead man, not even hearing the thunder, let alone sleepwalking and stumbling around.

She was furious and left the house, hesitating momentarily before ultimately not staying at the shop. Instead, she sought out a few women she had good relations with to inquire if there were any suitable young women around, thinking perhaps Zheng Dafu might be a decent match after all.

In his early years, Zheng Dafu, when guarding the door or drinking on the street, enjoyed boasting about the size of beautiful women, comparing chests and bottoms, his eyes never idle, his hands even less so, and his mouth never quiet, saying he had lost his soul among their garments, hoping to find a partner. 

Such a worthless fellow, who couldn’t even bring a wife home, lamented his unlucky fate. In the end, a lustful old bachelor with dishonest intentions couldn’t gather the courage to find a proper woman as a wife. It was to be expected; with his looks and lack of prospects, who would want to endure hardship with him? 

While the woman scolded him, she secretly urged her husband to help his junior brother find a way out. If all else failed, they could try to get him a decent job at Yang’s shop or the Dragon Kiln, and if he could find a suitable unmarried girl from the neighborhood, they could set something up. Even if he had to marry into her family, as long as Zheng Dafu spoke fewer crude words, whether as a shop assistant, a farmer, or a woodcutter, he could at least support a small household.

Once the woman left, Li Er began discussing serious matters with his junior brother, “Just hang in there until we get there and break through. You know how to manage this situation; since Master has returned your remaining soul, don’t waste it. If you accidentally break through during your travels, it could lead to trouble. Fuyao Isle is too far from Baoping Isle, and it would be difficult for Master to help you find your way, nor would it be appropriate for him to intervene.”

At Lion Peak, Li Er helped Zheng Dafu train, finally allowing him to return to the sixth realm of martial arts. Although he still had a long way to go before reaching the peak of his former martial prowess, it was not a significant issue. Moreover, Zheng Dafu had newly forged a brave heart of a warrior, which was no small feat. After all, he was a pure martial artist who had once earned the title of ‘strongest.’ Having endured hardship, his spirit had not faltered, which was the best tempering of fortunes and misfortunes.

A pure martial artist's prowess in boxing depends on the vigor and length of their spirit. Before throwing a punch, one must hold the ambition to make the heavens and the earth tremble.

Zheng Dafu placed one leg on the bench, took a sip of wine, and nodded, “I’m aware.”

When the woman returned home, hoping to share good news with her husband, whether it would come to fruition depended on Zheng Dafu’s own fortune. However, she found that Zheng Dafu was already absent from home, and she hadn’t seen him on the way back either. At the wine table, only two empty jugs remained, and the dishes were finished.

The woman wondered aloud, “He left just like that?”

Li Er replied with a grunt.

She sighed and sat down, gazing outside. “I wonder how you men think. You don’t understand what draws you to the world.”

She referred not only to the perpetually unruly Zheng Dafu but also to Chen Ping’an, whom she regarded as half a son-in-law.

Li Er found himself at a loss for words. He stood up to clean the table again, bending down to pick up Zheng Dafu’s jug and shaking it gently, realizing it was completely empty.

Seeing this, the woman scolded with a laugh, “Look at your lack of ambition.”

Li Er hesitated, his expression awkward.

Outside, guests had arrived.

The woman tentatively asked, “What’s this? You’re not planning to travel far, are you?”

Li Er scratched his head.

Indeed, he intended to make a trip to the Bone Marsh, where his daughter was still located, and he felt uneasy about it. Moreover, it was only right that he put in some effort.

Had it not been for his son Li Huai and junior brother Zheng Dafu arriving here one after another, Li Er would have already discussed it with his wife. Recently, a couple of guests had come to Lion Peak, planning to visit the southern sea of the Bone Marsh. One was a renowned sword immortal from the Taihui Sword Sect who had helped Qi Jinglong with his sword inquiries, and the other an old martial artist who had just regained some clarity of mind and free will.

Both were now waiting outside for Li Er’s news.

One was a well-known sword immortal from North Julu Island, and the other a tenth realm martial artist who had once provoked multiple sword immortals to surround and beat him.

They were all waiting for Li Er, or more precisely, for him to persuade his wife to allow him to travel far.

This didn’t seem too strange, as the men from North Julu Island were famously fearless, except when it came to their own women.

The woman slammed the table angrily, “Are you wild just because you drank a bit of horse piss with Zheng Dafu and heard a few crude words?!”

She lamented loudly, “Oh, what a miserable life I have! My son is the most filial and understanding, yet he’s rarely around. My daughter is so stubborn, looks like her mother, yet has her father’s lack of talent. In the end, she’s become an old maid, unable to marry... Who can I blame? I chose a useless man back in the day, one with no skills. After a drink, he’s lost even the little decent spirit he had. In the end, he’s just a heartless man, dreaming every day about the young women wandering by, flaunting their chests and swaying their hips. If I can't blame myself, who else can I blame...”

Li Er remained silent, not daring to interject.

The woman wiped her eyes, “He seems like a simple and honest man, yet inside he’s full of tricks and rotten thoughts. What kind of karma have I created, ending up with a man like you as the pillar of the family…”

Li Er glanced outside, at the sword immortal watching the commotion, who exchanged a few teasing remarks with the old martial artist. 

Li Er ignored them, informing them that they should head out first, as he would not arrive later than them at the Bone Marsh.

The sword immortal turned to leave, while the old martial artist shared a few more laughs. The sword immortal then struck up another conversation, and they both appeared quite lively.

Li Er frowned./n/n“Are these two asking for a beating?” 

The woman caught a glimpse of Li Er’s furrowed brow from the corner of her eye. It was an unprecedented situation, and her heart sank even further. She leaned on the table, feigning a show of tears earlier, but now she genuinely felt anxious and heartbroken. Softening her voice, she whimpered, “Now they dare to throw me a tantrum. I can’t live like this anymore. They won’t say it out loud, but in their hearts, they resent me as a nagging old hag…”

Li Er sat down beside her and gently patted her hand. He explained softly, “Liu Er is out there on her own, and I plan to go check on her. I’ll be back home soon.”

The woman lifted her head, her expression doubtful. “Are you going to help Li Huai and Li Liu find some vixen to be their second wife?”

Li Er shook his head. “You know I can’t do such shameless things.”

He couldn’t even bear to repeat what his wife had said. 

Watching Li Er’s expression, the woman murmured, “Actually, Li Huai and Da Feng are just like that; they come and go as they please. I can tell your mind isn’t here whenever you zone out. Go on, be careful on the road. Even if you learn from Da Feng’s flirtations, don’t let him take advantage of you out there. But of course, it’s best if you don’t learn anything at all.”

Li Er nodded, wiping the corner of her eyes. When she asked when he would leave, he replied he would set out today, the earlier he left, the sooner he’d return. The woman got up to help pack their belongings. 

Outside, an old man’s cursing continued endlessly. Li Er, who had been patiently waiting at the door for the packages, suddenly stood up and strode out. Hearing the commotion, the woman, who had been dawdling, quickly asked Li Er what he was going out for. He replied casually, “There’s a dog barking outside.”

Zheng Dafeng traveled from North Canglu Continent to White Snow Continent, passing through Liuxia Continent and Jinjia Continent, and finally entering the gate in the middle of Fuyiao Continent. As he was just a martial artist from another continent and not at the Golden Body level, he managed to enter the Fifth Realm with a bag of gold coins.

The Fuyiao Continent was different from the Tongye Continent, where everyone below the Nascent Soul could seek refuge. Not to mention Golden Core Earth Immortals; even the middle-level cultivators of their continent generally couldn’t expect to cross the gates. The amount of divine money needed would make even an entire sect or a top-level cultivator feel the pinch. Moreover, it wasn’t enough to just have money; one needed a higher-level master or fellow disciple who had died fighting on the eastern coast of Fuyiao Continent to earn a pass, which led many desperate old cultivators, particularly those whose souls were decaying, to flock to the coastal areas.

This was to pave a way for their juniors and offer a risky yet opportunity-filled path for cultivation.

The customs of Fuyiao Continent reflected this reality. The mountains and valleys were interconnected, accustomed to fighting to the death, making them far more spirited than the stagnant waters of Tongye Continent.

As Zheng Dafeng’s feet touched the ground of this realm, he quietly ascended to the Golden Body level, though without the blessings of martial luck. The reason was simple: among the martial artists of this realm, there was a remarkable talent at the sixth level who had honed his physique. The only reason he came here was that he couldn’t find any martial luck in the Haoran realm and sought to take advantage of this place. Such a person was not someone Zheng Dafeng valued as a companion. 

Zheng Dafeng was indifferent to the concept of martial luck. Whether he entered the seventh, eighth, or even ninth realm with the strongest sixth level was of no importance to him. He was not in a rush at all; if the old man were worried about it, he would have sent him to Tongye Continent to wait. In fact, the old man had advised him long ago not to regard martial luck as a given; it was meaningless. The primary focus should be on breaking through, and reaching the tenth realm as soon as possible would be sufficient.

At the latest, within a hundred years, he should at least reach the peak of the Mountain Summit realm. Otherwise, he might as well just wait to eat and die in this realm.

Zheng Dafeng planned to take a look at the center of the world, as he had heard that the Sword Qi Great Wall was located at the city left behind from the great war known as "Ascension."

Around the same time Zheng Dafeng entered this new realm, Huang Ting, the female disciple of Taiping Mountain from Tongye Continent, who had been stuck at the Nascent Soul level, crossed another gate into this world. Traveling alone with her sword, she moved swiftly, and after a month, she finally paused to rest. Choosing a mountain that caught her eye, she decided to nurture her sword intent there. Unexpectedly, she attracted the attention of a strange being. Good fortune smiled upon her; she broke through and entered the Jade Purity realm, discovering an excellent location for cultivation, rich in spiritual energy and natural treasures beyond her imagination.

When it came to luck and destiny, Huang Ting had always been fortunate. Otherwise, the renowned He Xiaoliang from Baoping Continent wouldn’t have been called her second.

After entering the Jade Purity realm, Huang Ting erected a stone monument on the mountain peak, inscribing “Taiping Mountain” in sword characters, and then descended to wander around, hoping to encounter some familiar faces.

She had always enjoyed the tales of the Jianghu.

During her journey south, Huang Ting encountered a young, unassuming scholar in black clothing. However, they merely exchanged glances.

Earlier, the black-clad scholar seemed to recognize her, folding his fan and stopping to nod in greeting.

Huang Ting ignored him.

As she saw more and more cultivators traveling north, Huang Ting learned that the old immortals of Tongye Continent had seemingly begun “moving mountains.” Besides the increasingly heavy atmosphere on the old mountains, there were also some new developments. For instance, among the current practitioners of various schools, those who could calculate directions and select suitable locations for travel, such as the Yin-Yang practitioners, the Feng Shui masters who could accurately assess treasure locations, and farmers, herbalists, and merchants skilled in making money, had all become highly sought after. In short, any Qi practitioners who could aid in the construction of mountains were now in high demand.

As for the once notorious four difficult spirits of the mountains—the sword cultivators, military strategists, legalists, and the female disciples of the Knife Room—they had all been rendered obsolete due to the collapse of the Upside Down Mountain. The dynamics of the world had drastically changed; nowadays, besides the center, the sword cultivators were indeed scarce in the east, west, south, and north. Military cultivators were often forcibly conscripted for battles back home, and the legalists faced the same fate. As for the female disciples of the Knife Room, there were likely very few left even in the Haoran realm.

In this new world, by the fifth year of Jia Chun, the situation had become increasingly chaotic.

Both a martial artist at the Golden Body bottleneck and a cultivator, Yang Ningzhen had taken on the alias Yang Hengxing. Along with his younger brother Yang Ningxing, who had already refined the treasured mirror of Baoping Mountain, the two entered the Fifth Realm one after another without even greeting each other, not even considering a reunion.

As a small celestial from the Chongxuan Bureau’s Yunxiao Palace, Yang Ningxing had gathered the elemental treasures of the five elements and came here solely to break through into the Jade Purity realm and ascend to become an immortal.

There was an unknown Qi practitioner named Shu Zhongshu, whose origins were unclear, who occupied a picturesque spot and built a transcendent platform, setting prohibitions that forbade any Earth Immortal from entering within three hundred miles; otherwise, they would be killed without mercy. This individual had several maidservants named Xiao Ping, Jiang Se, Cai Yi, Da Xian, and Hua Ying, all of whom were middle-level sword cultivators.

Ji Hai, the sect master of the Fuji Sect, specialized in writing green and blue verses to invite gods and even spirits.

Ji Hai summoned a divine general named “Catching Willow” and a ghostly immortal named “Flower Seal.” Both were at the Nascent Soul level and joined forces to protect the next sect master of the Fuji Sect as they entered this new realm.

A young man in white with a flowing sash, who appeared to be a wild cultivator from the mountains, did not rush to travel after entering this world from Tongye Continent. Instead, he started wandering around, specifically choosing Qi practitioners who were poets, lyricists, musicians, and essayists. These individuals, upon entering the new realm in a hurry, began loudly reciting their poetry and songs—heroic ballads, frontier poems, lyrical verses, and even the delicate complaints of the boudoir—all in hopes of resonating with this new world, seeking harmony between their works and the greater universe.

After losing interest in all of that, the young man finally began to travel alone. Eventually, he sat down by a riverside, where the water and clouds danced vibrantly. He took out brush and ink, closed his eyes, and with memory as his guide, painted a long scroll depicting mountains and rivers, naming it “Mustard Seed.” The scroll bore only a single ink dot but was titled “Mountains and Rivers.”

The young man produced two seals, stamping one on the “Mustard Seed” scroll, inscribing “In harmony with the moonlight at the white cloud and azure stone’s fair spot,” while the other on the “Mountains and Rivers” scroll, inscribing “Once intoxicated by plum blossoms for a decade, then misled by osmanthus brew for half a lifetime.”

The young man reclined back, using his arms as a pillow, murmuring with a smile, “What moves my heart are the bright moon, beautiful women, falling snow, and the light of swords.”

The city of the Sword Qi Great Wall had just been named Ascension City.

Lu Chen returned to the Qingming realm, and Sun Daolong had already taken the lead, returning to the Xuandu Temple.

Lu Chen arrived at the White Jade Capital and encountered his tall senior brother. Lazily, he leaned against the highest railing of the tallest city among the five, smiling, “There’s no need to be angry. In Xuandu Temple, from Sun Daolong to the youngest acolyte, everyone has feelings toward you.”

Lu Chen watched the clouds rise and fall like tides at sea, softly saying, “It’s a reasonable principle to allow family members to have a little emotion.”

For this Grand Master of the White Jade Capital, the entire Qingming realm, whether or not they were cultivators, all dwelled under one roof.

Many emotions defied reason, yet Lu Chen said that was precisely the principle.

The tall Daoist remained silent.

Lu Chen turned around, leaning against the railing and stretching lazily. “Who would help outsiders and not help senior brothers? Five hundred spirit officials, that’s no mistake.”

Dao Lao Er remarked, “Is that fellow still being pressed by Tuo Yue Mountain?”

Lu Chen laughed, “He can’t blame anyone else; after all, back in the day, he was a guest and would scribble on the shoe soles, one saying Dao Lao Er and the other saying Lu Chen. Now he’s facing the consequences, huh?”

On Tongye Continent, the boundaries between the mountains and the valleys were starkly defined. First, the immortal forces of this continent were not as numerous as those of other continents. Secondly, the cultivators of Tongye had long grown accustomed to sweeping the snow in front of their own doors, showing far less interest in the bustling markets below than the rest of the eight continents in the Haoran realm.

Furthermore, Tongye Continent spanned vast territories, which meant many remote areas on this continent were unaware that the world had long since become unsettled.

In a remote vassal kingdom’s capital, a wealthy family, both official and scholarly, had an elderly man in his seventies explaining the significance of a royal porcelain bowl gifted by the Emperor and a royal inkstone awarded by the King to his newly literate grandson. He elaborated on why the Retreat Thought Hall crafted this bowl and why the Advancement Thinking Hall made this inkstone, explaining the essence of retreating to think and advancing to think.

In a small county town, a little girl practiced bending and curling her fingers like the opera performers, while the young men and women paid her no mind. An elder saw her and scolded her a few times.

A traveling scholar rested at an inn, flipping through the notes from the literati of a previous dynasty. He found it curious that well water could tell the time and that the flower growing in the palace had its own rules.

A man with a mouth full of gold teeth led a group of rascals, living a life of luxury with abundant food and drink in his hometown. He had only heard rumors of immortals on the mountains but felt no envy whatsoever.

In a prefectural city, there was a profession specializing in the imitation of certain famous calligraphers and painters, capable of producing works that could easily deceive even the discerning. They charged exorbitantly per character and were currently haggling with a long-time client.

Then, one day, everything was gone.

Under a dense cloud cover, a hole suddenly opened in the sky above a coastal immortal mountain of Tongye Continent. Sunlight poured down, weapons clattered to the ground, and a great demon crashed heavily to the earth.

Another boulder as large as a mountain tilted and crashed into the majestic city of a dynasty.

On top of the massive stone was a slender girl, dragging a sword, followed by armored puppets that shook the ground with every step.

In the sixth year of Jia Chun in this Fifth Realm, the vast Tongye Continent had fallen, except for three academies and a dozen immortal mountains.

During this time, a man named Zhong Kui, once a gentleman from an academy, emerged to turn the tide.

Meanwhile, in the waters of Fuyiao Continent, Cao Ci broke through to the tenth realm during a fierce battle at sea, turning the tide against a great demon.

In the icy plains of White Snow Continent, a group of northern cultivators hunting demons encountered a formidable beast. Trapped in a desperate situation, they could only flee southward. Exhausted, they stood waiting for their doom when a young woman appeared, slowly walking out from the white snow, holding a walking stick and carrying a green bamboo box.

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 822: The Eleventh of the World**

Amidst the swirling snow and wind, a slender figure emerged. The vast whiteness of the world accentuated her slightly darker skin, making her appear even more conspicuous. Her hair was styled into a playful bun, revealing her high forehead, devoid of any adornments or hairpins.

As the young woman stood firm, roughly ten paces away from the group of bewildered hunters, she pulled out a meticulously crafted geomantic map from the northern region of Aiai Continent, stored in the treasury of Lion Peak. After a quick glance, she noted that the nearest celestial abode on the mountains was the Zhanfan Daoist Temple, located in the northern territory of Aiai Continent. Unlike the sects of the "Zong" character, this temple was relatively peaceful. The city below was Tuili City, part of the Rainworker Kingdom, known for its Lin Tan Prefecture. She tucked the map back into her sleeve, first offering a respectful salute to the crowd before speaking in the refined dialect of Aiai Continent, "May I ask how far we are from Tuili City?"

An elderly cultivator rose cautiously, his voice trembling, "Senior, are you Master Liu?"

This was the best-case scenario. The worst, however, would be if she were actually a powerful demon in human guise, toying with them like fish on a hook.

On the vast ice plains, four formidable demons each ruled their territory. The southernmost one claimed the name Xiliu, often seen riding a snow-white lion as he patrolled his domain. Rumor had it that he preferred to manifest as a handsome man. Over a decade ago, he had engaged in a life-and-death struggle with Master Liu, who had come to the area to "earn some pocket money for cosmetics and gather a dowry." Even those far away in Tuili City felt the overwhelming aura of that battle. Though severely injured, Master Liu had turned misfortune into fortune, breaking through a bottleneck in the strongest travel realm to successfully reach the Ninth Realm. It seemed Xiliu had suffered significant injuries as well, retreating into seclusion ever since. 

In the years that followed, cultivators from Aiai Continent had taken advantage of the temporarily weakened demons in the southern ice plains, banding together to hunt the various creatures and gather precious materials without restraint. 

However, Xiliu had two loyal generals guarding his territory. One was a rogue demonic cultivator, self-styled as the Autumn Water Daoist, and the other was an old demoness with a wrinkled face, carrying a large burlap sack. When she spotted cultivators, she would smile and say, "Looks like we have a fresh meal for our young master Xiliu. Thank you, everyone."

Both were rarely seen together, and any unfortunate encounter could leave one’s fate in the hands of the next life.

In fact, there had once been another tyrannical demon in the southern ice plains, but that one had been skinned by the Master Liu that the old cultivator had mentioned.

Pei Qian shook her head. "No."

The honorific title made her uncomfortable. However, being in a foreign land and meeting by chance, where intentions could be hidden, she chose not to reveal her own name.

Pei Qian was aware of who this so-called Master Liu was. A Ninth Realm martial artist, she was named Liu Suiyu, a registered devotee of the Liu family, the wealthiest in Aiai Continent, and the one most likely to become the second Tenth Realm martial artist. Previously, while practicing punches on Lion Peak, Elder Li Er had casually mentioned the martial arts landscape of Aiai Continent and the names of its masters. The top martial artist of Aiai Continent was Pei Axiang, known for her peculiar surname and even stranger name, nicknamed "Thunder God." Her fists were powerful, and her residence was a humble Thunder God Temple, little known to the world.

Liu Suiyu was one of Pei Axiang’s three direct disciples. This old martial artist, renowned for both training and teaching, had fought countless battles on her path to the pinnacle of martial arts, partly due to the name "Axiang." One such battle was against the oldest Tenth Realm martial artist in the northern regions, Wang Fuxue, over the latter’s habit of referring to her as "Axiang Sister," bragging that the martial arts of Axiang from Aiai Continent were very masculine.

It was said that after returning from the sea, though battered and bruised, Wang Fuxue remained spirited. When asked about the outcome by friends on the mountain, he merely scoffed, "How heavy could the fists of a girl from Aiai Continent be?" The outcome of that Tenth Realm duel was clear. After that, Pei Axiang had indeed secluded herself in Thunder God Temple, not seen for decades.

Later, Gu You and the Sword Immortal Ji Yue both died, leaving the northern regions without a Tenth Realm martial artist. The news from Aiai Continent was far more extensive than that of the northern regions, mostly filled with schadenfreude.

The assembled cultivators were on edge, hesitant to approach the unknown young woman.

In the ice plains, demons were known to be eccentric. Could this woman truly be passing by and choose to save them? Or was she simply toying with them like a cat with a mouse? 

Hunting demons in Aiai Continent was a perilous business, where one’s life hung by a thread. Thus, it was crucial to go in numbers. Each hunter venturing into the ice plains would sign a life-and-death contract with the Northern Summit Alliance, clearly stating the terms for compensation. Of course, if they returned empty-handed or suffered total annihilation, everything would be over.

Typically, a minimum of three people would team up: one as the formation master responsible for setting traps—this role was crucial. A pure martial artist or soldier should carry both a defensive heavy weapon and an offensive treasure, tasked with luring demons into the forbidden zone of the formation, as they were the most physically resilient and could both protect themselves and stall those tough-skinned demons, preventing an immediate collapse if they encountered a demon. Additionally, there needed to be a Qi practitioner skilled in water techniques to seize the advantage of time and terrain, coordinating their techniques to slay the demons.

If the leader could gather a five-member team, they would often add a formidable Qi practitioner, known for the so-called "one deadly strike," to deal a fatal blow during the encirclement. They might also include an alchemist cultivator to assist in prolonged combat. This way, the hunting team would be able to attack and retreat, ensuring that even if the ice plains expedition yielded nothing, they could at least preserve their lives and safely retreat to Tuili City or the Zhanfan Daoist Temple to regroup.

Yet, even with companions, unforeseen accidents were common.

Today, they had set out without consulting the almanac and encountered a Golden Core demon.

Pei Qian understood their concerns and did not wish to elaborate. She needed only to head straight south to Tuili City for a brief respite, and their doubts would naturally dissipate.

Whether traveling through Northern Julu Continent with Li Huai or now wandering alone in Aiai Continent, Pei Qian focused solely on her training, never aspiring to make friends or acquaintances like her master. As long as there was mutual affinity, she would drink without asking names.

Pei Qian believed she could not achieve that.

Just as Cui Dongshan privately thought, as long as her teacher, Chen Ping'an, was not beside her, the vast world outside the Lotus Flower Blessed Land still revolved around the streets and alleys of the capital of the Southern Garden Kingdom. For Pei Qian, apart from her master and the destitute mountain, her journey through the martial world had hardly changed—it was difficult to alter that fact in the past, present, or future.

Suddenly, Pei Qian halted, plunging her walking stick into the snow with force. She declared to them, "You all go ahead, hurry to Tuili City, and be careful on the way. Danger still lurks."

Then, Pei Qian furrowed her brow, glancing at the distance behind the group of Qi practitioners.

It was somewhat too late.

Besides an old woman, who appeared to be shuffling awkwardly yet moved with surprising speed, carrying a large burlap sack, the snow and wind parted before her as she advanced. The old woman stopped about a hundred paces from Pei Qian, coughing persistently, squinting her eyes, and rasping, "What a fierce little girl with her fists. Heading south, yet you’re willing to leave behind all those demon cores for us to find. A pure martial artist like you, practicing for the sake of training without seeking wealth, is truly more contemptible than that lunatic named Liu."

Alongside the old woman, on the path south taken by the hunters, there was a barefoot Taoist clad in a crane cloak, trudging through the snow while loudly reciting the Taoist classic "Nanhua Qiushui." The Taoist held several branches of blooming plum blossoms, occasionally plucking a few to chew on while mixing them with snow, swallowing both with each bite. With every chew, a radiant glow emanated from his meridians, presenting a striking aura of a successful cultivator.

North and south, they blocked the path.

Seeing that the old woman and the barefoot Taoist had no immediate intention of attacking, Pei Qian stepped forward, quickly reaching the side of the old cultivator. She removed a bamboo box and reminded the gathering cultivators, "You focus on forming your defenses. If possible, under the premise of ensuring your safety, help me look after this box. If things get urgent, each of you should flee. I will do my best to protect you."

Pei Qian paused a moment before adding, "I will try my best."

Since the old woman and the barefoot Taoist were clearly targeting her, Pei Qian felt it was only right to throw a few punches, both for others and herself. In the martial world, one must uphold righteousness.

Earlier, she had casually slain a demon to save those cultivators, and it had truly been a casual act. Since she had the strength, she should throw her punches without expecting anything in return.

As for the goodwill and malice of the world, what relation did it have with Pei Qian's training and striking? None.

What mattered to Pei Qian were only her teacher's teachings and the拳法 passed down by Elder Cui—just those two things.

The old woman cast another glance at the green bamboo staff left behind by the young woman. Earlier, when she focused her gaze, she found it impossible to fully see through the illusion, only vaguely sensing the chilling aura emanating from the staff. This was a significant reason why the old woman had not rushed into action.

An old demoness like her, who had cultivated in the ice plains, feared provoking the Liu family disciples of Aiai Continent more than anything, and she was also wary of the direct disciples of Pei Axiang from the Thunder God Temple. Beyond that, she had no worries. Whether they were chewed raw or stewed, it mattered not. Apart from those two types of individuals, occasionally sects bearing the "Zong" character would come here to train, but they often had Yuan Ying Earth Immortals to protect them. The old woman had enough discernment to know that the opponents would generally exercise caution. Those delicate young disciples would not strike too harshly, nor could they.

Pei Qian turned to the old woman, whose expression shifted between doubt and certainty. "I am merely passing through. I have not provoked you. But if I find myself outmatched and become a meal for demons, I accept that. My fists may be strong, but if demons wish to eat people and are killed, they cannot blame me for hitting hard."

The old woman chuckled, "From the traces of your punches and your path, it seems you landed in the north and have been heading south ever since? Little girl, are you from another continent? Northern Julu or Liuxia? How could your elders let you travel alone across the entire ice plain from north to south?"

The old woman’s greatest confusion was why the young girl was allowed to swagger through the territory of her enemy, Xiliu, right under her nose. If not for the fear of attracting trouble, she would have struck long ago. The skirmishes along the way were all fought by Sixth Realm cultivators. Even if they held back and concealed their strength, a mere girl at most in the Golden Body realm would surely die.

Pei Qian replied, "You need not attempt to test my background with words. I will accept your challenge, whether it be with fists or swords."

An elderly cultivator, anxious, whispered, "Senior, regardless of her true identity, we can scare her off by claiming she’s a Liu family disciple. Otherwise, in this encirclement, it’s hard for you to fight against four hands, especially since there are surely many demons controlled by that old woman. In Aiai Continent, the Liu family disciples are the greatest talisman of protection. Master Pei and Senior Liu are both devotees of the Liu family. As a martial artist, you could easily disguise yourself as a third-generation disciple of the Thunder God Temple..."

Pei Qian's voice was firm. "I have my own teacher; I dare not speak out of turn."

The old cultivator sighed deeply, not daring to insist further. In life-and-death situations, there was no time for rigid formalities. 

At this point, no one questioned the identity of the senior any longer.

It was indeed unnecessary.

That Autumn Water Daoist alone was enough to crush all the hunting cultivators except her.

For cultivators from Aiai Continent, whether they were disciples of the classic schools or wandering practitioners, even if they had not personally encountered those exalted beings of the Fifth Realm and above, they were generally aware through the mess of news reports that their numbers were not significantly fewer than those in Northern Julu and certainly more than those in the northwest Liuxia.

However, when it came to Eighth and Ninth Realm martial artists, they were truly few and far between, far less than in Northern Julu, and even fewer than in Liuxia.

The martial fortune of Aiai Continent was notoriously meager. The legendary Tenth Realm martial artist was but one, Pei Axiang of the Thunder God Temple, who had once lost to Wang Fuxue, who later went mad and was captured by the Sword Immortal. Northern Julu had once possessed a sword cultivator who crossed the seas, and even after Gu You's death, they still had one more limit-breaking martial artist than Aiai Continent. This left the mountain practitioners of Aiai Continent feeling rather low, especially since the Liu family, as the first among cultivators, had publicly expressed that their skills could at most match half of those of the Fire Dragon True Man of the Paragons of the Peak. This made Aiai Continent's cultivators feel as if, apart from wealth, they were vastly inferior to the "Northern" faction of Julu.

Pei Qian glanced at the barefoot Taoist cloaked in a crane robe. She had seen records in the book "The Immortal's Tome" purchased by her junior brother from the Upside-Down Mountain. There was indeed a historical mountain Taoist who loved to recite "Nanhua Qiushui," traveling barefoot through the world, rumored to wear an iron crown of the Taoist sect, seeking to cleanse his insides with the blossoms of plum and snow, carving decay into white bones to form a Taoist temple, willing to reveal his path after completing his cultivation and return to the heavens. He had no fixed abode, wandering far, and his iron staff could transform into a blue dragon upon being thrown.

That elusive mountain Taoist was a genuine, accomplished being, and certainly not the pretender blocking the path before her.

Although Pei Qian had yet to strike her stance, the moment she focused, her mind cleared. As she held her breath and concentrated, she began to unleash her intent. Her eyes began to see visions.

In a fleeting moment, everything fell silent. It felt as if only Pei Qian existed in the world, an unrestrained being, free to move without hindrance.

Yet deep down, Pei Qian knew that the stillness she perceived was not a true halt of time; rather, the flow around her seemed to slow to an excruciating crawl.

The closer the danger approached, the more the flow of time seemed to freeze.

In her solitary practice, Pei Qian essentially had but one purpose: to try and make the river of time appear as if it had come to a complete standstill, allowing her body and mind to move freely. When she unleashed her punches, no martial artist would be able to question her; in their presence, they would have to witness her countless strikes!

Of course, her master was the exception. Pei Qian practiced her punches solely to catch up with her master, never daring to hope to stand alongside him in martial arts.

During their travels along the Sword Qi Great Wall, her master had once said something peculiar: he wanted to learn this divine ability from his first disciple.

Her master’s jokes were indeed quite entertaining.

Why would her master learn from a disciple?

But this once heartwarming joke, which had made Pei Qian smile secretly and beam, was becoming less and less amusing. The fact that her master had not returned home day after day, year after year, turned what had once been a comforting joke into a cage that made her heart ache, nearly suffocating her and making her want to shatter it with a punch. Earlier, when she had chosen to travel across continents, abandoning her ability to fly and opting to tread the waves instead, every punch she delivered had aimed for that invisible river of time.

In an instant, the old woman lost sight of the young martial artist./n/n“Is that really the anticipated Golden Body Realm? Whether they are cultivators or pure martial artists, while their realm might be obscured, age is something that can usually be discerned based on their bone structure, as long as the difference in cultivation isn’t too vast. That woman clearly doesn’t look to be over thirty. Could she really be a new third-generation disciple from the Lei Gong Temple’s Pei Ah Xiang lineage? Otherwise, among the younger generation of talented martial artists in the Aiai Continent, there’s no one like her! In Aiai Continent, any Golden Body Realm martial artist under forty is a celebrity, and Liu Caishen has a saying that’s widely circulated, ‘Unfortunately, I can’t smash my way to martial fortune with divine money.’”

In a moment of desperation, the old woman turned around, and the large burlap bag behind her suddenly expanded, shielding her figure. 

With a resounding crack, a punch struck the old woman’s protected back, shattering the wind and snow within a radius of several dozen yards. 

The old woman, with her back to the attacking girl, was utterly defenseless. She was propelled off the ground and sent flying straight ahead, not even given the chance to change her trajectory, showcasing the sheer weight of that punch. 

At the same time, the old woman vaguely sensed a gust of fierce wind brushing past her, a blurred figure leaping over her and rushing forward. Then, a few dozen yards away, the opponent slid and suddenly twisted her body, delivering another punch directly at the old woman. Startled, the old woman had no time to think; she used a Golden Core as the core of her personal world, spinning it rapidly within her life energy center, igniting countless golden rays that intertwined with her three souls and seven spirits, desperately stabilizing her trembling soul. She then projected her shadow outwards, drifting back, leaving her body behind while summoning two precious items for offense, preparing to unleash her techniques to prevent the fierce girl from becoming too rampant.

The other precious item, left within her body, was driven by the Golden Core, suddenly glowing brilliantly. An intricate and mysterious formation appeared around the old woman, a pavilion built from countless strands of snow-white silk, crystalline and ethereal, resembling a glass fairyland. Atop the petite pavilion, a tiny old woman of thumb height sat, fingers forming seals to continuously draw the great snow water energy from heaven and earth, stabilizing the formation.

However, the old woman, who had set up this defensive stance, did not wait for that fearsome second punch.

One practitioner was surprisingly adept at manipulating talismans, vanishing in an instant.

The barefooted man in the crane cloak, holding a plum branch, had originally intended to take advantage of the chaos and target a Qi Practitioner to relieve his boredom. He had just plucked a plum blossom with his fingers, ready to toss it lightly at someone.

As for the identity of the young woman, he had roughly gauged her strength; she was indeed a Golden Body Realm with an impressive physique. Although rare, she was still inferior to the distant traveler, Liu Suoyu, from back then.

Just as the barefooted man, who called himself the Autumn Water Daoist, felt a twinge of unease, his body began to glow with white light, and he was about to cast a spell to escape.

Yet, for no apparent reason, a strange inertia struck him. The once radiant crane cloak was forcibly pulled back into its original form, as if the scattered snowflakes were being compressed into a snowball. This self-proclaimed demonic cultivator, the Autumn Water Daoist, reappeared as if he were a dazed goose, taking a direct punch from the young woman.

Pei Qian also withdrew her fist after delivering the blow.

The Autumn Water Daoist fell into a pit in the snow, sitting on the ground. He inhaled deeply, chewing the plum blossoms he had gathered, blood streaming from his seven orifices, but the gruesome sight disappeared in an instant.

He stood up, shaking off the snowflakes from his cloak, and bowed towards the distance, calling out to his master.

Pei Qian reached out and summoned her walking stick from afar.

Facing both the old woman and the barefooted man, Pei Qian didn’t employ her divine beating technique.

Because the real enemy was not either of them.

Once she exerted her strength to kill one of them, it would be of no use and would only place her in true peril.

In fact, she had detected that shadow even before the old woman and the Autumn Water Daoist.

In the distance, a young nobleman stood atop a snow-white lion, watching the battlefield with an amused expression.

The ruler of the southern region of the Aiai Continent. The jade purity realm demon, Xi Liu.

Pei Qian didn’t consider a jade purity realm to be that formidable.

Because she had been to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Suddenly, the snow-white lion appeared beside the old woman, and Xi Liu did not hide his curiosity, observing the young woman who was very likely a traveler in the distant realm. He smiled and said, “Firstly, we, the hidden demons of the icy plains, rarely initiate attacks in the south. Secondly, you are a remarkably law-abiding passerby; I won’t make things difficult for you. Therefore, there’s no need for us to escalate matters too much. As long as you are willing to leave and hand over this group to my friend, the Autumn Water Daoist, we can call it even.”

Xi Liu smiled again, “Of course, there’s another option. If this group of celestial beings can leave and you remain, then they can live. But you, my dear, will have to become my guest here in Xi Liu’s abode. Regardless, one side must stay to enjoy the snow with me.” 

Xi Liu shot a glance at the Autumn Water Daoist, who immediately stepped aside.

The old woman chuckled, “My master always keeps his word; you should think it over.”

In the southern region, Xi Liu, this major demon, indeed meant what he said.

Thus, the Qi practitioners began to communicate silently, and almost simultaneously made their decision to retreat south.

In the end, only the young martial woman remained.

Xi Liu smiled and said, “You threw a punch for those ungrateful and vile characters, creating a path for yourself, yet ended up in a predicament. Don’t you think that’s a bit unworthy?”

Pei Qian walked over to the bamboo box, shaking her head. “A punch for oneself.”

Placing her walking stick atop the bamboo box, she slowly rolled up her sleeves. It seemed there was a fight about to unfold.

Perfect.

This was what she had been craving.

But Xi Liu continued with a curious inquiry, “Putting aside your previous encounters while heading south, which were clearly justified, is it right for you to deal with demons for these Qi practitioners today?”

Pei Qian still shook her head, replying, “I didn’t kill it. Whether you believe it or not is up to you, Senior Xi Liu.”

Since the other party was willing to be reasonable, even if it was only temporary, Pei Qian was willing to say a few more words.

Xi Liu was taken aback, turning to the old woman, whose expression was slightly awkward. “Reporting to the master, this young girl simply scared off that flower demon with a single punch.”

The flower demon that had previously chased the Qi practitioners was named Zhuo Hua. It had merely been injured by the young martial artist’s punch, but was terrified and mistakenly believed she was a disciple of Liu Suoyu, a Nine Realm martial artist, and had already fled hundreds of miles away.

And the major demon, Xi Liu, had been drawn here by the intent of Pei Qian’s punch, which was why he had mistakenly assumed Zhuo Hua had been killed somewhere.

Xi Liu’s curiosity grew. “Which sect do you belong to, little girl? Your style doesn’t resemble that of the Lei Gong Temple’s Pei Ah Xiang lineage at all.”

As for the respectful title of “Senior Xi Liu,” it made this jade purity realm demon on the snow-white lion feel rather amused and taken aback.

Pei Qian hesitated but shook her head.

Xi Liu seemed to ponder, then pressed his hand against his forehead, groaning in discomfort. 

What on earth was happening today? First, there was a young girl who was quite reasonable yet had an unreasonable martial cultivation, and now another woman was making him uneasy.

The latter was undoubtedly a sword immortal.

Sword immortals from the Northern Julu Continent were rare.

Adding to the fact that this one was a woman, Xi Liu concluded her identity: a sword immortal named Xie Songhua, who didn’t particularly enjoy her hometown, Aiai Continent.

It was said that Xie Songhua’s strikes were devastating and decisive, ending battles with a single blow.

Though Xi Liu felt apprehensive, he wasn’t overly fearful. Being in the southern icy plains, he had the advantage of terrain. If it came to a fight, he wouldn’t stand a chance, but he could at least witness the sword immortal’s elegance before leaving.

The woman with the bamboo box approached, riding a sword and gliding in, her sword qi parting the snow and wind around her, creating a clear path, while the surrounding storm still obscured the sky.

She hovered in midair, her expression cold, looking down at Xi Liu, who preferred to hide.

Xie Songhua had left her two direct disciples behind in the city of Tuo Ling, named Zhao Mu and Ju Xing.

She had sensed something unusual in the area, which was why she had taken to the skies.

Besides Xie Songhua, who was recruiting disciples in a foreign land, there was also Li Cai from the Floating Sword Lake in the Northern Julu Continent, who had taken two sword-seeking disciples, Chen Li and Gao Youqing, away from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

As for the sword immortal from the Golden Armor Continent, Song Ping, she too had taken two young girls as her direct disciples, named Sun Zao and Jin Luan.
