Meanwhile, Pu He from the Liuxia Continent had descended to the Golden Core stage after encountering difficulties at the Sword Qi Great Wall and had taken a pair of teenagers with him, named Ye Du and Xue Zhou.

After returning to the Haoran World, Xie Songhua had exchanged messages with Li Cai, Song Ping, and Pu He through flying swords, each making an appointment for a reunion sixty years later.

Of course, this wasn’t a competition to see whose sword techniques were superior; it held little meaning. Especially for Li Cai and Pu He, who had suffered severe injuries that affected their fundamental sword path, and even the highly accomplished Xie Songhua didn’t feel her skills worthy of boasting compared to the great sword immortals. Moreover, could those of them who were still alive and returned to their homeland compare with those like Xie Zhi and Yuan Qingshu, who had died in battle? They couldn’t.

Given this, the four sword immortals compared their abilities to teach their direct disciples sword techniques, agreeing to meet in the Northern Julu Continent, where Li Cai resided, sixty years later.

Xie Songhua noticed the young woman standing by with the bamboo box and walking stick.

She hesitated to speak.

Back at the Sword Qi Great Wall, she had heard that the young Hidden Official’s disciples often had this kind of demeanor. However, the girl before her was certainly not Guo Zhujiu from the Sword Qi Great Wall. There was also a young girl with the surname Pei, who back then was quite small; even after all these years, she didn’t quite match the young woman in the snow.

What were the chances of encountering someone related to the young Hidden Official in this desolate northern icy plain?

Then, the young woman lifted her head, gathering her voice into a thread, and spoke in the dialect of the Sword Qi Great Wall, “Are you Xie Sword Immortal?”

Xie Songhua immediately descended on her sword, her long blade sheathing itself back into the bamboo box. She smiled and asked, “Is it really you? What was your name again, Pei...?”

“Pei Qian!” the young woman replied, clasping her hands together, her smile radiant.

Xie Songhua’s expression softened considerably as she carefully examined Pei Qian. “Very good, as expected of our Hidden Official’s foremost disciple. Excellent, excellent.”

Xie Songhua nodded towards Xi Liu. “So, have you been bullied? No worries, once I take a shot, we can head to Tuo Ling City together.”

Pei Qian scratched her head. “I was just following my master’s example, discussing reason with Senior Xi Liu.”

Xi Liu looked a bit helpless, nodding. “That’s indeed the case.”

Xie Songhua said, “In that case, I’ll just avoid the southern region and won’t trouble you.”

Then, Xie Songhua left Xi Liu behind, helping Pei Qian retrieve her walking stick and bamboo box. Pei Qian took back the walking stick and slung the book box over her back.

Xie Songhua spoke through her mind, “Have you heard the huge news? It’s somewhat related to your master, and it just spread not long ago.”

Pei Qian’s eyes widened. “What news?!”

Xi Liu watched the figures of the large and small disappear into the distance, shaking his head. What kind of situation was this?

Xie Songhua said, “I don’t know who first proposed it, but they’ve selected ten young talents from across the world.”

Pei Qian’s spirits lifted. “Where did my master rank?”

Xie Songhua shook her head, suppressing a laugh. “It explicitly stated that the ten don’t have a ranking order. Among them are the sword cultivator Ning Yao from Flying Ascension City, the martial artist Cao Ci from the Da Duan Dynasty of the Central Land, the Daoist Shan Qing from Bai Yu Jing, and the first of the Hundred Sword Immortals of Tuo Yue Mountain, Fei Ran. Your master isn’t among the ten.”

Pei Qian was puzzled. How was this related to her master?

Xie Songhua rubbed Pei Qian’s head, saying, “They clearly stated ten young talents, yet there’s no ranking, which is quite odd. They listed eleven individuals and placed ‘Hidden Official’ at the eleventh position. Your master is the only one not named directly, only described as a mountain peak realm martial artist and sword cultivator. So now, the cultivators in the Haoran world are all speculating about who this Hidden Official is. Those of us who know your master’s identity aren’t too eager to indulge in this speculation; we’ll let them guess.”

Pei Qian shook the bamboo box, gripping her walking stick tightly, and looked around at the swirling snow. She shouted, “It’s my master!”

(End of chapter)

 **Chapter 823: Another Year’s Dragon Boat Festival**

Xie Songhua did not hurry to return to Tuo Ling City on her flying sword; instead, she chose to walk south alongside Pei Qian. 

In a small border town, no matter how many hidden talents there might be, one must still consider the swift blades of a female sword immortal. Her two direct disciples, although not yet at the peak of the Mid-Fifth Realm, were still sword cultivators, budding sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall. Even if something unexpected happened, Xie Songhua's flying sword would arrive in an instant. 

Moreover, prior to entering Tuo Ling City, Xie Songhua had taken Zhao Mu and Ju Xing to explore the northern peak of the Northern Yue Mountain in the Rain Worker Kingdom. There, the Northern Yue King would surely take care of the two children. If any mishap were to befall a direct disciple of a sword immortal within his domain—especially one belonging to Xie Songhua, who might delay their path to enlightenment—it would surely weigh heavily on a mere mountain king, potentially dragging the entire Rain Worker Kingdom into Xie Sword Immortal's memory.

Xie Songhua's temperament was well-known to be quite fierce across the Aiai Continent.

After chatting with Pei Qian, Xie Songhua felt a wave of emotion wash over her. She hadn’t anticipated that even she couldn't discern Pei Qian's depth of martial prowess. 

It turned out that this girl, barely over twenty, was already a pure martial artist in the far-travel realm. Such a rare talent, one that, if placed atop a mountain, would be considered a Yuanying sword cultivator in her twenties. If it weren't for Cao Ci’s past and Chen Ping’an’s present, Xie Songhua might have doubted Pei Qian's identity.

Yet, Xie Songhua felt more comforted than anything else. 

In truth, she had never met Pei Qian before, and they were not related, but seeing Pei Qian traveling with her cane and bundle gave Xie Songhua a sense of familiarity. Whether it was merely affection for someone associated with her or not didn't matter; if Xie Songhua found someone pleasing to the eye, the heavens had no say in it. If she found someone displeasing, they could certainly try to manage her flying sword, but they had better have the courage and capability to do so.

Thus, Xie Songhua chuckled, “If you’re worried that Auntie Xie’s swordsmanship isn’t up to par and that I won’t fare well against Xi Liu, then there’s no need for that roundabout way of speaking. Just tell me honestly, and I’ll go chop Xi Liu down right now. It’ll only take me about the time it takes to burn half a stick of incense to return. Killing a jade purity realm sword cultivator from the demon race isn’t that hard; without the title of sword cultivator, it becomes much easier.”

Pei Qian quickly shook her head, “Auntie Xie, it’s not like that. If Xi Liu were truly pushing hard and using her authority to pressure others, I would’ve asked for a duel right there.”

Xie Songhua nodded, “Then it seems Xi Liu has been lucky and has had her incense burned high. I initially planned to take Zhao Mu and Ju Xing to temper their sword intent in the southern ice plains, and I would definitely have a chat with Xi Liu. Zhao Mu has two life-bound flying swords, one named ‘Rainbow’ and the other ‘Pouring Rain’; it’s quite suitable for nurturing here. Ju Xing’s sword, ‘Thunder Marsh’, doesn’t benefit much from the ice plains. So, we’ll need to visit the Temple of Thunder to consult with Pei Axiang and see if Ju Xing has any opportunities for enlightenment over in the Ma Lake Prefecture.”

At the moment, Pei Qian didn’t quite understand what Xie Songhua meant by “having a chat with Xi Liu” or “visiting the Temple of Thunder.”

However, the fact that Xie Songhua was willing to reveal the true names of her two direct disciples’ flying swords indicated her closeness to Pei Qian, treating her as family.

Xie Songhua had always held a poor opinion of her hometown, Aiai Continent. After ascending to the Earth Immortal realm years ago, she had traveled extensively through the Liuxia and Jinjia Continents. Before taking on her direct disciples, every time she returned home, she would not disclose her whereabouts, nor would she flaunt her identity as a sword immortal. This led to quite a few conflicts, and not small ones at that. Xie Songhua never considered herself a reasonable person, so every time she would fight the young and the old alike. If the founding ancestor were still alive, that would be even better. Thus, the cultivators of Aiai Continent both feared and were troubled by this sword immortal from their own land.

Now, Xie Songhua’s prestige in Aiai Continent was at its peak.

As a female sword immortal, she had traveled the Sword Qi Great Wall, achieving remarkable military exploits, including slaying formidable demon beasts at the jade purity realm. Moreover, crucially, Xie Songhua had returned alive to the Haoran world.

For the cultivators atop Aiai Continent, a dead female sword immortal would just be that—a dead sword immortal. Aiai Continent had no custom of memorializing swordsmen like those at the Great Zhou.

The most shocking news for the people of Aiai Continent was the rumor that Xie Songhua was highly likely to break through the jade purity bottleneck and ascend to the immortal realm within a few decades, becoming the first great sword immortal from Aiai Continent to reach that level in a millennium.

For cultivators, a few decades could be as brief as a nap for an immortal atop a mountain.

Xie Songhua laughed and asked, “Now that we’re all martial artists of the Eighth Realm, why not fly on the winds for our travels?”

Pei Qian blushed a little and replied softly, “My master said that traveling downhill can set you back two realms. You mustn’t imitate someone who lets a move go free during duels.”

Pei Qian continued, “Auntie Xie, you can fly your sword, and I’ll ride the wind; there’s no need to be so particular since I’m following you.”

After all, Xie Songhua was a senior sword immortal, and this journey to the ice plains was to impart the swordsmanship teachings to her two direct disciples.

Xie Songhua burst out laughing, “As expected of his first disciple! No worries, we’ll continue walking to Tuo Ling City. Consider it a leisurely stroll.”

Curiously, Xie Songhua asked, “Who is this person? Can you tell me?”

Anyone that the young hidden official would mention wouldn't be simple. 

For instance, that wine-loving sword immortal, who was now the head of the Taihui Sword Sect in Beiju Lu Continent.

Pei Qian smiled, “Auntie Xie, there’s nothing I can’t tell you. My master’s friend is a military cultivator from the Ghostly Axe Palace in Beiju Lu Continent, named Du Yu. He enjoys roaming the world, and my master met him by chance during his travels in Beiju Lu Continent and learned some talisman techniques from him.”

Xie Songhua nodded, “Although I haven’t heard of the Ghostly Axe Palace, someone who can engage your master must possess quite the ability. However, in a duel, you certainly shouldn’t let your master take a hit.”

Pei Qian scratched her head. 

She was no longer that little charcoal girl from years ago, and she wasn’t even really a girl anymore, but this action still revealed a rare bit of innocence from her.

On the southern ice plains, Xi Liu was returning to her residence with the old woman and Daoist Qiu Shui, leisurely strolling through the blinding snow and wind.

The old woman softly asked, “Master, was that really the sword immortal Xie Songhua?”

Xi Liu smiled and nodded, “The sword intent contained within that bamboo box she carries is unmistakable.”

Daoist Qiu Shui, draped in a crane cloak and holding a plum branch, no longer possessed the demeanor of an immortal; he grinned, “That little girl has a heavy punch. I still ache all over from that one hit. When she landed that punch, my Qi Palace and the three souls and seven spirits felt like they were flipped upside down by a raging bull. That talisman that can shrink mountains and rivers? To have a pure martial artist use it in close combat is truly deadly. No wonder the founder of that lineage has been scolded for thousands of years.”

Xi Liu remarked, “Looking back, that little girl must have been deliberately hiding her strength. Perhaps when she punched at you, it was to conceal her true abilities. After I revealed myself, she likely considered me her only opponent. I suspect even that talisman was just a diversion. I guess if that little girl were to fully unleash herself, she would be faster than using a talisman. In that case, I should thank the sword immortal for not letting me lose my troops, and also thank that little girl for averting a disaster.”

Xi Liu couldn't help but feel, “Isn’t the natural order clear? Karma is indeed real?”

The old woman, puzzled, asked, “Master, your aura has been subdued and is without flaw, no less than that of a scholar from the academy. Even I can’t perceive a trace of it. How could that little girl have noticed?”

Xi Liu sighed, “You ask me? Who do I ask?”

Tuo Ling City served as the prefectural capital of the Rain Worker Kingdom's Lin Tan Prefecture and was one of the two important crossings leading to the southern ice plains.

At the city gate, Pei Qian presented a travel document. During her travels in Beiju Lu Continent, she had collected many stamped passes, and Senior Li Er from Lion Peak had helped her forge a new travel document, one specifically for mountain cultivators, which was also an important item for the wealthy and collectors down below.

Naturally, Xie Songhua did not have any travel documents, and upon glancing at Pei Qian, the guards at Tuo Ling City turned a blind eye and let them pass.

At the celestial inn, Pei Qian met the two budding sword immortals, both children of about ten years old, one boy and one girl. The girl was named Zhao Mu, while the boy was named Ju Xing; both appeared quite clever.

However, Ju Xing seemed slightly more serious, his eyes calm and subdued, which was not quite fitting for his age.

As was customary, Pei Qian presented them with two specially made bookmarks from the Fallen Star Mountain as a token of their first meeting.

Upon hearing that Sister Pei Qian was the first disciple of the hidden official, Ju Xing suddenly brightened up, while Zhao Mu also beamed with joy, as the little girl shared the same street as Guo Zhujiu, who liked to refer to herself as “the temporary disciple of my master.” Besides, there were innumerable stories about that hidden official.

Whether it was conning people out of their money selling wine or getting ripped off in gambling, the tales of extraordinary supernatural beings and scenic stories filled her mind, and she believed that Ning Yao and he were a match made in heaven. For her, he had traveled thousands of miles twice just for her, passing through three barriers, even defeating Qi Shou and Pang Yuanji in combat, willingly replacing Ning Yao to face the Li Zhen on Tuo Mountain, becoming famous in a single battle, and becoming the youngest and first outsider to be the hidden official in the history of the Sword Qi Great Wall. Even Yu Juanfu had taken a hit from him, ultimately leading to three consecutive victories, with countless peculiar remarks that would make any great sword immortal’s heart ache. He personally wrote the “Ba Jian Immortal Seal,” maneuvering affairs at the summer palace, and on the battlefield, he was even more treacherous than the great demon Shou Chen, and he had even disguised himself as a woman while picking up scraps all over.

The little girl, who owned the two flying swords named “Rainbow” and “Pouring Rain,” pinched the bamboo leaf bookmark between her fingers, raised it high, and gently twisted it in the sunlight, clearly delighted with the gift.

After receiving the gift, she cautiously glanced at Ju Xing, and only when he accepted it did Zhao Mu dare to take her own.

After arriving in the Haoran world, her master had taken them through Jinjia, Liuxia, and Aiai Continents, passing by many celestial residences. Many kind elders would offer gifts to them, but Ju Xing always had a detached expression, his hands tucked into his sleeves. Her master didn’t mind, so she had also refused gifts. Once, she privately asked Ju Xing why, and the usually reticent boy suddenly became furious, asking if she still had any shame left. Zhao Mu was left scared and crying, and seeing her cry only made Ju Xing angrier. He dropped the threat that she should never speak to him again, or he would hit her.

Eventually, it was her master who came to comfort her, and only then did Zhao Mu feel a little better. In truth, during their travels through Aiai Continent, Ju Xing really had not spoken a word to her. Zhao Mu wanted to talk to Ju Xing but was too afraid. She tried to initiate conversation several times, hoping to get closer, but Ju Xing always acted like he was deaf.

So today, Ju Xing accepting a gift was a rare event.

Ju Xing had gently tucked the vibrant green bookmark, engraved with beautiful characters, into his sleeve to treasure carefully. In this Haoran world, reading had become the most ordinary thing.

Xie Songhua joked, “Having one who acts deaf and mute and another who cries at the slightest provocation is really difficult. Pei Qian, to be honest, your master is really something; it’s more challenging than being a hidden official.”

Xie Songhua gave a thumbs-up.

Pei Qian felt somewhat embarrassed.

Her master had indeed had a tough time taking her on journeys during those years.

While Xie Songhua complained, deep down, she felt more pride. She truly didn’t believe that the likes of Li Cai’s Chen Li, Gao Youqing, Pu He’s Ye Du, Xue Zhou, and Song Ping’s Sun Zao, Jin Luan, and all the other scattered children across the Haoran world could outshine her two disciples. It was absolutely impossible! She only accepted these two disciples, pouring her heart into them, and sixty years later, they would surely surpass the early little hidden official Chen Li.

Even if they didn’t, so what? Zhao Mu and Ju Xing would still be her beloved disciples.

Ju Xing sat on the railing with his arms crossed, gently swinging his legs. Back in his hometown, he had liked sitting like this atop the city walls; it was a habit he would never change in this lifetime.

Zhao Mu softly retorted, “Master, it was just three times, not ‘at the slightest provocation’.”

Ju Xing scoffed.

Immediately, Zhao Mu looked sickly.

Xie Songhua stood up and said, “Pei Qian, you chat with them; I’ll go find someone to discuss a few matters. I had an appointment to meet her here, and she should be arriving soon.”

Pei Qian accompanied the two children in casual conversation. 

Zhao Mu was like a chirping little sparrow, and when Pei Qian inquired about the recent excitement with the young ten, the little girl elaborately shared all the happenings.

Ju Xing, of course, had to defend the hidden official, insisting that apart from Ning Yao, at most Cao Ci could be added, but the other eight had no right to push the hidden official out of the top ten, only managing to grab the “eleventh” spot.

Pei Qian curiously asked, “What’s the story with the Ascension City?”

Zhao Mu laughed, “The fifth realm of the world, named Jia Chun, is based on our hometown, which was named Ascension City at the time of the world’s creation.”

Ju Xing added, “There’s news that Sister Ning Yao is not only the first jade purity realm sword cultivator of that realm, but she has also ascended to the immortal realm now.”

Pei Qian looked at this lively little girl and couldn’t help but miss the little millet from Fallen Star Mountain and the ever-youthful Sister Nuan Shu. 

At this moment, Pei Qian finally realized that Sister Bao Ping had grown up, and so had she. 

If her master, Bao Ping’s little uncle, found out about this, would he feel happy or sad?

Pei Qian opened her book box and began copying texts. 

Zhao Mu sat quietly beside her, resting her chin in her hands, watching Sister Pei write.

Ju Xing was lost in thought about the second opening of the fifth realm; soon, he would be able to return home. 

He heard that the fifth realm would open its doors for thirty years, after which it would be permanently closed. 

After that, if he wished to travel between the two worlds, he would have to become a great cultivator at the Ascension Realm.

Ju Xing felt a twinge of envy for Sister Pei’s walking stick and bamboo box. The little boy imitated the hidden official, with his hands tucked into his sleeves, dazedly sitting on the railing.

The young ten selected this time were all under fifty, and there was no distinction among them. 

The reasoning was simple; being too young, one needed at least a hundred years of mountain climbing and cultivation to truly attain enlightenment.

The Ascension City’s Ning Yao had broken through two realms in the fifth realm and ascended to the immortal realm. 

Great martial artist Cao Ci had reached the tenth realm while in the waters of Fu Yao Continent. 

Daoist Shansheng from Bai Yu Jing was at the jade purity realm, possessing no magical artifacts because all of his life-bound items were immortal weapons or semi-immortal weapons. He followed the path of the five elements and was regarded as the best in the world.

The first of the Hundred Sword Immortals of Tuo Mountain, Fei Ran, was a jade purity realm sword cultivator. It was said he enjoyed suppressing his realm.

There was also a direct disciple of a sub-saint, rumored to be a young scholar from the Qing Ming realm, who had been brought back to the Haoran world by the sub-saint in his early years. Not only had he received a gust of wind for flipping through books, but he had also formed the beginnings of a life-bound character.

A young monk who entered the fifth realm, wielding a twelve-ringed iron staff. 

From Qing Ming realm, a previously unknown female Daoist under twenty, who had only cultivated for eight years, stagnated for six years at the Liu Jin realm, then soared to the jade purity realm in one leap.

And in the Haoran realm, there was also Liu Cai, a formerly unremarkable wilderness cultivator, currently at the golden core realm sword cultivator, though his flying sword's killing power surpassed imagination. Even just reading about him in the reports would leave cultivators speechless. Since Ning Yao, Cao Ci, and Shansheng were truly the pride of heaven, their realms were sufficiently high, yet Liu Cai was merely at the golden core realm. Generally, let alone golden core sword cultivators under fifty, even Yuanying sword cultivators wouldn’t be a match for him and were completely unqualified to be listed.

With Liu Cai’s emergence, two long-lost sword nurturing gourds were revealed: the “Heart’s Desire” and “Immediate.” Liu Cai possessed two life-bound flying swords. The “Heart’s Desire” nurtured the flying sword “Biluò,” known for its ability to break through myriad laws, while “Biluò” could break through myriad swords. The “Immediate” helped nurture Liu Cai’s second flying sword “Bai Ju,” whose subtleness and swiftness could ignore the flow of time.

Thus, in the Haoran realm, it was said that the only sword cultivator who could compete with Ning Yao was Liu Cai a hundred years from now.

The young disciple of the Heavenly Master Qizhen, who had traveled to the Central Plains, served as the keeper of the archives. It was rumored that within three years, he had read every text of Daoism.

From the Barbarian realm, a young cultivator named Shi Yue burst onto the scene like Liu Cai and the female Daoist.

Lastly, there was a young person who had gained some fame from another continent, notorious for the “Chen Ping Case.”

Earlier, it was said there were still ten substitutes, but they had yet to be announced.

Zhao Mu mustered her courage and turned to steal a glance at Ju Xing, who hadn’t acknowledged her in a long time.

In truth, he was younger than her, born in the same month and year, but Ju Xing was a few days later.

However, the little girl always felt that Ju Xing was much older than her.

Ju Xing noticed Zhao Mu’s gaze and immediately glared at her. Zhao Mu blinked innocently, as if to say, “I’m not even talking to you; how is this your concern?”

Ju Xing’s fingers came together and lightly gestured for the little girl to turn her head back.

Zhao Mu complied, resting her chin on the table, continuing to watch Sister Pei write.

The little girl wanted to ask this sister why she had to leave her hometown if she was already home. 

If she could stay in her hometown, she would surely never travel far.

Sister Pei was truly brave and could endure hardships all on her own.

Zhao Mu was unaware that this tall, slender, slightly dark-skinned Sister Pei, who made her feel safe, was actually once a little girl who cried out in pain after just a light squeeze on her shoulders and arms at the pharmacy in Longcheng, even more so than Zhao Mu would have. Back then, Pei Qian was actually slightly older than Zhao Mu. As for courage, Pei Qian had very little when she was young, perhaps even less than little millet. Even now, she still carried a plain yellow talisman.

Sister Pei was focused on her writing. 

Suddenly, Zhao Mu felt a rush of panic and quickly turned to look at Ju Xing.

Ju Xing looked back at Zhao Mu and raised a finger to his lips, shaking his head, signaling for her to stay silent.

Zhao Mu stood up quietly, realizing that Sister Pei was copying the text and somehow shedding tears.

Pei Qian was feeling sorrowful; the next time her master scolded her, it seemed he might not need to bend down anymore.

Then, even if the master and disciple finally reunited and traveled together again, perhaps her master would never again reach out to hold the little girl’s hand.

How had she grown up so quickly?

Once, her older brother, the big white goose, had told a joke, asking her, the elder sister, if she knew who in the world had the most worries.

Pei Qian naturally said it was her master, as he loved to think things through and take care of others.

The little brother had laughed and shook his head, giving a rather absurd answer.

He said it was a fellow named “Grown Up.”

In the capital city of Dali, the elder statesman Guan sat in a rattan chair under the eaves, even though the old man was bundled up thickly, he still felt cold. Holding a warming stove, he gazed at the green parasol tree in the courtyard.

The old man smiled, extending his thumb to lightly touch a tooth, sighing heavily.

His diligent direct descendant Guan Yiran had returned to the capital this time, officially resigning from the position of the overseer of the Qi Crossing project. He was about to fill a vacancy in the Ministry of Revenue but had not been promoted to a ministerial position like Liu Qingfeng. To be honest, even compared to the young Liu Xunmei, Guan Yiran’s promotion seemed rather meager and stingy in the emperor’s eyes. 

Although Guan Yiran, who hailed from the military background at the borders, was reluctant, it was not that he despised the lowly position, but rather he had long been accustomed to the rough life on the battlefield. Nonetheless, he obeyed the orders of his great-grandfather and chose to return to the capital to serve.

Upon returning home, Guan Yiran immediately rushed to the old man’s side.

Guan Yiran squatted down beside the old man, pressing his hand against the warming stove.

The old man chuckled, “The Ministry of Revenue is an ungrateful place; get used to it. The Ministry of Personnel is out of the question; don’t ever dream of working there in your lifetime. After all, others think the Ministry of Revenue belongs to the Guan family, but if you Guan family members truly believe that, it’s a path to death. You must leave some room for others. Squatting in the latrine without relieving yourself or staying too long will get you stoned, and then you can’t complain about anyone else.”

Guan Yiran smiled. The earliest batch of important ministers in the Dali court were actually rather uncouth, even those from scholarly backgrounds.

The old man looked up at the beautiful scenery of the sunset sky, sighing, “Teeth fall, hair falls, and I can’t walk anymore. How vexing. When I see a young, beautiful girl, I’m left with no heart or strength; at most, I can only reminisce about the past and think of the young heroes. Being young is good; there are promotions to be had. The flying deities in the sky are also enviable.”

The old man spoke to himself as the young man listened.

“The country is broken, but the mountains and rivers remain; the city is full of spring grass and deep woods. The person rolling up the curtain still says things remain the same. This is a collection of verses by a literary master from the Lu clan, beautifully written. It’s a pity that while his writing is good, his governance skills are quite lacking.”

“The fragrance of food when starving, and the scent of powder from young girls is delightful, but there’s another fragrance that’s not bad, you know? That’s when you scratch your feet on a summer’s cool mat.”

“Go, help great-grandpa steal a pot of wine. A few pots that were hidden in the study earlier have been secretly taken by your father and placed in his own study. What a rotten thing. After putting down the wine, let great-grandpa sit for a while by himself. Haha, a good one to drink and gorge, but don’t let the younger generation know.”

Guan Yiran hummed in agreement and stood up to leave.

Suddenly, the old man called out, “Yiran.”

Guan Yiran immediately turned around.

The old man smiled without saying a word.

Guan Yiran understood, saying, “Got it, I’ll take two pots.”

The old man nodded, “When you’re an official, be sure to do a good job, but don’t forget to be a good person first. Don’t imitate those big overseers, who rarely go out, but when they do, they’ll follow an official with a bigger hat, and first borrow a pair of badly worn boots. Don’t do anything foolish like that, or else great-grandpa will really lose sleep.”

Guan Yiran’s eyes turned slightly red, nodding vigorously, “Understood!”

After the young man left the courtyard.

Old Master Guan gently patted the arm of the rattan chair, softly calling, “National Teacher? Are you busy? If not, come and chat with me?”

The National Teacher of Dali, Cui Zhan, appeared.

Old Master Guan did not pay his respects, nor did he even greet him; he simply continued gazing at the darkening sky, murmuring, “Cui Zhen, will the world get better? I asked you this question when I was young, and you only said I should see for myself. Now that I’m getting older, my eyesight is failing, and I can’t see far even when I squint, and in the future, I won’t see anything at all. Cui Zhen, what do you think? So I can walk with peace of mind.”

Cui Zhen replied, “At least during Guan Yingche’s time in office, the Dali state was better.”

The old man softly said, “But there are still many grievances that make one uncomfortable. I don’t even know how to express them or to whom I should speak.”

Cui Zhen replied, “Every household’s meals and every family’s couplets are the answers to the grievances in the hearts of scholars.”

The old man nodded, “Once, a well-read young scholar said that the blooming and withering of flowers, the dying and flourishing of grass, are all responses to the moonlight above. Your words are spot on, Cui Zhen.”

Cui Zhen smiled, “Who would disagree?”

Dali once had a cold clan scholar preparing for the imperial examination, who, at a youthful age, boldly claimed, “Who else but me could be the literary master of the nation?” Yet in reality, his poetry and prose were quite mediocre.

The old man lamented, “It’s not that I fear death; it’s just that it’s hard to let go.”

That young man came from the Cliffside Academy.

The old man said, “Cui Zhen, I’m glad to have met you and Qi Zhen. During my time at the academy, learning from Qi Zhen, and serving in the court with you, Cui Zhen.”

Cui Zhen nodded, “I believe Qi Jingchun will also be glad to have a Guan Yingche among his students.”

The old man asked, “Then can I curse the national teacher a few times for Qi Zhen?”

Cui Zhen smiled, “You should first curse the Minister of Personnel, then you can curse me.”

The old man laughed, shaking his head, “Let’s skip that.”

Many conversations between old men were like final verdicts.

When Guan Yiran returned with two pots of wine, only the national teacher could drink.

In the sixth year of Jia Chun in the fifth realm, half of the Sword Qi Great Wall in the Barbarian realm had been isolated by formation, truly wandering alone year after year.

Ever since Fei Ran left, he had been walking on the cliffs, occasionally using his knife to break through formations for a moment, gazing at the vast demon army marching northward.

After six years, he still hadn’t seen the demons retreat southward.

In the end, he simply sat in a place that could barely be called a cave, occasionally drawing his knife to break seals, left with nothing to do but watch the demons continue northward.

Yet, every time Chen Ping’an drew his knife, the seals would quickly mend themselves.

Upon learning of this, Li Zhen suggested that Tuo Mountain be even crueler and set up a solid formation between the two cliffs that even a jade purity realm sword cultivator couldn’t break, denying that young hidden official any opportunity to savor it.

Unfortunately, the Jiazi account had put this plan on hold for now, saying it would be discussed later.

On this day, a young hidden official in a bright red robe sat cross-legged, a broad sword resting on his knee, gently tapping the sword sheath with his hand.

In one sleeve, there was a collection of densely written characters from that travelogue, packed tightly as if a great army was assembling.

In fact, when Chen Ping’an first finished reading the book, he realized the hidden secrets within.

That was why he had the thought, “It’s a good thing I didn’t write about what I truly care about; otherwise, I wouldn’t be able to speak properly in the future.”

Chen Ping’an was extremely sensitive to the “eleven,” and as for the “gain word,” he knew well that those many bamboo slips were not engraved for nothing. He had a greater fondness for collecting obscure and complex words and phrases than many others who had read since childhood. Especially regarding decoding, he had learned early on in the streets near the tavern, where the children had already experienced the prowess of this second shopkeeper.

Now, when drawing his knife to break seals, besides observing the number of demon troops and deducing the situation of the war, Chen Ping’an also needed to determine whether that great door would occasionally close, worrying that Tuo Mountain had already noticed the secrets of the travelogue and might close the door to isolate the two realms, or that they had already set up other mountain and water prohibitions. If Chen Ping’an were to act hastily, it would instead cause Cui Zhen’s secret plans to fall through.

Just knowing that the travelogue was extraordinary was meaningless. This was also what made Cui Zhen the most meticulous.

In these years, after inscribing all the words in the travelogue, Chen Ping’an had racked his brains to decipher that sealed letter, arranging those words in various formations, which was extremely laborious. He had reread the travelogue repeatedly, perhaps in a certain chapter, taking one character from every eleven characters, gathering them all to see if he could form a sealed letter, perhaps focusing on the characters “Lian” and “Chan,” expanding in various contexts, or using reverse chronology to search for clues...

Cui Dongshan had said that anyone whose mind was normal couldn’t unravel this thread of reasoning.

But in truth, his teacher had not only grasped the thread after reading the travelogue once, but even the act of throwing the book and retrieving it had been a distraction. Since then, he had been refining characters while pondering thousands of miles.

All the trivial matters in life that felt burdensome and uncomfortable might eventually shine brightly like scattered stars at some point on the road ahead.

Chen Ping’an curled up, his hands tucked into his sleeves, lost in thought.

Today in the Haoran world, it was the fifth day of the fifth month.

When there were people around, Chen Ping’an wouldn’t pay much attention to whether it was the fifth day of the fifth month. 

But when alone, he would think of it each time.

After his parents passed, one day at the end of Mud Bottle Alley, a family opened their door. Later, that family had a little snot-nosed kid, and he soon met his neighbors, Song Jixin and Zhi Gui, and later Liu Xianyang. 

Then he left his hometown, and with Li Bao Ping and Li Huai, and later Zhang Shan Feng and Liu Yuanxia, and also Pei Qian, he had Fallen Star Mountain. Even at Shujian Lake and upon reaching the Sword Qi Great Wall, he had people who mattered by his side.

Yet, in these past years, Chen Ping’an had once again been alone.

He gently exhaled, tapping his chest lightly, thinking that being alone still allowed for some self-talk.

On the high cliffs across from him, Li Zhen and Liu Bai had come to the Dragon King’s side together today.

Li Zhen smiled and asked, “Why is our hidden official so quiet lately? Has he taken to heart that old saying in the Haoran world, ‘The dog that bites doesn’t bark’?”

The Dragon King glanced at him, disinterested in responding.

You’re the one who likes to make noise.

Liu Bai smiled slightly, clearly understanding the Dragon King’s expression.

Li Zhen shouted, “Hidden official! If the travelogue doesn’t say otherwise, today is a good day!”

Chen Ping’an lifted his head, and the next moment, he appeared atop the city walls.

Li Zhen grinned, “I have two pieces of good news for you. One is that the ‘Hidden Official’ is quite famous in several realms now. The second piece of good news is that the Jiazi account is increasingly valuing our hidden official; they’re going to shut the door for good.”

Li Zhen waved, “Next time we meet, please don’t come with a tail begging, alright?”

The Dragon King shot Li Zhen a sideways glance and said, “Just a reminder.”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “I’ll be at jade purity soon.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 824: The Hidden Beauty

On the land of Tongye Continent, amidst the countless celestial mounds, there were only a few mountain sects that could rely on the formations of mountains and rivers to resist the invasion of the demon clan. 

The formation known as the Three Enclosures and Four Symbols, created collaboratively by the Yuguizong, Tongye Sect, Taiping Mountain, and Fuji Sect, was growing increasingly dim. If one were to look down from the heavens upon the continent, the flickering lights of human settlements appeared to gradually extinguish. Each time a light vanished, it heralded the fall of a celestial sect, marking the erosion of Tongye Continent’s fortune, which was instead being absorbed by the demon race. As this cycle continued, the mountain dwellers found themselves trembling with fear, realizing the outcome was already set.

To the south lay the Xuanju Sect, predominantly composed of female cultivators, with their ancestral mountain, Konghou Mountain, housing a hall of ancestral masters known as the Thunderous Hall.

Although it was not a particularly large sect, its remote geographical location made it somewhat inconsequential, allowing it to temporarily evade the onslaught of the demon army.

Currently, the Xuanju Sect had gathered dozens of displaced cultivators from various mountain sects. Once high and mighty celestial masters, they now all felt like stray dogs without a home.

Among them was a young swordsman in a green robe, hailing from a small sect. Previously, he held a jade token from the ancestral hall of his sect and paid a sum of celestial money to seek refuge in the Xuanju Sect.

Today, he ventured alone to a picturesque location within Konghou Mountain, known as the Xiuzhu Rock Water Viewing Platform. Below the Xiuzhu Rock was a deep pool, its depths unfathomable. As the green-robed swordsman ascended the platform, he used a horn of a thousand-year-old lamp to illuminate the depths, observing the aquatic creatures and ethereal beings that inhabited the dark waters. With the aid of celestial spells, the mundane eye could perceive many bizarre and unusual aquatic beings, which, after being tamed by the Xuanju Sect’s celestial masters over centuries, swam leisurely about, remarkably docile.

Sitting on the water-viewing platform, the green-robed swordsman held several pieces of intelligence acquired recently. Among them was the report on the thirty military camps, including the Jia Shen Camp, which had already occupied various ancestral halls of celestial sects or the capitals of worldly dynasties. They had effectively encircled the three major academies, including the Dafu Academy, and the four major sects, including Yuguizong, completely sealing off any escape routes. The chaotic world was continuously devouring, seizing, and transforming the fortune of Tongye Continent, while the pressure from the demon army, upon landing, grew increasingly oppressive.

If it weren’t for that Zhong Kui, who continually restrained the great demon Bai Ying—making it exceedingly difficult for Bai Ying’s skeletal armies to form an effective offensive—every encounter with Zhong Kui would result in their self-collapse. His astonishing innate divine arts often caused numerous remnants of ghostly entities found on battlefields below to vanish in an instant, as if they had died a second time, creating significant troubles for the front lines of the chaotic world. Otherwise, the Dafu Academy and several sects, including the Fuji Sect, would have certainly fallen by now.

Following the suggestions of Shoucheng and the Jia Shen Camp, the various military camps began actively recruiting cultivators from Tongye Continent while also imposing restrictions on their advancing troops, prohibiting any further indiscriminate slaughter of cities. They aimed to replicate the strategies employed by the Great Li Iron Cavalry in Baoping Continent, making suitable modifications to drive the armies of the lower kingdoms and vassal forces to attack the mountain sects.

In the eyes of the green-robed swordsman, the only flaw was that the military camps of the chaotic world were still not comparable to the civil and military officials of the Great Li Song family, lacking the kind of strict adherence to orders. 

To put it simply, while they excelled at killing, they were utterly inept at strategy. However, this was all expected. It wasn’t just the chaotic world; even many scholars in the Haoran world found themselves lost in a fog when it came to economic strategies. There was no need for excessive demands; once the Yuguizong or Taiping Mountain fell, the last remnants of morale and spirit among the people of Tongye Continent would be shattered.

As for the strategic choices regarding Yuguizong and Taiping Mountain, Feiran, the sword immortal Shoucheng, and several military camps—including Jia Shen Camp—suggested first breaking Taiping Mountain. As for Yuguizong, located at the southernmost point of Tongye Continent, what would it matter to delay for a few more years? There was no need to entangle with it too deeply. They should quickly gather their forces; as long as they could capture the Tongye Sect that was stationed nearby, they could then cross the continent and crush Baoping Continent. They absolutely must not give the Great Li Iron Cavalry any more opportunities for troop movements.

Yet, more military camps believed that capturing Yuguizong and completely seizing the fortune of the entire continent was the most secure choice. Moreover, with so many sword cultivators in the chaotic world, the earlier encounter at the Sword Qi Great Wall, where they were thwarted, provided a perfect opportunity to test their swords against Yuguizong. Breaking the ancestral hall of Yuguizong would serve as a fitting conclusion to this war on Tongye Continent.

The young swordsman, who had come to seek refuge in Xuanju Sect, was none other than Feiran, the late arrival to Tongye Continent and the junior brother of the great demon Qie Yun.

Thus, when Feiran saw the last piece of intelligence, he couldn’t help but laugh and cry at the same time. He had inexplicably found himself among the ranks of the ten young elites of the world, standing alongside the likes of Ning Yao, Cao Ci, and Shan Qing, which made Feiran feel quite uncomfortable. Especially the evaluation that labeled him as “adept at pressuring borders” filled him with resentment; he wished that the cultivators of other factions would remain oblivious to his existence for as long as possible.

Unsurprisingly, Shoucheng was already at the Yuzhi Peak, which was a rather tough nut to crack, being a major sect of Tongye Continent with a very resilient mountain protection formation. Shoucheng did not raise any alarms and deliberately redirected his military forces to attack other sects, secretly driving tens of thousands of displaced people towards Yuzhi Peak. In the ancestral hall of Yuzhi Peak, a compassionate female master, moved by pity, stood firm against the majority and ultimately chose to lift the restrictions of the mountain and water formations, allowing the refugees to take shelter at Yuzhi Peak.

Unlike Feiran’s leisurely exploration of the mountains, Shoucheng was heading straight for the ancestral hall of Yuzhi Peak.

Feiran looked up in the direction of Yuzhi Peak, where a beam of sword light shot up into the sky, alongside a familiar array of spell lights, showcasing the grand strokes of his senior brother Qie Yun.

From this moment on, Yuzhi Peak would become a tale of human affairs recorded in history, and after some time, it would simply be an old chapter forgotten.

A young boy rushed towards the Xiuzhu Rock Water Viewing Platform, awkwardly approaching Feiran and saying, “Brother Chen, everyone says the Xuanju Sect definitely won’t hold. What should we do? I feel bad for making you spend so much money. If we die, how can I repay you?”

The boy squatted down, grumbling, “I’m not worth that much money. That’s celestial money…”

The young man, now going by the name “Chen Yin,” smiled and said, “That celestial money is just like the coins in your pocket to me, so you don’t have to worry too much about it.”

Still concerned for “Brother Chen,” the boy whispered, “Celestials can’t just waste money like that…”

Feiran chuckled dismissively.

Not only had he changed his name, but he had also altered his appearance to resemble that of a young hidden official, purely out of boredom.

As for the boy, a simple woodsman from Tongye Continent, he had met Feiran during his travels. The boy had no family and had once rescued a mountain spirit on the verge of transforming into a human. To express gratitude, the spirit often brought hunted prey to the boy’s doorstep. Feiran had fortuitously witnessed this scene and decided to take the boy along to the Xuanju Sect’s Konghou Mountain, thousands of miles away.

Feiran brought the boy to observe the myriad of peculiar aquatic creatures.

As dusk approached, several beams of rainbow light suddenly broke through the mountain and water formations of the Xuanju Sect. Once glimpsing Feiran’s figure on the Xiuzhu Rock Water Viewing Platform, the lights changed course, bypassing the Thunderous Hall atop Konghou Mountain, landing instead beside Feiran, along with his senior brother Qie Yun and the swordsman candidate Yu Si.

Also present was a slender girl with a short knife at her waist, nicknamed Doukou. She was a naturally “unfocused” and fragile being, prone to attracting malevolent spirits, yet contrary to fate, she had cultivated a small world within herself, resembling a blessed land.

The girl’s eyes were vacant and hollow, but she still nodded at Feiran.

Qie Yun raised two fingers to twirl a strand of hair at his temple, squinting with a smile. “Junior brother, what’s the point of bringing along a little one with no aptitude for cultivation?”

Feiran smiled back, “I’m just bored.”

The girl turned her gaze toward the Thunderous Hall atop the mountain. Qie Yun said, “Little lady, I’m begging you, please don’t go on another rampage like you did at Yuzhi Peak. There are plenty of beautiful women around; can’t you just refrain from making a move?”

The girl rasped, “I’ll just take their heads and leave them for senior brother Qie Yun. As for the male cultivators, you don’t need to worry about them.”

Qie Yun clasped his hands together. “Alright, alright. Just remember to keep the women safe!”

The girl drew her short knife, lightly flicked her wrist, and the short knife suddenly transformed into a dazzlingly bright giant blade that resembled a horse-slaying sword. She soared into the air, heading toward the ancestral hall of the Xuanju Sect.

Yu Si turned to Feiran and said, “Senior brother Shoucheng is still at Yuzhi Peak cleaning up the aftermath. The next target is the Mirage City of the Great Spring Dynasty.”

Feiran nodded. “Do as you please.”

Qie Yun suddenly laughed. “Senior brother just received word that Mr. Zhou has already arrived at the gates of Dafu Academy. There’s a good show to watch now. Once I finish my makeup, I’ll rush over to cheer for Mr. Zhou. Junior brother, what do you say? Want to join me?”

Feiran shook his head. “I’ll pass.”

The woodsman boy wasn’t foolish. Although he couldn’t understand the conversations around him, he could guess their identities, leaving his mind in a whirl.

Feiran crouched down and smiled at the boy in the local dialect, “I’m sorry, but I’m from the demon clan. However, don’t be afraid; just continue treating me like your Brother Chen. Even if the sky falls and the earth cracks, it has nothing to do with you.”

Feiran loved to learn the local dialects of every place he visited, purely out of boredom.

The boy was sweating profusely and stammered, “Brother Chen, what’s going on?”

Feiran thought for a moment and replied, “It’s probably a group of bad guests arriving uninvited, breaking down the door and leaving the host without a meal.”

The boy’s gaze gradually hardened. “Brother Chen saved me. No matter who they are or if they’re demons, they’re my benefactors! I don’t care how others see Brother Chen!”

Feiran smiled and nodded, then suddenly slapped the boy, causing his spirit to flee in fright.

Qie Yun was somewhat surprised and blinked, asking, “Junior brother, you killed him? Such a sensible child.”

Feiran stood silently, offering no explanation.

If the boy had even the slightest hint of resentment, no matter how well-hidden, Feiran would have allowed him to live, even giving him a chance to ascend the mountain for cultivation.

Feiran looked up at the distance, asking, “Senior brother, what will happen to that female master from Yuzhi Peak who insisted on opening the door earlier?”

Qie Yun gently patted his cheek, smiling without speaking. “In the ancestral hall, she had the loudest voice during the discussions, yet when it came to fighting, she was the least active.”

Yu Si added, “Senior brother Shoucheng originally intended to spare her life, but upon witnessing her kneeling and begging in the ancestral hall, he found it bothersome and changed his mind.”

Feiran nodded. “I hope the old dragon city in Baoping Continent will do the same.”

In the palace of the Great Spring Dynasty, Mirage City.

A young empress with a furrowed brow, incredibly beautiful, sat there looking melancholic, her fingers playing with an exquisite copper incense stick, gently stirring the ashes within the stove to prolong the burning of the charcoal.

Next to her sat her contemporary sister, Yao Lingzhi, who was spirited and energetic. Seeing her sister’s downcast demeanor, she was unsure how to comfort her.

Their grandfather, the Minister of War Yao Zhen, had donned his armor once more and led the Yao family’s youths to the border.

Earlier today, a prince responsible for guarding the capital and temporarily presiding over state affairs visited, ostensibly to discuss military matters, but his eyes had never strayed from her sister’s face. Had it not been for Yao Lingzhi protecting her sister, even going so far as to press her hand against the hilt of her sword to signal to him not to overstep, who knew what that lecherous man would have done? In the current palace, there was truly no one her sister could trust.

When that prince took his leave, the smile he wore as he turned to cross the threshold sent chills down Yao Lingzhi’s spine.

Yao Jinzhi raised her head and forced a bitter smile. “I’m fine.”

Yao Lingzhi felt a surge of anger; if this was fine, then what would be considered a problem?

Right now, inside and outside the palace, the situation was a mess, from the court to the rivers and lakes, to the battlefield.

That bastard wearing the dragon robe had actually left her sister all alone. He had sneaked away, taking with him a large number of celestial-grade offerings, escaping to the fifth realm. 

What pained her sister the most was that the excuse the emperor gave for leaving her behind was absurd—someone from the Astronomical Observatory had predicted that her sister was a calamity in the making, and keeping her around would only bring disaster.

The young empress of the Great Spring Dynasty cradled the warming stove in her hands, her heart feeling hot yet cold.

She remembered that during her journey to Mirage City, she had secretly calculated her fortune.

It was fortunate for her, but the omen for the Great Spring Dynasty was not good, and she had been perplexed back then.

Now, looking back, it was clear that both good and bad fortunes existed. The good was that the Great Spring Dynasty’s fortune was indeed on the brink of collapse, while the bad was that her own fate seemed destined to follow suit.

If it weren’t for her grandfather still leading troops at the border and Yao Lingzhi acting as her personal bodyguard, Yao Jinzhi truly didn’t know how to cope. She dared not die, and when she glanced at the beams, she didn’t dare think of that white silk. Once, she had mustered the courage to take a long look at the well in the palace, and that had only frightened her further. After entering the palace, Yao Lingzhi had fallen and cried on the ground one day after a discussion, asking her little sister through tears if there was any painless way to die.

At that time, Yao Lingzhi had squatted beside her, holding her sister tightly, afraid to tell her that being in the hands of those demons would be worse than death.

At this moment, Yao Jinzhi suddenly said, “For the next few days, you must stay by my side, never leaving my side. Otherwise, I won’t be able to hold on. But when the demons begin to attack Mirage City, and it seems we can’t hold out any longer, you must kill me. Just remember to be quick when you strike.”

Yao Lingzhi’s face went pale, and she nodded gently.

The young empress suddenly smiled, gazing out at the heavy snowfall, and inexplicably thought of a person.

If only he were here, regardless of the outcome, she wouldn’t be so frightened.

Over these years, she had only occasionally thought of that man she couldn’t quite say she liked.

In the remote small country of Aihai in the Aihai Continent, there was a modest Leigong Temple, presided over by a young man named Pei Axiang.

Today, this handsome young master, after lighting three sticks of incense at the incense burner, stepped out of the temple to welcome guests.

Those aware of his identity were hesitant to disturb him, while those who dared were generally welcomed by Pei Axiang.

He wore a white robe with a jade belt, a green bamboo flute at his waist, adorned with a yellowing bead at its end.

The bamboo flute, crafted from rare materials, came from the Qing Shen Mountain, a celestial cave in the Bamboo Sea, while the bead was a commonplace item that most wealthy families wouldn’t even glance at.

Three guests arrived: Liu Youzhou, the direct descendant of the Liu family’s God of Wealth, Liu Mama, a family matron, and Liu Suoyu, Mama Liu’s daughter, who was one of Pei Axiang’s three direct disciples.

Liu Suoyu, dressed in a white fox fur coat and carrying a short black scabbard, had once achieved the rank of the strongest in the distant travel realm and was a frequent visitor to the northern ice plains. 

From a distance, Liu Youzhou shouted, “Axiang! Axiang!”

Pei Axiang smiled slightly, deciding not to hold a grudge against the little brat for spending too much money.

Mama Liu could only softly remind, “Young master, didn’t we agree beforehand that when we see Senior Pei, we shouldn’t call him ‘Axiang’?”

Liu Youzhou laughed heartily, “Can’t help it, can’t help it!”

Pei Axiang sat on the steps at the entrance.

Liu Youzhou plopped down beside him.

Seeing her master, Liu Suoyu smiled and said, “Master, you look particularly spirited today.”

Pei Axiang teased, “It’s hard not to be happy when a benefactor like you pays a visit.”

Mama Liu sighed in relief, glad that Master Pei was in a good mood around her young master.

Liu Youzhou pulled out an incense burner and presented it to Pei Axiang. 

Pei Axiang glanced at it, waved his hand, and sent the incense burner back into the Leigong Temple.

Liu Youzhou had just returned from the waters and caves of Fuyun Continent, traveling through the routes of Jinjia Continent, Liuxia Continent, and Aihai Continent. 

In the waters and caves of Fuyun Continent, Liu Youzhou had given away more than ten magical treasures to new acquaintances he had made not long ago, treating it as a loan.

He hoped they would return the favor.

It wasn’t that he was reluctant to part with those treasures, but he didn’t want those freshly acquainted faces to fade into memories.

Pei Axiang asked, “How is that Cao Ci doing? What level has he reached in the ten realms?”

Liu Youzhou shook his head. “I didn’t ask.”

Pei Axiang felt somewhat helpless.

Liu Suoyu, sitting beside them, lightly tapped her knees, saying, “Among the young elites, there’s a mountain peak cultivator named Yinguang, who is also a sword cultivator. Considering the previous surge in martial luck at the Sword Qi Great Wall, he’s most likely the young man Liu Youzhou is familiar with.”

Pei Axiang inquired with confusion, “What do you mean?”

He had truly not heard of this matter before.

Liu Youzhou pretended to tidy his collar.

Liu Suoyu immediately kicked him playfully.

At the Liu household in Aihai, a painting of Liu Youzhou’s hung in his study, poorly drawn like a child’s scribbles, depicting a flat boat on the sea with a boy carrying a sword standing at the bow. 

The so-called boy was merely a circle with several branches, a poor representation of a human.

Years ago, when Liu Suoyu had seen this “masterpiece,” she had asked about it, and Liu Youzhou had boasted that his water pattern painting technique had captured about seventy to eighty percent of Ma Yuan’s finesse in “Water Map.” 

Even as a youth, Liu Youzhou had feared that Aunt Liu wouldn’t believe him, so he had casually flipped through his desk until he finally pulled out a genuine copy of “Water Map,” hoping to have Aunt Liu authenticate it.

As a grandmaster martial artist, Liu Suoyu had no interest in the priceless painting, only asking about the boy.

Liu Youzhou had recounted the events at Guifei Island, where they had encountered a storm, and Liu Suoyu had remembered that odd boy who had climbed the upside-down mountain but didn’t visit the Yuanrou Mansion.

Now, after being playfully kicked by Aunt Liu, Liu Youzhou chuckled, “His name is Chen, and he’s from Baoping Continent—a generous person.”

Pei Axiang smiled, “The person you described as generous must be extraordinarily generous.”

Liu Youzhou responded, “If I casually give someone a grain of Gu Yu money, it’s like a stingy person giving a common person a grain of Gu Yu money; that’s how it should be calculated.”

Pei Axiang laughed. “The entire Yuanrou Mansion has been dismantled and sold; isn’t your father upset?”

Liu Youzhou shook his head. “My father only regrets that there’s only one Yuanrou Mansion on the upside-down mountain.”

Pei Axiang sighed, “Sometimes, I have to admit that you wealthy people truly deserve to be rich.”

Old Mama Liu quietly added, “The young master foresaw the future of Yuanrou Mansion long ago. The master is quite pleased with this, saying that just based on this insight, it’s worth a Yuanrou Mansion.”

Liu Youzhou sighed helplessly. “I didn’t think this was such a good thing; why is Aunt Liu saying this?”

Pei Axiang turned to Liu Suoyu. “You’re in the mountain peak realm, and Yinguang is also in the same realm. Do you think you can compete with him?”

Liu Suoyu replied, “I’ll give it a try.”

Between them, who reaches a breakthrough first could gain martial luck, thus determining a victor without needing to truly fight.

Pei Axiang looked off into the distance. “Are they all gathering together? Did you all agree on something?”

Liu Suoyu followed her master’s gaze. “It seems to be that sword immortal Xie Songhua. Besides the two newly accepted direct disciples, there’s also a young woman with him…”

Pei Axiang nodded. “Just a pure martial artist, younger than you. Thankfully, she doesn’t look like you; otherwise, it would be a cause for concern.”

Pei Axiang frowned, standing up and muttering to herself, “Is that the one from the distant travel realm? How could this be possible?!”

Liu Suoyu’s eyesight was slightly inferior, discovering the clues a bit later.

Xie Songhua was flying far away, taking care of his two disciples, but the young woman didn’t seem to need any help from him to ride the wind.

The group landed in the quiet square outside the Leigong Temple.

The female sword immortal addressed him straightforwardly. “Xie Songhua.”

Pei Axiang ignored her.

Only when Xie Songhua reached the realm of celestial beings could he intimidate people just by name.

Liu Suoyu suddenly stood up, her spirits high. Being a martial artist made her excited. The thought of sparring with a sword immortal thrilled her.

Xie Songhua glanced at the famed Liu Suoyu from Aihai Continent, smiling. “Before discussing serious matters, you all chat first.”

Pei Qian clasped his fists. “I’m Pei Qian, wishing to ask Senior Pei for guidance on martial arts.”

Pei Axiang found it amusing, waving his hand. “No time.”

Pei Qian scratched his head, put his hands down, and simply said, “Alright then.”

Since Senior Pei wasn’t willing to guide him, Pei Qian could only give up. 

In martial arts, seeking guidance was not a death wish.

Old Mama Liu couldn’t help but chuckle; this girl was quite interesting.

She glanced at her own young master.

The two sword candidates, Zhu Xing and Zhao Mu, exchanged glances, ready to assist Pei Qian by carrying the book box and bamboo staff.

Pei Axiang finally became interested. “Little girl, how many times have you reached the strongest rank in the distant travel realm?”

Pei Qian hesitated for a moment. “Only five times.”

Liu Youzhou’s jaw dropped. 

Only five times, and she had said “only”? How could there be such a girl in the world?

What was her name? Liu Youzhou wanted to know such a friend from the martial world! One could be picky about money but not about friends.

Liu Suoyu rubbed her forehead.

Pei Axiang’s expression turned serious.

Liu Suoyu curiously asked, “In which two realms did you encounter difficulties?”

Pei Qian shook her head, remaining silent.

Liu Suoyu smiled, “If you tell me, I’ll stay in the distant travel realm and promise to spar with you.”

Pei Qian thought for a moment. “Could you not stay in the distant travel realm?”

I’m asking you to spar, and you’re not even teaching me martial arts; why stay in the distant travel realm?

Liu Suoyu stepped down the stairs. “Alright, I won’t stay in the distant travel realm.”

Pei Qian nodded, handing her walking staff to Zhao Mu and then taking off her book box, which Zhu Xing immediately caught with both hands. 

Zhao Mu lightly waved his fist, lowering his voice to say, “Sister Pei, be careful.”

Pei Qian rubbed the little girl’s head, smiling, “Stay away from me later.”

Xie Songhua took his two disciples and soared into the sky.

Liu Youzhou squatted on the steps behind Pei Axiang, tilting his head to look at the girl. Quietly, he asked, “Axiang, if it comes to fighting between the eighth and ninth realms, how can she compete?”

Pei Axiang responded, “You should ask that girl.”

Liu Youzhou rolled his eyes. “I’ve met a beautiful girl and have always been too shy to speak.”

Old Mama Liu laughed heartily.

The girl was not particularly pretty.

Liu Suoyu tossed aside her fox fur coat and casually dropped it onto the steps behind her.

With one hand behind her back and the other outstretched, she smiled, “From the Leigong Temple in Aihai, I am martial artist Liu Suoyu.”

Pei Qian took a step forward, slightly sinking her posture, her fists clenched together, and solemnly said, “From the Fallen Mountain lineage, I am the mountain-opening disciple Pei Qian. I wish to spar with Senior Liu!”

#### The Abode of the Sword Immortals

At the Ancestral Hall of Zhengyang Mountain, aside from the two old masters heading to the old dragon city, the remaining elder sword immortals of the Tao family had gathered today for several matters that required their joint decisions.

In the sword-rich Northern Julu Continent, even an Infant Transformation sword cultivator, upon being addressed as a sword immortal, might feel somewhat uncomfortable; however, in Baoping Continent, this was not the case.

Every Golden Core sword cultivator was undeniably a sword immortal in their own right.

A woman of unremarkable appearance sat with her seat placed slightly behind, her wrist adorned with a red string, sitting upright, appearing a bit restrained.

She managed the mountain and water reports and the reflections of flowers and moons at Zhengyang Mountain, having always been a mere errand runner. Although she held a seniority, her lack of sword cultivation and frequent absences caused her to be far less respected than the elder sword immortals.

Especially in this Zhengyang Mountain Ancestral Hall, in the eyes of those elder sword immortals, she was merely a clever yet not particularly wise woman—essentially, an unremarkable woman.

Su Jia had once been a disciple she brought into the mountain but had later been transferred to another peak. In exchange, she received a magical treasure, while Su Jia was later accepted as a direct disciple of the ancestral hall. This trade proved to be unfavorable for her.

Otherwise, while the lower realms enjoyed favor through maternal connections, the upper realms also had many idlers who lived off their disciples, creating a similar situation.

Of course, in the end, Su Jia’s fate didn’t turn out well.

At the Temple of Wind and Snow, she lost to the current owner of the Wind and Thunder Garden, Huang He, her sword heart shattered, unable to retain even her identity as a sword cultivator.

However, the Zhengyang Mountain Ancestral Hall merely reclaimed her purple gold sword nurturing gourd, not expelling her from their records, simply revoking her status as a direct disciple.

The first matter was to discuss several candidates for direct disciples, selecting an auspicious date to formally record their names in the hall’s records.

Zhengyang Mountain was a designated candidate sect of the Great Li, so they were now preparing for the selection of a sub-sect, which would certainly be located within the old Zhu Ying Dynasty.

Over the years, Zhengyang Mountain had absorbed a considerable number of young sword cultivators from the old Zhu Ying Dynasty. Additionally, there was a rather impressive sword immortal candidate, who the Longquan Sword Sect had foolishly neglected. After several years of cultivation at the Shenshou Mountain, even Ruan Qiong was unwilling to accept him as a direct disciple. After arriving at Zhengyang Mountain, he experienced rapid breakthroughs and now hoped to become a partner to the celestial maiden Tong Zhen of Hanlu Peak.

This first matter was relatively trivial, with no significant disputes arising.

The second matter was to discuss the descent of the second batch of disciples from Zhengyang Mountain. The previous group had already been sent to the old dragon city under the guidance of two elder masters.

Zhengyang Mountain had maintained a good relationship with the vassal king Song Mu, thanks to Tao Zi’s travels in Liuzhu Cave, which had forged a significant bond with the youthful Song Jixin.

However, for this second batch, who would be responsible for guiding them and which disciples to send were crucial matters. If the weight was insufficient, it could easily irritate the Great Li Song family. But if it was too heavy, Zhengyang Mountain could easily suffer considerable losses.

Thus, it required careful consideration.

The Tao family elder evidently had a plan prepared, offering a set of procedures with little dissent.

Next, they discussed the Night Banquet of the Mountain Lord of Zhongyue, which was also a minor matter. The only concern was to gauge the Mountain Lord’s stance to prevent any unnecessary complications in the selection of the sub-sect. After all, the Mountain Lord’s affection for the old Zhu Ying Dynasty was well-known.

The fourth matter was a delightful opportunity.

They discussed a potential marriage alliance with the Xu family of Qingfeng City.

Zhengyang Mountain had a talented disciple in Tao Zi, while Xu’s family in Qingfeng City had the son of the city lord. The two had traveled together in Liuzhu Cave and maintained a good relationship over the years. Their elders believed this was a match made in heaven.

Earlier, when Qingfeng City’s Xu family had experienced a series of unfortunate marriages, they had even married their legitimate daughter to a commoner son to mend the rift between Qingfeng City and the Great Li Dynasty.

The woman with the red string on her wrist gently asked, “Does Tao girl agree to this?”

The Tao family elder’s brow knitted slightly, as some words were difficult to speak.

Tao girl was indeed reluctant, and the elder also hoped for some hints from the old dragon city’s residence to Zhengyang Mountain.

Yet the young prince, whether feigning ignorance or genuinely treating Tao Zi as a sister, seemed unaware.

The Tao family elder gave the woman a glance, and she understood, saying, “Since this matter is not urgent, why not let Tao girl go to the old dragon city to see her senior brothers and sisters?”

The mountain lord merely stroked his beard in silence, seemingly hearing a voice inside, before nodding. “That’s fine.”

After the mountain lord made this decision, his expression turned solemn as he added, “Regarding the sword duel with the Wind and Thunder Garden, today we must provide a clear statement!”

On the surface, Zhengyang Mountain had only two Infant Transformation sword cultivators: one was the mountain lord of Zhengyang Mountain, while the other was the Tao family elder.

There was also the oldest elder who had been in closed-door cultivation for years and was about to emerge. 

Additionally, there were three Golden Core sword cultivator ancestors.

Zhengyang Mountain had always lacked a sword immortal at the upper five realms.

This was why they had been overshadowed by the Wind and Thunder Garden’s Li Tuanjing for hundreds of years.

Now that Li Tuanjing was dead, arranging a duel with the newly appointed garden master Huang He had become a pressing matter. Huang He’s aptitude was simply too exceptional; Zhengyang Mountain could not afford to be careless and risk nurturing a tiger.

Huang He’s brilliance was glaringly evident; he had already reached the Infant Transformation realm, likely to become the second Li Tuanjing. Thus, this matter could not be delayed any longer.

Zhengyang Mountain needed to find a suitable candidate to challenge Huang He.

However, whether it was the mountain lord of the same realm or the elder who was about to emerge as an Infant Transformation sword cultivator, neither was appropriate; the latter was even a whole realm higher.

The issue was that among the direct disciples of Zhengyang Mountain, there was truly no one capable of sparring with Huang He. It was possible that even Liu Baqiao’s sword would suffice to make the Zhengyang sword cultivators drink from the same cup.

As for the vassals and guest elders, there was a suitable candidate in the old Zhu Ying dynasty, a talented sword cultivator, once hailed as one of the two pillars, who had gained considerable sword fortune from the Zhu Ying dynasty. However, sending him to duel Huang He would still seem improper.

Unless that person was willing to become a direct disciple of Zhengyang Mountain.

Even if that person were foolish enough to agree to this, it could create a rift between Zhengyang Mountain and the Wind and Thunder Garden.

Thus, selecting someone for the duel had become a shared concern for all the elder sword cultivators of Zhengyang Mountain.

In the end, they still could not reach a foolproof plan today.

The Tao family elder angrily remarked, “If it comes to that, I’ll just swallow my pride and challenge a junior!”

The mountain lord shook his head. “That’s not suitable. We need to win with convincing authority.”

This Tao family elder had more hope of advancing to the upper five realms than himself. If he were to challenge the Wind and Thunder Garden and win, that would be fine, but if he were to lose or suffer an unexpected incident, dying under Huang He’s sword would mean the end of the mountain lord’s career.

Of course, the mountain lord was well aware that the Tao family elder was merely putting on a show, as he understood the mountain lord’s position.

Moreover, his words were filled with wisdom; since the Tao family elder challenging a junior was seen as losing face and bullying the weak, the mountain lord would be equally inappropriate in challenging with the same reasoning.

The woman, seeing the atmosphere in the hall grow heavy, said, “Perhaps there’s a way to make that guest elder become a direct disciple of the ancestral hall.”

She was looking at an elder across from her, who leaned forward slightly, intrigued, and asked, “What do you mean? If he becomes our direct disciple, he can challenge Huang He and win?”

The woman shook her head. “It’s unlikely. Although Yuan Bai is also an Infant Transformation sword cultivator, he is still inferior to Huang He. Yuan Bai’s only reliance is his innate magical skill that excels in trading injuries for injuries with his flying sword.”

The elder tugged at the corner of his mouth. Was this woman looking for trouble?

The woman immediately added softly, “But there’s a chance to establish Huang He’s position as the second Li Tuanjing, such as his identity and… realm! However, if this were to happen, Zhengyang Mountain might lose this highly anticipated duel.”

As soon as this was said, half of the sword cultivators in the ancestral hall remained indifferent, as this group of elders had never cared for Zhengyang Mountain’s affairs, focusing solely on sword cultivation.

However, the other half, often holding important positions, began to exchange thoughts rapidly.

The elder across from her coldly smiled, “That Yuan Bai isn’t foolish. Once he becomes our direct disciple, he’ll have to duel Huang He, and perhaps he’ll be dead tomorrow, leaving no future.”

The woman hesitated, wanting to speak but holding back.

The mountain lord frowned. “Speak your mind.”

Finally, the woman cautiously said, “The reason Yuan Bai is willing to become our guest elder is that he hopes to protect the old Zhu Ying-born sword cultivators. If we Zhengyang Mountain agree to grant him a direct disciple title every fifty years, ensuring that this disciple will certainly advance to the upper five realms, then let’s say the contract is void after five hundred years. This way, Yuan Bai will find it hard to refuse, and he might even be grateful to us.”

The elder across from her nodded, smiling. “Not only can we openly challenge Huang He from the Wind and Thunder Garden, but we can also protect the descendants of the old country. Yuan Bai should indeed be grateful to us, thanking us for giving him a chance to die with dignity and grandeur.”

An elder suddenly stood up, quietly leaving the ancestral hall.

Soon after, several elders followed suit, also taking their leave.

The mountain lord was not surprised and the Tao family elder was too lazy to glance back. This group of stubborn old folks, didn’t they enjoy practicing their swords? Why not use their skills instead? If only they could cultivate their swordsmanship for hundreds of years and still not have a chance to unsheathe their swords. 

Could Zhengyang Mountain really become the leading sect in Baoping Continent relying on these useless old folks?

The woman felt anxious.

Perhaps she would end up regretting her words.

The mountain lord gazed at her, an unusual smile gracing his features. “Let’s settle this. You go persuade Yuan Bai to become a direct disciple of the ancestral hall. Once that’s accomplished, we’ll immediately announce that Yuan Bai will challenge Huang He of the Wind and Thunder Garden.”

The woman nodded gently.

The mountain lord felt in good spirits, and his gaze turned favorably toward the woman.

Within Zhengyang Mountain, only he knew a secret: the purple gold sword nurturing gourd that Su Jia had been bestowed by the ancestral hall was something this woman had discovered. She was astute enough to have exchanged it for a seat in the ancestral hall. This secret was revealed to him by his late mentor, so he kept it in his heart, ensuring that it wouldn’t be leaked.

The mountain lord said, “The last matter to discuss is about Liu Xianyang.”

Upon mentioning this, the mountain lord glanced at the Tao family elder, harboring some resentment. Years ago, Tao girl had traveled to Liuzhu Cave with the mountain guardian, yet unexpectedly, they hadn’t managed to recover that sword scripture, nor had they resolved the matter. Even a country boy from a rural area hadn’t been dealt with properly, leaving behind such a significant hidden danger. 

Although at that time Li Tuanjing was still alive, and that Liu Xianyang’s innate porcelain had reportedly been handed down to the Wind and Thunder Garden, the mountain monkey had some reservations, considering Zhengyang Mountain’s interests.

Now thinking back, it made the mountain lord feel a headache; nothing churned his stomach more than the thought of “if only I had known!”

The Tao family elder turned to her, raising his chin, and nodded toward the woman before addressing the mountain lord. “According to her intelligence, Liu Xianyang is now a direct disciple of the Longquan Sword Sect.
