Due to the Liu family’s ancestors being the tomb guardians for the Chen family’s ancestral graves, they later studied with the Confucian Chen family in Nanpuzhou for ten years. What realm has Liu Xianyang reached now? Has there been any contact with the Wind and Thunder Garden?”

The woman stood up, pulling a piece of paper from her sleeve. The Tao family elder reached out to grab it, beginning to examine it.

The mountain lord remained indifferent, treating it as unimportant. 

The Tao family elder frowned. “These are all trivial matters? Since he could become Ruan Qiong’s disciple, what realm is he in? Is he a sword cultivator? What’s his innate magical skill? During his studies with the Confucian Chen family in Nanpuzhou, did he cultivate any connections? Do we not know anything?!”

The Tao family elder pushed the paper over to the mountain lord.

After he read it, the mountain lord said, “From the information, this Liu Xianyang was a loose-lipped show-off in his youth. When he returned home, did he not mention his studies?”

The woman shook her head. “His temperament has changed significantly. Although he enjoys wandering every day, when speaking with neighbors, he only recounts stories of his hometown and never mentions the Confucian Chen family. In fact, in the entire Huaihuang County, apart from a few people like Cao Duzhao, hardly anyone knows he has become a disciple of the Longquan Sword Sect. And at Shenshou Mountain, the Longquan Sword Sect has too few members; Ruan Qiong’s direct disciples are especially few and hard to gather information from, lest we offend Ruan Qiong. Ruan Qiong is a character who, although he’s the chief guardian of the Great Li, has a good relationship with the Wind and Thunder Temple. We should avoid provoking them prematurely.”

The Tao family elder laughed, “You’ve said a few insightful things.”

The mountain lord sighed. “If only there were a Wei Jin, Zhengyang Mountain wouldn’t have to worry about its future. I would even be willing to give Wei Jin the position of mountain lord.”

Wei Jin had challenged the Tianjun Xie Shi of North Julu Continent twice.

He was undoubtedly the first sword immortal in Baoping Continent.

The woman feigned ignorance.

The mountain lord asked, “Is Liu Xianyang’s innate porcelain still in the hands of the Wind and Thunder Garden?”

The woman nodded. “It should be correct.”

The mountain lord rubbed his temples, feeling a headache coming on. “Since it has come to this, it’s a fatal grudge, especially for these young folks who can’t suffer even the slightest grievance. If he were to challenge us as a direct disciple of the Longquan Sword Sect, how would Zhengyang Mountain deal with him? Should we kill him or let him live? No matter how we look at it, it’s a hassle. If he were to connect with the Wind and Thunder Garden, they could team up to target Zhengyang Mountain. Even if the issue isn’t significant, it’s still undesirable.”

The woman tentatively said, “I have an idea; do listen.”

The mountain lord smiled, “Speak. If it can resolve a potential problem, Zhengyang Mountain is always fair in rewards and punishments.”

When the mountain lord mentioned this, he glanced at an empty seat that was slightly ahead of where the woman was seated.

The woman understood and immediately smiled, but suddenly hesitated.

The mountain lord was more understanding and said, “Today’s discussion hasn’t brought forth any major issues. You all can go back to practice swordsmanship.”

Some elder sword cultivators stood up and left, leaving the ancestral hall half-empty.

Only then did the woman say, “A female cultivator from our Qionghu Peak, while traveling through the Fox Nation, developed feelings for a disciple of the Lu family from Qingfeng City who originates from Liuzhu Cave. Why don’t we take advantage of this opportunity and let them become a couple, uniting as a pair of celestial partners in the mountains? Then, we can negotiate with the Xu family of Qingfeng City, allowing that man to join Zhengyang Mountain. This person is originally from the Great Li’s Huaihuang County, born into the Lu family on Fulou Street, and bears a grudge against Liu Xianyang. Not only that, but he nearly killed Liu Xianyang in a narrow alley. During Tao girl’s visit to Liuzhu Cave, he was also chosen by the woman of the Xu family, who helped lead the way.”

The mountain lord nodded, having understood the gist, feeling a sense of unexpected delight. Could it be that this woman, who had always adhered to the rules and disliked being in the spotlight, could actually be of great use to Zhengyang Mountain?

The woman continued, “If we hold a grand wedding, we can release rumors to Huaihuang County. Liu Xianyang is sure to hear about it. It’s better to resolve a grudge than to let it fester. Even if Liu Xianyang makes a scene at the wedding and kills that Lu family disciple, it’s better than letting him harbor resentment in his heart. After a ruckus, it could actually be a good thing, and afterward, he would have no excuse to entangle with us Zhengyang Mountain.”

The elder across from her chuckled, “Such a woman’s benevolence.”

The woman did not refute him.

That elder said, “As long as Liu Xianyang dares to act at the wedding, I can ensure that the Lu family disciple dies just right. Moreover, we can let the bride-to-be from Qionghu Peak commit suicide afterward. Whether she truly dies or not is unimportant; it’s all up to us to decide. At worst, we can let her follow the path of Su Jia and live incognito. Zhengyang Mountain wouldn’t mistreat her. I don’t believe that a ruckus of this magnitude won’t make Ruan Qiong lose face while protecting Liu Xianyang.”

The woman softly replied, “Elder Yan is remarkably perceptive.”

That elder leaned back in his chair, “Good talk.”

The mountain lord said, “We still need to think of a reason that compels Liu Xianyang to come.”

The Tao family elder chuckled, “Simple. Let the city lord of Qingfeng City attend the wedding as well. He’s still wearing that scarlet armor that belonged to Liu Xianyang’s ancestors. I believe Qingfeng City would prefer Liu Xianyang to perish sooner rather than later.”

The woman let out a breath, seeming somewhat fatigued after discussing so much.

At Zhengyang Mountain, on a snow-capped peak, a pair of master and servant were admiring the scenery in a celestial residence built on the cliff.

The man was Yuan Bai, a sword cultivator from the old Zhu Ying Dynasty. The maid beside him, Liusai, appeared emotionless, a dull presence, and not particularly pleasing to the eye.

Yuan Bai felt somewhat melancholic, not anticipating that a mere journey to Aihai Continent would result in losing both his home and country.

The maid’s hometown wasn’t precisely part of the Haoran world, but rather a renowned celestial blessed land in Aihai Continent.

The blessed land was the private property of the Liu family in Aihai. Initially discovered as a lowly blessed land with scant spiritual energy, it had been transformed into a high-quality blessed land through sheer expenditure of celestial money.

Every year, there would be a grand event known as “Heavenly Maiden Scattering Flowers,” where young women from the Liu family would don colorful robes and scatter snowflake money.

It wasn’t that the Liu family lacked wealth; rather, the blessed land was restricted by an invisible overarching principle, preventing it from being elevated beyond its current status.

Even the cloud cave blessed land controlled by the Jiang family of Yuguizong couldn’t compare.

Despite the inability to upgrade the blessed land, the Aihai Liu family’s God of Wealth wasn’t deterred by this. It was said that Liu Youzhou, in his youth, had jokingly mentioned creating a small cave during his time, which later became his cultivation ground.

Thus, the God of Wealth of Aihai felt that this idea could indeed work.

Afterward, the Liu family’s extravagant spending became a bottomless pit, filling it with snowflake money.

Hence, there was a humorous saying circulating in the Haoran world that whoever married Liu Youzhou would be the richest housekeeper in the world.

The man turned to the maid, softly saying, “Don’t worry; I will help you find the former owner of the blessed land.”

The maid nodded.

A woman who had just descended from the ancestral hall appeared in the corridor.

Yuan Bai and she exchanged greetings.

The woman, wearing a troubled expression, conveyed the proposal that had been discussed in the Zhengyang Mountain Ancestral Hall.

After hearing it, Yuan Bai didn’t hesitate. “I agree.”

The woman let out a gentle sigh.

Having been confined to Zhengyang Mountain, Yuan Bai smiled, saying, “Senior, there’s no need for such formality.”

After the woman departed, Yuan Bai expressed his guilt, saying to the maid, “Liusai, I will strive to obtain a direct disciple identity from Zhengyang Mountain for you, serving as a protective charm on your path of cultivation. However, I’m afraid I will have to break my promise regarding finding your master.”

The maid nodded. “It’s alright.”

The woman slowly returned to her mountain peak. Zhengyang Mountain had strict regulations; each cultivator’s sword riding and wind traversing paths were predetermined and had their own hierarchies.

Arriving at a rather humble cultivation area, the woman chuckled softly, recalling the old enmity between Zhengyang Mountain and the Wind and Thunder Garden—notably a muddy child fighting in the water, a crab flipping in the pot.

Currently, her only interest lay in the long-absent senior brother, who had taken the unprecedented step of reaching out to her, asking for help in watching over Liusai, who had emerged from the blessed land of Aihai, ensuring her safety without further complications.

However, she dared not act hastily nor touch the girl; otherwise, in her usual style, Liusai might find some fate intertwined with Yuan Bai, eventually leading to some unexpected entanglement.

The calculations of her senior brother were indeed unfathomable. Otherwise, it wouldn’t have been possible for him to press the entire Yuzhou Yin Yang family into submission.

She could only manipulate and control the flow of sword fortune in the continent, honing her own path through the grand schemes of the continent.

Yet her senior brother was far beyond this.

In his eyes, it seemed he always kept an eye on the entire world.

She murmured, “Senior brother, what does it mean to consume one to eliminate another?”

At the blacksmith shop by Longxu River, Liu Xianyang sat on a bamboo chair, basking in the sun and dozing off.

Previously, he had received two water reports from Shenshou Mountain that put him in a good mood.

The first report mentioned the young elites of various realms, while the latest provided a list of the candidates.

Liu Xianyang admired not only the behind-the-scenes reviewers of these reports but also the ones who could quickly provide more detailed inside information.

Were these celestial beings wandering around all day, simply enjoying the gossip?

Liu Xianyang instantly snapped out of his daze, lifting his head with a grin. “Brother Yumi!”

It was the sword immortal Mi Yu, whom the Mountain Lord of Wei had tossed in his direction.

Mi Yu carried a bamboo chair, sitting beside Liu Xianyang, then handed him a handful of sunflower seeds.

As they cracked the seeds together, Mi Yu smiled, “I just heard from Piyun Mountain that the young man from the Lu family on Fulou Street is going to marry a celestial maiden from Qionghu Peak.”

Liu Xianyang chuckled, “Then the city lord of Qingfeng City will certainly show up at the wedding.”

Mi Yu was stunned for a moment. “Aren’t you planning to crash the party? I’ve already made plans to accompany you to Zhengyang Mountain.”

Liu Xianyang spat out the husk of a sunflower seed, grinning. “My little Ping’an must have informed you early on, asking you to keep an eye on me and not let me act recklessly?”

Mi Yu shook his head. “Not at all.”

Liu Xianyang became furious. “That guy is so heartless! He didn’t even let Brother Yumi protect me?! Damn it, once he has a wife, he forgets his brothers. He probably forgot the taste of a monkey stealing peaches.”

Mi Yu felt a headache coming on.

Liu Xianyang’s thought processes were quite unconventional.

It was no surprise that he was the brother of the hidden official.

Liu Xianyang continued cracking seeds, bending over to gaze into the distance. “If it weren’t for that water report, I would’ve truly gone to Zhengyang Mountain by now. But since little Ping’an is still alive, let’s wait until he comes back. If he’s ungrateful, I’ll be the one to be grateful.”

Mi Yu chuckled. “There’s a candidate named Ma Kuxuan from Xinghua Alley among the ten candidates.”

Liu Xianyang nodded. “Poor Banchai, having to spend every day with that foolish Ma—he must be sick of it.”

Mi Yu asked, “Banchai? Who?”

Liu Xianyang explained, “That Song Jixin from Niping Alley, now the vassal king Song Mu.”

Mi Yu didn’t delve deeper. He wasn’t particularly interested in matters related to the hidden official.

Liu Xianyang finished cracking the seeds, wrapping his arms around his head, and sighed, “Liu Daye is truly unremarkable. Not to mention I haven’t made it onto either list; even the young ten chosen from Baoping Continent before didn’t include me. There’s no reason I should be worse than little Ping’an.”

Mi Yu dismissed his complaints. 

Otherwise, in his own broken mountain, in the small county of Huaihuang, it would easily confuse outsiders, making it difficult for them to comprehend.

Mi Yu was more interested in those two lists.

The newly minted candidates did not have a ranking. 

Aside from the true martial mountain’s Ma Kuxuan, there was also the first disciple of the great demon Liu Cha from the chaotic world, Zhu Ke.

A certain female crown of the sword lineage from the Daqing Continent at Qingming Heavenly Capital.

A monk from the Shouxin Temple.

A talisman practitioner from the fifth realm, who had traveled through the Shuzhong region, the only son of the master of the Tianyu Cave, born during the Mid-Autumn Festival. 

When he was born, several white lotuses bloomed at Taiye Pool, and a celestial maiden appeared, offering him a white jade spirit flower and blessing him by touching his forehead. 

Moreover, he was gifted a talking flower that blossomed six petals, each with a character, creating an everlasting phrase. The seventh petal, which would likely be inscribed with the character “new,” was soon to bloom.

In the Bamboo Sea Cave, the girl was pure and blue, the only disciple of the Lady of Qing Shen Mountain. 

She excelled in alchemy, talismans, swordsmanship, and martial arts, mastering them all.

She was also the only one among the young ten and candidate ten whose age was noted down to the day of birth.

She was merely fourteen years old.

In the Daqing world, the unacknowledged descendant of the Baiyu family was a rogue named Wang Yuanlu.

A young man named Xu Bai from the central continent was born into a small vassal state. 

There was a market wishing bridge in the city, where the keeper’s surname was Xu. He had a son with outstanding talent, resembling a celestial being, thus nicknamed Xu Xian.

It was said that Xu Bai, in his youth, had been helped by celestial beings behind him to light his lamp while studying.

Later, while sleeping on the bridge, he dreamt of an old man with a cane wandering over, appearing to be a person of the Dao.

The boy, half-asleep, suddenly lit his lamp, and in that moment, he was surrounded by starry skies while fish swam in the heavens.

Another young man from Liuxia Continent, who was known as a dream wanderer, had a strange tale.

In the Daqing world, there was a pure martial artist nearing fifty, stuck at the peak of the mountain realm.

Besides that, there was an eleventh candidate, as the earlier hidden official had been deemed the “eleventh,” giving him the nickname “Twenty-Two.”

This person had not lived a long life; his life was practically a legendary tale filled with the most bizarre and fantastical experiences. Initially of decent talent, he only became an unnamed external disciple of a sect, suffering through many hardships, including love troubles. 

Afterward, during a journey down the mountain, he tragically perished while saving others, ultimately transforming into a half-dead ghost.

When he regained consciousness, he held the power of a celestial cave.

At a young age, he became a sect leader.

He reorganized the sect, even with a multitude of ancestors from the past, yet managed to garner respect.

It was rumored that he had crossed paths with the Confucian sub-saint who traveled through the Daqing world, as well as the three heads of the Baiyu family in his own realm, and the number one alchemist.

His celestial partner was even more astonishing.

She was the founder of another sect, having attained ascendance.

The two were starkly different in age, cultivation, and status.

The key was that the two sects had been arch-enemies for thousands of years.

Thus, when they became partners, nearly half of the cultivators in the Daqing world were left dumbfounded.

Liu Xianyang swung his small bamboo chair, murmuring, “That dream wanderer from Liuxia Continent has quite a bit of intrigue.”

At present, many cultivators from Baoping Continent not only felt proud but also lamented. Wei Jin, the sword immortal from the Wind and Snow Temple, had just passed fifty, and the vassal king Song Changjing was in a similar situation. 

Otherwise, with both Song Changjing and Wei Jin simultaneously among the young elites, holding their respective places, and with Ma Kuxuan closely following behind to secure a spot among the candidates, the minor Baoping Continent would monopolize three positions among the young ten!

Liu Xianyang suddenly turned to look at Mi Yu, saying seriously, “Brother Yumi, with your outstanding looks, if there’s ever a chance for a blooming flower for the fallen mountain, you’ll definitely make a fortune. When that time comes, don’t forget to bring me along; I’ll be your foil!”

Mi Yu widened his eyes in shock, suddenly realizing the sincerity behind the hidden official’s gaze.

Thus, Mi Yu straightened up, feeling it was only proper to involve the Mountain Lord of Wei, “We’ll share both the blessings and the misfortunes!”

Liu Xianyang immediately said, “Bring me more sunflower seeds to celebrate!”

Mi Yu took out a handful of seeds gifted by a little girl and divided them with Liu Xianyang.

In the bustling Qingfeng City, where diverse backgrounds mingled, everyone was clamoring for wealth.

With the Xu family possessing connections to the Fox Nation, Qingfeng City was known throughout Baoping Continent as a gentle haven for heroes.

A young man running a spice shop hadn’t yet reached his thirties and presented himself like a fallen nobleman.

Having settled here a few years prior, among the celestial beings populating Qingfeng City, this shopkeeper remained inconspicuous.

Those who frequented the spice shop were mainly women, either affluent housewives or beauty-obsessed young ladies.

Although the young shopkeeper appeared to be in his early thirties, his eyes seemed to possess the wisdom of someone far beyond that age.

Such a man, selling spices, even if he wasn’t overly attentive to his guests, his courtesy would suffice, and his business would not suffer.

The young shopkeeper enjoyed visiting bookshops, leading to a friendship with a well-off book merchant.

That merchant, with a considerable background, was the largest bookseller in Qingfeng City. However, in Qingfeng City, he wasn’t considered a grand lineage; compared to those affluent families frequented by celestial beings, he didn’t stand out.

Today, the shopkeeper was dragged by the merchant to his home for drinks. After getting tipsy, the merchant began calling the shopkeeper “brother,” lamenting how difficult it was to establish themselves in Qingfeng City and how challenging it was to marry a beautiful daughter, which had proven so complicated that even the future in-laws looked down on him, claiming that his business was nothing more than a small country’s wealth.

In reality, his once-sorrowful daughter had long since stopped crying every day. Just like today, she would occasionally check with her father if there were enough food and drink.

The young shopkeeper suggested a rather peculiar way of making money, twirling his cup and slowly saying, “Brother Yuan, I can’t guarantee you’ll earn big money, but I can ensure your descendants will have a steady income for three generations.”

The merchant was taken aback and asked quietly, “I’m all ears, brother.”

The young shopkeeper smiled, “I believe I’m reasonably skilled in writing, painting, and seal carving, but not so exceptional that I could become a master. However, it’s not difficult to make a living from this. I just lack the capital, and Brother Yuan happens to have it, so it’s perfect for me to show off my skills. Since you are the largest bookseller in Qingfeng City, printing books will be quite easy. I’ll be responsible for compiling a printed book for you every year, using a hundred seals. Most will be genuine, with only a few fakes. This way, you can secure solid profits.”

The merchant hesitated, “Fake? How do we sell that? It’s not that I don’t trust your seal carving, but people with money are usually discerning and hard to fool.”

The young shopkeeper took a sip of wine, smiling, “I’ve read numerous historical records and local chronicles. For instance, if I help Brother Yuan carve a seal mimicking a famous seal carver, I’ll intentionally change one character in the inscription, creating a seemingly flawed yet not entirely incorrect detail. In reality, it’ll conform to the clan record. Therefore, this deal won’t earn you any commoner’s money; it will attract those scholars who read extensively and broadly. With a little verification, they would mistakenly think they’ve stumbled onto a great fortune. Similar methods abound.”

The merchant felt slightly tempted. “Can it really work?”

The young shopkeeper glanced at the woman behind the screen. “Let’s agree on this: if I cause you to lose money on the printed books, I’ll drink punishment wine, apologize to you, and compensate you. I truly have no money. If we make a profit in the future, just remember to treat me to a cup of celestial wine.”

After some detailed calculations, the merchant felt that this could likely work. Finally, he swayed back into his seat and asked his daughter to see the young shopkeeper off.

After the daughter returned, the merchant sat at the table, asking, “Are you sure this is the accent from the old Zhu Ying Dynasty?”

The girl nodded. “Unfortunately, he isn’t a sword cultivator; he’s just a sixth realm martial artist, but he’s quite talented. As long as we can confirm he’s from the Zhu Ying descendants, we can attract him.”

The merchant frowned. “He doesn’t seem like a greedy person and speaks elegantly, quite extraordinary.”

The girl joked, “Brother Yuan considers him a true brother, but unfortunately, he thinks of you as his future father-in-law.”

The merchant couldn’t help but laugh, shaking his head. “You little vixen, you’re not likely to win his heart. If you think you can make him wholeheartedly serve the Xu family, you’re dreaming.”

The girl hesitated and said, “It could be arranged for my grandfather to personally intervene.”

“Are you joking?!” 

The merchant began weighing the pros and cons. “There’s no need to go to such lengths unless…”

The girl nodded. “Unless he can reach the Golden Body realm. It would be best if he can become a grandmaster in the distant travel realm. Our Qingfeng City lacks martial luck, not literary luck!”

The merchant said, “No rush; we’ll observe for a while. Whether your grandfather appears or not isn’t something we can decide; we need to consult the matriarch.”

The drunken young shopkeeper returned to his shop, feeling dejected. He murmured, “By the Zhuque Bridge, at the Wu Yi Alley, in front of the Wang family hall, in the homes of ordinary people. Yesterday, what day was it? What day is it today? What day will it be tomorrow? As the snow falls, I bid you farewell, and as the flowers fall, I will meet you again. Without drinking, wishes come true. When drunk, dreams become reality…”

Suddenly, a passerby bumped into the young shopkeeper’s shoulder and stumbled, saying “Sorry,” before continuing on his way.

This person returned to the merchant’s home, recounted every word the young shopkeeper had said, and then remarked, “The foundation of a sixth realm martial artist is quite good. It makes me wonder if he has already reached the seventh realm.”

The merchant and the girl exchanged glances.

The temporary martial artist who had been assigned here was indeed a true sixth realm martial artist.

As for whether the young shopkeeper would grow suspicious because of this, it was no longer important. He would soon be a fellow in Qingfeng City.

Approaching the spice shop, on a somewhat secluded street reminiscent of Qilong Alley, the young shopkeeper slowly descended the steps, noticing a little girl in a cotton coat being chased by a large white goose—she was dirty and dark, laughing and running, but when pecked, she cried while continuing to flee.

The young shopkeeper paused, watching the scene, his eyes narrowing in a gentle smile.

A woman was just at the foot of the alley, slowly walking up the steps. As she saw the scene, her heart felt heavy.

The young shopkeeper brushed past the woman.

A gentle breeze brushed against the young man’s temple as he swayed slightly. The fragrance from the pouch at his waist mingled with the lingering scent of wine.

When the young man’s gaze wasn't on her, it only made him more noticeable to the woman.

Returning to the temporarily closed shop, it was still early, and some women were already waiting, complaining. When they saw the young shopkeeper, their faces immediately bloomed with smiles.

Business was still good today.

The shop had not yet closed, but there were finally no customers for the moment. The young shopkeeper placed a small stool at the entrance, noticing a pair of childhood sweethearts walking hand-in-hand down the street.

Moments later, the boy returned, squatting down next to the young shopkeeper, saying awkwardly, “Shopkeeper, I didn’t dare to give her that pouch.”

Then the boy raised his head, encouraging himself, “Tomorrow, I will definitely give it to her!”

The young shopkeeper smiled, “No worries; you’ve already given her a gift, and she accepted it. It’s better than the pouch.”

The boy was puzzled. “But I didn’t give her anything.”

The young shopkeeper laughed, “You did. It was a box of rouge.”

The boy was confused. “What?”

The young shopkeeper looked up at the clouds and said softly, “When you look at her earnestly, she’ll blush.”

The boy thought for a moment, seeming to comprehend partially.

He picked up the small stool and closed the shop.

Returning to the courtyard, when a subtle ripple of energy gradually dispersed, the young shopkeeper still lay on a rattan chair, gently waving a folding fan, enjoying the cool breeze.

Over the years in Qingfeng City, this outsider businessman had always been so leisurely.

The folding fan had long been regarded as a symbol of coolness and a way to shield one’s face.

After some time, a woman accompanied by two maids came to purchase spices, her discerning gaze revealing her picky nature. The young shopkeeper leaned against the counter, answering whatever questions she posed.

Later, as business boomed, the young shopkeeper found himself too busy and hired a woman to assist.

Unexpectedly, the business began to plummet.

The young shopkeeper remained indifferent, leaving the shop’s affairs to the woman while he lounged in the back courtyard, enjoying the breeze while fanning himself. 

That woman, standing at the entrance of the back courtyard, lifted a bamboo curtain, gazing at the young shopkeeper lying on the rattan chair, and teasingly asked, “Do you know who I am?”

The young shopkeeper leisurely waved his jade bamboo fan, lazily saying, “You’re not that Xu family lady.”

The woman said, “You’ve actually seen her before.”

The young shopkeeper responded with an “oh.”

The woman continued, “I know you’ve covered your face; if you’re willing to show your true self, I’ll reveal mine too.”

The young shopkeeper closed his fan, gently spinning it, and finally grasped it to lightly tap his forehead. “But I’ve gotten used to your current appearance.”

The woman felt a mix of irritation and embarrassment, biting her lip, then suddenly glaring at him. “Since you’ve already realized I’m not a common woman, why do you pretend not to know? Or do you have designs on Qingfeng City? Intentionally keeping me around?”

The young shopkeeper slightly turned his head, looking at the woman who had cast an illusion, smiling, “You decide.”

The woman asked, “Who exactly are you?”

The young shopkeeper looked back at the sky, “Just a drunkard.”

The woman scoffed, “If I’m not mistaken, you don’t drink.”

He casually replied, “I’ll drink tomorrow.”

The young shopkeeper, who was about to become the third rank offering of the Xu family in Qingfeng City, still had a barrier to cross.

However, after spending so much time with him, the woman found it hard to let go.

Yet, considering the Xu family’s cunning and her own precarious position, she still retracted her illusion and gently called out, “Yuan Fang.”

Upon hearing her voice, he slowly turned, immediately opening his fan to cover his face, no longer looking at her, smiling, “Turns out you’re the ruler of the Fox Nation. What a sight to behold in the mortal realm.”

The woman furrowed her brow, waving her sleeve, sending his fan soaring. 

In a flash, she stood before him, extending her fingers to his forehead, asking several questions.

She sighed in relief, pulling back her fingers. As she gazed at the seemingly drowsy young man, she smirked and reached out once more, gently tugging at his temple.

In that moment, she found herself taking a few steps back involuntarily.

Her eyes widened, one hand covering her mouth, the other clutching her heart.

The young man furrowed his brow, waking up, and coldly said, “Get out.”

She steadied herself, chuckling, “Oh, so you’re a hidden gem of the Golden Body realm.”

He reached for his fan, skillfully handling it, then stood up, laughing, and walked over to her, gently tapping her cheek with the fan. He squinted and said softly, “Be good; just be my maid in the future. No need to pledge yourself; you’re not that good-looking, so I’m worried I’d be at a loss.”

She tilted her head, diverting her gaze, then met his eyes again, raising her hand to push aside the fan. “You truly enjoy saying drunken nonsense.”

With the fan pushed aside, he slapped her face instead.

She seemed somewhat dazed. The ruler of the Fox Nation, an Infant Transformation cultivator, had just been slapped?

He acted as if nothing had happened, looking up at the night sky. She, feeling out of control, covered her mouth and pressed her heart.

He softly said, “Don’t sneak into my room tonight; there’s no need to warm the bed in the summer.”

She involuntarily asked, “Will you remove the illusion?”

He gently tapped her forehead with the fan once more, then reclined back, “On such a beautiful moonlit night, you and I are merely a distraction.”

She was momentarily speechless, then suddenly echoed a phrase previously spoken by him, “Actually, I’m already used to your current appearance.”

He hummed in response.

She asked, “Are you truly a martial artist at the peak realm?”

He lightly nodded.

With the departure of Senior Cui and the earlier exit of Li Er from Baoping Continent, only Song Changjing remained among the ten realm martial artists.

If he couldn't quickly ascend to the tenth realm, no matter how many faces he had, he would still be unable to face others.

He only needed one or two good fights.

Thus, the earlier intuition of the Fox Nation’s ruler was not wrong; this martial madman genuinely hoped she would relay a message to the Xu family.

Years ago, when this nobleman, Zhu Lian, wandered the Jianghu, drunkenly throwing punches, he had captivated many a woman’s heart, truly capable of enchanting.

She picked up a stool, sitting beside the rattan chair, admiring the moon with him.

Two people, wordlessly.

Zhu Lian gently opened the fan, fanning a gentle breeze.

The refreshing wind brushed past their temples.

She asked, “Zhu Lian, can the Fox Nation successfully relocate to the Fallen Mountain? Can I truly trust you? I fear for my life and more so for the entire Fox Nation being implicated by me.”

He said, “First, trust yourself, then trust me. Otherwise, within three years, even if you wish to take risks with me, you’ll expose yourself. That Xu family lady is smarter than you. You are no match for her; I am.”

She remained silent for a long time, ultimately unable to resist asking, “Why would someone like you willingly serve the Fallen Mountain?”

He answered without addressing her question directly, “Who isn’t a caged bird? Who isn’t a guest in this world?”

Zhu Lian, Zhu Lian, the beauty conceals herself.

(End of this chapter)

 ### Chapter 825: The Thawing Snow (Part 1)

Outside the Thunder God Temple in Mahu Prefecture, Pei Axiang couldn't help but exclaim, “What a great punch!”

It seemed that merely saying "great punch" wasn't enough to encapsulate its brilliance. As she lightly stroked her knees, her eyes sparkled with admiration, and she nodded vigorously, adding, “If we're talking about the punch's continuous flow and the weight of its intent, I can't compare to the founder of this style. It truly is a marvelous punch! Just look at that waterfall hanging from the sky; the technique is quite high, and the moment the fist strikes the ground, it lands heavily.”

In this world, no martial artist at the tenth realm was to be underestimated.

For a proud martial artist like her, who had reached the limit of her skills, to sincerely praise another’s technique was no small feat. 

It turned out that that little girl who called herself Pei Qian had delivered seventeen consecutive punches, all striking Liu Suiyu, Pei Axiang's most favored disciple. 

As a result, Liu Suiyu had to break off the flow of her intent, no longer daring to let Pei Qian accumulate her punch's weight.

Liu Youzhou, hiding behind Pei Axiang, craned his neck and whispered, “To land over ten punches and force Aunt Liu into only a defensive stance without any power to counter is just too exaggerated. If this gets out, no one would believe it.”

Pei Axiang laughed and scolded, “What do you know? Those seventeen punches from the little girl count as just one punch.”

On the plaza outside the Thunder God Temple, the air crackled with energy as Pei Axiang’s martial intent flowed smoothly, quietly protecting Liu Youzhou behind her.

As for Liu Suiyu, she didn’t receive such protection. Even though the old woman was at the Earth Immortal realm, just watching the punches from afar made her feel somewhat uncomfortable.

The plaza was filled with distorted light as the martial intent swirled, a clear sign of a pure martial artist shaking the heavens and earth with their fists.

Liu Suiyu wasn't worried about losing; there were countless martial artists on the Aiai Continent, and while Pei Axiang was the most powerful at the Thunder God Temple, the martial fortune of the entire continent meant that as long as Suiyu could reach the pinnacle of the mountain realm, she would have the greatest luck. Liu Suiyu had achieved the title of “most powerful” three times, which was quite strange. According to her master, Pei Axiang's deductions regarding the fluctuations of the world's martial fortune, Liu Suiyu's repeated failures to grasp the title of “most powerful” seemed to have more to do with the little Baoping Continent.

This implied that, besides Song Changjing of the Great Li Dynasty, there were at least two masters of at least the ninth realm hiding there.

Liu Youzhou sighed, “I’ve heard of the Fallen Mountain on Baoping Continent, and how it has a close relationship with the North岳山君, Wei Bo. The business at the Niu Jiao Mountain ferry is quite prosperous, and now they’ve formed significant trade with both the Julu Continent’s Pima Sect and the Spring Dew Garden. But I’ve never heard of such a young girl with remarkable martial skills. Baoping Continent really is a strange place, a territory no bigger than a grain of rice, yet it constantly surprises people. The martial artist Song Changjing, the sword immortal Wei Jin, the cultivator Ma Kuxuan—none of them are to be underestimated.”

Pei Axiang teased, “Where are you pointing your elbow? Are you pretending to be a married woman?”

Liu Youzhou exclaimed, “Aunt Liu has finally thrown a punch!”

From his tone, it seemed that Liu Suiyu being struck without countering was the norm.

Pei Axiang had no choice but to patiently explain to this outsider, “This little girl was both asking questions about the punches and was a guest. Given Suiyu’s age and realm, she is technically the other’s senior, making her a half-host. According to the rules of the martial world, she naturally has to take a punch first, so she’s at a slight disadvantage. Of course, the little girl has refined that punch to perfection; that’s fundamental. If the opponent’s punches are good, we have to acknowledge them. As for Suiyu’s punch, it’s something I realized when I saw a dragon crossing the river—the Great River Horizontal Style—so it won’t be too shabby.”

In fact, Liu Suiyu’s punch that interrupted the other’s intent was quite remarkable and truly passed down from Pei Axiang.

Of course, Liu Suiyu, being at the peak of the realm of martial intent, was a level above Pei Qian, which was quite important. Otherwise, if they were both at the same realm of distant travel, judging by this punch alone, deciding a winner would have to rely on life or death.

Not only did Liu Suiyu interrupt the opponent's intent with one punch, but her second punch also landed squarely on Pei Qian's temple, sending her flying several feet.

Pei Qian’s head spun as her figure twisted in the air. She quickly pushed against the ground, abruptly grabbing it to halt her movement, flipping backward. In an instant, Liu Suiyu appeared beside Pei Qian, extending half a punch. Since Pei Qian hadn’t ended up where she anticipated, if Pei Qian took this punch, it would likely have concluded their bout. A punch from the peak of the ninth realm would mean that this junior would have to stay at the Thunder God Temple for a month or so to recuperate before continuing her travels.

Liu Suiyu retracted that half punch but didn’t chase after Pei Qian’s figure; instead, she stood her ground, surprised that this little girl was surprisingly resilient.

Pei Axiang laughed, “If you could make the little girl the Liu family’s honored guest, your father would at least earn back a suspended mountain ape's residence.”

Liu Youzhou shook his head. “My father advised me never to hastily conduct business with true friends; it’s easy to ruin friendships and end business deals poorly; it’s always a loss.”

The Liu family had a saying: wealth in the world came in two forms, one being tangible money from the divine realm, and the other being goodwill.

Pei Axiang mocked, “Since how is this little girl your friend? Have you asked her, and did she agree?”

Liu Youzhou fell silent, watching the young girl with a pretty face, slightly tanned compared to the snow-white currency.

Above the Thunder God Temple, Xie Songhua let some sword energy flow like drifting clouds, providing a solid foundation for the two direct disciples. Holding a bamboo box in one hand and a mountain staff in the other, she noticed that this green bamboo staff was surprisingly heavy. Her master explained that the staff had an illusionary effect. Its real material was akin to the condensed liquid from the Thunder Pool, merely shaped into a staff. As a result, Chao Mu said there seemed to be threads of pure sword intent within the staff. After Xie Songhua received it and carefully felt the strands of sword intent, she sighed softly, saying it was a gift from the sword immortal Zhou Cheng of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Ju Xing asked, “Master, can Sister Pei’s current martial arts level compete with that of an Infant Transformation cultivator?”

Xie Songhua replied, “As long as she’s not a sword cultivator, Pei Qian has a decent chance against an Infant Transformation opponent.”

However, this female sword immortal quickly corrected herself, “I should say she has a great chance.”

Because once Pei Qian experienced a life-and-death battle, it was highly likely she would break through again and become a peak martial artist.

Seeing Liu Suiyu stop her punches, Pei Qian had no choice but to stabilize her staggering figure. She furrowed her brows slightly, seemingly puzzled as to why this senior Liu did not take the chance to pursue the advantage, which caused her follow-up punch to miss. Earlier, after being struck heavily on the temple by Liu Suiyu's intense punch, she certainly didn’t feel well, but Pei Qian truly didn’t think it would diminish her combat power. Otherwise, her years of practicing punches in the bamboo loft and the punches dished out at Lion Peak by Senior Li would have been a huge joke. The lineage of Fallen Mountain, from her master to Old Man Cui, even including that old chef, down to her, the one with the least talent and the lowest realm, had only one use for injuries: to enhance her punch's intent! And to use the illusionary method.

When the next punch comes, it would still be the Godly Drumbeat Style, and it would be faster and heavier than the first punch.

The old chef once said, “Unless I die, I won’t stop asking about punches.”

And the first important aspect of a martial artist practicing punches is to first strike down the instinctual fear of death and pain within one's small personal universe.

At that time, Pei Qian had just started practicing punches on the second floor of the bamboo loft. The old chef, while busy with an apron, cooking in the kitchen or dishing out meals, casually spoke, and Pei Qian had let each of those words pass by her ears like the wind. It wasn’t until later, while traveling in the Northern Julu Continent with Li Huai, that she found time to practice her punches daily and naturally rediscovered those deliberately forgotten words, like savoring pickled vegetables from a jar, crisp and delightful, realizing that the old chef's words held a bit of wisdom.

Liu Suiyu laughed and asked, “Pei Qian, the punch techniques of the Thunder God Temple of Mahu Prefecture aren’t just about taking hits. Once I truly strike, it won't be light. Should we treat this sparring session as merely a friendly exchange, or are we going all out?”

Pei Qian replied without hesitation, “Let’s go with the latter. Senior Liu, you don’t have to worry about my injuries from now on. Once the sparring ends, both of us standing means it doesn't count as sparring.”

Liu Suiyu nodded with a smile; Pei Qian was quite agreeable.

Since she had been able to use the Great River Horizontal to receive Liu Suiyu’s punch and then interrupt the opponent's intent, if we consider this sparring session, it would be a case of Liu Suiyu gaining the upper hand with the first punch.

However, Liu Suiyu was indeed a realm above Pei Qian, and since she hadn't allowed her opponent to deliver a full punch, then this first punch could barely be considered a tie.

Pei Qian lightly tapped her toes against the ground, fixing her gaze on Liu Suiyu. “Senior Liu’s previous punch displayed your seniority, which I appreciate! But if you continue to intentionally let me hit you, it would mean that the Thunder God Temple’s techniques look down on the Fallen Mountain’s techniques.”

Liu Suiyu laughed heartily, “Good! Then I’ll take your Fallen Mountain martial artists a little more seriously!”

Pei Qian concluded, “If I lose, it means I’m lacking in skill, not that the Fallen Mountain’s techniques are inferior.”

Liu Suiyu slowly opened a stance, her arms crackling with bolts of lightning, her golden-hued eyes narrowing. “No matter how high or low your skills may be, I only want to hear you lie down and talk!”

Pei Axiang extended her finger, rubbing her forehead. “This little girl seems used to being a brat.”

Liu Youzhou said, “Let’s not ruin the atmosphere.”

Pei Axiang straightened her back, grasping the green bamboo flute from Qingshen Mountain. “Being vague in sparring only damages the atmosphere. A proper contest, where punches are divided by skill, is the true martial way.”

Liu Youzhou, seeing the two combatants on the plaza, noticed that Aunt Liu already held the upper hand. Not yet at the Golden Core Earth Immortal level, he was merely a Dragon Gate realm cultivator, and he couldn't clearly see the figures of the two women. He could only vaguely discern their movements through the colors of their clothing. Each punch from Aunt Liu produced a thunderous aura, intertwining lightning that lingered in the air. As she continued to punch, the plaza transformed into a thunder pool formed by her martial intent.

Aunt Liu seemed like a deity of thunder, recently exiled to the mortal realm. In truth, the Thunder God Temple's martial artists were renowned for their powerful techniques. Once they reached a high level, they bore a divine aura, and ordinary techniques struggled to break through that martial intent. The greatest headache for those who fought against them was that among Pei Axiang's direct disciples, Liu Suiyu best grasped the true meaning of their fist techniques.

Seeing her student Suiyu throw punches, the old woman couldn’t help but feel gratified.

Xie Songhua shared with her two disciples through inner voice, “Behind the Thunder God Temple, there’s a small hill called the famous Thunder Fan Mountain. However, few know that nearby, that mountain is said to be the place where ancient thunder deity weapons were forged. Ju Xing, your life sword ‘Thunder Marsh’ is most suitable for tempering here, yielding great results. For a sword cultivator, if they can attain the half-immortal weapon rank, it would be vastly different from a Qi practitioner refining a half-immortal weapon.”

Of course, crafting a sword required significant wealth in divine money and rare materials, making it a bottomless pit compared to other Qi practitioners, a widely accepted fact.

For example, if Ju Xing were to refine his sword at Thunder Fan Mountain, Xie Songhua had already prepared three offensive treasures and a substantial sum of Gu Yu money as compensation for Pei Axiang of the Thunder God Temple. The problem was that Pei Axiang might not agree.

This meant that Xie Songhua would need to haggle using the sword hidden in her bamboo box.

Chao Mu cheerfully remarked, “The evaluation of the Summer Resort has placed Ju Xing’s ‘Thunder Pool’ at the B rank, quite a high rank indeed.”

Every top-quality flying sword from the Sword Qi Great Wall, such as Wu Chengpei’s “Sweet Dew,” was best suited for large-scale battlefield slaughter, hence they were rare. More often than not, the Summer Resort’s selections were strategic choices. Once off the battlefield, the competition among the mountain cultivators tends to be more intense, as the second-rate flying swords selected by the Hidden Officials showcased outstanding killing power, especially those with a B rank or higher, all possessing astonishing innate abilities like Chen Sanqiu’s “White Deer,” which attained its rank due to literary fortune.

Ju Xing’s “Thunder Marsh,” having been rated as “B rank,” was undoubtedly due to the innate abilities of his flying sword, which could be used for both dueling and battlefield scenarios, showcasing numerous talents.

In contrast, the young girl Chao Mu, while possessing two innate flying swords “Pouring Rain” and “Rainbow,” were only rated “C rank” and “B rank,” respectively.

However, the term “only” was relative to Ju Xing. Beyond the A rank, B and C ranks encompassed a total of six tiers, meaning that all innate flying swords were considered valuable.

Next to Xie Songhua, Ju Xing, Chao Mu, and even Chen Li, the direct disciple of Li Cai, all these sword cultivators taken by the transcendent sword immortal had innate flying swords ranked B or C.

Yet, the rank of a flying sword was one thing; its practical performance in battle was another, as there were always unexpected variables in the world.

It was similar to the bureaucratic ranks below—the Hanlin Academy’s officials are often favored over ordinary scholars, making it easier to gain positions and noble titles.

Ju Xing stubbornly stated, “Master, I’m not too keen on relying on others to nurture my sword.”

However, he added, “But if Master insists on me doing so, I won’t slack off in sword refining.”

When he said this, he sounded a bit deflated.

Chao Mu, worried that her master might get angry, looked on.

Xie Songhua gently pressed down on the child’s head, speaking softly, “The Hidden Official once said that once you enter the world of Haoran, don’t act hastily. Learn to adapt to local customs. Just as he learned to respect the customs of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Ju Xing, can you meet the Hidden Official’s expectations?”

Ju Xing nodded vigorously, his spirit brightening as he said, “I often review that letter from the Hidden Official, which was passed to Master through Deng Liang. The letter mentions that we should gradually learn the various customs of Haoran, not to be hasty but to remember them with care. Good or bad, we need to observe more. Once we’ve seen enough, we must think about why. At the end of the letter, it also advised us to practice swordsmanship well first. When we reach a higher realm, at least capable of self-defense, then we can negotiate with others.”

Ju Xing then glanced at the small girl beside him, holding the mountain staff, and laughed at his master, “The Hidden Official’s teachings to me in the letter were lengthy, but Chao Mu’s were quite short; she’s just a little tofu block. It seems the Hidden Official knows she’s not destined for greatness. Master, you can rest easy; I’m enough.”

The little girl’s face crinkled in complaint, her eyes glistening with unshed tears, looking pitiful.

Ju Xing, seeing her expression, felt a rare pang of regret. Sister Pei had once privately advised him not to always frown at Chao Mu, as she was just a little girl, and he was a boy. Bullying her wasn’t a mark of skill. Since they were both from the same hometown and sect, it was a rare connection, and he should protect her more, at the very least not let her be bullied by others.

Ju Xing thought Sister Pei’s advice was quite reasonable and pledged to do so. However, he sometimes just couldn't help but say a few words to Chao Mu.

Moreover, he wasn’t just anyone. Alas, it was unfortunate that no one else had bullied this silly girl Chao Mu; his master was too kind, and he was too invincible in Aiai Continent, which troubled the disciple.

On the plaza, Pei Qian was struck in the cheek by Liu Suiyu’s elbow, crashing to the ground. Immediately, she raised her hands to block Liu Suiyu’s foot aimed at her heart.

If that foot hit, it would likely end the sparring.

Pei Qian slid across the ground for several feet.

Just as she slapped her palm on the ground and floated back up, Liu Suiyu shadowed her, driving her knee into Pei Qian's chest.

This slender young girl was sent flying backward with a crash, landing on the ground.

As Liu Suiyu's feet touched the ground, she let out a breath of foul air.

After a series of punches from the ninth realm, while not every punch was at peak strength, this was the end of a pure martial artist’s true energy.

Liu Youzhou felt that today’s sparring could be considered a fulfilling exchange for both sides. He watched as the young girl stood up, spitting a mouthful of blood on the ground, only to adopt a fighting stance once more, seemingly unaware of her injuries. This reminded him of the ancient battlefield ruins where Yu Jianfu had sparred with Cao Ci, perhaps a similar scene, yet slightly different. However, he couldn’t articulate precisely how they differed; perhaps Yu Jianfu was aware of his disadvantage?

But this strange girl before him didn’t necessarily think she was inferior to Aunt Liu? The more she thought this way, the heavier Liu’s punches would become in response.

Liu Youzhou felt a twinge of empathy and turned his gaze to Pei Axiang's bamboo flute, asking, “Axiang, what’s the origin of that bamboo flute? I feel a bit awkward about that offering money; do you feel comfortable accepting it?”

Pei Axiang, upon hearing the inquiry, looked somewhat peculiar, shaking her head as she gently swirled the bamboo flute in her hand. The yellowing bead dangling from it lightly tapped against the flute, producing a crisp, pleasant sound. Pei Axiang chuckled, “The past is not worth revisiting.”

Liu Youzhou, unbothered by this, quickly lowered his voice, “The offering money from the past decade has at least doubled.”

Pei Axiang raised two fingers.

Liu Youzhou swatted her fingers away, laughing, “Axiang, you’re quite the straightforward person. It’s a deal!”

Only then did Pei Axiang say, “Have you heard of a scoundrel named A Liang?”

Liu Youzhou nodded, “What nonsense are you talking about? That elder’s name is truly well-known. Moreover, my aunt has always been unable to forget that man; who in Aiai Continent doesn’t know this? He once broke a great river in the Central Plains with a punch and even carried a clan's ancestral mountain several miles away. But that’s not what I admire most; I’ve heard he enjoys reciting poetry before a fight, and I truly respect that. He dubbed himself ‘A playful butterfly amidst the flowers, a handsome lad in the ten miles radius.’ In my opinion, that’s not just empty talk. The fairies who long for him are truly countless.”

Liu Suiyu couldn’t help but feel anxious.

Her young master mustn’t learn from that man.

Pei Axiang raised the bamboo flute, “After being beaten by that person, I received this compensation.”

Liu Youzhou couldn’t resist prodding, “Did several of you challenge him at once?”

Pei Axiang sighed helplessly, “Five or six of us, I suppose.”

Liu Youzhou gently patted her shoulder, “Axiang, you really are impressive; this will bring you some glory.”

Pei Axiang laughed, “That’s true.”

It truly wasn’t embarrassing. After all, there had been cases where ten mountain cultivators surrounded one person, and only one had managed to escape.

In fact, during the time of Haoran, that man’s swordsmanship was not particularly prominent. It was only after he journeyed for a century in the Sword Qi Great Wall, slashing down the peak demons of the Ascension realm, that the entire Haoran world, especially the Central Plains which he had wreaked havoc on, finally realized just how remarkable that doggone man was; he had previously been quite subtle and reserved in his strikes. Later, this person ascended and left the world of Haoran, heading to the Celestial Realm, ultimately exchanging a punch with the “truly invincible” Daoist Old Two of Bai Yujing, sending each other back to their respective homes, which was truly astonishing.

To share the same age and coexist in the same era, it seemed both pitiable and honorable.

It was like Pei Axiang and her group, encountering A Liang.

Those who were even earlier had met the most favored of the human realm, who had drawn the waters from the heavens with a single stroke.

Now, all the young martial artists in the world faced Cao Ci and the eleventh “Hidden Official.”

Pei Axiang pondered this and cast a glance at the two still sparring on the plaza.

Pei Qian was once again sent reeling by Liu Suiyu’s whip kick, struggling to stabilize her figure as Liu Suiyu unleashed a flurry of six punches, landing on her forehead, cheek, and neck, each double-fisted strike.

The delivery of two punches to the same target was one of the core essences of the Thunder God Temple's techniques, known as “Overlapping Thunder,” which Pei Axiang had newly developed after reaching the tenth realm. It returned to its original state, appearing as the same move, but its intent was exactly opposite, capable of severely crippling a martial artist’s intent or a Qi practitioner’s energy.

In the end, Pei Qian was struck hard in the chest by two consecutive punches, her feet leaving the ground as she fell heavily.

Yet, the slim, young woman, barely over twenty, managed to elbow the ground, twisting her body to elegantly rise again. Though she had suffered significant injuries, her martial intent remained steadfast and even increased.

Blood streamed from her seven orifices, but for a distant traveler martial artist, it was a trivial matter.

Pei Axiang nodded in approval.

Liu Suiyu’s expression became grave, and she felt a spark of frustration.

She had already exchanged two bursts of pure true energy while her opponent had not changed even once.

Of course, it wasn’t that Liu Suiyu’s martial intent was weaker; it was more that she held a mindset of training and feeding her opponent. It made Liu Suiyu wonder if this little girl was too strong. Did she truly think that the Thunder God Temple's techniques were inferior to those of the Fallen Mountain? Was she determined from the start to measure the weight of Liu Suiyu’s ninth realm punches?

Ju Xing and Chao Mu watched nervously.

They realized that when Sister Pei was sparring, she was wholly different from her usual serious self when copying books, silent while traveling, or smiling during chats.

Xie Songhua sighed in admiration; the Hidden Official had an eye for apprentices.

Opportunities to truly teach Pei Qian the techniques of punching were certainly rare, considering she was still quite young while the Hidden Official had long since gone to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Thus, the Fallen Mountain, shrouded in mist and not widely known, must have some high-level figures presiding over it.

As for Liu Youzhou, he had long been aware of the Fallen Mountain, largely due to his status as the future god of wealth of Aiai Continent, leaving him with ample free time.

In Xie Songhua’s view, the spirit and energy of Pei Qian and her master, Chen Ping’an, were remarkably similar, as if they were carved from the same mold.

However, the choice of techniques and styles they employed against their opponents differed significantly. Pei Qian conducted her punches fearlessly, consistently forward.

As for her master Chen Ping’an, he had to weigh his options heavily, rarely seeking that kind of unrestrained, varied fighting style, focusing instead on adapting to the situation, person, and place, almost to the point of being overly meticulous. Each punch was laid out and calculated to maximize benefits. But Pei Qian was entirely different; when she threw punches, she exuded the spirit of a bold hero, as if from a young age, she'd grasped the concept that “there is no one else in the world, and in asking about punches, one only questions oneself.”

Xie Songhua, being a sword immortal who loved distant travel and had connections with the tenth realm martial artists of the Liu and Jin Jiao continents, had some good friends among them. Among the two elder martial artists with vastly different styles and temperaments, the only commonality was their appreciation for the profound scope of “Heaven and Earth are ancient, one person with two fists.” Yet, while this great principle might seem simple to express and easy for others to understand, truly grounding oneself in this idea was ethereal and challenging to manifest in one’s martial way.

However, Xie Songhua had another question; since her hometown was a place of few gatherings, why did Pei Qian hold her master in such high regard?

Her two direct disciples, Ju Xing and Chao Mu, certainly understood and respected her, not only seeing her as a pillar but also as a family elder. Therefore, Xie Songhua felt satisfied, unable to find fault in her disciples. Yet compared to Chen Ping’an and Pei Qian, there seemed to be a slight difference.

Although the saying in the martial world suggests that taking a master is akin to being reborn, making the master and disciple like father and son, it seemed that in Pei Qian’s heart, the roles of heaven, earth, king, parent, and teacher had already merged into one.

In guiding children, it seems the young Hidden Official was adept at it.

Xie Songhua could only interpret it this way.

Always observing the sparring, Pei Axiang remarked, “Being able to engage in such sparring will surely be beneficial, and perhaps Suiyu will gain unexpected insights.”

Liu Youzhou muttered, “You still haven’t mentioned the origin of that bamboo flute. I feel a bit shy about that offering money; do you feel comfortable accepting it?”

Pei Axiang laughed, “There’s nothing I can’t say about it, but just consider it. Don’t go spreading it around.”

Liu Youzhou nodded.

It turned out that in the beautiful bamboo sea cave years ago, Pei Axiang, as the youngest ninth realm martial artist in Aiai Continent, was at her most spirited. At a water banquet on Qingshen Mountain, she had traveled with several friends, drinking and enjoying the scenery when she had a dispute with a scruffy man who had been secretly digging up bamboo whips and shoots. She had never encountered such a shameless person before; initially, he claimed to be the land deity of Qingshen Mountain, saying he was digging bamboo shoots to treat distinguished guests. After being exposed, he insisted he was a guest at the personal banquet of the lady of Qingshen Mountain, claiming that digging a few bamboo shoots was nothing. As a result, a young sword immortal immediately flew over to inform the mountain deity. This man, bold in demeanor, leaned against a bamboo pole with arms crossed, smugly declaring, “You’re in for bad luck for provoking me; wait till the lady orders you to leave! After this, you won’t be able to set foot in the bamboo sea cave again; I’ll take your surname.”

Later, the mountain deity replied, saying the lady did not recognize him, and thus Pei Axiang and her group chased after the thief as if driving a dog away. At first, no one took it seriously; it was more of a jest. But then, when a sword cultivator inadvertently struck too hard, the man shouted, “One punch for each little brother,” and knocked everyone down. Not only that, he buried everyone in the ground, claiming that tomorrow many jade-purged sword immortals and mountain peak martial artists would sprout from the ground as his gift to Qingshen Mountain.

When he was burying Pei Axiang, he asked her how her punches were.

Those who had attempted to break free were knocked unconscious by a single punch. Burying the crowd up to their necks was like a field of bamboo shoots emerging after rain.

Pei Axiang didn’t dare to move, lest she humiliate herself.

The young sword immortal friend who had been filled with the most earth was particularly unlucky; as the man piled up dirt, he grumbled, “You sword immortals are the most numerous and flamboyant, really annoying. Today, you’ve fallen into my hands...”

In the end, it was a female envoy from the mountain deity’s palace that appeared and saved everyone.

The man who had been squatting and piling dirt on Pei Axiang stood up in an instant upon seeing the envoy, leaning against the bamboo pole, spitting in his palm, smoothing down his hair, exposing a large forehead, and clasping his hands in greeting, calling himself A Liang, all in one breath, as smooth as flowing water.

So natural, it was merely a matter of familiarity.

The envoy ignored him and directly asked, “If you are a scholar and a sword cultivator, why resort to fighting? Is it to intentionally humiliate these people?”

She glanced at the man, who had a sword on his back, and asked, “Daring to steal bamboo shoots and whips here? Is it not related to scholars; do you intend to challenge us at Qingshen Mountain?”

The man shook his head, slightly adjusting his belt, and shyly smiled, unable to meet her gaze.

A true man never easily draws his sword.

Everything was left unsaid.

After that, a wild chase ensued, and the fellow named A Liang scurried around the bamboo sea, his earlier phrase of “Do you believe countless fairies chase after me?” proving somewhat accurate.

Perhaps the chase could also be seen as a form of pursuit.

Until he encountered the legendary lady of Qingshen Mountain, described as “beautiful, fond of going barefoot, with hair as dark as jade.”

Thus, another untold story unfolded, leaving countless versions without a definitive conclusion.

As for A Liang, he seemed to have taken a liking to Pei Axiang, striking up a friendship through combat, helping her cut a segment of green bamboo from Qingshen Mountain, which he carried out of the bamboo sea cave.

After hearing this vivid story, Liu Youzhou couldn't help but ask, “Axiang, didn’t you later return to Qingshen Mountain for a night banquet? Did A Liang end up taking on your surname?”

Pei Axiang sighed, “He meant that he wouldn’t mind changing his surname to be our ancestor.”

Liu Youzhou’s eyes widened in disbelief. “Is that even possible? There’s some logic to it.”

Pei Axiang rose with the bamboo flute in hand, intending to call an end to the sparring between the two.

If this continued, the little Thunder God Temple would genuinely end up with another patient.

This single-minded girl had already tumbled to the ground seven times.

Liu Suiyu was also getting fired up; each punch she threw was increasingly embodying her martial intent at the peak of the ninth realm. Just the Overlapping Thunder technique alone, a typical distant traveler realm martial artist would have fallen by half, bleeding profusely, and it wasn’t simply a matter of breaking bones—serious problems could develop.

Even the most solid distant traveler physique couldn’t withstand the onslaught of a peak martial artist.

The two were merely sparring.

Even if Liu Suiyu could gain martial intent through this, enhancing her skills, Pei Axiang didn’t think it was in accordance with the rules of the martial world.

In the martial world, pure martial artists need to have a sense of proportion when protecting their own people. Heavily injuring a younger girl of a lower realm to increase the martial fortune of the Thunder God Temple would be a disgrace.

Pei Axiang couldn’t afford such shame.

Thus, she called out, “That’s enough.”

Xie Songhua nodded lightly. Pei Axiang was still somewhat reasonable; otherwise, if she hadn’t spoken, Pei Axiang would have unsheathed her sword.

She would directly challenge the Thunder God Temple, questioning the oldest and highest-ranked person.

Though Liu Suiyu was still somewhat unwilling, she hurriedly retracted her punches. Pei Qian, however, seemed to have lost herself in the moment, still throwing out a punch, only suddenly awakening and forcefully reversing a mouthful of pure true energy, struggling against her surging blood to retract her punch and step back.

The slender, weak young woman swayed unsteadily, her slightly tanned face marred with cuts, one eye swollen red, making her appear quite disheveled. She tilted her head slightly, blood oozing from her ear.

As a fellow woman, Liu Suiyu’s ninth realm punches were indeed not light.

Pei Qian’s pitiful state made Liu Youzhou’s scalp tingle; it was terrifying.

Pei Qian raised her hand, wiping the red streak of blood that had trickled down from her temple to her cheek.

Liu Suiyu began to retract her martial intent, looking at Pei Qian with undeniable admiration in her eyes, nodding and smiling, “This time I didn’t win, and you didn’t lose, so we’ll call it a draw. When you break through, let’s have another spar. Whether you come to Mahu Prefecture to find me or I go to Fallen Mountain to find you, it’s all fine.”

Pei Qian clasped her fists in respect, remaining silent, as if she had something to say.

Ju Xing noticed sweat pooling in the palms of his hands, glancing at Chao Mu, who was also sweating profusely.

Chao Mu, sensing his gaze, turned and forced a smile.

Ju Xing suddenly felt a surge of anger, saying, “Sister Pei is already injured, and you’re smiling? Why don’t you just stretch your mouth to your ears...”

Before he could finish, he received a reprimand from Xie Songhua, “Chao Mu is just a little girl; whether she cries or smiles, you can’t criticize her, right? Should she learn from you and be a mute?”

Ju Xing sighed, “She’s so silly; how could she learn from me?”

Xie Songhua recalled something and addressed Ju Xing seriously, “Apologize to Chao Mu. What did the Hidden Official say in the letter? A true hero acknowledges their mistakes and corrects them, right?”

Ju Xing was taken aback. Well, it was clear that even his master knew to use the Hidden Official to keep him in check. Though he was unwilling, he still stubbornly muttered, “Sorry, I guess.”

Xie Songhua raised her hand, pretending to strike, “You’d better mean it!”

Seeing Chao Mu shaking her head vigorously, he softened and said, “I’m sorry.”

Damn, could he be any more awkward?

Chao Mu smiled brightly.

Xie Songhua unexpectedly recalled another phrase from the letter. She previously thought the young Hidden Official was overly meticulous, especially for writing something so grand for two young kids. She hadn’t realized why it shouldn’t be deemed too early; on the contrary, it seemed that the young man had written too little. Principles like “adapt to local customs and carry forth the traditions of the great sword immortal” were indeed worth repeating.

She believed that Ju Xing and Chao Mu would truly recognize the weight of the Hidden Official’s expectations in their future paths.

Standing on the distant steps outside the Thunder God Temple, Pei Axiang regarded Pei Qian with growing admiration. The martial way, which emphasizes that effort yields results, suggested that the younger the genius, the more likely they would carry hidden dangers in their physical training, hindering their future martial progress.

Martial arts masters sparring with each other often hold both advantages and disadvantages. The benefit is an increase in martial intent and refinement of techniques, but the downside is that repeated injuries, if not fully healed, could leave subtle, undetectable roots of illness, which would exacerbate problems as their realm increases. For instance, the first level of the limit realm is said to be one of great energy; if the body’s bones and meridians suffer much damage, how could one maintain that great energy?

Pei Axiang had learned this lesson the hard way. Although her name suggested a delicate and refined nature, her martial arts were famously robust, and in her youth, her temperament was quite rebellious. It was no wonder she became the third honored guest of the Liu family; it certainly wasn’t for the meager divine money, as a pure martial artist, she focused on the idea of being without external possessions, primarily concerned for her disciples’ future paths and the inheritance of the family’s fire. Don’t look at Pei Axiang’s youthful appearance; in reality, she was quite aged, much like the old man Wang Fuxu from the Northern Julu Continent. Pei Axiang had made many enemies in her youth, and Wang Fuxu was just one of them.

Pei Axiang understood her own struggles. Though she had reached the second layer of the tenth realm, her earlier excessive energy had caused significant damage. Now, Pei Axiang was trying to muster her spirit, not allowing herself to fall into despair regarding the “divine reach.”

Thus, in recent years, as she occasionally guided Liu Suiyu and her other three direct disciples, she wanted them to remember that while seeking high techniques, they should also pursue greatness, aiming for a spirit as grand as mountains and rivers, like learning from the distant sword immortals of the Northern Julu Continent. However, aside from Liu Suiyu, none of the other direct disciples or the seven subsequent disciples truly understood Pei Axiang’s meaning; none went to the Sword Qi Great Wall to temper their physiques or martial intent.

Some pretended not to understand, unwilling to head to the Sword Qi Great Wall for what they deemed a certain death. The reasoning was simple: even sword immortals could die, and martial artists would die faster. Often, stepping outside the city meant certain doom. Others believed they had reached the peak of martial arts and began to enjoy life, dedicating themselves to passing down the techniques of the Thunder God Temple’s lineage to the third generation, cloaking it as helping their master Pei Axiang spread the teachings and secure their place in the continent. Of course, some were busy serving their monarchs as military generals, needing to stabilize and consolidate their nation’s martial fortune, making it impossible for them to leave. 

In many cases, after painstakingly selecting a few promising disciples and investing years of effort in their training, as time passed, their disciples would develop their lives, and eventually, only the title of master and disciple would remain. Even if those disciples still respected their master deep down, they often found themselves unable to act on their martial paths. Pei Axiang felt a hint of regret about this but didn’t dwell on it too much.

Within her own Thunder God Temple lineage, aside from Liu Suiyu, who had become independent, there was also that young disciple, capable of inheriting the teachings and lineage.

In fact, during that time when she encountered A Liang in the bamboo sea cave, he had already told Pei Axiang to broaden her horizons. There was no need to keep staring at the tenth realm; it would not run away. She should explore greater, more expansive vistas, climb the peaks of Sui Mountain, visit the Sword Qi Great Wall, stroll through the Northern Julu Continent, and perhaps take a trip to the Tianyu Cave.

Unfortunately, at that time, Pei Axiang hadn’t given it much thought. Of course, she also blamed that doggone A Liang, who quickly changed the subject, his eyes glimmering as he drunkenly rambled on about a certain fairy’s figure.

Pei Axiang sighed deeply. Life was always unexpected, throwing a punch that was neither heavy nor light, leaving one feeling powerless to resist. Perhaps this is what it meant to feel powerless.

Tenth realm martial artists were no exception.

Pei Axiang reined in her thoughts, smiling, “Pei Qian, if you don’t mind the small place, feel free to stay here to recuperate for a while.”

This little girl who claimed to be the “founding disciple” of Fallen Mountain was truly a remarkable distant traveler, her foundational training astonishing.

Here, she wouldn’t need to recuperate for long.

Pei Axiang became increasingly curious about the Fallen Mountain, the one who taught Pei Qian punches and helped her temper her physique. Who could this master possibly be? Was it someone of the ninth realm besides Song Changjing of Baoping Continent? A limit realm martial artist? The likelihood was quite slim; otherwise, Pei Axiang would have surely heard of such a name. 

Masters of the tenth realm in the world of Haoran were exceedingly few when compared to those at the fifth realm. For instance, in neighboring Northern Julu Continent, there were only three ninth realm martial artists—Wang Fuxu, Gu You, and a martial artist of the Li surname. One ninth realm martial artist was already crucial to the transfer of martial fortune across the continent, making it hard to hide too deeply.

After the sparring, what gave Pei Axiang a headache was the female sword immortal Xie Songhua.

From any angle, she didn’t seem to come in peace.

Finally breaking her silence, Pei Qian spoke, “I have one last punch that I’d like to ask Senior Liu about.”

Liu Suiyu held up two fingers, gently pressing them against the sides of her temple, lightly kneading them.

Xie Songhua hesitated for a moment and asked, “Pei Qian, are you sure you want to do this?”

Pei Qian nodded, turning to look at Xie Songhua, a smile breaking across her face. “I’ll only throw one punch.”

Liu Suiyu turned to glance at her master behind her.

Pei Axiang considered for a moment, “Then let the little girl stay here for a few more days.”

What she meant was that Liu Suiyu needn’t be overly concerned about the differences in rank and realm.

However, Pei Axiang gathered her voice into a line, reminding her disciple, “Remember, you can make the punches heavier, but you must never harm the opponent’s foundational martial path.”

She neither wished to create enmity with Fallen Mountain nor stray from the martial intentions of a senior.

Liu Suiyu smiled in response, “Where would I dare to harm her? The more exceptional talents there are in the world, the better.”

Pei Qian clasped her fists in respect, saying, “I know I was rude to Senior Liu… and I also owe an apology to Master Pei.”

Liu Suiyu nodded. “Then we’ll exchange one punch. Consider it a gift for our first meeting, and I’ll return the favor to the Thunder God Temple.”

Xie Songhua couldn’t help but smile as she remarked to the two children, “You should all learn from Pei Qian; that’s how a true lady behaves.”

Ju Xing nodded, “I’ll learn as I wish, but I can’t say the same for someone else.”

Chao Mu gently tugged at Xie Songhua’s sleeve, her voice trembling, “Master, I’m a bit scared.”

Then Pei Qian suddenly stopped, performing a strange motion. She lifted her palm and lightly tapped her forehead.

On Lion Peak in Northern Julu Continent, Chen Ping’an had advanced from the sixth realm to the seventh realm, attaining the Golden Body stage under Li Er’s punches.

Li Er’s punches had always been precise and targeted, making many punches unsuitable for a sixth realm martial artist but perfect for tempering Pei Qian’s physique.

Thankfully, Li Huai had spent the last six months at the foot of the mountain, helping his mother with business, and had not seen Pei Qian’s training methods. Otherwise, her motivation to practice might have entirely vanished.

Practicing punches was indeed arduous. 

And the fear of hardship, years ago, Pei Qian and now Li Huai, were essentially the same.

However, Li Huai was indeed luckier than Pei Qian, as he remained blissfully unaware that he didn’t have to endure hardship.

In general, one could argue about knowledge and courage in comparison to Li Huai, but when it came to stepping out and stepping in dog poop, there was truly no comparison.

Pei Axiang suddenly asked, “What was the name of that first punch?”

Given that the intent was clear, asking about the opponent’s technique didn’t violate the rules of the martial world.

Pei Qian gradually stepped back, increasing the distance between herself and Liu Suiyu, answering, “The punch originates from Fallen Mountain, but it wasn’t taught to me by my master. It’s called the Godly Drumbeat Style.”

Pei Axiang nodded with a smile, “How old is your master?”

Pei Qian shook her head.

What could she say? She understood well what should be said and what shouldn’t. 

Things that shouldn’t be said, she simply kept quiet, treating others with sincerity.

Years ago, during the martial exchange at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Yu Jianfu had interrupted her master’s Godly Drumbeat Style.
