Today, outside the Thunder God Temple in Mahu Prefecture, Pei Qian had also been interrupted by Liu Suiyu, only delivering seventeen punches.

Indeed, the world of martial artists was filled with extraordinary individuals.

Pei Qian was certain that as long as she could deliver twenty-four punches, the opponent would surely fall. Even a ninth realm martial artist would be no exception.

However, the opponent could still interrupt her intent before her twenty-second punch, just as easily severing her martial path.

Whether it was in friendly competition or life-and-death clashes, she would ultimately lose.

There was nothing to be done about it; the difference in realms between pure martial artists was a reality she couldn’t ignore. 

At that moment, all she could do was throw this one punch.

It was something she had comprehended herself.

She hadn’t thought of a name for it yet and would have to wait until her master returned home to help her name it. 

Her master had a knack for naming things.

Jing Qing, Warm Tree—how wonderful!

But looking at herself, Pei Qian, “Paying Back”? 

Pei Qian surveyed her surroundings, inhaling deeply, her spirit sinking into focus, her eyes shining brightly. 

With her knees slightly bent, one palm lifted in preparation, and a tightly clenched fist before her.

This punch had yet to be thrown; it was merely a stance.

Xie Songhua moved with the two children, riding the wind away several dozen feet.

Pei Axiang squinted her eyes from the steps, then gently stepped forward to stand before Liu Youzhou.

Behind the young girl, it was like a great sun breaking through the sea surface, emerging into the world, only to suddenly rise rapidly into the sky.

As my punch is unleashed, it is like the sun at its zenith.

Only then could martial artists across the world bow in respect.

———— 
(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 826: The Melting Snow (Part Two)

In the Sixth Great Dynasty of the Central Earth, the Shao Yuan Dynasty, the National Master Chao Pu sat with his favored disciple Lin Junbi, reviewing the early strategies of the embroidered tiger on Baoping Continent.

Inside the pavilion, the warmth of spring enveloped them, yet outside, the snow fell in heavy flurries. The National Master, however, was seldom talkative, allowing Lin Junbi to explain the intricate strategies of the Great Li Dynasty, both from the mountaintops to the valleys below. He encouraged Lin Junbi to articulate his thoughts freely, without fear of being incorrect. 

This was not unusual in the National Master's residence. Chao Pu believed that a significant issue in the world stemmed from the disparities in people's knowledge, yet many fancied themselves as teachers, unaware of how to truly guide others. Therefore, he had a peculiar habit of allowing his self-assured disciples, regardless of age, to emulate the teaching methods of scholars, either by elucidating principles to others or persuading themselves in their studies first, using logic to convince themselves before others.

During moments of silence from Lin Junbi as he pondered, Chao Pu would often interject with tangential topics, ensuring their teacher-student relationship remained unaffected by distractions.

Chao Pu, who towered above a multitude in the Shao Yuan Dynasty, wore a tall hat and flowing robes, his demeanor refined, holding a snow-white whisk draped over his arm. The key was that the old man exuded an air of cultured ease, appearing less like someone entrusted with state affairs by the emperor, and more akin to a leisurely scholar enjoying the beauty of nature.

With a smile, Chao Pu remarked, “The three and a half direct disciples of the Sage of Letters could barely be counted as four. Of course, there’s now an additional closed-door disciple, the Hidden Official Chen Pingan. Our Confucian lineage generally branches into six main threads, with the old scholar’s line being the most faded, particularly since one individual refuses to acknowledge his position within the Confucian lineage, only recognizing the Master and not the Temple of Literature's doctrine. These four individuals, each with their own demeanor, have been likened to the four seasons—spring, summer, autumn, and winter.”

The old scholar continued, “Regardless of who it is, being with Qi Jingchun feels like basking in a spring breeze.”

Lin Junbi asked, “I’ve heard that before Mr. Qi became the master of the academy, his temperament wasn’t particularly pleasant?”

Though his teacher could call Qi Jingchun by name, Lin Junbi still addressed him respectfully as Mr. Qi. Even in the teacher-student relationship, Lin Junbi refused to overstep boundaries.

Chao Pu chuckled, “The chill of early spring can be harsh on the young.”

He then elaborated, “A scholar should be approachable, upholding reason and propriety, but that doesn't mean merely being a pushover. The spirit and resilience of a scholar should not resemble a puddle of mud.”

“Now, the Sword Immortal, on the other hand, may evoke the sweltering heat of summer, making it difficult for outsiders of the Sage of Letters lineage to approach. He conducts his studies with stark straightforwardness, devoid of human sentiment. Later, when he shifted to sword training, he inadvertently became unmatched in swordsmanship. There’s no reasoning with that.”

“That one referred to by the old scholar as the ‘big fool’ has no definitive name. Even among the Sage of Letters’ disciples, he’s used to being called Liu Sixteen. This person vanished after leaving the Merit Forest, and no one knows where he went. Some say he’s an exceptionally old tenth realm martial artist, while others suggest he might be a ghostly immortal. It’s even rumored he has some connection with the most favored one, having once ventured into the mountains together to gather herbs and seek immortals. However, there are no records of this person at the Temple of Literature, as it seems the old scholar wrote about him only to have it secretly erased.”

“This man speaks little and is the most reticent among the Sage of Letters’ disciples. Many accounts are merely third-hand hearsay and should not be trusted. In the chilling autumn winds, he made his only move, causing a massive uproar. Ultimately, it was still the old scholar who intervened; I’m not sure whether to call it cleaning up a mess or stirring up an even bigger one, resulting in a mountain sinking. However, the righteous world only knows the aftermath and is unclear about the true cause.”

Upon hearing this, Lin Junbi expressed his confusion, “Such a hidden figure, when the Pearly Jewel Cave fell, did not make an appearance. When the Left Sword Immortal headed to the Sword Qi Great Wall, he remained unseen. Now with the embroidered tiger guarding Baoping Continent, it seems there’s still no word from him. Teacher, isn’t this too unreasonable?”

Chao Pu nodded, “Thus, there are rumors that this person has gone to another realm, to that western Buddhist country.”

Lin Junbi’s expression became peculiar as he recalled an incident where Ah Liang caused a ruckus at a certain academy. There was a famous saying that cautioned the gentlemen and virtuous: “Don’t stay up late, as it’s hard to obtain a monk’s genealogy. Be careful, or you might go bald, and the temple won’t accept you.”

Chao Pu waved his whisk, switching arms, and smiled, “Ah Liang’s close association with the Sage of Letters lineage caused quite a stir at first. After the dispute of the three and four, Ah Liang went to the Sword Qi Great Wall, undoubtedly feeling greatly disappointed.”

The old scholar then spoke of the embroidered tiger, Cui Zhan, who was once the first disciple of the Sage of Letters and had the potential to become the ‘beloved of winter.’ 

As the master of the academy and the sacrificial wine of the learning institution, as well as the deputy leader of the Central Earth Temple of Literature, he could easily become a highly regarded honorary sage. 

Most importantly, Cui Zhan maintained excellent relationships with many influential forces outside the Temple of Literature. He had collaborated with the lord of the Martial Emperor City, established a deep friendship with the elder of the Yu family, and had ties with the sword immortal whose given name is ‘Shui,’ along with the novelist elder from the White Paper Blessed Land... All of them genuinely acknowledged Cui Zhan’s intelligence and character. However, later criticisms surged, and due to the inevitable changes, Cui Zhan, who was not one to seek out friends, fell into deeper silence, only re-emerging on the world stage during a time of chaos, making it difficult for anyone to ignore him.

For instance, Chao Pu had long harbored disdain for Cui Zhan, wishing he would quietly fade away in his position as the National Master of the Great Li. Now that Cui Zhan was helping the Great Li occupy a continent, hindering the demon race’s advance to Baoping Continent, Chao Pu admired him yet could not accept Cui Zhan’s betrayal of the teachings. Chao Pu viewed Cui Zhan’s hasty rise to prominence followed by his betrayal of the teachings as the pivotal moment marking the decline of the Sage of Letters lineage.

However, as the National Master, Chao Pu was compelled to acknowledge that Cui Zhan’s accomplishments in Baoping Continent were executed to near perfection. 

The land of one continent, both above and below the mountains, was indeed under Cui Zhan’s control.

Chao Pu sighed softly, “Winter is the best time to read. Human hearts are dark and private, just like the embroidered tiger bringing them to light. Otherwise, which vassal state in Baoping Continent hasn’t experienced enmity? The hearts of the people can’t be much better than those in Tongye Continent.”

Lin Junbi lowered his head, gazing at the Baoping Continent chessboard before him, murmuring, “The embroidered tiger is truly ruthless. Both in heart and action.”

Even on a continent that was a nation in itself, amidst impending disaster, scholars resigning from official positions, and celestial masters retreating from their sects, many hidden in the mountains and forests, the Great Li Dynasty seemed to have anticipated this. Before the situation could escalate further, they quickly produced a comprehensive set of countermeasures, clearly demonstrating that they had been waiting for these individuals to resurface.

The young emperor of Great Li, Song He, issued a decree, commanding all vassals of the continent. 

All officials and generals within the continent’s vassal states who dared to defy the laws of Great Li, whether by covertly disobeying or being negligent in governance, would be held accountable according to the law, with clear evidence and regulations to follow.

Those who dared to withhold information, report joyous news while concealing the bad, or muddle through when issues arose, would have their vassal monarchs recorded. They would be required to submit detailed reports immediately to the military presence of Great Li. Local forces of Great Li had the authority to bypass the vassal monarchs and execute decisions first, reporting afterward.

The hundreds of officials who resigned from their posts in Baoping Continent, per the newly published laws of Great Li, would see their descendants barred from serving in official positions for three generations, reducing them to commoners. Not only that, but local courts would also revoke any honors or accolades bestowed upon their families in history, either dismantling or confiscating them. Furthermore, the court ordered local officials to amend the local county records to specifically name those who resigned from their posts.

At the Guanhua Academy, a scholar known as the “Great Gentleman” personally handled this matter, collaborating with the two deputy ministers of the Ministry of Justice and the Ministry of Rites, traveling far and wide.

This scholar, known for his gentle demeanor and rigorous academic approach, was often praised, but his overly accommodating nature led to a perception of indecisiveness. However, during the accountability tour of the vassal lords of Great Li, he demonstrated a remarkably decisive and ruthless approach. He repeatedly appeared beside the monarchs, issuing stern warnings, especially one time where he bypassed the academy’s rules entirely and directly confronted the court officials, scolding them harshly, particularly targeting the noble and official scholars.

His words, which Lin Junbi learned of in the Shao Yuan Dynasty, were likely known throughout the entire Temple of Literature and the learning institutions.

“Reading is like eating excrement; during ordinary times, you’re allowed to be a corrupt Confucian. At this critical juncture, who dares to defile the sacred texts? If there’s one, I’ll hold them accountable! Which monarch dares to shield them? I’ll give up my title as a gentleman if I have to, just to knock you off your throne. Furthermore, I’ll relinquish my title as a sage to drive off another. I’d even give up my identity as a scholar to take on another monarch’s position.”

Due to the overwhelming stance displayed by this Great Gentleman, coupled with the strict enforcement of Great Li’s seemingly harsh laws, 

During this time, an old scholar suggested that at this perilous juncture, it might be better to set aside disputes and allow those individuals to make amends, which could benefit the larger situation.

The result for him was getting kicked down by a deputy minister of the Ministry of Justice who had been watching indifferently.

On the coastal battleground, the Great Li cavalry faced death first, while these pampered officials seemed entirely unconcerned.

Another deputy minister of the Ministry of Rites sneered at the scene, “Every official is adept at their role, but once in office, they forget how to be human.”

Within the court, the entire assembly of officials trembled in fear.

As for those celestial masters who shrank back in the face of crisis, the military orders from Great Li reached the halls of the various immortal sects. Those in charge of the law would lead the charge to enlist them into the ranks of Great Li’s military. If there was resistance, they would be executed on the spot. If they failed to capture them within a year, Great Li would hold the mountain tops accountable, allowing Great Li’s accompanying cultivators to take over.

One of the three Senior Supervisors of the Great Crossing, Liu Xunmei, along with the left deputy minister of the Ministry of Justice, was jointly responsible for this matter.

Lin Junbi suddenly said, “If the local civil and military officials of Great Li had another thirty years to digest the strength of the continent, it certainly wouldn’t be so hasty and laborious.”

Chao Pu nodded, then shook his head.

Lin Junbi understood and, with a complex expression, remarked, “Whether there is an embroidered tiger or not.”

Chao Pu took it a step further, “Having an embroidered tiger is certainly best. If not, as long as the scholarly lineage of accomplishments endures, Great Li's national strength can continue to ascend. Qi Jingchun has nurtured a significant number of visible and invisible scholarly talents in the Cliffs Academy for half the continent, while Cui Zhan has imparted and utilized accomplishments. This is the tacit understanding between Qi Jingchun and his senior brother, with both scholarly pursuits both restraining and complementing each other.”

Chao Pu pointed to the chessboard, “Junbi, share some subtle insights. Discuss those exquisite aspects that our Shao Yuan Dynasty wishes to achieve but cannot.”

Lin Junbi replied, “On the coastal frontlines, all strategic strongholds are divided into two armies within the Great Li cavalry. The rear army is relatively sparse, while the front takes the lead, sacrificing themselves to uplift morale and ensure the hearts of the soldiers. The rear oversees the middle army and other vassal forces.”

At this point, Lin Junbi sighed, “Often only a few thousand troops can oversee tens of thousands, which shows the might of the Great Li cavalry.”

Lin Junbi continued, discussing the reports from the celestial mountains, which could even be posted in the various vassal states of Baoping Continent, showcasing the astonishing control the Great Li Dynasty had over the cultivators of the continent.

A flying sword brought a message into the pavilion.

Chao Pu, holding the whisk with one hand, pinched the flying sword between two fingers, opened a letter sealed with purple clay from the mountains, and sighed heavily, “The Fuyun Continent could not be held. Zhou Zhenzhi has already perished in battle. Qi Tingji has begun to lead his team to retreat to the Golden Armor Continent, where he will continue to serve as the mainstay, but most likely can only strive to safeguard half of the Golden Armor Continent while awaiting reinforcements. How many of the scholarly seeds from the learning institutions will just vanish like this?”

Lin Junbi’s heart felt heavy.

Before this, there were also dire tidings; compared to the orderly retreat from the Fuyun Continent, many cultivators from there had fallen back to the Golden Armor Continent. The situation was even more dire for the Tongye Continent.

Taiping Mountain had been breached. Not a single cultivator survived there.

Having lost the Three Ranges and Four Symbols formation, the entire Fuyun Sect faced annihilation, with not a single person surviving.

The Great Fu Academy was personally assaulted by the great demon known as Zhou Mi, who used Confucian methods to suppress the academy.

This meant that the entire Tongye Continent was left with only two remaining flickers of human light, one deeply rooted in the Yu Gui Sect and the other defending against foes with the sword of the Tongye Sect.

Although the land of one continent had not entirely submerged, the fortune of the continent had largely fallen into the hands of the demon race.

Lin Junbi asked, “Teacher, what about the pure Confucian Chen family?”

Chao Pu felt even more sorrowful, as he hailed from the line of the Sub-Sage.

Moreover, the pure Confucian Chen Chunan from Nanshuo Continent was a pillar of the Sub-Sage lineage.

Chao Pu lamented, “Mr. Chen made the worst choice; when the world deemed he should die, he lived, and when he should have lived, he chose not to.”

Chao Pu stood up, gazing at the heavy snow falling outside the pavilion, murmuring, “What does it mean to die? In the eyes of the world, he became the first to die gloriously in battle for the righteous world’s ascension. What does it mean to live? The question of right and wrong; as long as Chen Chunan lives and guards Nanshuo Continent, there will be an opportunity to clarify why he chose not to die back then. Even if Mr. Chen says nothing, I, Chao Pu, and our Sub-Sage lineage will explain it for him.”

Lin Junbi rose, following his teacher, “But without Mr. Chen stationed in Nanshuo Continent, it cannot be held. Even with the mountain search map gifted by that White Mr., it still cannot protect the continent. The moment Mr. Chen chooses to abandon Nanshuo Continent for the sake of his reputation, it would seem like a grand gesture of martyrdom, but in reality, he would be the true culprit responsible for the downfall of the righteous world.”

Chao Pu stated, “As long as Mr. Chen does not leave Nanshuo Continent, all cultivators associated with Tongye Continent and Fuyun Continent will still harbor resentment towards him, even if they understand this reasoning. If this is human nature, it’s only natural, but there are countless people who only speak of grievances without understanding the reasoning behind them. Those who ascend the mountains to practice Dao only scratch the surface and cultivate strength without nurturing their hearts. The repercussions are endless.”

The old scholar’s expression grew somber, “It’s said that Zhou Mi, in the Great Fu Academy, mockingly remarked, ‘Since you Confucians are in power, why delegate authority to the secular monarchs? Knowing human hearts, why remain indifferent for thousands of years? What a good human nature is inherently good; it’s your Confucianism’s fault, so I’ll wield the demon-revealing mirror to show you all in the righteous world, whether it is truly filled with righteousness or, under the mirror, human nature’s good and evil may be fully exposed. If one Tongye Continent isn’t enough, then let’s see a few more continents.’”

This was not merely Zhou Mi’s outrageous rhetoric, as within Nanshuo Continent, how many were secretly whispering and pointing fingers at Chen Chunan?

With two continents fallen, only Nanshuo Continent remained unscathed.

And as for Tongye Continent and Fuyun Continent, if snow were to fall now, there were hardly any left to clear it away.

Chao Pu chuckled lightly, turning to Lin Junbi, “By the way, there’s at least one piece of good news: the young vassal king of Great Li in Old Dragon City has refused any cultivators from Tongye Continent to cross over. Not only that, this Song Mu has also issued a decree that any cultivator approaching within ten miles of Old Dragon City will be treated as enemies of Great Li. All Tongye Continent cultivators are not only barred from entering Old Dragon City but are, in fact, prohibited from stepping foot on any part of the coastal regions of Baoping Continent. If discovered, it’s immediate execution, regardless of identity.”

Lin Junbi exclaimed, “No wonder the embroidered tiger trusts this person to oversee the capital and guard Old Dragon City.”

Chao Pu continued, “But the bad news is that the focus of the demon race has always been on the line of Tongye Continent, Baoping Continent, North Julu Continent, and Ai Ai Continent. Prepare yourself; the first move of the Grandmaster of Tuo Yue Mountain in the righteous world will definitely target Baoping Continent. And it will surely be some grandiose plan beyond imagination.”

The old scholar glanced at the sky.

He fell silent for a moment, deliberately or inadvertently stating, “Junbi, to turn the tide when it has already fallen is a feat; to mend the mountains and rivers is another. To forge deep friendships with upright gentlemen and pure individuals is essential, but one must also learn to navigate through the scheming and lowly people; only then can you truly accomplish something substantial. Otherwise, at most, you’ll remain a mere academic, a teacher, or a distinguished scholar, which is not enough.”

Lin Junbi bowed, “Teacher’s teachings, I am grateful. For now, it’s hard to prevent the heavens from tilting; I wish to be a craftsman mending the heavens.”

Chao Pu nodded.

Now, as the snow grew heavier, it already felt like a bone-chilling wind, but once it melted, the roads would become even muddier.

The time of snowmelt is the coldest, revealing the hearts of men.

Suddenly, the old scholar asked, “That Hidden Official, what kind of person is he?”

Lin Junbi pondered for a moment before answering, “A good person, quite intelligent.”

Chao Pu muttered to himself, “With Qi Jingchun gone, the Left is trapped in the Tongye Sect, and Cui Zhan is stationed at Baoping Continent, while the closed-door disciple remains at the Sword Qi Great Wall. The old scholar is truly... generous.”

Lin Junbi couldn’t help but interject, “Chen Pingan once said that true feats can be seen everywhere in the world; the light of human kindness is always within reach, depending on whether we are willing to open our eyes to see the world.”

Chao Pu laughed, “In a snowy night, a traveler far from home, even a flicker of light can soothe the heart. On the journey of life, indeed, every little light we see, even amidst the darkness of the world, will brighten the heart.”

The old scholar suggested naming the fifth realm the Righteous World, but the Central Earth Temple of Literature did not agree, and this matter remained unresolved.

Chao Pu suddenly burst into laughter, “Well, if we don’t discuss good and evil in terms of human nature, but rather focus on good people and kind hearts, allowing the Confucian lineage to exert more strength in education, this statement clearly comes from you, aimed at our Sub-Sage lineage scholars.”

Lin Junbi felt a bit anxious.

Another flying sword message arrived.

After reading the secret letter, Chao Pu fell into a daze.

Lin Junbi softly called out, “Teacher?”

Chao Pu snapped back to reality and said, “Within our lineage, a moral essay has been specifically written to explain what pure Confucianism is.”

Lin Junbi’s expression darkened, “Is it incited by someone behind the scenes, or is it from the heart?”

Chao Pu tossed the letter aside, smashing it with his whisk, and scoffed, “It’s truly foolish.”

Lin Junbi rubbed his face vigorously.

The old scholar self-deprecatingly said, “I suddenly envy Cui Zhan a little.”

---

The sword cultivators, aside from the central Ascension City, under the leadership of the Criminal Officer lineage, worked alongside commoners to open up eight spiritual peaks brimming with aura around the city. They engaged in large-scale construction, either building residences on the mountains or establishing cities by the water, continuously crafting various formations and secretly placing suppressive items.

This essentially created an alternative barrier covering a thousand miles.

This would be the first layer of the Ascension City’s geographical realm, and it would naturally continue to expand outward.

A sword cultivator traveling afar became the first visitor to Ascension City.

In fact, he wasn’t exactly a guest in the true sense, but more like half a family member.

This was Deng Liang from Ai Ai Continent, a former sword cultivator of the Hidden Official lineage of the Sword Qi Great Wall, who had spent several years in the Summer Palace, naturally familiar with Xu Ning and Guo Zhujiu.

Upon leaving the Upside-Down Mountain, Deng Liang, as a bottleneck sword cultivator at the Nascent Soul stage, received a personal letter from a young Hidden Official.

His sect quickly began operations in secret to facilitate Deng Liang’s entrance into the fifth realm, where he would seek opportunities for breakthrough, which would bring extra blessings. This was beneficial for both Deng Liang and his sect.

In the letter, the young Hidden Official advised Deng Liang that if he could persuade the sect's Patriarchs to allow him to enter the new realm, it would be best to go to Tongye Continent rather than Nanshuo or Fuyun Continent, but he must not speak of this to the sect. 

Ultimately, at the end of the second year of Jia Chun, everything was in place, and Deng Liang chose to embark on a journey through North Julu Continent, Baoping Continent, and Tongye Continent. He purposefully passed by the Taihui Sword Sect on the soaring peak of North Julu, the Floating Duck Sword Lake in the central region, and the Falling Down Mountain and Wind and Snow Temple in Baoping Continent, without making any visits.

Even though his sect had already communicated with a learning institution in the Temple of Literature to secure a significant pass, Deng Liang still harbored concerns about unexpected events, fearing that Tongye Continent, with its vastness, would be filled with muddled minds. In truth, his fundamental issue was that he had an exceedingly poor impression of Tongye Continent and held a similar view of the three academies there. Deng Liang had even prepared himself to be turned away.

Deng Liang arrived at the gates of Tongye Continent at the turn of spring and summer in the third year of Jia Chun. He then changed his mind and stayed for nearly three years, guarding the gates alongside his seniors and fellow sword cultivators until the very last moment before the gates were about to close, when he finally entered the fifth realm.

He then rode his sword toward Ascension City.

On the way, thanks to the battles he fought alongside his seniors at the gates for three years, he accumulated sword intent. With the guidance of his seniors, he finally reached the Jade Purity stage in the new realm.

Just southeast of Ascension City, Deng Liang encountered the leader of the Criminal Officer lineage, Qi Shou, who had also achieved the Jade Purity stage.

Qi Shou appeared pleasantly surprised at Deng Liang's arrival and welcomed him warmly, taking him on a tour of Purple Mansion Mountain. They visited an ancient stone tablet, now designated as a forbidden area, inscribed with two lines of ancient script: “Six Caves, Danxia Xuan Shu, Three Pure Purple Mansion Green Chapters.” 

Qi Shou had nothing to hide from Deng Liang, candidly stating that at the foot of the mountain, they had unearthed an ancient jade box, but they were currently unable to open it. They were too afraid to act hastily, worried that a single misstep might trigger ancient prohibitions and lead to the destruction of both the box and its contents.

Even though Deng Liang hailed from the old Hidden Official lineage, he genuinely appreciated Qi Shou’s sincerity, as they had once collaborated on the battlefield, displaying remarkable synergy. In fact, Qi Shou had a mediocre impression of the younger outsiders like Cao Gun and Xuan Can, but he felt a special affinity with Deng Liang.

Upon reaching Purple Mansion Mountain, Deng Liang wasn’t in a hurry to enter Ascension City.

After all, he would not be able to leave this new realm without reopening the gates in a hundred years.

Deng Liang was not foolish enough to think he could break through to the Ascendant stage within a hundred years.

Fortunately, there was a year name.

It was said that the timing and weight were still subjects of uncertainty.

Upon hearing this, Qi Shou was slightly taken aback, clearly not fully grasping the significance of these two matters.

Deng Liang didn’t conceal his thoughts, directly explaining to Qi Shou why these two matters should not be underestimated; one pertained to the manifestation of a certain Great Dao linked to seasons and historical laws, while the other determined the measurement and calculation of the weight of all things in the world.

As for the currents swirling within Ascension City involving the Criminal Officer, Hidden Official, and Treasury lineages, Deng Liang pondered briefly and could roughly guess the general situation.

After all, when it came to sect affairs and the proliferation of mountains, the scholars of the righteous world were far more familiar than those from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Deng Liang would not actively involve himself in these matters.

Thus, Deng Liang followed Qi Shou into Ascension City, but he did not resume his identity as a sword cultivator of the Hidden Official lineage; instead, he became the first named offering in the history of Ascension City.

He then met Dong Budu, a girl who made Deng Liang realize he was destined to seek without obtaining.

Dong Budu had just returned to Ascension City and had gone to the Shattered Peaks Tavern for a drink. As Deng Liang walked down the familiar street, he noticed the tavern was without the head and second head of the establishment. Business was still decent, but the acting manager had become a hunchbacked outsider, who was currently sharing a table with Dong Budu, drinking together. Luo Zhenyi and Guo Zhujiu were also there, each occupying a long bench. The manager, whose surname was Zheng, was all smiles as he rambled about the customs of Baoping Continent.

As Deng Liang took a seat, the man was just talking about the Pearly Jewel Cave and the young Hidden Official’s past.

No one was particularly polite to Deng Liang; after a brief greeting, the small talk faded. Deng Liang mentioned that he had finally broken through, receiving a congratulatory remark from Luo Zhenyi, while Guo Zhujiu applauded. Dong Budu didn’t even bother to say anything.

Deng Liang, on the other hand, enjoyed this familiar atmosphere, as it did not make him feel like an outsider.

Guo Zhujiu continued to help Zheng Dafeng pour drinks.

Zheng Dafeng continued recounting a little story about how Chen Pingan earned a copper coin by sending a letter.

Dong Budu was there to drink away her sorrows, casually listening to Zheng Dafeng’s ramblings, while Guo Zhujiu insisted on getting more stories about her master.

As for Luo Zhenyi, she simply listened and occasionally took sips of her drink, remaining silent.

Guo Zhujiu listened intently as Zheng Dafeng shared about her master, recalling how he used to rush through Fulu Street, Peach Leaf Alley, and Zhalan Gate every day, and that was where he first encountered Ning Yao.

As for the handsome and charming Zheng manager, he was certainly a witness to the events.

Guo Zhujiu felt as if she was hearing the most wonderful story in the world, exclaiming, “No need to think; my master must have recognized my master as soon as he saw her!”

These were tales that her master had never spoken about, nor had her master ever mentioned.

Zheng Dafeng nodded, “Yes, yes! At that time, your master was already quite astute, knowing early on the difference between women who trained in martial arts and those who didn’t. He left me stunned for days trying to figure it out. It’s not surprising; a poor child learns quickly.”

Guo Zhujiu tilted her head, frowning, thinking that Zheng manager's words didn’t quite add up.

Luo Zhenyi was slightly surprised, lowering her head to sip her drink, but still said nothing.

Zheng Dafeng cleared his throat and continued, “Let me tell you about the Mud Bottle Alley. It’s truly a place of good fortune. Aside from our Falling Down Mountain’s master, there’s also a ruffian called Gu Can, and a sword immortal named Cao Xi. The ancestral homes of the three families are all clustered in that one alley.” 

At this point, Zheng Dafeng felt a little awkward, knowing that discussing this in the righteous world could be intimidating. However, discussing it with sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall was rather pointless.

Guo Zhujiu leaned on the table and suddenly said, “My master has spent all those years wandering around Mud Bottle Alley, leaving the ancestral home alone, and returning home alone. Wouldn’t he be very lonely?”

Zheng Dafeng rubbed his chin and nodded, “Probably a little lonely. Anyway, every time your master returns home from a long journey, he always goes to sit for a while at the ancestral home in Mud Bottle Alley.”

Guo Zhujiu whispered, “Zheng manager, what did my master look like when he was young? I can’t even imagine. I can’t even imagine what he was like as a child.”

Zheng Dafeng laughed, “He was dark and thin from the sun and wind, not very tall, so he was quite inconspicuous. When he was even younger… aside from wearing straw sandals, he probably looked about the same.”

Guo Zhujiu scratched her head, continuing to lean on the table, staring at the white wine bowl before her, “I always thought my master just poofed into a young man, and then poofed again into the master I know.”

Zheng Dafeng took a sip of his drink and fell silent.

Deng Liang suddenly said, “Someone recently selected a list of the ten youngest individuals across the realms, and the unnamed ‘Hidden Official’ was ranked eleventh. At the very least, it shows that the Hidden Official is still at the Sword Qi Great Wall and has reached the pinnacle of martial arts, becoming a Golden Core sword cultivator.”

Guo Zhujiu sat up straight, “Really?!”

Deng Liang nodded, smiling, “Absolutely true.”

Deng Liang glanced at Luo Zhenyi.

Dong Budu shot a glare at Deng Liang, who was not being sincere.

Deng Liang poured himself a bowl of wine as punishment, resulting in Luo Zhenyi giving him an unhappy look.

Deng Liang had to change the subject, asking, “Has Sword Immortal Ning not returned to the city yet?”

Guo Zhujiu sighed, “What can she do? My master’s wife must miss my master more than anyone else, but she can’t bear to drink away her sorrows in front of us, so she runs off alone, far away, where no one can see her, desperately missing my master. Sigh, if only my master’s wife had brought me along, I could have lent her my sleeve to wipe away her tears…”

Just then, Guo Zhujiu’s head was suddenly pressed down, her forehead touching the table. 

As her head pressed against the table, Guo Zhujiu could only laugh and then murmur, “Master’s wife… why did you come back and not explode a series of thunderclaps in the sky riding a sword? I didn’t even have the chance to announce to the world that our master’s wife is the only immortal in this realm…”

Ning Yao pressed down twice forcefully, causing Guo Zhujiu’s small head to thud on the table, and only then did she release her grip. Before taking her seat, she called out to Zheng Dafeng, “Uncle Zheng,” and then greeted Deng Liang.

This was the first time Zheng Dafeng had seen Ning Yao since their parting at Pearly Jewel Cave. The young lady was no longer a young girl after many years; she had now become a stunning immortal.

Zheng Dafeng laughed, “Ning Yao, rest assured, at least in this Falling Down Mountain, where I have watched over for many years, Chen Pingan has never harbored any ill thoughts toward anyone.”

Ning Yao smiled and paid no mind.

Guo Zhujiu sat next to Ning Yao, raising her hand and whispering, “Master’s wife, before you came, I calculated that my master must have already reached the pinnacle of martial arts and is about to become a Jade Purity sword cultivator.”

Deng Liang felt a bit helpless; if only Gu Jianlong, Cao Gun, and Xuan Can were here, then it wouldn’t be just Jade Purity; the Ascendant stage would also be within the grasp of the Hidden Official.

In this fifth realm, despite the gates of Fuyun Continent and Tongye Continent being closed, chaos still reigned. Remarkable people and odd occurrences were countless.

The son of the cave master of Tianyu Cave, Shu Nan Yuyan, after suffering from heat stroke, built a transcendent platform and met a black-clad scholar who visited, finding a kindred spirit.

The latter was named Chen Wen, hailing from North Julu Continent, yet he was not a sword cultivator.

Then there was a practicing Qi cultivator named Yang Hengxing, who excelled in talismans and had a terrible temper, constantly clashing with the cultivators from Tongye Continent. As a result, he drew the wrath of many and was hunted down by nearly a hundred practicing Qi cultivators. Unexpectedly, he quietly ascended to the Nascent Soul stage and the far-travel stage, turning the tables and killing more than half of his pursuers.

It was also rumored that a female sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall had flown south alone, coming extremely close to the southern gate and slashing several people.

Meanwhile, someone from the Central Earth Dynasty set out on a journey and happened to pass by the Wish Bridge.

In the night, a figure in white, reading alone on the bridge, Xu Bai stood there, gazing at the bright moon atop the mountain across the way, where a horseman rode along the ridge.

Xu Bai focused his gaze and saw a woman in red riding a white horse, a narrow blade and a wine gourd hanging at her waist, as if she were riding into the moon.

In the Lei Gong Temple of the Ma Lake in Ai Ai Continent,

Pei Qian, at the eighth realm, delivered an unnamed punch equivalent to the completion of the ninth realm.

Liu Suiyu, at the pinnacle of the ninth realm, countered with a punch from the tenth realm.

They exchanged blows.

Pei Qian’s punch served both to question and to receive the blow, sliding back several dozen feet. Although she was drenched in blood and her body shook several times, she still gathered her breath, causing her feet to sink into the ground several inches, before she finally fainted yet remained standing.

Liu Suiyu was sent crashing through the outer wall of the Lei Gong Temple, stumbling within and spitting out a mouthful of blood.

Pei Ah Xiang quietly murmured, “Another one with the surname Pei.”

Pei Qian woke up three days later and spent more than a month recuperating in the Lei Gong Temple.

During this time, she paid no attention to the stranger named Liu Youzhou and merely inquired about matters related to the Sword Qi Great Wall with Aunt Xie and the students Ju Xing and Zhao Mu.

For example, she asked what her master had done and said after she left the Sword Qi Great Wall and he took on the title of Hidden Official.

She also asked Aunt Xie whether it was difficult to become a Golden Core sword cultivator.

Ultimately, before leaving, Pei Qian took a trip outside, crafting an ordinary material book box and a bamboo staff as parting gifts for Ju Xing and Zhao Mu.

Since they referred to her as Sister Pei and she was over ten years their senior, she was essentially half an elder.

First, she thanked and bid farewell to the two predecessors, Pei Ah Xiang and Liu Suiyu, before loading the new bamboo box on her back. She held the hiking staff and said her goodbyes to Aunt Xie and the three students outside the Lei Gong Temple.

She bent down, smiling at the two sword cultivator seedlings, “Practice your sword well, read more, travel more, and try to stay together and leave less.”

Ju Xing, with the new bamboo box on his back, nodded vigorously, “Sister Pei, wait for me! Next time we meet, I’ll definitely be two realms higher than someone!”

Zhao Mu clutched the hiking staff tightly, nodding as if pecking at rice, “Sister Pei, we’ll visit Falling Down Mountain in the future, and you must be home!”

Pei Qian smiled, stood up straight, and patted the heads of the two children, “As long as you have your master by your side, there’s no need to rush to grow up.”

Aunt Xie asked the two disciples to stay, and she escorted Pei Qian partway.

Ju Xing and Zhao Mu looked on from a distance, wondering if Sister Pei had grown a little taller?

Liu Youzhou sat on the outer steps, lost in thought, not paying attention to the Lei Gong Temple.

He took out a snowflake coin, holding it high; it was indeed beautiful. 

In the distance, Pei Qian merely looked down at the ground, softly saying, “My master once told me in our hometown that his ability to take care of himself is no boast; it’s rare in the world, and my master is not lying.”

Aunt Xie had no words to respond.

Pei Qian hurried away, then smiled and walked backward, waving goodbye to Aunt Xie.

Aunt Xie smiled, “Be careful on the road, take care of yourself.”

Pei Qian turned back around and quickened her pace, executing a six-step stance before suddenly lifting off the ground, riding the wind to travel across the heavens.

Liu Youzhou looked up; the snowflake coin was beautiful, and the moonlight tonight was also beautiful.

In the Righteous World, 

The old scholar revealed himself in the northern part of the Fuyun Continent, shouting with his heart, “Hey, hey, hey, Brother Bai, are you there? Answer me! Damn it, there’s someone asking if you have an immortal sword in hand; if it were me, I absolutely couldn’t tolerate it!”

Daoist Sun unexpectedly returned to the gate where the two realms met, proclaiming loudly, “What sword? Just take it!”

Thus, a scholar, originally guarding the peach blossoms and the grass hall, easily cleaved through the sky with a sword and re-entered the Righteous World’s Fuyun Continent, looking at a great demon on the throne as the scholar calmly said, “Alright. Bai has arrived.”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 827: The Fourteen Realms

By the cliffs of the half-completed Sword Qi Great Wall, a figure in a gray robe fluttered in the wind.

Liu Bai had come here to bid farewell to her senior, the Dragon Lord. She had just stepped into the Nascent Soul realm and had received two pure sword intents as gifts.

Most of the over ninety aspiring sword immortals from the Tuo Yue Mountain had already broken through or obtained a portion of sword intent, allowing them to leave the city wall one after another, riding their swords towards the vast world, heading for the battlefield of the Three Continents.

These strands of pure sword intent, drifting between heaven and earth for a hundred, a thousand, or even ten thousand years, were impartial. As long as one's sword heart was clear, those who resonated with them would be recognized as sword cultivators by the world and would gain an opportunity—a pure inheritance devoid of any so-called incense or master-disciple relationship.

There was only one type of existence that could never attract the favor of sword intent, regardless of talent or aptitude.

For example, Sha Yue, one of the ten outstanding youths of the Wild World, and the girl nicknamed Doukou.

Liu Bai spoke softly, “Dragon Lord, I am about to leave for Tongye Continent to follow my master and senior brother. Is there anything you would like me to convey to him?”

The wind howled atop the city walls, but the figure in the gray robe remained silent.

Liu Bai did not dare to rush this unpredictable senior. She was in no hurry to leave the city walls, so she gazed across the cliff, but could not see the figure in the bright red robe.

Under the command of the Jiazi banner, a powerful mountain-water barrier had been set up against the half-completed Sword Qi Great Wall, thoroughly isolating the two realms. Liu Bai could see the scenery on the other side clearly, while the opposing city wall was shrouded in thick fog.

The Dragon Lord beside her was indeed too enigmatic. As one of the three old sword immortals who had sought swords at Tuo Yue Mountain a thousand years ago, he had once been a close friend of Chen Qingdu, and they had once swung their swords together on the vast expanse of the earth, seeking swords in the heavens. After becoming a convict, he ultimately became a puppet of Tuo Yue Mountain alongside Guan Zhao. However, unlike the scattered soul and confused mind of Guan Zhao, the Dragon Lord had willingly abandoned his physical form, even allowing the White Crystal Throne to crush his head. On the battlefield, he had slain the last sword immortal of his lineage, Gao Kui.

Gao Kui sought the sword, while the Dragon Lord wielded it; that was all.

In the end, he was personally severed from the last ember of the sword path by the elder.

Liu Bai truly did not understand the thoughts and actions of the Dragon Lord.

In fact, Liu Bai could not even fathom Li Zhen, who still remained on the city wall, seemingly determined to clash head-on with that young hidden official.

As each aspiring sword immortal from Tuo Yue Mountain achieved their own successes, the flow of sword fortune naturally made the half-completed Sword Qi Great Wall thinner and thinner, placing that guy’s situation increasingly in jeopardy. For the stability of the half-completed Sword Qi Great Wall was closely related to the sword path’s fortune; surely that young hidden official, who resonated with the half-completed Great Wall, would sense this clearer and more acutely than anyone else.

The ordinary folk below, muddled and ignorant of their fate and longevity, were blissfully unaware of their approaching old age or when their time might come.

However, that young hidden official, like someone staring intently at a longevity lamp in the ancestral hall every day, could only watch helplessly as its flame dimmed with each passing day.

The Dragon Lord finally spoke, “Tell your master to summon Liu Cha back here to exert his full strength in swordplay. Within a year at the latest, we must force that kid into the Jade Pure realm. Delay, and there will be changes.”

Liu Bai was taken aback, unsure why the Dragon Lord insisted on that person reaching the Jade Pure realm. Could it be? No, she must not let that person’s words influence her state of mind; the Dragon Lord could not possibly be connected to him.

Thus, with doubts in her heart, she asked directly, “Dragon Lord, why is that? Please enlighten me!”

The Dragon Lord smiled and explained, “For Chen Ping’an, breaking the Golden Core and forming the Nascent Soul is merely a matter of course. Becoming a Nascent Soul sword cultivator is not easy, yet not too difficult either; he just needs some time for refinement. He is not the slightest bit anxious about raising his Qi Refining realm. Instead, he is more focused on how to enhance his fist intent. This is perhaps what that little mad dog considers urgent. After all, cultivation relies on oneself; he has always been like climbing a mountain, yet when it comes to practicing his fists, he is unwavering—how could he not feel anxious? In the vast world, martial artists at the summit realm are indeed impressive, but is that enough here?”

Liu Bai felt dizzy and stammered, “Didn’t he say he was about to reach the Jade Pure realm?”

“What you believe is what you believe,” the Dragon Lord scoffed. “The truth is he was just trying to scare you and Li Zhen. I originally intended to say he was about to reach the Nascent Soul realm, but seeing you all take it seriously, I didn’t bother to clarify.”

Liu Bai let out a soft sigh.

The Dragon Lord looked across, “Isn’t it hard to discern this kid’s temperament? Everything he sees in his eyes, regardless of distance or difficulty, as long as he sets his mind to it and there’s a path to follow, he won’t feel the slightest bit anxious; he merely works quietly, step by step, making it seem easily attainable. But don’t forget, what he is worst at is creating something out of nothing, relying solely on himself to find that ‘one’. He has the least confidence in this.”

At this point, the Dragon Lord smiled and asked, “Do you doubt this?”

Liu Bai was at a loss for words.

The Dragon Lord’s words left her feeling both convinced and doubtful.

The Dragon Lord helplessly said, “It seems he truly has frightened you with those two life-bound flying swords of his. Let me ask you, is a young martial artist at the ninth level, who has become a hidden official as a foreigner and is a clever person capable of commanding respect, ever able to comprehend a true punch belonging to himself? Has he? No.”

Liu Bai suddenly understood and nodded gently.

The Dragon Lord continued, “Every action is within the rules; you all have forgotten his other identity—he is a scholar. Self-reflection, self-restraint, and caution are all part of his cultivation, but they also bind him heavily.”

Therefore, the more so, the less he should have the chance to truly comprehend a punch. That would mean the young hidden official, who had focused on refining his heart, could potentially draw outlines for the world with his own strength. Especially, he must not truly understand a sword. Generally speaking, if something is unfair, it will resonate; this young man has enough pent-up emotions: anger, killing intent, resentment, and sorrow...

When he eventually consolidates all this, his sword may very well change the colors of heaven and earth.

At this point, the Dragon Lord condensed countless strands of fine sword qi, forming a blurry figure, reminiscent of how Chen Ping’an first appeared at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The Dragon Lord extended a hand to disperse the mountain-water barrier and continued, “If he wishes to cultivate his heart step by step, then we must force him to take shortcuts, to act irrationally. Even if he becomes a Nascent Soul sword cultivator, it will still be difficult for him to enter the Jade Pure realm in haste. In a rush, he will likely have to use a shortcut secret method that incurs a loss in the height of his path as a price, compelling him to drink poison to quench his thirst. Once he enters the Jade Pure realm, he will completely share the fate of the remaining half of the Sword Qi Great Wall, truly becoming the second Chen Qingdu.”

Liu Bai glanced at the opposing cliff, finding no sign of that person, and tentatively asked, “Is it really that difficult to leave the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

“That’s why you all worry about him reaching the Jade Pure realm; in fact, he fears it even more,” the Dragon Lord nodded. “If he cannot reach the Jade Pure realm and is stuck at the pitiful level of a true Nascent Soul or a pseudo-Jade Pure, continuing to cling to the city walls would be better. With Liu Cha’s sword strike, the opposing city wall would be split in two again, and he would be injured at the root of his path, left half-alive. Even if Liu Cha strikes several more times, he wouldn’t die, but his cultivation path would be utterly ruined. The sword path would lead to a dead end before the martial path, and his resonance with the Sword Qi Great Wall would become meaningless. Even if he reached the tenth level of martial arts, what good would it do? He would merely be waiting to be slaughtered, sitting there and waiting for death. Sooner or later, whether it be me, or you returning to this place, or Shou Chen, Fei Ran, whoever strikes, it will be the same. Every sword will damage the root of his path.”

When others ascend the city, they are merely visiting a grave; within the grave mound, there is a living person, but in truth, they are no different from the dead.

Liu Bai seemed to see the light at the end of a tunnel, as if she had suddenly found clarity.

The only eyesore was that after the Dragon Lord deliberately opened the barrier, that figure in the bright red robe seemed to arrive as promised. She saw him holding a narrow blade, lightly tapping it on his shoulder as he slowly approached, ultimately standing across from the cliff.

With the narrow blade resting on his shoulder, they stood in opposition.

Although Liu Bai had just stepped into the Nascent Soul realm, she felt no joy; instead, she was filled with deep concern, even more so than if she had fallen from grace.

As a former prominent figure among the hundred sword immortals of Tuo Yue Mountain, unexpectedly stepping into the upper fifth realm of sword immortals due to a siege had suddenly become a burden. Until she truly stepped into the Jade Pure realm, Liu Bai would find it hard to let go. Especially when she thought about how to break through the Nascent Soul bottleneck in the future, she would have to face that inner demon, making her achievement in the Nascent Soul realm feel like a step closer to that person. The horror of the inner demon lay in the profound truth that the higher the path, the stronger the demon. Talent, law, realm, and even disposition seemed like clouds drifting in the sky; how could she ever surpass the solid rock that was that inner demon?

Many who had reached the upper fifth realm could conquer their inner demons primarily because they were initially unaware of what the inner demon was. Accepting it as it came made it easier to break through the bottleneck.

But if, when facing her inner demon, that young hidden official had already perished, Liu Bai would rather that inner demon be Chen Ping’an.

Because then, deep down, she could maintain a sliver of clarity, knowing that the inner demon was a thing of the past.

After hearing the Dragon Lord’s words today, Liu Bai’s heart steadied. She looked at the person across from her and smiled, “Please convey my farewell to the Hidden Official. I hope we can meet again.”

With this certainty in her heart, Liu Bai felt her sword heart grow even clearer, making her eager for the originally lopsided sword contest to come.

That person wore a smile, unexpectedly remaining silent, refraining from speaking to disturb her resolve.

Liu Bai could see that the other party had not been well these past few years. After finally stepping into the summit realm, their appearance had stabilized, yet they grew more haggard by the day.

For someone who had long resided in the mountains, unaware of the seasons, sleeping for years or even decades, like a dead dragon lying in a deep pond, or a statue seated in a temple, it was not surprising.

Take the Fire Dragon Zhenren from the Bei Ju Lu Continent, who was famously known for his deep slumber, draped in snow as clothing.

And the newly ranked one of the ten outstanding youths, the dream traveler from Liu Xia Continent, was likely also a fellow practitioner of the Fire Dragon Zhenren.

Or perhaps one who sat in forgetfulness, diligently cultivating for years, only pausing for a brief moment to nourish their soul. Such brief rests were significant, resonating with the concept of “great death of the human body,” and were greatly esteemed in mountain cultivation as a method of deep sleep, allowing one to be free of all delusions. Thus, compared to the most ordinary night’s sleep of mundane people, this method was more beneficial for nurturing the three souls and seven spirits, providing a sweeter experience for Qi Refiners.

The gaze from above, the intention of sitting in meditation, indicated a state of tranquility without dreams, which was a sign of a Qi Refiner stepping into the middle fifth realm.

However, a Qi Refiner remaining awake for seven years, perpetually caught in overthinking, was rare and would naturally harm their spirit. 

Thus, despite having a realm, their mind gradually withered.

Chen Ping’an smiled and asked, “Dragon Lord, I just can’t understand. Did I ever kick you in the alley or stop you from stealing bones from Li Zhen? Why are you two so intent on biting me?”

The Dragon Lord chuckled, “Though only half of the Sword Qi Great Wall remains, that old bone of Chen Qingdu is indeed a bit hard to chew. You've endured all these years, and it’s something to be proud of.”

Chen Ping’an shifted his gaze and said to Liu Bai, “Aren’t you leaving? Even if I pity you, there’s a limit.”

Liu Bai’s gaze hardened, “Today, when we part, it might well be a farewell of life and death. So you might as well say more; after all, when I confront my inner demon, it won’t truly be the Chen Ping’an anymore.”

Chen Ping’an waved his hand, “I advise you to take the hint and leave quickly, while I’m still in a good mood.”

Liu Bai stood firm, her figure unwavering.

The Dragon Lord mocked, “Just by comprehending a shallow view of the white bones, to wash away your heart’s resentment, and your mood improves a little? Zen flavor cannot be clung to; still waters do not hide dragons. Zen meditation is not about being still at set times; you are still far from it. Let’s be frank, the white bone view for you is genuinely a side door; no matter how long you comprehend it, you won’t achieve anything. Even if you see yourself transform into the purest white bone, your thoughts collapse, from broken to complete, from white bones to flesh, eventually glowing and shimmering, yet your spirit remains outwardly focused, your mind filled with nothing but a mix of white bones—what a pity that it ultimately does not align with your path. Is it just that the book says those who died wrongfully at Qingtong Lake are merely white bones?”

At this point, the Dragon Lord glanced at Chen Ping’an, gently shaking his head in disbelief, “If you want to deceive yourself, scattering countless thoughts on top of the white bones to force yourself to rest for a moment, you should obediently hide away and not come here seeking humiliation.”

In truth, Chen Ping’an would never go too far down the path of the white bone view. As the Dragon Lord stated, it was merely a clever method to temporarily take a “little nap.” Therefore, even if Chen Ping’an did not come today, the Dragon Lord would still have made his point, never allowing him the slightest opportunity for soul nourishment.

Chen Ping’an slightly furrowed his brow before breaking into a casual smile, holding his sword and pointing it at the blurry old man within the gray robe, “Dragon Lord, you have such profound laws; how can I thank you for guiding me to avoid going astray? Your years of hard work in safeguarding the path have truly fortified my resolve. If it weren’t for your appearance, I might have mistaken you for the left protector from my hometown, Qilong Alley.”

The Dragon Lord laughed, “When one is about to die, their words are kind. You, on the other hand, act contrary to that.”

Chen Ping’an turned his head again, curious, “You’re really not leaving? Do you truly believe standing still and looking at me is sharpening your path and sword intent?”

Liu Bai glanced at that young man and couldn’t help but feel a pang of sympathy, “You’re truly pitiful.”

Chen Ping’an squinted and smiled.

The Dragon Lord suddenly unleashed a surge of sword qi, cutting off the connection between heaven and earth, preventing Chen Ping’an’s words from reaching Liu Bai’s ears, even blocking her from getting another glance at him.

With the Dragon Lord’s sword qi suppression gone, the mountain-water barrier that concealed the half-completed Sword Qi Great Wall closed once more.

Liu Bai found her vision blurred, unable to see anything on the other side. She was stunned for a moment, “Dragon Lord, why is this?”

The Dragon Lord replied, “You only need to understand one thing: his earlier suggestion for you to take the hint was correct. Moreover, his statement was a setup for the final line; otherwise, if he spoke, and you heard it, it could cause your inner demon to surge.”

Liu Bai shook her head, “I don’t believe that!”

The figure of the old man, composed of intertwining sword qi, gradually dissipated, transforming back into an empty gray robe. The Dragon Lord earnestly said, “Enough. There’s no need to lower yourself to the level of a mad dog. Practice your sword well in the future. If you can truly cut down the inner demon manifested by that person, it will greatly benefit you. Through calamity comes fortune; your path may very well surpass what it was before.”

Though Liu Bai did not fully understand the implications, she was filled with curiosity about Chen Ping’an's words. Yet, she would not defy the Dragon Lord’s teachings and dared not treat her sword path lightly by engaging in a pointless rivalry with Chen Ping’an. She promptly mounted her sword and left the city wall.

After Liu Bai departed, Li Zhen, who had been standing not far away, approached the Dragon Lord.

Li Zhen complained, “You treat that little girl Liu Bai much better than you do me.”

The Dragon Lord merely turned to gaze at the remnants of the northern city.

A thousand years ago, the convict who had moved here with a guilty conscience; everything came from nothing.

Li Zhen asked, “Why are you so hostile toward Chen Ping’an?”

The Dragon Lord replied indifferently, “What enmity could a young man have with me? It’s just that anyone who wishes to become the second Chen Qingdu must die.”

Li Zhen then asked, “Although I am not Guan Zhao, I know that Guan Zhao is merely disappointment. Why are you so?”

The mentality of Guan Zhao is somewhat akin to that of the old blind man among the ten thousand mountains; sword immortals like Zhang Lu are likely the same. They share the same mentality toward the new and old worlds of the vast realm.

The Dragon Lord withdrew his gaze, remaining silent.

Li Zhen asked, “Has our Hidden Official truly not reached the Nascent Soul realm yet and is still a broken Golden Core?”

The Dragon Lord couldn’t be bothered to respond.

Li Zhen muttered to himself, “It’s not surprising that Liu Bai genuinely feels pity for him.”

The world was desolate, and alone, how could the sunlight and moonlight not be far behind?

Occasionally, birds flew toward the city wall, swiftly passing through the mountain-water formation. If the sun and moon were unseen, there would be no distinction of day and night, let alone the change of seasons.

Reborn, spirit condensed, with a body outside the body, this is the Yang Spirit, which delights in light; it is the best dwelling place for the Golden Core. 

A single spark of spirit, emerging from obscurity and entering the nether, is the Yin Spirit, which delights in nocturnal wanderings; it is the place for the Nascent Soul to cultivate during waking and sleeping.

Chen Ping’an’s resonance with the Sword Qi Great Wall came at a great cost.

The three had long since fused into one; otherwise, he could not bear the weight of that great demon’s true name, nor could he truly resonate with the Sword Qi Great Wall. From now on, the young hidden official would be destined to have no more opportunities for his Yin Spirit to venture out, and as for the Confucian sage’s life-bound character, that was utterly impossible.

Li Zhen laughed, “Liu Bai may be a bit foolish, but a little foolishness is good; her future inner demon won’t be too tightly knotted and unsolvable.”

The Dragon Lord decisively severing the connection to the world was equivalent to saving Liu Bai’s life.

Otherwise, that hidden official only needed to say a single word to potentially cost Liu Bai half her life.

It was simple; a single “Why do you like me?” could lead to Liu Bai’s heart collapsing significantly.

As to whether Liu Bai truly liked him, it mattered not; that was precisely the most troublesome point.

After all, disliking someone in this world is merely inconsequential, but liking someone can take on a thousand forms, with countless reasons.

The Dragon Lord suddenly isolated a small realm that was not easy to notice with sword qi, asking, “What exactly did you see?”

Li Zhen countered, “What are you talking about?”

The Dragon Lord said gravely, “Your life-bound flying sword is called ‘Time’.”

Li Zhen smiled, “So what? Are you not clearer than anyone else that I am probably the most idle sword cultivator in the world, at least one of them? With my current level, what can I see, and what can I do?”

Li Zhen shook his head to himself, self-mockingly declaring, “I haven’t seen anything; I haven’t done anything.”

The reason Li Zhen was reluctant to become Guan Zhao stemmed from that life-bound flying sword, which resembled a grand prison of heaven and earth.

In the past, many young sword cultivators had surrounded and killed Chen Ping’an, and afterward, Zhu Ke had noticed Li Zhen’s dispirited state and personally advised him. Given his current mindset, he might not achieve even as much as Liu Bai in a hundred years. Zhu Ke also inquired of Li Zhen, who earnestly sought “to distance himself from the true self of Guan Zhao,” whether he could genuinely cultivate as a sword cultivator, truly wielding a sword. At that time, Li Zhen’s response was rather strange, inquiring back whether Zhu Ke had ever walked through the river of time, ultimately providing the concepts of “riverbed” and “fate.”

The top sword immortal, Chen Qingdu, had once expressed a sentiment after encountering a “former friend” that if he could flow upstream in the river of time for ten thousand years, returning to the battlefield, he could ask swords from any “elder.”

Li Zhen looked toward the other side, murmuring, “I really envy you.”

And that young hidden official, whom Li Zhen envied, carried the sword Zhan Kan at his waist, slowly throwing punches atop the city wall.

Just like back then, he left alone, throwing punches; at that time, there were two small thatched cottages atop the Sword Qi Great Wall, where the old sword immortal still remained, and even Cao Ci, who had defeated him three times, was present.

Compared to Chen Ping’an, whose thoughts were constantly swirling, the passage of time felt unbearably slow. Each punch seemed to be a journey back and forth between the mountain's summit and foot, digging a handful of soil, ultimately moving mountains.

On the opposing half of the Sword Qi Great Wall, every time a great cultivator of the human race was slain by the Wild world, a large character would be inscribed on the city wall. Moreover, it seemed the Jiazi banner had changed its mind; there was no need to kill a single ascendant; even a celestial being or a certain sect master would suffice. Characters would be inscribed not only for the names of great demons but also for those they had slain.

Due to the tremendous commotion caused by the demon’s inscription, especially regarding the circulation of heaven and earth’s fortune, even across a mountain-water great formation, Chen Ping’an, who occupied half the Sword Qi Great Wall, could faintly perceive the unusualness over there. Occasionally throwing a punch or a blade to break the great formation was not a mere trivial act.

The Sword Immortal Gu Xia’s master, one of the ten in the Central Earth Divine Continent, Zhou Shen Zhi.

A celestial being from Fu Yao Continent. In addition, the old Heavenly Lord of Tai Ping Mountain in Tongye Continent, the mountain lord of Tai Ping Mountain, and the sect leader of Fu Ji Sect, Ji Hai. Among the three scholars of the academy, there was also the master of Jun Zi, the mountain lord of Da Fu Academy...

All had perished.

Fortunately, Chen Chun’an from Nan Po Sha Continent had not been present, nor had his seniors.

Xun Yuan from Yu Gui Sect in Tongye Continent and Jiang Shangzhen were also unharmed.

Through these events, Chen Ping’an could roughly gauge the advancement speed of the demon clan within the vast realm.

It was originally meaningless, only adding to his troubles.

However, after obtaining that volume of “Mountain and Water Travels,” once Chen Ping’an refined all the texts contained within, receiving the secret letter from the Grand Li National Master, it became critically important.

Then, a feeling arose within Chen Ping’an that this Cui Zhan, if he weren’t crazy, would never think of such a way to send a message.

The true brilliance of Cui Zhan lay not in betting that Chen Ping’an would piece together this secret letter, but in confidently assuring that the old fox who claimed to be a bookworm, Zhou Mi, would learn of this secret letter after him! What was particularly terrifying was that it seemed to Cui Zhan that whether Zhou Mi knew about this matter made no difference to the larger scheme he had in mind. If Zhou Mi was completely unaware, that would be best. Yet even if Zhou Mi became aware, it would not impact the overall plan.

But there were several larger and smaller meanings hidden within, making Chen Ping’an regret that his mind was as deranged as Cui Zhan’s, having accidentally pieced together this secret letter.

Knowing was worse than not knowing.

At the old site of the Da Fu Academy in Tongye Continent, a large demon in the guise of a scholar in a blue robe twitched slightly, immediately sending someone to retrieve a volume of “Mountain and Water Travels.” After refining all the texts, he pondered briefly before successively refining the characters of Cui, Zhan, and the five others. He tried all combinations and ultimately found the eight-character secret letter in his heart’s lake: “The timing is right, the mountains and waters are reversed.”

Zhou Mi chuckled, calling out to Cui Zhan with his heart voice, then extending his hand, “Please, Cui Guoshi, let’s chat for a bit.”

The other party was merely a public plan, betting on whether Baoping Continent could determine the trends of the world.

If Baoping Continent could hold its ground, the so-called reversal of mountains and waters would hold meaning; after all, the remaining half of the Sword Qi Great Wall still belonged to the territory of the vast realm. If they could not hold it, Cui Zhan would merely be trading one life for another, saving at most a young person, and it would also depend on whether that person was willing to leave the Sword Qi Great Wall and switch places with him, Cui Zhan. The most interesting part was that Zhou Mi dared to assert that if Chen Ping’an truly sought assistance from Cui Zhan, who had a fallen Baoping Continent, he would likely be incredibly disappointed, ignored by Cui Zhan; that would truly be a most intriguing inquiry of the heart.

Cui Zhan slowly materialized before Zhou Mi.

Zhou Mi asked, “So-called ‘the timing is right,’ is that when Baoping Continent successfully halts the Wild world’s northern advance, and ultimately, the two realms are at a stalemate?”

The old Confucian scholar, who had descended in the Da Fu Academy of Tongye Continent, nodded with a smile.

It was indeed the Grand Li National Master, Cui Zhan.

If Zhou Mi were not at the academy ruins, Cui Zhan naturally would not appear.

Zhou Mi then asked, “Cui Guoshi is so certain that Chen Ping’an has already received the secret letter first, and is also certain Baoping Continent will hold its ground, and also certain Chen Ping’an can hold out until that day? Especially needing to be sure that Chen Ping’an can endure the worries of life and death, so as not to change places with you too early, thus ruining your previous efforts?”

Cui Zhan said, “As a disciple of the Sage of Literature, I at least have this bit of brains and responsibility.”

Zhou Mi smiled and asked, “Cui Guoshi, I only have one final question: how can you be sure that half of the Sword Qi Great Wall can hold until you say the timing is right? Are you not worried I might step in personally to target him?”

Cui Zhan replied indifferently, “Between you and me, we contend not only for the trends of two realms. If you lack this bit of courage, you are not qualified to discuss reestablishing the Confucian path, gathering the literary veins, and establishing teachings to honor your ancestors.”

Zhou Mi fell silent for a moment, shaking his head with a sigh, “Cui Zhan, so you intend to use the life of Chen Ping’an and the half of the Sword Qi Great Wall as bait in exchange for the life of the Li Sheng... No, rather, the second sage in exchange for mine?”

Cui Zhan smiled, “It could also be the Sage of Literature himself making a move.”

Zhou Mi laughed, “That is something one could only dream of.”

Cui Zhan said, “Quickly have that Tuo Yue Mountain ancestor break the heavens’ curtain; I want to see what kind of ancient gods, hindered by the Li Sheng, can stir up on my Baoping Continent.”

Zhou Mi nodded, “As you wish.”

Then the two almost simultaneously looked toward the direction of Fu Yao Continent, Zhou Mi chuckling, “Why provoke him?”

The old blind man in the ten thousand mountains of the Wild World had long since stated that he would remain an observer.

The Daoist in Donghai Guan Dao Temple, that foul-nosed figure, had chosen to stay out of it. He even aided a bit before his ascension from the Dao Temple.

That old monk was temporarily uncertain of his whereabouts, but most likely, he had already arrived at Baoping Continent; this was still within Tuo Yue Mountain’s expectations.

The only one who, according to previous calculations, was hailed as the most accomplished scholar of the Central Earth Divine Continent, upon reaching the fifth realm, would remain there, returning the sword to the Xuan Du Temple of Qing Ming Continent.

He should not have returned to the vast realm with the sword.

Unexpectedly, this person had indeed drawn his sword.

As a cultivator of the Fourteen Realms, the scholar Bai Ye, wielding a celestial sword, appeared in the southwestern Fu Yao Continent, which could already be considered part of the Wild World’s territory. He consecutively unleashed three strikes, one sending his opponent flying out of Fu Yao Continent, one crossing the sea, and the last landing near the old site of the Upside-Down Mountain, slaying a lord-level demon.

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 828: Contending for the World with a Single City (Part 1)**

In the spring of the seventh year of the Jiachun era, the Zushi Hall of Ascension City held its second official meeting, which was mandatory for all direct disciples to attend. Everyone who had established a residence outside or was traveling as a sword cultivator was required to return on time.

It had been six years since the first time offerings were made to the ancestral portraits.

In the grand hall of the Zushi Hall, forty-one chairs were arranged. Two chairs remained vacant beside the table beneath the ancestral portraits. On the left sat the representatives of the Justice Enforcer lineage, while the Hidden Officials and Wealth Store lineage occupied the right side. There was a subtle air of confrontation between the two sides.

The leader of the Justice Enforcer lineage, Qi Shou, had recently entered the Jade Purity realm. Below him sat two elder Yuan Ying sword cultivators, each hailing from small families on Tai Xiang Street and Yu Hu Street, which were once vassals of the Chen and Nalan clans, respectively. Their relationship with Qi Shou was lukewarm at best. Both elders were well past their prime, with only a century of life left, so they had taken a greater interest in helping Ascension City flourish, eager to impart their sword techniques to the younger generation.

This scenario resembled the political landscape of mundane dynasties, where soon-to-retire elders often became more forthright, willing to say and do things they previously would not have dared. 

Now, with Ascension City undergoing a rejuvenation, sword cultivators practiced freely, without the constraints of old sectarian biases. The Hidden Officials lineage had previously sifted through archives and organized secret records, unveiling many locked-away sword manuals and techniques left by ancient sword immortals. 

Yet, on the path of cultivation, there remained a principle that teachings should not be shared lightly, and methods should not be handed out indiscriminately. Thus, young sword cultivators had to rely on their innate talents, achievements, and the quality of their destined flying swords, particularly the essence of their flying sword techniques, before they could access various secret archives and manuals after being assessed by both the Justice Enforcer and Hidden Officials lineages. While there were still barriers to entry, they were significantly lower compared to the past.

Moreover, the Hidden Officials lineage had also released an improved method for cultivating the Eighteen Stops of Sword Energy, available to all sword cultivators in Ascension City. It was said that this new method was originally passed down from A Liang and was cultivated by a select few young talents, including Ning Yao, Chen Sanqiu, and Die Zhang. 

One by one, sword cultivators entered and took their seats. The vast majority were young faces, and indeed, they were genuinely youthful. Among them, the least experienced were all at least at the Dragon Gate level, with a few exceptional prodigies yet to reach their twenties, rumored to be potential candidates from the Hidden Officials lineage. 

In the Zushi Hall of Ascension City, there were too few elders and too many young people, a sight unseen in any other ancestral hall of the vast world. 

As the appointed time approached, there was still about the time it takes to burn an incense stick left. Qi Shou had taken his seat and was engaged in discussion with an elder Yuan Ying sword cultivator next to him. Currently, the Justice Enforcer lineage wielded the most power within Ascension City, with endless tasks to attend to. Qi Shou personally oversaw the selection of sites, placement of critical materials, and the establishment of formation arrays on the eight surrounding mountains, showcasing his exceptional talent as he ascended through the ranks amid such busy times. 

Over the years, Qi Shou had not merely focused on sword training, relentlessly pursuing the Jade Purity realm. Instead, he had tirelessly dedicated himself to the affairs of Ascension City, which earned him substantial goodwill among the populace. 

With Ning Yao yet to appear, the atmosphere in the Zushi Hall remained relatively relaxed. Everyone understood that Ning Yao alone could command half of the hall's influence. 

Guo Zhujiu casually rested her walking staff across the armrests of her chair, lightly swinging her legs. Beside her sat an elder maiden and a fair-minded individual. 

Gu Jianlong voiced his thoughts, “Lv Duan, why hasn’t Ning Yao ascended to the Ascension realm yet? Honestly, I’m a bit disappointed.”
