The way to address Ning Yao had become a significant dilemma for the former Hidden Officials lineage. Calling her “Lord Hidden Official” felt inappropriate, while addressing her by name seemed too familiar, given that she was a bona fide sword immortal. Yet calling her “Sword Immortal Ning” felt overly formal. Fortunately, Ning Yao had previously opened the conversation by mentioning her name, so now no one was shy about it. After all, the Hidden Officials lineage was not known for their politeness. 

Guo Zhujiu lightly tapped her green bamboo staff, echoing in thought, “What do you know? It’s just the matriarch showing face for the Justice Enforcer sword cultivators.” 

Dong Buduo suddenly slapped Guo Zhujiu on the back of her head. 

Guo Zhujiu raised her hands defensively, her shoulders shaking as if she had dispersed Dong Buduo’s “punching intent.” Annoyed, she exclaimed, “Sister Dong, what’s the deal? I haven’t said anything bad about you, I swear!” 

Dong Buduo twirled a frost jade book seal between her fingers, smiling, “Just itching to do something.” 

Guo Zhujiu muttered under her breath, “With Master Hidden Official not here, and Mistress Hidden Official yet to arrive, you’re really taking the opportunity to bully me.” 

Wang Xinshui suddenly asked, “What about Sword Immortal Mi, and our good brothers Cao Gun and Xuan Can? Do they still count as sword cultivators under the Hidden Officials lineage?” 

Gu Jianlong rolled his eyes, “Are you being silly? What’s so hard about moving a few chairs? Our own family records still have their names, right?” 

Wang Xinshui nodded, “You’re right.” 

In the early days of the former Hidden Officials lineage, Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, Cao Gun, and Xuan Can had formed a brotherhood, viewing each other as comrades. They had been dubbed the "Four Lackeys under the Hidden Official" by Dong Buduo, with their combined strength equivalent to a single Guo Zhujiu. 

Luo Zhenyi felt a pang of melancholy. 

In the current Ascension City, she felt somewhat like Song Caiyun, Zhou Cheng, and Nalan Caihuan from the former Sword Energy Great Wall—not only was she naturally beautiful, but she was also destined to become a female sword immortal. 

Back when the former Hidden Officials lineage was still active, Sword Immortal Chou Miao was around, and the young outsiders like Lin Junbi and Song Gaoyuan were present. 

Simply watching Lin Junbi and Cao Gun or Xuan Can play chess, with piles of discarded pieces behind them, each one relishing their role as the military strategist, hadn’t seemed particularly interesting at the time. Looking back now, Luo Zhenyi realized it had been quite amusing. 

One young man, standing with his hands tucked inside his sleeves, had little skill in chess but loved to point out moves, seemingly eager to stir chaos. 

If Cao Gun or Xuan Can managed to win against Lin Junbi, Guo Zhujiu would lead the four lackeys in boasting about it. If they lost, that young man would confidently throw out, “What, is it my fault?” 

Fan Dache took his seat, his expression solemn and quiet. He was the most composed of the Hidden Officials sword cultivators but also the most sentimental. 

The girl he liked had already married, and when they had met by chance on the street, her child had called him “Uncle Fan.” For reasons he couldn’t explain, he had felt a bit sad then, but now he found he wasn’t heartbroken. Looking at the child, who bore her resemblance, Fan Dache only knew he smiled at that moment, unaware of how his smile appeared to the woman who had become a wife and mother. 

His best friend, Chen Sanqiu, had gone to the vast world. 

The young Hidden Official he trusted the most remained behind at the Sword Energy Great Wall. 

He missed that call of “Dache!” 

Fan Dache quietly turned to glance behind him, a self-deprecating smile forming on his lips before he quickly withdrew his gaze, focusing again on cultivating his sword intent in silence. 

He knew his swordsmanship wasn’t on par with any sword cultivator in the Hidden Officials lineage; he had stumbled his way into the Golden Core realm through numerous hardships. In contrast, Guo Zhujiu and Gu Jianlong possessed exceptional innate talent and far surpassed him with their efforts. Thus, Fan Dache felt considerable pressure. 

As the second-in-command of the Justice Enforcer lineage, Nian Xin rarely made appearances. Typically clad in a loose robe, she was at the Yuan Ying realm but wasn’t a sword cultivator. 

Her true identity seemed to be somewhat of a mystery, even to the former Hidden Officials lineage. She had emerged in Ascension City and inexplicably become a significant figure within the Justice Enforcer lineage. 

She was one of the latest four eccentricities of Ascension City. 

Nian Xin’s chair was located behind the Justice Enforcers and the two elder Yuan Ying sword cultivators. 

However, like Ning Yao, Nian Xin had yet to show herself. 

Three chairs to the south of Nian Xin sat another one of the four eccentricities, a trio of Golden Core sword cultivators, with the lone male dressed in women’s attire. 

They hailed from the private abode of the sword immortal “Bapi Zhai,” which had once been adjacent to the Zongyu Immortal Pavilion. With the magical techniques passed down from their master, the three were now tasked with helping Ascension City find young sword cultivators. 

In truth, they were more than willing to be sword cultivators of the Hidden Officials lineage, but they had yet to receive Ning Yao's approval, who was currently posing as the acting Hidden Official. 

The elder sword immortal from Bapi Zhai had a close friendship with A Liang and possessed numerous ancient inkstones. Thus, Xuezhu, Shuiyu, and Guanzhen, all relatively low in cultivation but notably powerful in combat, were quite familiar with Guo Zhujiu, who had a penchant for sneaking around as a child. 

Consequently, while the Zushi Hall appeared to be factionally divided, the interconnections among them were intricate, whether through friendship, familial ties, or shared history. 

A woman entered quietly through the main door and took her seat without greeting anyone or even exchanging glances. 

It was Nian Xin. 

Nian Xin began to meditate with her eyes closed, determined not to speak during today’s meeting. 

Currently, for a sword cultivator to become a member of the Justice Enforcer lineage in Ascension City, only those from the sword cultivator class among the Qi practitioners had this qualification—a strict rule for Ascension City. 

In contrast, the Hidden Officials and Wealth Store lineages had no such restrictions; practitioners from various schools could freely join. 

For those who were not Qi practitioners seeking to join the Justice Enforcers, they could only do so by being pure martial artists from the former Hidden Officials lineage. 

The former Hidden Officials' martial artist lineage had hired Zheng Dafu, a tavern owner, as their boxing instructor. 

However, Zheng Dafu had declined the offer to serve Ascension City, instead teaching boxing to the group of young swordsmen led by Jiang Yun while only accepting a salary. 

Now, the number of martial artists under the Justice Enforcers had surged to over sixty. Excluding the ten who had been taught boxing by Bai Lianshuang and the two children Nian Xin had recently taken in, the rest were mostly five or six-year-old children. 

While martial arts had far lower requirements for aptitude than sword cultivation, it was still generally accepted that one should start training early. 

Thus, the Justice Enforcers had unconsciously formed a three-headed pattern among their ranks. 

With Qi Shou holding power, Nian Xin responsible for nurturing martial artists, and the two elder Yuan Ying sword cultivators collaborating well with the trio from Bapi Zhai, who were teaching sword techniques and searching for sword cultivators, everything flowed smoothly. 

Yet even so, Qi Shou, who oversaw nearly half of the sword cultivators, was still the undisputed power in Ascension City. 

After discussing matters with the elder sword cultivator next to him, Qi Shou returned to his seat and glanced at the chair opposite him. 

Across from him sat the Hidden Officials lineage, led by Ning Yao, along with Dong Buduo, Xu Ning, Luo Zhenyi, Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshui, Chang Taiqing, Guo Zhujiu, and Fan Dache. 

There were a total of nine individuals. 

In contrast to the mountain-like presence of the Justice Enforcers, the Hidden Officials lineage had fewer members, and the camaraderie among them was evidently stronger, far beyond what the Justice Enforcers could rival. 

Upon Ning Yao’s second return from her travels, Qi Shou had noticed she was clearly at the bottleneck of the Immortal realm, genuinely a great sword immortal. 

Yet from the perspective of all the sword cultivators in Ascension City, it was surprising that Ning Yao had returned home without breaking through. 

This illustrated Ning Yao's standing in Ascension City. 

Becoming a sword immortal was difficult, becoming a great sword immortal even more so, but achieving the Ascension realm was akin to reaching for the heavens. 

However, Ning Yao was the only exception. 

Qi Shou felt no resentment about this, knowing that Ascension City truly needed such a presence. 

After all, in this world, many forces vied for control, and Ascension City was not the only power. 

While the path of swordsmanship might be destined to fall short compared to Ning Yao, Qi Shou had an entire world to contend with. 

Qi Shou’s gaze shifted slightly. 

The chair belonging to the Marquis of Gaoye was positioned beside Ning Yao. 

This individual had arrived at the Zushi Hall earlier than Qi Shou. 

Currently, the Marquis of Gaoye remained at the Yuan Ying realm; breaking into Jade Purity would not come in just three to five years. A slow step could lead to many slow steps, and Qi Shou did not regard him as a rival and was even willing to befriend him like Deng Liang. 

The Wealth Store, overseeing the financial power of Ascension City, was unified under the leadership of the Yuan Ying sword cultivator, the Marquis of Gaoye. However, as the God of Wealth, he was not particularly skilled in financial matters; the actual management was handled by several sword cultivators promoted from the Yan and Nalan families—older but not particularly high in cultivation, making them the most suitable for bookkeeping. 

The name “Wealth Store” was clearly the work of the young Hidden Official; otherwise, it wouldn’t sound so refined. 

Qi Shou had once fought alongside Chen Pingan atop the city walls. 

Their public and private matters were clear. On the battlefield, they were more than just friends; Chen Pingan had even engaged in a significant transaction with Qi Shou. 

However, outside of the battlefield, they each had their own ways of making things difficult for each other, but it never reached the point of life and death. 

Deep down, Qi Shou had to admit that if that fellow had come to this world with them, he would undoubtedly feel constrained in every way, but it might also spark within him a greater fighting spirit. 

Moreover, aside from the deep roots of the Qi family, their ancestor, Qi Tingji, remained the only old sword immortal still at the pinnacle of the sword path. 

Even though Qi Tingji was now in the vast world, continuing to wield his sword against demons, he still posed a significant deterrent to the present Ascension City. 

Deng Liang's position was near the entrance, sitting alongside the younger, talented children. 

This arrangement was somewhat out of the ordinary; as the first named offering in Ascension City, his seat should ideally be near the Marquis of Gaoye and Nian Xin. 

It was Deng Liang’s insistence on this arrangement. 

This also made Deng Liang’s already good rapport in Ascension City even better. 

He hailed from the prominent sect of Jiudu Mountain in the Aiai Continent, a direct descendant and a Yuan Ying sword cultivator, and upon returning home, he had secretly achieved a green status as a scholar within the examination system, a feat more challenging than becoming a direct disciple of the Zushi Hall. 

Once a scholar of Jiudu Mountain achieved a green status, the cultivator could share in a portion of the sect’s fortunes. 

Deng Liang was of the former Hidden Officials lineage but maintained a close relationship with Qi Shou, the leader of the Justice Enforcers. 

Thus, Deng Liang chose not to align entirely with either side, wisely maintaining a degree of distance from the Hidden Officials lineage. 

Deng Liang had three main goals for this trip: to break through his sword cultivation, to seek out the great sword immortal he admired, and to serve as a bridge between Ascension City and Jiudu Mountain. 

Deng Liang hoped to contribute to Ascension City while also minimizing the hostility between the sword cultivators of the Justice Enforcers and the Hidden Officials lineage. 

Therefore, his position needed to be neutral, allowing the words spoken as a named offering to resonate with the sword cultivators of Ascension City. 

During this visit to Ascension City, he brought a substantial amount of unique sect supplies, including the most favored New Year wine from the local lord and precious “Zhongsi Rice” along with “Quegui Talismans.” Deng Liang had also carried a special item and a compact item from his sect, containing ample spiritual energy, consisting of sixty vats of celestial wine and eight hundred jin of “Zhongsi Rice,” which resembled pomegranate seeds, bright red in color, with a flavor akin to water chestnuts. 

It was the perfect tonic for martial artists in the lower five realms, mild in nature and highly nutritious for the cultivators on the mountain. 

Especially valuable were the three hundred Quegui Talismans, which were extraordinarily rare in the Aiai Continent, known as “Green Muscle Gold Charms.” The charm paper was made from a unique celestial leaf exclusive to Jiudu Mountain, which gleamed golden under sunlight or moonlight, akin to an entity protecting one’s home when affixed. 

Deng Liang gifted all of these to the Wealth Store. 

Ning Yao appeared at the entrance. 

Whispers around the Zushi Hall abruptly ceased. 

Throughout the years, Ning Yao had balanced breaking through and traveling extensively. 

No one understood this world better than her. 

Ning Yao did not take a seat but instead went to offer incense to the ancestral portraits of Ascension City. 

Qi Shou of the Justice Enforcers and the Marquis of Gaoye followed closely behind. 

The nine incense sticks offered by the three would be presented by the oldest elder in the Zushi Hall. 

This was the first formal meeting of the Zushi Hall, and a new rule was established by Ning Yao, with no one dissenting. 

The elder sword cultivator from the Justice Enforcer lineage was the one to present the incense today, and it was his first time doing so for the three, causing him to become somewhat emotional. 

Previously, this place would host a few meetings each year, but since Ning Yao had always been away, her absence from offering incense meant the meetings could not officially be considered gatherings of Ascension City. 

Moreover, prior meetings had often seen half the chairs in the Zushi Hall empty. The elder sword cultivator had never shown such sentiment when presenting incense to Qi Shou and the Marquis of Gaoye in the past. 

After the three offered their incense, everyone else in the Zushi Hall stood up. 

Once Ning Yao took her seat, she remained silent. 

Qi Shou announced, “Let the meeting commence.” 

This grand gathering of the Zushi Hall had raised concerns among the Justice Enforcer lineage, even among the two elder Yuan Ying sword cultivators and the three Golden Cores from Xuezhu. They feared the possibility of the Zushi Hall becoming a one-man show from this day forward. 

These worries were not solely based on self-interest. 

It was common knowledge that Ning Yao had once returned to Ascension City and cut Qi Shou down with a single sword strike. 

So, would future instances of the Hidden Officials lineage feeling “aggrieved,” regardless of reason, result in Ning Yao simply using her sword to settle matters? 

No one doubted Ning Yao’s role as the leader of the city, nor did they think she would abuse her power; the reasoning was far too simple. There was no need for her to concern herself with such authority. Ning Yao held no interest in these so-called powers. 

For her, with her sights set on the magnificent landscape of the Ascension realm, even Qi Shou and the Marquis of Gaoye understood that to become the foremost sect in the Fifth World, Ascension City could do without anyone except Ning Yao. 

However, to firmly establish itself within the Fifth World, Ascension City ultimately could not rely solely on Ning Yao’s cultivation and swordsmanship to resolve all matters. 

Thus, a group of elder sword cultivators had secretly convened before this meeting, expressing a desire for Ning Yao to detach from the Hidden Officials lineage entirely, to become an existence above it all—or more directly, to become a second Chen Qingdu. 

Let all major decisions be made by her, but for the daily affairs and trivial matters of Ascension City, it would be best if Ning Yao refrained from intervening, allowing her to focus solely on her sword training, ultimately rising to become the first Ascension realm sword immortal in this world! 

Deng Liang, the offering, was fully aware of the general sentiments among the three lineages in Ascension City. 

After all, as an offering from Jiudu Mountain, one of the significant sects in the vast world, and having spent many years as a wild cultivator, Deng Liang didn’t view these mixed feelings as necessarily negative. 

In fact, he felt that currently, Ascension City, if not considering combat strength, was even more vibrant than the Sword Energy Great Wall of old. 

Tai Xiang Street and Yu Hu Street were still within the city, yet there were no longer any genuinely prominent families or sword immortal heads. 

There were hardly any elders left. 

After all, most sword immortals had fallen in distant battles. 

It seemed that during that war, the greater sword immortals had intentionally pressured all sword immortals and elders to clear a path for the younger generation. 

Though this place was now a foreign land, it would one day become the home of an increasing number of young people and children from Ascension City. 

Qi Shou was the first to speak, summarizing and filtering all news regarding celestial forces, especially focusing on those sects with “sect” in their name, such as Bai Yujing in the far east, Xuandu Guan, and Suichu Palace. 

Another priority was to gather intelligence on all talented cultivators who had reached the Jade Purity realm. For instance, the female Daoist Huang Ting from Tongye Continent had already achieved the Jade Purity realm and had erected a stone monument at a mountain peak, inscribing “Taiping Mountain.” 

Additionally, there was a man using the alias Yang Hengxing, a formidable figure who was both a martial artist in the Wandering realm and a Yuan Ying cultivator, not to be underestimated. 

Besides Ning Yao who had traveled alone, four sword cultivators from the Justice Enforcers were dispatched in various directions to gather information. They also collected a wealth of reports from Fuyou Continent and Tongye Continent. 

Qi Shou proposed, “We should compile two records according to the old practices of the former Hidden Officials lineage—one documenting all sect forces and the other recording those at the upper five realms and Earth Immortal cultivators. What do you think?” 

Ning Yao nodded. 

The Marquis of Gaoye added, “No objections here.” 

After six years of continuous expansion, due to Ascension City’s central location, it began to interact more frequently with the outside world. 

Sword cultivators ventured further afield, and others began to visit in droves. 

Aside from the visible growth and orderliness of Ascension City, many matters from other families gradually surfaced. 

Among the young ten, Bai Yujing’s Daoist Shan Qing was a disciple of the Daoist Patriarch. A young monk wielding a twelve-ringed staff was traveling alone. 

Among the candidates, there was also the Tian Yu from Liuxia Continent, who had already established an extraordinary platform. 

Furthermore, there were several Jade Purity realm cultivators in this world, including a female disciple from the Sword Immortal lineage of the Xuandu Guan in the Qingming world. 

The Hidden Officials lineage, after all, had established old practices to follow, proceeding step by step. In fact, the former Hidden Officials lineage had long devised a detailed scheme. 

Previously, the Hidden Officials lineage had dispersed across the city to survey its mountains and rivers. The Justice Enforcers subsequently selected eight spiritually potent locations to expand the territory of Ascension City, delineating a vast new realm as the foundation for its future endeavors. 

The former Hidden Officials lineage had left behind a comprehensive book, written by the young Hidden Officials and collaboratively compiled by all the foreign sword cultivators, including Lin Junbi and Song Gaoyuan. 

This book was divided into several sections, including the Structure Chapter, detailing the operations of sects like the Pima Sect in Beijulu Continent, Chunlu Garden, Taiping Mountain in Tongye Continent, and the Deer Horn Palace where Song Gaoyuan resided, along with the Hall of Worship and battlefields of the Shao Yuan Dynasty. 

The External Expansion Chapter discussed how to establish celestial residences, arrange formations, insert spies, and detailed the customs and practices of various sects, further subdivided into twelve major topics. 

The People’s Heart Chapter included methods for establishing educational institutions and related considerations. 

The Mountain and Water Chapter specifically detailed the various sacred mountains and water spirits throughout the vast world. 

This extensive book, totaling over a hundred thousand words, was distributed to all members of the Zushi Hall, except for the deleted People's Heart Chapter, ensuring that everyone was somewhat familiar with the intricate rules of the vast world, if not entirely knowledgeable. 

“Justice Enforcer, I have something to say.” 

Gu Jianlong suddenly stood up, smiling, “Among the fourteen sword cultivators of the Justice Enforcers, those heading south and north have clashed significantly with cultivators from Tongye Continent and Fuyou Continent, and I’ve heard they’ve even killed some. Upon returning to Ascension City, the focus of conversation at the tables has been on how these cultivators from those two continents are worthless. Upon hearing this, I feel like it’s as if the cultivators from those two continents could be regarded as merely Observers in the Golden Core realm. If this is true, then as a mere Golden Core sword cultivator, wouldn’t I be able to run rampant in both regions?” 

Gu Jianlong added, “Of course, the individuals killed by the Justice Enforcers were all deserving of their fates; I must clarify this point. However, returning to the matter, what is deemed ‘deserving of death’ or ‘should be killed’ is merely based on the assertions of the Justice Enforcers’ roaming sword cultivators. As for the facts, whether they align with the truth requires further verification from our Hidden Officials lineage. 

If someone is indiscriminately killing outside and bringing fame to Ascension City, while their intentions may seem noble, I’d have to confront them directly to seek justice.” 

A Golden Core sword cultivator named Shuiyu from Bapi Zhai frowned slightly, “Gu Jianlong, are you overreacting?” 

Wang Xinshui countered, “Shuiyu, is there really such a thing as a small matter in this world? What major issue isn’t born from a minor one?” 

Just as Shuiyu was about to continue speaking, he was interrupted by his senior brother Xuezhu using silent communication to stop him. 

A young sword cultivator from the Justice Enforcers scoffed, “During the great war, some individuals didn’t contribute much, but now that they’re idle, they’re all too eager to attack their own. If this is the case, I think from now on, whenever we encounter outsiders, the sword cultivators of Ascension City should proactively step aside and apologize first, how about that?” 

Do you think only your Hidden Officials lineage cultivators can say such sarcastic remarks? 

Who can’t? 

Dong Buduo and Luo Zhenyi stood up almost simultaneously. 

Unexpectedly, Ning Yao glanced at that young sword cultivator. 

In an instant, both the young man and his chair flew out of the Zushi Hall. 

Then Ning Yao stated, “The meeting is concluded; it’s time for a change of personnel and a new chair.” 

That young sword cultivator fell to the ground, frightened and furious, ready to speak, but seemed to be enveloped by sword energy, turning him into a pitiful bloody figure, causing him to faint on the spot. 

Ning Yao continued, “Let’s proceed with the meeting.” 

Qi Shou maintained his composure. 

The Marquis of Gaoye remained indifferent. 

An elder Yuan Ying sword cultivator hesitated to speak. 

Deng Liang sighed softly, pondering whether that individual outside was truly speaking without thinking. 

Gu Jianlong had spoken about the matter at hand, while the one outside had targeted the entire old Hidden Officials lineage. 

Major principles, personal morals, good and evil, merits and faults, right and wrong—how complex! Once one begins to judge others rather than the matter at hand, how can one clarify any reasoning? 

Ning Yao looked at the silent crowd, who were slow to speak, and said calmly, “Those sitting here may not all be sword cultivators and may not hold high realms, but they must not be too foolish. Ascension City has only this many people; having delineated a thousand miles of territory has already made us feel stretched. Thus, engaging in the petty politics of the temple and hall below is premature. 

The only rule for discussions in the Zushi Hall is to focus on matters, not on people. If you prefer to focus on people rather than matters, then don’t occupy a seat here.” 

Ning Yao then turned to Qi Shou and asked, “Who are the recommenders and guarantors for this individual in the Justice Enforcer lineage?” 

Qi Shou provided two names. 

Two Golden Core sword cultivators immediately stood up in the Zushi Hall. 

Ning Yao turned to Xu Ning and said, “Record this matter and then check the records of that individual outside.” 

Xu Ning stood up to comply before sitting back down. 

Ning Yao gradually said, “Including the Hidden Officials lineage, from now on, everyone, including Gu Jianlong, should be mindful of their speech. Previously, during discussions in the Sword Energy Great Wall, typically only those in the Jade Purity realm could appear, while only old sword immortals could speak.” 

Gu Jianlong immediately nodded, “Understood, I will be more careful.” 

Ning Yao turned her gaze toward the entrance of the Zushi Hall and sneered, “In less than seven years, have they all grown so arrogant? After a hundred years, won’t they all be invincible?” 

The atmosphere grew intensely serious in an instant. 

Deng Liang had to stand up to explain, “If we continue to view all Qi practitioners outside Ascension City as potential enemies, then one day, Ascension City will become a desolate stronghold surrounded by adversaries. If we consider all Qi practitioners in the world as mere decorative pillows with little combat ability, we will surely suffer greatly, as other forces will exploit this to encircle us. 

Eventually, we will find ourselves fighting with others, and it won’t be about the sword but rather about unexpected encounters, leading to inevitable demise.” 

Deng Liang’s tone grew heavier, “What we think in our hearts and how we act are entirely different matters. If the sword cultivators in our Zushi Hall become arrogant, what can we expect from the outside sword cultivators? 

If we prefer to view all outsiders as lesser beings, deeming their lives insignificant, believing we can kill anyone we choose, then I think there is no need for Ascension City to strive for dominance in the world; if we can stand firm in a hundred years, we should consider it a blessing worthy of burning incense for our ancestors in the Zushi Hall. 

The Qi practitioners of the vast world, even if they are lower in realm and insufficient in combat strength, are still formidable. The bloodshed and political intrigue among them run deep, often hidden for centuries, making it all too easy to kill without a trace. My words are not alarmist rhetoric!” 

Deng Liang concluded with a fist salute, “In the other sects of the vast world, an offering ultimately remains half an outsider, and such words, which may offend everyone, should not be spoken. 

I simply cannot help but express my thoughts because the position I hold compels me to pour a bucket of cold water on everyone!” 

The Bapi Zhai sword cultivator, Shuiyu, stood up and said, “I’ve been taught.” 

The Marquis of Gaoye seldom spoke, but this time, he chimed in, “In this world, Ascension City occupies all advantages of time and place. Even if our hearts are scattered, no other force will be able to compete with us in the next hundred years. 

However, for long-term development, as Deng Liang has said, we must learn from the strengths of the Qi practitioners in the vast world to complement our own weaknesses. Only then will Ascension City possess unparalleled swordsmanship and equally adept political acumen, giving us hope to dominate this world. 

Otherwise, a hundred years later, when our shortcomings become apparent and chaos ensues, it will be too late to rectify it. Even if Ascension City maintains a majority of sword immortals, it will be of little help.” 

This was a prudent perspective. 

The sword cultivators present in the Zushi Hall felt it was only natural. 

Qi Shou agreed, “Sword cultivators and the hearts of people are the foundation of Ascension City. Beyond that, high realms, extensive territories, and large numbers are merely superficial advantages.” 

The Marquis of Gaoye nodded, “Thus, the urgent task at hand is to clearly delineate the powers of the Justice Enforcers, Hidden Officials, and Wealth Store lineages, reducing unnecessary friction. Each lineage must know precisely what they must do, as well as what they can and cannot do.” 

This statement could be seen as the Wealth Store lineage’s candid counsel to the Justice Enforcers, seemingly inappropriate but actually quite fitting. 

This was likely the broader perspective of the Marquis of Gaoye. 

He had already prepared his arguments and began to elaborate on the duties and boundaries of the three lineages. 

During this discussion, Xuezhu from the Justice Enforcers raised an objection, while Xu Ning and Luo Zhenyi from the Hidden Officials lineage expressed differing opinions. 

However, with the earlier contention serving as a foundation, the discussions among the three lineages became relatively lighthearted, even amidst some disagreements. 

Ultimately, they reached a consensus regarding this matter, leaving only minor details to be further adjusted. 

Ning Yao had remained silent throughout. 

These matters were indeed more suited for Dong Buduo and Xu Ning to handle. 

Thus, Ning Yao saw no need to speak up. 

She had never been fond of meddling in trivial matters, and by the time she found it necessary to intervene, it indicated that Ascension City was facing significant issues. 

Qi Shou’s subsequent conclusion struck like thunder on a clear day, “Starting today, while sword cultivators in Ascension City may feel superior, it should not be overly apparent. The habit of determining the significance of matters based on realm must change.” 

Almost everyone turned their gaze toward Ning Yao, as Qi Shou’s words seemed to carry a deeper meaning. 

However, Ning Yao’s expression remained unchanged as she said, “From now on, if any sword cultivator from the Hidden Officials lineage violates regulations, the Justice Enforcers and Wealth Store can bypass me and impose penalties directly, and each punishment should be severe rather than lenient.” 

This statement surprised everyone, yet they felt a sense of relief. 

Strangely, the sword cultivators from the Hidden Officials lineage appeared calm, showing no signs of grievance. 

Ning Yao trusted all the sword cultivators from the Hidden Officials lineage. 

Moreover, she thought that in a few short years, or at most a few decades, they would either seek her out or she would find them, and when that time came, they could let him handle the busywork. 

She had no desire to deal with such affairs; after all, he was the most skilled at it. 

Furthermore, the atmosphere, rules, and principles of the former Hidden Officials lineage had all been established by him. 

In the future, both named and unnamed offerings, as well as those visiting or settling in Ascension City, would inevitably increase. 

Ascension City would gradually become a melting pot of diverse characters. 

The conflicts between outsiders and the indigenous sword cultivators of Ascension City, whether overt or covert, would continue to accumulate, further impacting the sentiments of the local sword cultivators, making the dynamics even more complicated than during the years of the Sword Energy Great Wall. 

The People’s Heart Chapter from the former Hidden Officials lineage had long acknowledged this. Since they had chosen this new path, they could only take it step by step, correcting mistakes as they went. Each rectification was not a bad thing but rather a gain. 

The author of the book had emphatically stated that as long as they used a method of gradually correcting small mistakes to avoid large ones, the hearts of the people would not become chaotic. 

They shouldn’t emulate the sects of the vast world that covered up errors; the sword cultivators of the Sword Energy Great Wall must possess the courage and capability to correct mistakes. 

With power comes arrogance. 

Since the sword cultivators of the Sword Energy Great Wall no longer faced the life-and-death enemy of the wilderness, their true enemy lay within themselves, thus necessitating more focus on cultivating their hearts. 

In the Zushi Hall, as long as the intent was for the benefit of Ascension City, all sword cultivators from the Hidden Officials lineage must be willing to tolerate harsh words and the occasional outburst, and such individuals must not harbor resentment or be excluded once they left the Zushi Hall. 

If those willing to engage in reasoned debate became increasingly difficult to persuade, over time, they would all fall silent. Then, whether or not the Zushi Hall had sword immortals or how many were present would become inconsequential. 

Moreover, all the children raised in the city must remember the senior sword cultivators, both from Ascension City and those from the vast world, ensuring that both parties hold onto their memories. Through educational institutions and the teachings of various scholars, they would learn the true essence of sword cultivators and what it means to be a genuine sword immortal. 

At the end of the booklet, a piece of paper was tucked in, bearing a phrase written in the customary formal script by a young Hidden Official, which read, “To distract you was never my intention.” 

Guo Zhujiu was the first to flip through the book and found this paper, proudly taking it to her master to claim credit. However, when Ning Yao took the paper, she pitied Guo Zhujiu for knocking her head against the door, thumping it repeatedly. 

Ning Yao remained silent for a moment, before adding, “As for when and where I draw my sword, anyone can attempt to stop me.” 

Guo Zhujiu clapped her hands quickly, her palms not touching, making no sound, demonstrating impressive skill. 

Yet, despite Ning Yao’s words hinting at a significant retreat for the Hidden Officials lineage, instead of creating a heavy atmosphere, it fostered a sense of long-lost familiarity. 

It felt as if with Ning Yao present, her saying such words served to reaffirm that Ascension City was still the same as the former Sword Energy Great Wall. 

It was still that city brimming with sword cultivators, where sword immortals flourished the most. 

It remained that hometown where a city of sword cultivators stood against the demons of the vast world. 

After Ning Yao spoke, she continued to listen to the meeting while her thoughts wandered far and wide. 

Currently, she found herself particularly concerned about an enigmatic sword cultivator—one who also ranked among the top ten young talents across several realms—Liu Cai. 

This individual possessed two Sword Nourishing Gourds, using his “thoughts” to nurture the flying sword “Bilu,” and the other to nurture the flying sword “Baiku.” 

Thus, he was the only outsider who truly captured Ning Yao’s attention. It wasn’t due to the claim that “only Liu Cai could rival Ning Yao in the same realm a century later.” 

Rather, it was Liu Cai’s two flying swords that bore exceedingly strange fundamental techniques, seemingly aimed at targeting and even restraining Chen Pingan. 

The flying sword Baiku disregarded the flow of time, surpassing Chen Pingan’s caged bird. 

The flying sword Bilu could break through myriad swords, directly countering Chen Pingan’s Well Moon technique. 

Ning Yao slightly furrowed her brows. 

Qi Shou continued discussing the arrangements for leading teams on excursions. Without the Sword Energy Great Wall, the growth of sword cultivators would slow significantly. 

There were also plans to place spies in the north and south, as well as to cultivate martial artist candidates. Additionally, they needed to rank the sixty pure martial artists currently in Ascension City. 

To achieve true orderly succession, seemingly tedious matters were indispensable. 

As for nurturing spies and assassins, this was a matter of great importance, which would involve the possibility of creating a separate lineage. 

Alternatively, the sword cultivators of the Hidden Officials lineage could take full responsibility for this, thereby augmenting their own authority. 

Qi Shou had already made a decision regarding this matter and directly stated, “This task will be assigned to the Hidden Officials lineage. Otherwise, merely monitoring Ascension City would be a waste of resources.” 

Deng Liang nodded gently. 

As a Justice Enforcer, one should possess this level of generosity. 

This not only prevented the Hidden Officials lineage from nitpicking at the Justice Enforcers, leading to excessive internal strife, but it also allowed the sword cultivators of the former Hidden Officials lineage, who were most adept at intelligence and battle maneuvers, to truly assist Ascension City in focusing on the broader world. 

After today’s meeting at the Zushi Hall, Deng Liang gained a deeper understanding of Qi Shou, the Marquis of Gaoye, and Xuezhu, who were all rising in status among the sword cultivators. 

In Deng Liang’s view, it was possible that Xuezhu, Shuiyu, and Guanzhen, who held unique techniques passed down from their masters, might not yet realize that their small group of three, along with those two elder Yuan Ying cultivators, essentially formed a key existence akin to half of an administrative office and half of a military department. 

Moreover, compared to the two elder sword cultivators, the three from Xuezhu were younger and had higher achievements in their paths. 

Thus, if Deng Liang had the chance, he would surely invite them to drink. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 829: Contending for the World with a City (Part 2) 

Deng Liang had always acknowledged and faced his own selfishness. Those who understand others possess wisdom, while those who understand themselves possess clarity.

They subsequently discussed the strange entities that Ning Yao had slain—remnants resembling ancient deities, yet differing from descriptions found in ancient texts.

Lord Gaoye inquired whether these entities could be subdued and utilized as local spirits to stabilize fortunes and gather spiritual energy.

Ning Yao responded, “It’s very difficult to tame them. There’s a slim chance, but it’s possible. The Hidden Officials will release a book on this later, but it shouldn’t be widely circulated.”

Currently, only a handful of cultivators capable of slaying such beings existed across the realm, making each word in that book invaluable—akin to celestial currency.

Qi Shou said solemnly, “Aside from the sword cultivators of the Hidden Officials, at most ten people in the Ancestor Hall can peruse it. If even a hint of it leaks out, the Hidden Officials will pursue accountability to the end!”

Afterward, the Executioners had work to do. Qi Shou planned to allocate ten Earth Immortal sword cultivators to specifically deal with these entities.

Lord Gaoye requested to accompany them.

The mountains occupied by these entities often housed a considerable quantity of rare materials, and there was a chance of encountering fortuitous caves and blessed lands. This was evidenced by the female Daoist from the Peaceful Mountain of Tongye Province.

Naturally, the Spring House, which controlled all celestial currency, would not sit idly by or have any reason to remain uninvolved.

Even if Lord Gaoye chose to be a recluse, other cultivators under the Spring House would protest vehemently. After all, wealth and power were inseparable. Recently, rumors circulated within the Spring House that their sword cultivators lacked sufficient cultivation realms, so they should resort to accumulating celestial currency instead. Especially among the younger sword cultivators, many would often spout phrases like "not a blade of grass grows," or "picking up scraps is also a skill..."

The atmosphere was concerning.

Currently, the four strange entities of the Ascension City were under Ning Yao’s precarious management.

As for Ning Yao breaking through her realm, it was the least surprising development.

There was also the true identity of Nian Xin.

She donned the attire of a sword cultivator from the Boqi Zhai.

This had caused two young sword cultivators, who had only recently joined the ranks of the Xie Prefecture and the Genzhen Sect, to frown and ask before taking their vows: “Do we really have to wear women’s clothing?”

This infuriated the Xie Prefecture, and junior disciple Shui Yu echoed Gu Jianlong’s words of reason, laughingly asking the two rascals, “What’s wrong with wearing women’s clothing? That esteemed Hidden Official wore it on the battlefield back in the day, looking quite graceful!”

Finally, it was the young generation of accountants in the Spring House who gleamed with ambition, eager to amass wealth.

The subsequent discussions were no trivial matter.

An old sword cultivator at the Nascent Soul stage reported on the current number of sword cultivators in Ascension City and the anticipated number of local sword cultivators over the next century.

Thus, Shui Yu proposed to lead a long journey. The number of sword cultivators didn’t need to be large—three to five would suffice—as he intended to seek out sword cultivator prospects from afar for the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Lord Gaoye suggested developing four additional cities beyond the eight mountain peaks that belonged to Ascension City. This would not only allow for local governance but also accommodate more people, while also serving to hinder external infiltration of Ascension City to a certain extent.

The eight mountain peaks, including Zifu Mountain, had successfully passed their selections today. The Executioners secured five positions while the Spring House obtained three seats, one of which was fiercely contested by Lord Gaoye, resulting in a heated argument between the Spring House cultivators and the Executioners.

The Hidden Officials had too few members to intervene, but Gu Jianlong spoke a few words in favor of the Spring House.

When Lord Gaoye proposed the four new cities, Luo Zhenyi stated that the sword cultivators from the Hidden Officials, or those they nurtured, must occupy a city and serve as the local lord in the future.

Lord Gaoye and Qi Shou exchanged glances and nodded in agreement.

When the conversation shifted to city construction, Luo Zhenyi also brought up the issue of “exclave” areas distant from Ascension City, emphasizing that preparations needed to be made early.

This was a matter of great importance that required utmost caution.

It was highly likely to conflict with various factions.

Due to the prior accountability demanded by the Hidden Officials from the Executioner sword cultivators, and after Deng Liang’s heartfelt words, the cultivators within the Ancestor Hall were momentarily hesitant.

They were genuinely worried about attracting trouble.

Ning Yao said coldly, “In today’s world, aside from the four corners—the extremes of the East, West, South, and North—everywhere else is unclaimed territory. There are no properly established mountain peaks that definitively belong to anyone. We can venture far and seek high ground in each direction, erecting a stele inscribed with the words 'Sword, Qi, Long, City.' Anyone who dares to contest our territory and defy us will be treated as enemies of the Ascension City! If the sword cultivators cannot withstand their celestial techniques, I will personally confront them!”

Within the Ancestor Hall, everyone felt an immense sense of relief.

Deng Liang smiled knowingly, deeply impressed. Truly, this was Ning Yao.

A woman who had never been to the Summer Palace.

Ning Yao rose and stated, “A sword cultivator is a sword cultivator. A hundred or a thousand years from now, at least half of the members of the Ascension City Ancestor Hall must be sword cultivators. Regardless of what happens later, for a thousand years or ten thousand years, if there are any realms left in this world, the last remaining sword cultivator must be here in this Ancestor Hall.”

“After a century, the number of sword immortals in Ascension City must surpass the total of sword immortals in all other realms.”

“In the world, the most sword cultivators will be in Ascension City. The highest sword Dao will also be in Ascension City. This is not some grand ambition; it is simply the natural order.”

Ning Yao wore a golden robe and carried a sword box on her back.

Her brows and eyes sparkled with determination.

Qi Shou was the first to stand, smiling, “What does the Lord of the House say? When will you reach the Jade Purity stage?”

Lord Gaoye stood as well, laughing, “I won’t keep the Executioners waiting too long.”

Everyone in the Ancestor Hall, especially the budding sword immortals, displayed resolute expressions.

The two old Nascent Soul sword cultivators simultaneously rose. The elderly man responsible for incense offerings in the Ancestor Hall clasped his fists and said solemnly, “Then I’ll leave it to all of you!”

In the Chen family mansion on Tai Xiang Street, there was a peculiar child over the years who loved to bask in the sun, living in seclusion and occasionally glancing out at the empty street from the entrance of the Chen family mansion.

His name was Chen Zhi.

This was the new name he had chosen for himself.

In Ascension City, only the Hidden Officials’ Ning Yao, the Executioners’ Nian Xin, and the Spring House’s Lord Gaoye knew his real name.

Aside from them, only a dead servant from the Chen family and a young maid remained. The former was nominally a Gold Core sword cultivator but was, in reality, a Nascent Soul. This young Nascent Soul sword cultivator was not only extremely young and talented but also devoted to the Chen family, ready to sacrifice his life for this child named “Chen Zhi” at any moment.

Zhi means “to comprehend,” while Xi means “brightness.” In the "Book of Songs," it is said that “Zhi Xi means brightness.”

To stabilize the hearts of the people, Zhi NIng inside and out. To create rites and music was to achieve peace through one’s own efforts.

Now, the seven-year-old Chen Zhi—or rather, the former sword immortal Chen Xi of the Sword Qi Great Wall—had actually read quite a bit of books.

Otherwise, the Chen family wouldn’t have a descendant like Chen Sanqiu.

The Chen family of Tai Xiang Street had a small custom. Each year, on the day the character “Chen” was engraved on the city wall, a large basket of illuminating pearls would be scattered onto the street, leading the children of Tai Xiang and Yu Hu Streets to gather early in the morning, waiting to snatch those pearls. Among the generations of children, many eventually became sword immortals, while even more perished in battle before they could.

Today, Chen Zhi stood at the entrance, gazing at the desolate street, and smiled.

There used to be a scoundrel who would push and shove his way through the children, using his fists and feet to steal a large handful each year, only to have a crowd of weeping children follow behind him, crying for their parents.

At this moment, a young maid of ordinary appearance stood beside Chen Zhi, carefully watching the street. She gently reminded, “Master, it’s time to go back.”

Chen Zhi nodded and turned to return to the mansion.

After undergoing a reincarnation, his previous soul was incomplete, and he hadn’t fully awakened. However, his memories remained intact. By relying on a longevity lamp in the Chen ancestral hall, he managed to restore his soul, inevitably altering his temperament somewhat.

The seamstress Nian Xin, who had come from the old prison, had quietly sent a secret letter to him, the master of the Chen family. In the letter, the young Hidden Official asserted that within the city, there were key pieces placed by the wild world, likely low in realm but deeply concealed. As the city expanded rapidly into the fifth realm, one must be cautious of certain pieces that appeared to claim high positions without leaving traces, lest they conspire with those from the three continents who entered this new world.

Thus, within the next sixty years, he earnestly requested the senior Chen Xi to find an opportunity to remind the Summer Palace, especially to closely monitor those familiar faces already in the Ancestor Hall, as well as the newcomers with potential to ascend based on their merits. The Hidden Officials must be vigilant in their inspection. Additionally, they should keep an eye on those sword cultivators who were originally not young, lacking in talent, yet suddenly broke through quickly. If any Earth Immortal could achieve two breakthroughs within a century, they must be particularly cautious.

Walking through the familiar mansion, Chen Zhi smiled slightly.

This Hidden Official truly cared deeply for the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The letter was written in gentle language, meticulously composed, and importantly, it addressed the sender as a junior.

Moreover, the young Hidden Official’s greatest concern was that the old sword immortal Qi Tingji, responsible for guarding the waters of Fuyun Continent, would breach the agreement and enter the fifth realm.

He absolutely could not let Qi Tingji control the lives and deaths of all sword cultivators.

Therefore, it was crucial to be wary of Tongye Continent closing its gates first, while Fuyun Continent would ultimately close later than Nanposuo Continent.

Chen Zhi muttered to himself, “Thank goodness.”

Indeed, the gates of Fuyun Continent closed the latest, but Qi Tingji remained in the Haoran world.

Ultimately, that young man was still worried about the safety of that bride-to-be.

Facts eventually proved that Chen Ping’an had overthought matters.

First, it became evident that Qi Tingji’s resolve was not as thick-skinned as Chen Ping’an had imagined.

Furthermore, Ning Yao’s rapid breakthrough was a mitigating factor. Even if Qi Tingji harbored extreme ambition, attempting to seize power first and rally the sword cultivators of the city to challenge Confucian norms, with Ning Yao present and the Sage of Literature helping to keep watch, he wouldn’t easily succeed. Moreover, Bai Ye's relationship with that old scholar and the power held by Qi Shou’s descendants would surely have led Qi Tingji to weigh his options carefully.

However, Chen Zhi did not think that this “after-the-fact concern” was unnecessary. On the contrary, it was quite essential.

After all, Qi Tingji had nearly become the second Xiao Xian back in the day.

Such a person, if he had never entertained the thought of being the first in a new realm, seizing the fortune of the Dao and ultimately ascending to the Fourteenth Realm, no one would believe it.

In fact, the young Hidden Official was the first to disbelieve, and Chen Zhi was the second.

Once Qi Tingji became completely unhinged and tore off the facade, choosing to invade the fifth realm, the first person he would target would undoubtedly be Ning Yao, and the second would certainly be him, “Chen Xi.”

As for Chen Zhi himself, he had taken it slow over the years, breaking through one realm a year, and now he had just reached the Gold Core stage.

The reason why two chairs remained empty at the table beneath the portraits in the Ancestor Hall was significant.

One chair was reserved for the future city lord, while the other was meant for the first Ascension stage sword immortal in the history of Ascension City.

One represented the face of Ascension City, and the other represented its inner strength.

However, whoever could become the face of Ascension City would not be lacking.

If all went as expected, it would be Chen Zhi sitting in one chair, and Ning Yao sitting in the other. 

Yet, Chen Zhi didn’t mind if Ning Yao occupied both chairs alone; he would even welcome Qi Shou maturing quickly and becoming capable enough to occupy the city lord’s chair that originally belonged to him.

After his reincarnation, Chen Zhi’s soul had slightly changed, and his disposition had inevitably altered. He was more interested in the Haoran world and the Qingming world.

He genuinely wished to fly alone with his sword in the future and roam through the two realms.

However, if within a hundred years, no suitable junior could demonstrate the qualification to secure the position of city lord, there would be no choice but for him to step into the Ancestor Hall of Ascension City.

Regardless, the rise of Ascension City was unstoppable.

Even if there were those who obstructed it, Chen Zhi was still Chen Xi.

He was the sword cultivator who had carved characters on the walls of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

As dusk fell and the shop was about to close, Zheng Dafeng, the temporary shopkeeper who had worked hard all day, leisurely drank wine with one foot propped up on a long bench, scanning the two rows of taverns lining the street. With no women in sight, his gaze swept past, but once a woman appeared, he couldn’t help but stare.

A young boy poured a bowl of wine for the temporary shopkeeper and shook his head, saying, “Dafeng, you’re really slacking off. Today’s meeting in the Ancestor Hall was such a big event, and you didn’t even get a chance to listen in as a mere doorkeeper? You still have the face to teach people how to punch?”

Zheng Dafeng bent down, sniffing the aroma of the wine, not in a hurry to drink. He raised his head to smile at Feng Kangle, “Is your big brother Dafeng someone who cares about these trivial names? In that Ancestor Hall, how many girls do you think I could see? How could it compare to sitting here?”

Currently, aside from the out-of-town Zheng Dafeng, everyone else in the tavern were familiar faces.

The two young helpers, Qiu Long and Liu E.

The two errand boys, Feng Kangle and Tao Ban.

The wine remained the same—Bamboo Sea Cave Sky Wine, Qingshen Mountain Wine, and the wine from the Mute Lake, accompanied by pickled vegetables and plain noodles.

The bowls were the same size as before.

Feng Kangle spat disdainfully, “This Zheng Dafeng relies on that smile and gaze that even a personal scholar can’t learn, scaring off who knows how many women who used to come here for drinks. If it weren’t for the extra old bachelors and gamblers today, my good friend Tao Ban would say he’s going to revolt against Zheng Dafeng.”

In the distance, Tao Ban, who was wiping the tables, couldn’t help but ask again, “Dafeng, do you think I’m the kind of martial arts genius that no one can see?”

When this boy was still a child, he had asked a similar question to the second shopkeeper, only changing “martial arts genius” to “sword immortal prospect.”

Zheng Dafeng was still in charge of teaching martial arts.

This wine-loving shopkeeper, who was particularly keen to steal the limelight, never drank before or after teaching martial arts.

Jiang Yun, Xu Gong from the Mumei Alley, and Yuan Zao Hua.

These three were the fastest learners of martial arts. With the favorable timing from the new realm, Jiang Yun had obtained martial fortunes twice, while Xu Gong and Yuan Zao Hua each had one.

There was also a little girl from Yuhu Street, Sun Qu, who had a younger sister named Sun Zao, a sword immortal prospect who had been taken away from the Sword Qi Great Wall by a female sword immortal. Learning martial arts was also an option.

In truth, the first batch of ten children showed great potential in martial arts. The two selected later by Nian Xin were also quite promising.

The following forty or so children were of a lesser caliber.

The so-called “strongest” refers to a kind of horizontal comparison among martial artists of the same realm.

However, the stronger one’s foundation, the more martial fortunes one receives. If at the time of breakthrough, there’s a height of “unprecedented,” when martial fortunes arrive, it becomes even more spectacular.

Whether one could achieve the strongest breakthrough also depended on luck, such as being at the same realm as Cao Ci or Chen Ping’an, and breaking through before them—how could one compete for the title of strongest?

Before Cao Ci and Chen Ping’an, being in the same realm as senior brother Li Er and Prince Wang Changjing was a similarly bleak situation for other pure martial artists.

Zheng Dafeng took a sip of wine, leaning back, and turned to his side, “In any case, I can’t see it. I only see that you kid has good fortune with the ladies.”

Tao Ban complained, “What’s the use of good fortune? You’re still far behind the second shopkeeper. When the second shopkeeper was around, there were so many female customers, but now that you’re here, they’ve all run off.”

Zheng Dafeng clicked his tongue, “You’ve got to be struck by lightning for saying that.”

A beautiful girl’s gaze can make one feel as if they should wear an extra thick cotton coat in winter. Yet, it can also have a bewitching effect, making a man feel as if he’s shedding clothes in the scorching summer, feeling cool yet warm at heart.

Unfortunately, the young boy was ignorant of such matters.

Zheng Dafeng glanced elsewhere.

Liu E liked Qiu Long, but Qiu Long had long had a sister in his heart—the true owner of the shop, the head shopkeeper, Die Zhang.

Zheng Dafeng still had some insight into this.

So, behind the scenes, the man glanced at Liu E, who was greeting customers in the distance, half-jokingly advising the young man who seemed to be perpetually troubled, “Why not cherish the one in front of you?”

After all, no matter how good the sister far away might be, she was still out of reach. Sadly, Qiu Long probably understood this simple principle but couldn’t act on it.

Liking someone isn’t too hard, but not liking someone you once liked is not easy.

With a completely different style of business from the young Hidden Official, Zheng Dafeng quickly established himself in Ascension City. Although business was still not as good as in previous years, at least it was no longer desolate.

Moreover, Zheng Dafeng also had a gambling habit. Most importantly, in the beginning, all the gamblers and punters viewed Zheng Dafeng as a kindred spirit of the second shopkeeper, being cautious around him. It wasn’t until several encounters later that they realized it had been a false alarm. It turned out that Zheng Dafeng was of great integrity, with superior gambling quality, and would lose every time.

As time went on, the drinkers all began to claim that the character of the second shopkeeper, who used to be ignored even by dogs, had been picked up by brother Zheng.

Everyone addressed Zheng Dafeng as “brother,” claiming that if there were more heroes like him in the Haoran world and fewer like the second shopkeeper, the people would indeed live a simpler life.

Zheng Dafeng’s catchphrase was to hold up an empty wine bowl and say to everyone, “I’ll propose the first toast!”

Indeed, he would raise a toast, but he always lifted the guests’ drinks.

Additionally, Zheng Dafeng pointed out the ten great fairies and the top ten beauties of the younger generation, with the bachelor drinkers praising him and giving him thumbs up.

It was rumored that Guo Zhujiu secretly gave some money to purchase a few more jars of wine for the tavern, negotiating with Zheng Dafeng to elevate a certain old maiden’s ranking, so as not to appear too pitiful and risk her not getting married.

The ones who loved to stroll around here the most, aside from Guo Zhujiu, were Gu Jianlong, who enjoyed listening to stories, and those who liked to drink while listening to tales.

Of course, Zheng Dafeng would tell different stories to different people. Guo Zhujiu only liked to hear stories related to her master; the size of the story was not that important. This inevitably left Brother Dafeng feeling unsatisfied, thinking he had eighteen skills but nowhere to use them, and thus began to tell Gu Jianlong stories about celestial battles, which were the best accompaniments to wine.

The speaker had intention, and the listener grasped it; it could be said that they were half-master and half-disciple.

Gu Jianlong preferred tales of conflicts between men and women, so when Brother Dafeng told a story about women fighting, she was dumbfounded. The next time they drank, even Wang Xinshui eagerly followed along, wanting to seek knowledge from Brother Dafeng.

Zheng Dafeng drank a bowl of sorrowful wine, sighing.

That bunch of kids learning martial arts from him, especially the group led by young Jiang Yun, were simply too annoying.

They either complained he wasn’t handsome enough or criticized his punching style. 

He was far inferior to the young Hidden Official, at least by eighteen streets.

Zheng Dafeng felt a sense of helplessness.

If only his father looked like Wei Ban or Jiang Shangzhen, would he still be single today? Wouldn’t he have to stand at the door every day to prevent girls from barging in and being inappropriate?

But when did he become inferior even to Chen Ping’an?

Zheng Dafeng rubbed his chin, thinking he was still pretty outstanding compared to that mountain lord, right? 

Just consider that Cen Yuanji every time she passed by the gates of the Fallen Mountain, she would look at him, wanting to speak but then shy away. But when she saw the young mountain lord, she never said a word and wouldn’t even glance his way.

Feng Kangle and Tao Ban sat nearby, each eating a bowl of plain noodles.

Feng Kangle curiously asked, “Dafeng, what does ‘Get up and scratch your head’ mean? Why are there so many drunks fond of randomly spouting that phrase now?”

After getting drunk following a teaching session, Zheng Dafeng had once blurted out a nonsensical speech beginning with “Get up and scratch your head.”

Zheng Dafeng shifted into a cross-legged position, casually saying, “It’s a dish meant to trick people into drinking more, or rather, a kind of snack that doesn’t cost anything whether you’re selling or buying liquor.”

“Get up and scratch your head! Look at the flowers blooming and falling outside, the greenery thickening and reddening. Then look at that dim light, as a lovely lady walks by in a new skirt, her steps quiet. Finally, gaze at the bright moonlit night, where a beauty plays with her jade fingers, her nails like crystals. At last, raise a glass and gaze at the solitary light that shines, with one’s liver and lungs turning to ice and snow!”

Tao Ban remarked, “Some heartless bastards say that our second shopkeeper is a scholar, so he’s the blackest-hearted when it comes to selling wine. But Dafeng, you’re not a scholar, so why do you have that whole set of sayings?”

Zheng Dafeng laughed, “There was a saying I once read in a book that said, ‘Scholars can never bear to see money or power; once they do, they become worse than a whore!’ Such scholars, you aren’t the second shopkeeper, nor am I. I just can’t bear to see pretty girls passing by, their heads lowered in shyness, their steps too hurried. If it’s a hot summer day, then they can hurry a little faster.”

Tao Ban didn’t quite understand, only saying, “I don’t care whether you’re a scholar or not. I just know that those girls you see aren’t being shy.”

Zheng Dafeng slammed the table and turned to shout, “Liu E, what do you think of your brother Dafeng?!”

The young woman was startled and managed a smile, shyly saying, “The shopkeeper’s gaze isn’t right, but he’s actually a good person.”

Tao Ban chuckled, rolling up a chunk of noodles from his bowl, saying he would propose a toast too, while Feng Kangle laughed so hard he put down his chopsticks and clapped the table.

Zheng Dafeng straightened up, raising his wine bowl high, “Get up and scratch your head, I’ll propose a toast!”

Suddenly, Tao Ban said, “I heard that once the door closes, it’ll be a hundred years. I’m not a sword cultivator and can’t learn martial arts. Will I not see the second shopkeeper for the rest of my life?”

Feng Kangle fell silent in an instant.

Zheng Dafeng laughed, “Not a chance. Chen Ping’an wouldn’t let you all go. All our dear second shopkeeper’s travels are for the sake of reunion.”

Tao Ban laughed, “If you speak well, drink more. I can treat you to a jar of Mute Lake wine.”

Having drunk his fill, Zheng Dafeng gently shook his white bowl, “Riches scatter people, while the carefree are like small gods without worries. Who would’ve thought that here too, we could lead a comfortable life?”

Feng Kangle suddenly asked, “Dafeng, how old are you?”

Zheng Dafeng grinned, “Still a young lad who can fry pancakes. If you don’t believe me, I can fry you an egg next time.”

Tao Ban rolled his eyes, saying, “If you were a scholar, I’d let Feng Kangle take your last name.”

Zheng Dafeng looked at the darkening sky and said, “All right, let’s clean up and go back home.”

Zheng Dafeng had rented a small house not far from the tavern in Yan Chi Alley.

After closing the shop and arriving at his residence, Zheng Dafeng opened the courtyard door and cheerfully called out, “Nian Xin!”

For some reason, Nian Xin, who had come for business, saw Zheng Dafeng grinning and rubbing his hands together and simply left.

Zheng Dafeng was disheartened, feeling he hadn’t hosted properly. Once he seated himself in the inner room, he lit the lantern and began to peruse a book he had painstakingly borrowed from Zhu Lian about celestial beings from the mountains. Some pages contained colorful illustrations.

Sitting upright, engrossed in the book, Zheng Dafeng finally closed it, hunching slightly as he walked to the door, leaning against it with his arms crossed, gazing into the night.

Many wandering souls in the world journeyed as far as their strength allowed, glancing back at the distant mountains and waters—unafraid of the long road home, only fearing that when they returned, they would find their old stories had already been forgotten.

Today, Zheng Dafeng was suddenly reminded by Feng Kangle’s question that according to the calculations from the mountain below, as long as he didn’t remain single, he should already have grandchildren.

A man being single is a loss of an eight-foot frame. How could one not feel troubled?

Zheng Dafeng grabbed a handful of sunflower seeds from the table, poured himself a jug of Mute Lake wine, and sat on the threshold, drinking while cracking seeds.

Yet, while cracking seeds and sipping wine, thinking of the Fallen Mountain, Zheng Dafeng felt slightly relieved.

In the past, he had seen all the children of the young generation in that small town of Lizhu Cave Sky.

However, they were no longer young and certainly not children anymore.

After all, even Li Huai had long since come of age.

Zheng Dafeng drank his wine, pondering. Indeed, it was time to “Get up and scratch your head” and let the wine flow.

When Zheng Dafeng thought of that grand wave of martial fortunes surging, he raised his wine jug, laughing, “It’s worth a toast.”

In the realm of martial artists, the most critical was the martial arts summit of the Fallen Mountain.

Because at that peak of martial arts, four individuals would soon stand side by side, and two of them would surely reach the pinnacle, while the other two would at least have a chance of doing so.

The steward Zhu Lian was already at the peak. The first disciple Pei Qian was about to reach the peak. The doorkeeper Zheng Dafeng could reach it at any time.

As for the mountain lord Chen Ping’an, he was the strongest, having ascended to the peak with “unprecedented” might.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 830: The Round-Faced Girl

In the central region of Tongye Continent, it should have been a splendid season for the rain to nourish a hundred grains, clear and pure. Unfortunately, just like last year, no one had picked the tender, fragrant shoots before the rain. Countless green tea mountains were gradually becoming overgrown with weeds, and every household, rich or poor, no longer possessed even a hint of the fragrance of the pre-rain spring tea.

The Northern Jin Dynasty had enjoyed a long period of peace. However, compared to the rest of the continent, it was unfortunately located in a region that was a battleground for military conflicts. Previously, the border cavalry of the Yao family of the Great Quan Dynasty, separated by the 800-mile Songzhen Lake and the Jin Huang Mountain Divine Mansion, had maintained a relatively peaceful coexistence. But with the sudden onset of a celestial upheaval, all the strategies and efforts to strengthen the state were rendered meaningless. The Northern Jin Dynasty had now become a mere shadow of its former self, its vast lands in disarray and devastation.

The Southern Qi, located north of the Great Quan Dynasty, fared little better than the Northern Jin. In the end, they were left with a single emperor who had not shown his face in years, while the feudal lords governed in his stead and the empress acted as a puppet controller. They were still engaged in battles against the monstrous armies from the barbaric lands, but there was no hope of victory, only a continuous retreat, with the Great Quan’s border cavalry reduced to nearly nothing.

The old capital of Southern Qi had turned into a military encampment for the troops of the Taiping Mountain. Meanwhile, the Great Quan Dynasty had lost more than half of its territory, with border forces nearly wiped out. The various state and provincial armies could only retreat to the capital region, and it was rumored that once they captured the renowned Shinjing City, their military tents would be relocated.

The monstrous army from the barbaric lands had landed on the western coast of Tongye Continent years ago. With over thirty military encampments, they advanced methodically, primarily targeting the entrenched celestial sect strongholds. Their campaign spread from west to east, and from south to north, showing little regard for the human dynasties and feudal states along the way. Towns were submerged and ruthlessly destroyed, with no attempts at surrender or pacification. Cities fell, lives were lost, and the fallen were reanimated by the great demon Lord Bai Ying, transforming them into vast armies of bones that only knew death.

Under the golden sun, a vast expanse of golden clouds above the remnants of the Northern Jin lands suddenly saw six rainbow lights halt mid-air before plunging rapidly toward the earth.

A strong wind blew through the sky, ruffling the hair of six young figures—three men and three women. They broke through the cloud cover, revealing an expansive view below.

Among them, a man in a black robe, his hair tied with a white silk ribbon, descended from the sky, resembling an immortal fallen from grace.

Beneath the sea of clouds lay a towering yet dilapidated city, the remnants of a once-great state capital of Northern Jin, barely holding on amid the chaos. This state capital's defensive formation was said to be more robust than many smaller kingdoms' capitals, thanks to two extraordinary individuals within the city: a Golden Core master skilled in formations and a formidable Nascent Soul cultivator, who had worked diligently to keep the crumbling city intact. However, this was not the true reason for the city’s survival; the real reason lay in a celestial being, a major demon, who had earlier been stationed to oversee the grand formation. He had struck down a powerful enemy nearby, causing many of the great demons to avoid this place, deeming it too ominous.

Had it not been for the persistent efforts of Xun Yuan and Jiang Shangzhen from the Yuguizong, who relied on the concentrated fortune of the continent's formation to target celestial beings and ascendant demons, Tongye Continent would have fallen much earlier. Xun Yuan, with his high cultivation and the ability to treat the continent as a small universe, instilled fear in several ascendant demons. Meanwhile, though Jiang Shangzhen was only at the celestial level, his fierce and cunning flying sword made him a formidable adversary. Each time he descended with his sword, he targeted not the ascendant demons but the lower-tier demon cultivators, claiming countless lives.

With a single strike, he could reduce a demon at the Jade Core level—who could kill half a kingdom—either to death or to a state of collapse.

The two major demons, Yang Zhi and Fei Fei, who had returned from the waters between Baoping Continent and North Julu Continent, were specifically looking for traces of Xun Yuan and Jiang Shangzhen.

Yang Zhi had once fought fiercely against Xun Yuan, resulting in injuries on both sides. After that encounter, Xun Yuan had become even more elusive. Only Jiang Shangzhen continued to occasionally strike down enemies in the mortal realm. Fei Fei attempted several times to intercept him, but Jiang Shangzhen’s myriad illusions and methods of escape were extremely elusive, making it impossible to capture him.

In contrast, every time the head of the Great Fushu Academy took action, it was primarily to protect the dynasty and the academy’s formations, slowing the advance of the barbaric forces.

With the fall of Taiping Mountain and Fuyi Sect, there were no longer any grand formations left in Tongye Continent. The timing had shifted, placing Xun Yuan and Jiang Shangzhen in the heart of the barbaric lands, especially Xun Yuan, who had been ambushed by Yang Zhi and Fei Fei at the end of last year, leading to rumors that he had escaped from Tongye Continent and vanished into a secret marine realm, followed by a “little girl with braided hair” who had trailed behind.

The black-robed man wielded a long sword, first breaking through the defensive array and then shattering several incoming magical artifacts with a single strike.

In the city, a golden-armored deity, worshipped in a martial temple, stepped out of the threshold, seemingly alerted by the celestial master not to leave the shrine. This being, once a loyal spirit of the nation, brandished a treasured blade that had absorbed incense for hundreds of years, proactively emerging to engage in battle. He soared into the air, but the black-robed man shattered his golden body with his own flying sword, leaving the city raining down golden fragments.

The remaining five demon cultivators landed within the city. Although the city’s protective array had not been breached, they could not stop the intruders from overpowering it.

One towering demon warrior, over ten feet tall, landed and surveyed his surroundings. He chose a direction and charged straight through the city, smashing through the various markets and buildings, leaving a trail of destruction. Those unfortunate enough to be caught in his path were obliterated, their remains scattered. He continued until he reached the outer city wall, then switched routes, using his resilient physique as a battering ram, mercilessly cleaving through the city.

A sword cultivator picked a densely built area and moved slowly, absorbing the souls and blood of the living, leaving behind desiccated corpses.

Another demon targeted the City God Pavilion, suddenly revealing its true form as a three-hundred-foot-long python, scales glimmering, releasing miasma that corroded wood and stone. It surrounded the entire City God Pavilion and struck its head against the high walls, smashing a plaque bestowed by the Northern Jin monarch. The demon endured numerous magical attacks and heavy artifacts raining down upon it, while the City God and his underlings summoned numerous spirits to attack, all futile against the giant serpent.

A young woman dressed in a green gown, tall and slender, formed a hand seal, summoning her flying sword, “Peacock Feather.” Behind her, like a peacock displaying its plumage, appeared 81 dazzling sword lights made from peacock feathers. Each slender sword light had feathered eyes resembling those of a woman, creating more tiny flying swords, a manifestation of her sword art. As the sword lights shot forth, they left trails of green luminescence in the air, heading straight for the provincial governor’s residence, leaving destruction in their wake.

Another sword cultivator, resembling her, landed on the city wall crowded with soldiers.

Yushi landed on a high rooftop of a noble family’s mansion, not engaging in the rampant slaughter like her companions. She had merely come to unwind, traveling from the Southern Qi capital in search of some amusement. The others were all old acquaintances.

The sword cultivators charging alongside her were friends of Yushi, though they originally had not been well acquainted.

The scattered cities that had not yet been ravaged by the flames of war were few and far between. It was challenging to find remnants of large states like Northern Jin, which were mostly located in remote regions governed by feudal lords, where the military cultivators practiced their skills and vied for merits. Otherwise, such opportunities wouldn't present themselves.

Sitting on the rooftop, Yushi rested her sword across her lap, glancing at the chaos unfolding in the noble residence without concern.

After the Sword Qi Great Wall had been split in two and the cities “ascended” to the fifth realm, and after the old site of the Overhanging Mountain had been cleared for the army’s path at sea, capturing Fuyou Continent and Tongye Continent had actually taken longer than anticipated by two or three years. Otherwise, the barbaric lands would not have been merely a half-continent of Jin Jia Continent but would have included the entire Baoping Continent.
