The losses sustained at the Sword Qi Great Wall were significant, surpassing the initial projections of the Jiazi Camp by about thirty percent.

In truth, this was already a conservative estimate. Yushi knew the reality was more like a forty percent increase.

One misstep could lead to a cascade of failures; the battlefield at the Sword Qi Great Wall was far beyond mere “one thread pulled causing the whole tapestry to unravel.”

The established strategy of the Jiazi Camp was to divide their forces into three, but that was merely a facade to distract the Posa Continent while a small number of elite forces, including Liu Cha, led a fraction of the troops to hold off the enemy. As for Fuyou Continent, it was to be taken, but they were not in a rush regarding Jin Jia Continent. The initial strategy was to push northward from Tongye Continent, swiftly capturing Baoping Continent and North Julu Continent, assimilating the fortunes of the southeastern Tongye Continent and southwestern Fuyou Continent within four years. In fact, Tongye Continent should have changed hands two years ago, becoming part of the barbaric lands.

The Jiazi Camp was not led by sword cultivators, but the young man in wooden clogs had once made a metaphor that the influx of the barbaric army onto the two continents was like sowing beans in a field.

At the beginning of their landing, without dividing their forces, they appeared to be unstoppable. However, compared to the vast land of the continent, their numbers were still too few. They required a continuous influx of reinforcements to fill the gaps in the two continents' territory.

Afterward, they needed to carry out what Mr. Zhou referred to as “transplanting seedlings in wet rice fields,” not treating the two continents as a barren land to plunder. Following the initial shock, they must shift to pacifying the fragmented dynasties, winning over the rogue cultivators among the mountains, aiming to harvest a bountiful autumn within a decade, not expecting a bumper crop but at least managing to convert some of the human forces into the northern armies of the barbaric lands. The focus would be on those desperate mountain cultivators, scattered in the rivers and lakes, as well as various officials and warriors, who would be the first to unite into one army, selecting one or two individuals to enter the Jiazi Camp, taking their opinions seriously.

Thus, once they secured Baoping Continent and Jin Jia Continent, the barbaric lands could establish a firm foothold, trading away half of Fuyou Continent or a portion of Jin Jia Continent to reclaim North Julu Continent.

By then, the barbaric lands would control Tongye, Baoping, and North Julu Continent.

As for the so-called return of Fuyou Continent, in reality, the Jiazi Camp had long since established methods to ensure the complete subjugation of a continent, preventing the barbaric lands from seizing its fortunes. The righteous lands would only regain countless shattered “islands,” like pieces of broken porcelain. Just restoring the old mountains and rivers of the continent closest to the barbaric lands would require immense effort, resources, and goodwill from the central territories.

Due to his special status, Yushi was far from being just one of the Jiazi Camp cultivators or a fledgling sword cultivator under Taiping Mountain, thus he could discern these shocking truths.

A female sword cultivator changed her mind and flew over on her sword toward Yushi.

Her long sword was of considerable quality, drawing a vibrant, colorful arc of light in the air.

Her name was Xian Zao, and together with her sister Yin Su, they were a pair of sword cultivators. Although they were not listed among the hundred sword immortals of Taiping Mountain, they were direct disciples of the major sect, Guanghan City, and were both over three hundred years old.

Guanghan City was one of the sects under the great demon Fei Fei. Years ago, Fei Fei and the lord of the Liuluo River, Yang Zhi, battled for many years, with the female cultivators from Guanghan City contributing significantly.

When Xian Zao transformed into her human form, she appeared to be a young woman with a sharp chin and delicate features. She lifted her skirt, bowed, and called out to Yushi, “Young Master Yushi.”

Yushi did not rise but smiled and nodded.

In the barbaric lands, etiquette was of utmost importance. Those who were overly polite would only provoke the opposite reaction.

After she sheathed her sword, Xian Zao sat down not far from Yushi but did not dare to draw too close. She rested her chin in her hands, observing the chaotic city and softly said, “Young Master Yushi, I’m feeling a bit tired of all this killing. The Righteous Lands have so many cities—capitals, provincial capitals, county cities—more cities than people. Thankfully, they are too timid; they scare themselves half to death before they even think of resisting. In the beginning, I was excited, thinking I wouldn’t have to fight as dangerously as I did at the Sword Qi Great Wall, but now that I’ve killed so many, it’s becoming rather dull.”

Yushi chuckled, “That’s the Righteous Lands for you—prosperous. As long as there’s no war, and no major droughts or locust plagues, people get along harmoniously, and fighting is rare, so the population grows. It’s quite different from our homeland.”

Before the appearance of the great ancestor of Taiping Mountain, the barbaric lands had been in a state of chaos for ten thousand years.

The true world was tumultuous, with demons rampaging. In such a world, there was no concept of “indiscriminate killing.”

Xian Zao pointed toward a part of the city and asked, “I see these kinds of stone arches everywhere. My sister and I can’t read the words on them. Young Master Yushi, you’ve studied, so you know about the Righteous Lands. What are they for?”

The script in the barbaric lands was ancient, said to share a rough origin with that of the Righteous Lands, yet they had evolved differently. Because of this shared origin, even the Confucian sage’s original script was greatly feared by all demons. About a thousand years ago, a writing system called “Shuiyun Shu” began to spread, created by Mr. Zhou, known as the “Literary Sea of the World.”

Yushi explained, “These are unique to the Righteous Lands, used to honor virtuous men and women with good morals. I’ve read that those who are righteous are to be memorialized. Essentially, if a family erects an arch, their descendants will prosper.”

Xian Zao expressed her confusion, “These people sound impressive, but after all these years of fighting, it seems to have been of little use.” 

She had indeed encountered some odd individuals, such as an elderly woman with white hair holding a cane, standing at the entrance of a family shrine. Though she would ultimately die like a tattered piece of cotton, she was unafraid of death—was it because she had lived long enough? She had seen an elderly man clad in scholarly robes who, though facing imminent danger, could only wait for death, dying beside a table piled with books, his hand holding a child, urging the little one to “speak loudly.” Listening to the trembling voice of the younger generation, it might have been a family teaching or words from a sage’s book?

Regardless, when the old man died, his expression was far more composed than many cultivators who offered magical treasures and divine coins, or even the emperors and generals who lay prostrate.

Yet, what significance did it hold? Xian Zao felt it had no meaning; after all, whether old or young, everyone would die.

However, many places that the military camp had deemed “worth attacking”—battlefields, defensive lines, and fortresses—were often easily breached. 

Some high-walled cities fell within mere exchanges, easily conquered.

The newly minted armor was still bright, and the veterans were few.

Only a few sects and the elite troops from seven or eight dynasties had caused some trouble for the barbaric lands.

Especially in the assault on a place called Taiping Mountain, the casualties were heavy, causing two military camps to exhaust their entire forces, ultimately necessitating the dispatch of two additional armies.

Yushi chuckled, finding it difficult to explain the futility of these ethereal matters. They might have a role in educating the heart, yet were utterly useless in battles. Each arch, in a time of peace, was priceless, but in a chaotic world, seemed utterly worthless.

Yushi watched as an elder Nascent Soul cultivator finally could no longer restrain himself, having left the protective formation and engaged in battle alongside Yin Su. She had killed far too many and was deliberately showing off for him. That brute had even taken several heads and casually tossed them onto the formation, creating ripples as if blood had splattered against the walls. As for the giant python, it had resumed its human form and captured two deities from the City God Pavilion, crushing their golden bodies against the formation's outer wall.

Having spoken to him for a while, Xian Zao felt satisfied. She stood up, saying apologetically, “Young Master Yushi, I must go now. Otherwise, my sister will complain that I’m slacking off, and she can go on about it for a long time.”

Yushi waved his hand, smiling as he reminded her, “Be careful of those two human Earth Immortal cultivators. Don't let your guard down just because you’re a Golden Core sword cultivator. Human cultivators are clever, and once they set their minds to it, they can be quite decisive in death.”

Xian Zao nodded vigorously.

Young Master Yushi was of noble birth, yet he was always so easygoing and gentle in his words.

Yushi watched Xian Zao as she departed on her sword, still not intending to intervene.

Having been on the battlefield near the Sword Qi Great Wall too many times, he had accumulated quite a bit of merit and suffered little loss, except for that one significant incident.

After the barbaric lands breached the Sword Qi Great Wall, although their pace in this unfamiliar world slowed slightly, it felt like two Nascent Soul cultivators struggling to subdue an incredibly tough Golden Core sword cultivator, only to find it much easier to deal with a group of lower-tier cultivators whose morale had shattered.

Yushi stood up and looked down.

A well-dressed young man, whose face could almost be described as jade-like, was peeking through the window of a study, watching him.

Another young man, dressed in coarse clothing, was particularly interesting. Upon seeing Xian Zao soaring on her sword, he dashed up to the nearby rooftop, mustered his courage, and stammered, “Are you a mountain cultivator here to save people?”

Yushi replied in the elegant dialect of Tongye Continent, “I don’t understand your Northern Jin dialect.”

To his surprise, the young man immediately switched to the elegant dialect, “Immortal Master, can I practice immortal techniques with you?”

Yushi shook his head, “I’m a demon, not an immortal master. Naturally, I’m not here to save anyone; I’ve come to kill.”

The young man was taken aback.

Yushi waved his hand, “Quickly hide. Wait ten or twenty years, and you might survive.”

The young man’s expression suddenly changed. His eyes gleamed with fervor as he said, “I know where the treasures are hidden in the mansion. I’m willing to lead you there. Can I follow you later?”

Yushi smiled, “Sure, lead the way. I can indeed grant you great wealth. After the world turns upside down, it’s time for new beginnings.”

After all, he was free and had nothing better to do.

Recalling a saying from the Jiazi Camp regarding when the hearts of the people would settle after the barbaric lands took over a continent: it was when all survivors of the war believed they had no way back, no chance to rectify their mistakes. They needed to feel that even if they returned to the Righteous Lands, there would still be no path for them as they would surely be held accountable later. Only then could they be at ease in serving the barbaric lands, becoming even more ferocious and deadly than the demon cultivators themselves. For example, within a nation, ministers would slay their kings in the court, various officials would select someone to die, and within each family, the same principle would apply. This would also occur in ancestral temples, where people would commit heinous acts. Mountain cultivators would have their disciples kill their ancestors, leading to bloodshed among their own sects.

All the rules and rituals painstakingly established by Confucianism would crumble. They would start anew, and for the next thousand years, the only morality that would remain would be that established by Mr. Zhou.

It was said that the young man in wooden clogs was now not only following Mr. Zhou but had also received a surname from him.

Yushi floated down and reached out, pulling the young man, who felt as if he were riding the clouds, beside him. Yushi intentionally ignored the young man’s sweating face and casually asked, “Is there anything you wish to obtain? Perhaps a certain woman you never dared to hope for? Or someone you wish to kill, like someone you hate the most?”

The young man gritted his teeth and replied, “I don’t want anything for myself; everything should rightfully belong to you, Master. I dare not ask for anything. But I want to kill two people!”

Yushi raised an eyebrow in curiosity, “Who are they?”

The young man clenched his fists, trembling, “One is called Han Chengyi, the young master of this residence, and the other is Han Shuyi, his sister. She’s a woman who has just returned home.”

Yushi laughed, “What deep hatred do you have for that brother and sister?”

It was apparent that this person was a servant of the residence, possibly born into a lowly background.

The young man shook his head, then clenched his fists, trembling, with his head lowered, “I just want them to die! One is born lucky, and the other is an unashamed wretch!”

Yushi stopped and made the young man look up, meeting his gaze, the latter’s forehead beaded with sweat.

Yushi smiled, “In the Righteous Lands, the bad people are the good people in the barbaric lands. Don’t worry, you won’t die. I will also help you fulfill your wish. However, with me around, you might be worried about not being able to do what you once considered evil. Before you kill, you can do some things you’ve always wanted to do; for instance, if you want to kill two, then kill more. I’ll wait for you here. Don’t worry about me waiting too long; I’m quite free.”

As he spoke, Yushi took out a small, exquisite yellow silk pouch from his waist. When his fingers brushed against it, clouds and rainbows emerged. A small black dragon wound around the pouch’s surface, enveloping it in mist.

Yushi lightly shook the yellow pouch, and the black dragon fell to the ground, transforming into a robust man with pitch-black eyes. Yushi tossed the pouch to the young man, “Take it. In the future, this dragon servant will act as your protector, teaching you immortal techniques and helping you become an influential figure in Tongye Continent. Don’t think that just because you are from the Han family, even the once-mighty emperor or the mountain Earth Immortals will bow low and treat you with respect.”

“By the way, what’s your name?”

The young man took the pouch with both hands, his expression excited, voice trembling, “Master, my name is Lu Jianxin. Jian as in ‘to inspect,’ and Xin as in ‘heart.’ I once had an older brother named Lu Jiaoguang.”

Yushi chuckled, “To educate the young is to bring great brightness; to examine the heart is to be diligent and alert. Those are good names your father must have asked the family tutor for, right?”

Lu Jianxin wiped the sweat from his forehead, “Master is truly knowledgeable.”

Yushi waved his hand, “From now on, follow me, do more work, and speak less. You can skip the flattery and pandering; that will get you killed.”

Lu Jianxin no longer dared to speak out of turn. He bowed and ran off, the black dragon following behind, causing the young man to feel both frightened and suddenly emboldened.

Yushi planned to make this Lu Jianxin the lord of the state city, allowing the young man to experience a comfortable life as a local ruler. Then he would have the black dragon meticulously record the changes in the city’s customs and hand it over to the young man in wooden clogs for review.

As for why Lu Jianxin held such a deep-seated hatred for the siblings, who could say? Perhaps one winter, he had seen a young man wrapped in a white fox fur coat enjoying the snow, making him feel even more ashamed. 

Or perhaps he had long admired that woman and merely exchanged glances one day. Though she had said nothing, her unintentional gaze had spoken volumes.

None of this was strange; Yushi did not care what the truth was. What truly amused him was that at that moment, he could see Lu Jianxin’s genuine gratitude, admiration, and fear directed towards him, along with a determination to gamble everything, even his life. Lu Jianxin was clearly willing to act on a fleeting impulse to eliminate all his long-standing grievances. The barbaric lands needed more of these extreme and pitiable souls.

These individuals were likely to become what the young man in wooden clogs referred to as the “filling the tombs of Confucianism.” Mr. Zhou once joked that the Righteous Lands had too many scholars who loved to adopt false moralities while being true villains. They genuinely believed that their hypocritical demeanor was invisible to the world, but in truth, that was far from the case. Some were angry yet silent year after year, while others dreamed of becoming such people, thus digging their own graves. It was no wonder that many had come to fill in the graves.

Suddenly, Yushi raised his head.

A great omen filled the heavens, rapidly spreading from a distance. It was undoubtedly the immense aura of an ascendant being.

Otherwise, it would not have been possible for Yushi to clearly sense such a profound energy here.

A woman with scarlet eyes appeared beside Yushi, softly saying, “Young Master, please temporarily leave this place. The Yu Guizong’s Xun Yuan was first intercepted and killed by me and Yang Zhi, then pursued by Xiao Xuan, and has now entered that hidden marine realm, completely shattered. There’s no escape left for him. Xun Yuan is now projected at the Eastern Sea, intending to split Tongye Continent, which may very well affect this place.”

Yushi shook his head, “You only need to protect me and Xian Zao; I want to see how Xun Yuan plans to split Tongye Continent.”

The great demon Yang Zhi nodded.

Yushi furrowed his brow and asked, “What about Xiao Xuan?”

The great demon replied, “That secret realm is very peculiar, as if Xun Yuan was lured away to another world. It’s possible that this time, Xun Yuan’s escape was a deliberate diversion to lead Xiao Xuan away.”

She suddenly vanished, returning moments later with a slightly changed expression. “Xiao Xuan has finally drawn his sword.”

Yushi looked up at the sky. Above the Eastern Sea of Tongye Continent, a rift in the celestial canopy opened, as Xiao Xuan broke through another sky with his sword, allowing him to “ascend” back to the Righteous Lands. He then directed a magnificent sword light toward the towering projection of Xun Yuan, the momentum rivaling Bai Ye’s first strike on Fuyou Continent.

That unparalleled sword light intertwined with water, fire, and thunder.

The great demon Yang Zhi looked up, softly saying, “That old fellow is doomed.”

Yushi chuckled, “Compared to you, Xun Yuan isn’t really that old.”

Yang Zhi smiled slightly and said, “I’ll go and grab a few pieces of glass-like golden bodies for you.”

Yushi was about to shake his head when Yang Zhi had already darted off. After all, as a major demon, he could not casually reprimand or obstruct her.

Moreover, Yang Zhi had also quietly warned him to “be careful.”

Yushi remained expressionless as he strolled leisurely within the noble residence.

Suddenly, the flow of time around Yushi seemed to freeze inexplicably.

Yet Yushi felt no fear; the robe he wore was a gift from Yang Zhi, capable of withstanding several strikes from a celestial sword cultivator without him dying.

Moreover, should Yushi’s robe encounter any spells or flying swords, as long as Yang Zhi wasn’t a continent away, she could arrive in an instant.

Yushi turned to see a handsome young man in a golden robe, casually tossing the black dragon that was thrashing wildly but unable to escape from the yellow pouch.

The young man glanced at Yushi’s robe and smiled, “It’s rare to see something I desire, but my life is worth more.”

Yushi clasped his hands together, “I see you, Sect Master Jiang.”

Jiang Shangzhen raised a hand and waved lightly, “No need for such courtesy; it’s not every day a father reunites with his son. Just call me father. Remember to have that little servant Fei Fei massage and knead my shoulders, and you’ll have made up for some filial duty.”

Yushi was taken aback, laughing silently for a moment before asking, “What about that young man protected by the black dragon?”

Jiang Shangzhen smiled, “Oh, him? His soul has exchanged places with a handsome young man. I reckon when the flow of time returns to normal, he’ll be quite confused, wondering who he is and where he is, and what he should do.”

Yushi inquired, “Aren’t you going to save Xun Yuan, instead of chatting with me here?”

“Why save someone far away when you’re so close and haven’t killed? When I, Jiang, become clever, I often don’t even know what I’m thinking. How could you foresee that?” 

Jiang Shangzhen pouted, “Besides, this wild son of mine is nothing but a little useless; Fei Fei, that wretched girl, actually had the gall to gift you her precious robe. I’m too timid; killing you for a sword isn’t worth it, so I’ll just be satisfied with this half-immortal-grade yellow pouch I picked up.”

Yushi remained silent.

This robe had one of its abilities to “lock swords,” making it more mysterious than Du Mao’s sword-swallowing boat.

Yushi had long wanted to use himself as bait to provoke Jiang Shangzhen’s renowned sword, which was said to be able to “slice through immortals with a willow leaf.”

Jiang Shangzhen tucked the yellow pouch into his sleeve, and the frozen flow of time resumed its normal pace.

Yushi asked, “Why don’t you look for that She Yue or Dou Kou?”

One was among the ten young talents of several continents, while the other was a potential candidate.

The key was that they were unlike Yushi and his companions; they did not have a major demon as their protector.

Jiang Shangzhen smiled nonchalantly.

In a study, a handsome young man in elaborate clothing was locked in a struggle with Lu Jianxin. Without the protection of the black dragon, relying solely on strength, he could easily defeat Han Chengyi, the young master of the Han family, who was currently suffering from a beating that left him bloodied, regretting not having sought out that beautiful woman first. 

Lu Jianxin, fueled by his rage, relentlessly pummeled the “young master,” tears streaming down his face, his gaze exceptionally fierce as he cursed in a foreign voice, squeezing the neck of the “young master.”

Jiang Shangzhen smiled and said, “Alright, Sister Fei Fei, no need to hide anymore. You’re all grown up and beautiful; why not show yourself?”

Fei Fei unexpectedly stepped out from within Yushi’s robe, speaking to him, “Young Master, it’s just an illusion created by a secret technique, akin to the Nascent Soul level. Jiang Shangzhen’s true self isn’t here.”

Jiang Shangzhen nodded, “Of course. I never act unless I’m completely certain. If I’m not confident, I wouldn’t dare to kill me. I came here just to greet you two. Remember, whenever Sister Fei Fei wears that robe again, Young Master Yushi should obediently hide in the military tent; otherwise, it’s natural for me to beat my son.”

As Jiang Shangzhen’s illusion dissipated, the yellow pouch remained, as he was not foolish enough to let it leave with him. He had merely been teasing Yushi.

The latest disciple of the Yu Guizong, who might also be its last leader, felt a tinge of melancholy as he turned his gaze toward the Eastern Sea, where the golden body of an ascendant cultivator began to shatter. Even as the scene became magnificent, it was ultimately a reminder of the truth that living was better than dying.

Jiang Shangzhen muttered, “Cursing that old, immortal bastard for so many years, it’s genuinely painful to lose him. It’ll be difficult to ask for a curse after he’s gone.”

Jiang Shangzhen was left with only a head, as the remaining illusion overlooked the strange pair of master and servant, smiling, “New and old accounts must be settled. One involves bullying my woman, and the other involves plotting against Xun Yuan. In the future, Jiang will take his time to settle the score with you two; I’ll exhaust myself in the process.”

As the frost falls, the sun descends into the earth, and the yin energy begins to condense. The autumn dryness causes damage to fluids, so it’s best to guard against the cold outside and clear heat within.

Thus, there arose a custom of eating persimmons after a light rain, said to strengthen bones and prevent chapped lips in winter.

Under a persimmon tree adorned with bright red fruits like hanging lanterns, in the misty sky, dark branches contrasted with the vivid red, creating a festive atmosphere.

A young girl, appearing around seventeen or eighteen years old, with a slightly plump figure and round cheeks, was dressed in cotton clothing. She stood on tiptoe, straightened her back, and wielded a stick she had found to knock down several persimmons from the tree. After tossing aside the stick, she bent down to gather the bright red fruits in her coat.

Finally, she squatted in front of a county boundary monument, munching on a persimmon while examining the carved inscription, which read, “Established by the officials, Yongning County Boundary.” To the left were some small characters indicating the country and year.

She thought it was impressive that such a stone, which passersby wouldn’t spare a glance, could define the territory of neighboring regions.

In her hometown, it wasn’t like that. There were no such regulations, nor could they afford to care. Fights were too fierce, tempers too short, making it easy to lose everything.

After arriving here, she had traveled extensively, collecting coins made of gold, silver, and bronze from various countries, as well as books from various schools of thought. She found everything appealing, and in the war-torn cities, the more doors there were to wealthy families, the more likely they were to have been lost, making it easy to gather items once thought valuable, even easier than knocking down persimmons.

Currently, the Northern regions of Tongye Continent were actually more unstable than the south.

The celestial sects of Tongye Continent were relatively few compared to the nine continents of the Righteous Lands, with more significant mountains and fewer celestial beings. In any extensive territory, it remained quite challenging for common mortals to seek out immortals, much easier to encounter an emperor.

Many small nations in the increasingly impoverished and spiritually barren regions of Tongye Continent were, in the chaos, less prone to calamity. Even if there were a few so-called celestial beings with some knowledge, they were eager to abandon their mountains, taking their ancestral halls with them in haste, leaving no concern for others. Once ascended, they would cut ties, roam freely, and enjoy the essence of nature without many worries.

If she hadn’t preferred wandering and wasn’t coveting military achievements, treasures, and auspicious locations, perhaps the people of Yongning County would have waited several decades to encounter an outsider like her.

She came from far away yet was not merely an outsider. 

Having finished the persimmons, she picked up a branch, stood up, leaned against the boundary monument, and lightly scraped the mud off the soles of her shoes.

Earlier, outside the county’s literary temple, perhaps due to the frost-fall season, officials led a group of scholars in reciting blessings, whether plowing or weaving, to stave off wind and rain. “May the children and grandchildren prosper, for I am the granary…” 

In any case, she couldn’t understand, having only learned some of the grand dialect of the Righteous Lands. Furthermore, she couldn’t speak the elegant dialect of Tongye Continent and knew nothing of the various official languages and dialects. She simply observed the officials and scholars, gathering to petition for the people, which looked quite similar to what they were doing. Only that official wearing the official garb seemed a bit too portly, with a rosy complexion that made his neck nearly invisible. Shouldn’t learned men be lean like Mr. Zhou?

A group of children riding bamboo horses passed by, playacting a wedding. 

When they caught sight of the woman standing by the stone, they exchanged a few glances but paid her no mind, for she looked unremarkable.

She continued her solitary wander.

Following the traces of spiritual energy, she finally spotted a celestial sect, a small one, not commonly seen in Tongye Continent. 

However, it seemed that the cultivators of that sect were out, so she did not visit. Ultimately, between the two mountain peaks, hundreds of miles away, the fog swirled like a creek flowing gently. There were celestial cultivators setting up a magical net, aiming to catch a type of bird, akin to fishing in the valley, scaring the birds into the net. Several wind-riding cultivators kept startling the bird flocks, while those lower-tier cultivators, unable to ride the wind, kept running through the mountains, creating noise to frighten the birds.

The young woman in cotton clothing sat quietly on a low tree branch, observing the scene.

It seemed that after the barbaric lands arrived at Tongye Continent, it mirrored this scene, with startled birds constantly flying into the net.

Yet she wondered whether those celestial beings, who had once regarded the kings of the earth as mere puppets, would envy those lowly mountain ants when death approached.

They probably wouldn’t care; in an instant of life and death, even those so-called enlightened beings would likely be left in confusion.

She suddenly wished to find someone to chat with, not necessarily someone who spoke the language of the barbaric lands, but at least someone who could speak the grand dialect of the Central Earth, which was now difficult to come by. Small towns’ City God Temples and Water Gods’ shrines were of no use; they would likely only speak the dialects of Tongye Continent. Unfortunately, those scholars from the academies either died on the battlefield or retreated to the Yuguizong and Tongye Sect. The elite from great dynasties’ Five Mountains were certainly dead, and the merchant’s children were exceptionally nimble, proficient in both earning money and avoiding disaster, making them hard to catch.

As for the upper-tier cultivators, she once fortuitously encountered one hiding deep in the mountains who had not established a sect. He was what the Righteous Lands called a hermit. When she met him, she ignored him, mainly because she was too lazy to act, as she had previously visited a not-too-large celestial estate where a Golden Core and Nascent Soul Earth Immortal were stationed. The conversation had not gone well, and she ended up killing them with a single punch. 

It wasn’t much; during her early landing days, she had also killed a Jade Core cultivator without a second thought.

A group of young men and women practicing their lower-tier breathing techniques slowly descended the mountain. One female cultivator held freshly picked chrysanthemums, as frost had killed a hundred flowers, leaving only this flourishing grass.

The young woman in cotton clothing propped her hands on the tree branch, showing little interest in those female cultivators. Instead, she focused on the chrysanthemums, her thoughts wandering. She had heard that there was a place in the Righteous Lands called the Hundred Flowers Blessed Land, and among the flower gods, it seemed that this flower god held a high position. It had many elegant names, all quite melodious, such as Frost Petals and Smiling Blossoms, while the names like Sun Essence and Week’s Weaving sounded rather odd. The young woman preferred such chaotic matters, having always found the Righteous Lands filled with intriguing things, which was why she had come to explore.

The earlier reason she had “returned to the mortal realm from the heavens” in the barbaric lands and then arrived at Tongye Continent was due to the great demon Lotus Flower Temple Master, who had been killed by Dong San with a sword. After all, in a sense, she considered herself a neighbor of the Lotus Flower Temple Master. Of course, saying “neighbor” was somewhat exaggerated, as they were actually quite far apart. In the barbaric lands, three months could feel like suspended time, but the distance between two bright moons was merely an illusion of proximity. Occasionally, only someone named Yao Jia would visit her home.

Those young men and women walking through the mountains spoke of how “the moonlit autumn clouds had fallen into the water, setting fire to the cold stream and turning it to ash.” Their verses, some borrowed from books and some self-composed, were echoed among them.

The young woman understood nothing, feeling a bit vexed. In the past, she would have endured it; after all, she was just a passerby, but just as she thought to find someone to talk to, she felt irritated. In a fit of irritation, she habitually clapped her face with both hands, making a significant noise that caught the attention of some young cultivators, whose gazes turned unfriendly. Some regarded her as a petty thief, while others dismissed her for her unremarkable appearance, but the ones who looked at her as if she were a flying bird caught in a net angered her the most.

However, when she finally spotted a round-faced little girl staring at her with wide, curious eyes, the young woman grinned broadly, feeling quite pleased. Despite the language barrier, she raised her arm to wave at the little girl, greeting her.

The little girl quickly waved energetically, and when her seniors and older siblings glanced her way, she immediately tucked her hands behind her back, looking up at the sky.

Seeing the round-faced girl made the young woman smile, for there was nothing cuter than that.

The group ultimately did not say anything, oblivious to the narrow escape they had made from the gates of death, and returned to the mountain.

The young woman leaned against the tree branch, grinning, “So you’re Jiang Shangzhen?”

A man standing on a tree branch smiled and nodded, “Sister She Yue, with your round face, you look extremely beautiful. So I changed my mind.”

The young woman continued gazing into the distance, saying, “I’m not someone you can just kill at will. Why provoke me?”

Jiang Shangzhen sat beside her, waiting for the moonlight to descend upon the mortal realm. He asked, “Have you ever seen someone named Liu Cai, the sword cultivator who raises the most sword gourds? Mr. Zhou mentioned that apart from his heartfelt emotions and immediacy, this fellow has a long list of lower-tier sword gourds.”

Mr. Zhou wanted her to find Liu Cai, but she need not concern herself with other matters.

Jiang Shangzhen nodded, “I know him.”

He turned his head.

Jiang Shangzhen continued to smile and said, “Unfortunately, he doesn’t know me. Sister She Yue, let’s not talk about Liu Cai, but about my brother. Since we both have nothing to do, I can invite you for a drink.”

She turned her head back, “Don’t bother me; go bother someone else.”

Jiang Shangzhen sighed, “I’m about to be driven mad by all of Tongye Continent; who else can I complain to?”

She replied, “Then just go die.”

Jiang Shangzhen chuckled, “Sister She Yue, you’re genuinely good at conversation, so we should chat more.”

Gradually, the moon rose over the willow treetops, and the moonlight shimmered like water, filling the world.

The round-faced girl clapped her cheeks, and Jiang Shangzhen smiled slightly before taking his leave. 

She slowly stood up, wondering why Mr. Zhou placed such importance on that Golden Core sword cultivator.

Her expression shifted slightly as she took to the winds, ascending to the celestial canopy. Using her innate magical ability, she vaguely saw the distant celestial canopy of Baoping Continent, where multiple depressions appeared like great pits, rippling with waves. Ultimately, ancient deities emerged from the gaps, although they were suppressed by the heavens and their golden forms shrank considerably, they still bore the grandeur of the Five Mountains. Meanwhile, on the ground of Baoping Continent, it seemed a great sun was rising, its light excessively blinding, causing the round-faced girl to feel irritable, wishing she could stretch her hand to press that sun back into the earth.

In an instant, a willow leaf silently arrived at her brow.

She disappeared in a flash, reappearing on a mountain peak thousands of miles away, her soul and physical form reconstituting seamlessly, even her cotton clothing and boots remained intact.

Moreover, Jiang Shangzhen’s sudden sword strike had seemingly not irked her; her mind remained deeply immersed in the strange phenomena occurring in Baoping Continent, leaving her standing at the mountaintop in a daze.

Jiang Shangzhen appeared beside her, clad in a golden robe, his sleeves billowing. Inside the golden robe, it seemed he wore several layers of robes. He apologetically said, “Sister-in-law, it’s a misunderstanding, a misunderstanding.”

And then another willow leaf pierced through his brow.

The round-faced girl once again coalesced in another location, finally beginning to frown as she noticed many “Jiang Shangzhen” waiting nearby, “Are you really going to persist?”

“Good dogs fear the stick; good women fear the persistent suitor,” Jiang Shangzhen said, his hands tucked into his sleeves, eyes narrowed in a smile. “Since the old saying doesn’t work, and Sister She Yue shows no hint of romantic feelings, Jiang Da Ge can only act against his conscience, daring to destroy flowers.”

She replied, “Do as you wish. Sect Master Jiang’s happiness is what matters.”

After six successive strikes, Jiang Shangzhen chased after the moonlight, traversing thousands of miles. Ultimately, he stood beside the young woman, reluctantly retracting the willow leaf, pinching it between his fingers, “Forget it, forget it; indeed, I can't do anything to you, girl.”

One by one, the figures of Jiang Shangzhen, each wearing different robes and carrying various treasures, continually merged with the person beside Sister She Yue.

Then, in a deep ravine three thousand miles away, a sword light struck amidst a pool of moonlight.

Sister She Yue finally surfaced from the water, in a small pond, her round face evoking the vastness of the ocean under the bright moon.

Blood seeped from the corners of her mouth, and she fixed her gaze on the man standing by the pond’s edge, her expression dark as she said, “Jiang Shangzhen, are you really willing to damage the Dao?”

The one who drew his sword was none other than Jiang Shangzhen’s true self.

Jiang Shangzhen had been hunted many times; he had the skills to escape each time.

Certainly, he wasn’t just playing around; glancing into the distance, he withdrew his gaze and whispered to her, then laughed heartily as his form dissipated.

(The chapter ends here.)

 **Chapter 831: The White Clouds Send Liu Sixteen Back to the Mountains**

On a bustling stone arch bridge, wild grass thrived in the crevices of the blue stone slabs. 

A royal tomb, neglected for only a few years, had become a desolate sight, with foxes and rabbits scurrying about. 

Strange creatures from the mountains and marshes left their hidden caves in droves, rampaging through the streets below, brazenly shouting outside the Martial and Literary Temples and the City God Shrine, showing no fear at all. 

A king lay drunken in the embrace of a beauty, murmuring repeatedly that the fault was not his. The woman gently caressed the face of the man in the dragon robe. Earlier, in the grand hall, the military generals had looked pale while the civil officials jointly suggested that the king leave the city to present the imperial seal. 

During the previous Xiaoyuan Festival, on the fifteenth day of the tenth month, the Water Officer had performed rituals to avert misfortune. Normally, there would be customs of burning incense branches, offering gold and silver packages, and releasing prayer lanterns. However, this year, no one burned the incense or the gold and silver packages, nor did anyone release the prayer lanterns. 

In a hidden chamber, a father and son, both serving as Prime Minister and Minister of the Interior respectively, consoled themselves as the elder, a cultured leader of the nation, insisted that there must be a solution. “It makes no sense to completely eradicate us; they can't possibly leave nothing behind.” 

In a county town, a theater stood adjacent to a village school, where the old Confucian had always despised students attending performances by painted-faced actresses. Yet, that night, as darkness fell, the old scholar sat on a bench alongside the children, listening to the ghostly sounds of the play. 

In a remote little nation untouched by war, there was a Taoist temple built on a cliff, accessible only by a winding mountain path. 

A scholar in a Confucian robe led a young-looking sword cultivator up the mountain, as if they were visiting a small temple embedded in the cliffside. This place had been a temporary resting spot for a so-called "True Man of Taiping Mountain," who had taken in an unnamed disciple years ago. The incense had wafted there for ages, but it was ultimately a casual, heartless act, and the disciple had never amounted to much. As a practitioner of the Dao, he had aged over a hundred years, becoming frail and weak, with a few successors even less capable than he. It could be said that each generation had outdone the last in mediocrity. The old Taoist still likely had no idea who the "young" master in the ancestral hall portrait really was. 

The scholar and the sword cultivator traveled together without much purpose. The scholar had just returned from the Tongye Sect, while the sword cultivator had been stationed nearby and suggested this outing to clear their minds.

Not long ago, three great demons had plotted in Tongye Continent, with the one who successfully became the true disciple of Taiping Mountain receiving the most credit. When a young man from the Fuyi Sect exposed their scheme, it forced him to act prematurely, seemingly ruining their plans. Yet in the long run, this proved to be an accidental stroke of luck. Unfortunately, he had not been able to team up with the white ape to kill Zhong Kui. Since he had now gone missing, it was most likely due to some trickery from the old Taoist of the temple, and thus he would help gather whatever remaining incense offerings he could in the vast world. 

The scholar said, “You shouldn’t have killed her. It doesn’t matter if you kill a few from the Jade Purity realm, but this one was not meant to die. You even had to protect a whole Jade Zhi Ridge for her sake.” 

The sword cultivator replied, “Sir, I couldn’t help it when I saw her begging like a beggar.” 

The scholar laughed in anger, “If this were Feiran saying such things, I wouldn’t be surprised, but hearing it from you, it just doesn’t sit well.” 

The sword cultivator nodded, “Things went too smoothly in Tongye Continent, and I got a bit carried away.” 

The scholar continued, “The upheaval at Jade Zhi Ridge could have been a turning point for Tongye Continent, implying that the mountains and rivers of the entire region could gradually shift from chaos to order. Then I could help record your merit in the Jiazhi ledger. If I had known earlier, I should have thrown you over to Taiping Mountain to help your fellow disciples protect the path, so we wouldn’t have lost two. Including you, it’s not that you couldn’t die, it’s just that dying too early would be a waste of talent; you haven’t even had the chance to realize your ambitions with all you’ve learned.” 

Though saddened by the deaths of two of their fellow disciples, the elder brother, Shoucheng, felt no guilt at all. 

The scholar was Zhou Mi, and the sword cultivator was Shoucheng. They were a master and disciple pair. 

Zhou Mi walked the narrow path with his disciple Shoucheng and could already see the small temple ahead. 

People of the Dao observed the stars and the moon, and thus temples were commonly built on mountain peaks. 

Zhou Mi did not rush to enter the temple with its tightly shut doors but instead gazed out at the mountains and rivers with Shoucheng. He chuckled softly, “A person who has seen the sun, moon, and rivers, only to lose their sight, suffers more than a young blind person.” 

Shoucheng discerned the underlying meaning in his master’s words. 

A person who has lost something only comes to treasure what they currently have even more. Therefore, as long as the survivors on Tongye Continent plan things well in the wild world ahead, they won’t thank the vast world that has brought them all this. Most will secretly rejoice, grateful that the wild world has shown them some leniency, while they will continue to harbor hatred for the Confucian temples in the central lands, blaming them for all the suffering on Tongye Continent, and will despise all other continents that have not been affected by war. 

A young temple acolyte swaggered over to the two, bowed with respect, and in the local dialect, asked the scholar why he had come. 

The acolyte was about seven or eight years old, his tone filled with arrogance. He bowed at the door as if he had learned proper etiquette from his master and felt it unnecessary to be polite to two mundane scholars who would soon decay. 

Their master, the old temple master, was a divine being at the Sea Observation level, rarely meeting his match in the nation, and wherever he went, he would be respectfully called a celestial being or a true man. The master had mentioned in private that this ancestor was just two steps away from what was known as “Earth Immortal” in Daoist texts. 

These two mundane visitors from the mountains below—what did it matter if they were wealthy or well-born? After all, they were still just people from the foot of the mountain coming to see someone from above. 

Zhou Mi glanced at the little acolyte and turned to smile, “What a stroke of luck! To find something without even looking, it seems the timing and the Dao of Tongye Continent are truly on our side. Shoucheng, did you notice anything unusual?” 

Shoucheng looked confused, “Please enlighten me, sir.” 

Zhou Mi took hold of the acolyte’s arm and gently tapped his wrist with two fingers. The acolyte lifted onto his toes, like a chick being picked up, and for some reason, whether out of instinct or submissiveness, he refrained from cursing the scholar. 

Shoucheng focused intently and saw that after his master used his abilities on the young acolyte, faint glimmers of light flickered in the child’s palm before quickly vanishing into thin air. 

The acolyte’s hand had appeared as if it had been dipped in ink, now washed but still holding some remnants. 

Zhou Mi released the acolyte's wrist and asked, “Has this temple ever had a Taoist named Liu Cai who went down the mountain to wander? When he left, did he bring along a few gourds of various sizes?” 

The acolyte rubbed his wrist, stepping back nervously, “How do you know about that? But we don’t have a Liu Cai here, just a local fool nicknamed Liu Woodhead. He can do any odd jobs, from fishing to hunting to chopping wood. Whatever can make money, he’ll do it. According to my master, if there were a nunnery on the mountain, he could even sell rouge and powders there. That fool comes to our temple every now and then to swindle money; he’s quite a big patron of ours. My master hasn’t bothered with him in recent years. The last time he came to the temple, he brought a basket of pine torches and a few large fish, not asking for any copper coins or silver but rummaging through the storeroom for some old gourds that had gathered dust for years, claiming he’d use them as currency. I watched him curiously as he picked up all those worthless things, one by one, and held them up to his ear, shaking and swaying.” 

What was referred to as the storeroom of the temple was actually just a shed where old junk was piled. 

Zhou Mi cast a glance at the small temple and chuckled, “Everything is interconnected. Truly a remarkable person.” 

Shoucheng asked in thought, “Sir, are Liu Cai’s ‘Heart’s Concerns’ and ‘Immediate’ sword-raising gourds, sourced from here?” 

Zhou Mi shook his head, “Liu Cai had the two sword-raising gourds first; only then did he acquire those two ‘life-bound flying swords.’ Otherwise, the founding ancestor of this temple, as someone at the upper level, wouldn’t be so blind as not to see the quality of the sword-raising gourds. Moreover, he had a penchant for collecting them, so what truly made it unclear for him to distinguish between genuine and fake, depth and shallowness, should be those two strange flying swords.” 

What followed from the scholar’s words made Shoucheng’s expression grow serious. 

“That temple’s big patron is likely Liu Cai’s disciple and protector, because Liu Cai who came to this temple was merely a wandering spirit of his yin form; his real body might not even be on Tongye Continent.” 

Shoucheng asked, “Does sir want to find Liu Cai, not just to have him counter Chen Pingan, but also to meet this ‘patron’?” 

Zhou Mi sighed, “In this world, the arts of yin and yang are evolving, and one person monopolizes half the territory.” 

At the ancestral mountain of the Yuguizong, on the Divine Inscription Peak. 

The old sect master, Xun Yuan, had died a valiant death in battle. A great cultivator at the Ascension level, his glass-like body shattered into fragments scattered across the heavens and earth, mostly intercepted by the great demons. 

The current sect master, Jiang Shangzhen, had proven he was still alive and lively by appearing in the human realm with a stunning glance. 

However, the situation had collapsed. A celestial being without the protection of the heavens found it difficult to support a collapsing building. 

The master of Jiuyi Peak, Wei Ying, who had originally had a better chance of succeeding Jiang Shangzhen as sect master, had gone to Baoping Continent to serve as a subordinate sect master, temporarily working for the Da Li Song clan, and would be unable to return to Yuguizong. 

The old patriarch glanced at the chair opposite him, then at the two empty chairs beneath the ancestral hall portrait. 

Jiang Shangzhen had moved from the opposite seat to below the portrait. 

It was painful to look at for too long. 

He glanced at the moonlight outside the main door. 

A deity in charge of the Yuguizong’s finances, Tian Cai Di Bao, named Song Shengtang, exclaimed in anger, “Why is our sect master Jiang still wandering outside? Are we to watch our sect members die day by day? What’s the point of drawing swords if we don’t help our own mountain?” 

Calling Jiang Shangzhen “sect master” felt a little excessive—it was not merely dropping the surname “Jiang” from “sect master.” This was a subtle stance. 

Jiang Shangzhen had not genuinely won over the Yuguizong’s ancestral hall. 

However, one significant reason for such an awkward situation was the previous existence of the old sect master, Xun Yuan. 

Moreover, the Jiang clan’s control of the Cloud Cave blessed land had always been akin to a fiefdom within the Yuguizong, which irked many. Thus, Zhao Shengtang and Jiang Shangzhen had always been at odds; whenever the Divine Inscription Peak’s ancestral hall convened, it was famously a case of dogs biting dogs, yet Jiang Shangzhen always came out on top, even giving Zhao Shengtang the nickname, “Bald Old Dog Zhao.” 

An older ancestor, Liu Huamao, who bore a deep grudge against Jiang Shangzhen, sat near the main door. Her talent was not exceptional, having relied on spending a vast amount of celestial money and precious resources in her early years to barely reach the upper level. 

Jiang Shangzhen almost always initiated conversations with Liu Huamao during meetings. 

“Sister Liu, what a lovely name, full of grace and beauty, perpetually eighteen, and her face like today’s.” 

Under such dire circumstances, Liu Huamao had to force herself to say a word of truth to Jiang Shangzhen, “It’s certain that some great demon is watching over here, responsible for killing Jiang Shangzhen. There may not just be one old beast lying in wait.” 

There was no way she would call him sect master. 

Her reasoning was that when she was young, being close to the water’s edge, she wanted to explore the Cloud Cave blessed land. As for cultivating the Dao, that was just a side endeavor. 

However, Jiang Shangzhen, who was then the young lord of the Cloud Cave blessed land, had stealthily attached himself to a woman from the blessed land with some strange method, and when he and Liu Huamao met, they hit it off and called each other sisters. Afterward, they traveled together, and during one visit to a place called Furong Pu in the Cloud Cave blessed land, under the pleasant moonlight, the girl shyly began to undress, turning red as a tomato. Liu Huamao playfully teased her a few times and pinched the “girl’s” tender cheeks. 

Looking back, it was a tragic and calamitous memory. 

After that, Liu Huamao began to practice frantically, aiming to catch up to Jiang Shangzhen’s level, hoping to find an excuse to severely injure that bastard. 

Unfortunately, along the path of cultivation, talent, roots, and temperament all played a role, and there would always be someone better; Jiang Shangzhen, recognized as the next peak master of Jiuyi Peak, didn’t seem to be particularly diligent in his cultivation but always surpassed her by two levels. 

After she had caught up to him by one level, Jiang Shangzhen met her and, after flattering her for a while, turned around and left. Not long after, he broke through. 

There was an interesting dynamic in the Yuguizong ancestral hall meetings. 

Those who spoke more and had louder voices were less related to their realms; it was simply about who got along worse with Jiang Shangzhen. 

Over time, Liu Huamao, with her mediocre talent at the Jade Purity level, gained unexpected weight in the meetings at Divine Inscription Peak’s ancestral hall. 

In contrast, the older celestial beings, who were of a higher generation and had the same status as the old sect master Xun Yuan, had high levels of cultivation, but because they never got into heated arguments with Jiang Shangzhen and preferred to mediate, they were often overlooked when discussing important matters. 

“Did you ever even curse Jiang Shangzhen? Did you ever throw a chair at him?” How could you claim to be wholeheartedly for the sect? 

The old patriarch of the law had a heavy heart as he lightly tapped the armrest of his chair. “When the times change, the advantages and disadvantages shift; the old sect master shouldn’t have appeared.” 

With the protection of the Three Yuans and Four Symbols Great Formation, although Xun Yuan had only recently entered the Ascension realm, benefiting from the timing and location, his cultivation appeared flawless at the peak of the upper level. When Taiping Mountain and the Fuyi Sect fell one after the other, the formation dissipated, and he was immediately reverted to his original form. 

The old heavenly lord of Taiping Mountain, fighting to the death, wielded the Bright Moon Mirror and had once slain a great sword immortal from the wild world with a flying sword from the grand formation. 

As for the Taoists of Taiping Mountain, their achievements in slaying demons were numerous and unmatched across the continent. 

The Fuyi Sect’s master, Ji Hai, managed to sustain himself in the Jade Purity realm until after Taiping Mountain’s destruction, which was already a remarkable feat. 

The Yuguizong’s accomplishments mostly stemmed from Xun Yuan and Jiang Shangzhen. 

Ascension realm Xun Yuan had slain two celestial beings and a Jade Purity realm sword immortal. 

As for Jiang Shangzhen, with his east and west swords, he had unconsciously killed four Jade Purity realm cultivators, along with a large number of earth immortal demon clan members as a bonus. 

Song Shengtang wondered, “How did Xiao Qian go from being a hidden official at the Sword Qi Great Wall to a key figure in the wild world?” 

The patriarch of the law sneered, “Why does it matter? What’s important is that she shows signs of being aligned with the wild world, and she herself is an Ascension realm sword cultivator. Tongye Continent is now under the wild world’s domain. If Xiao Qian strikes next time with her sword, and it’s not just random punching, who can stop her from challenging the sword?” 

A less experienced elder sitting near the door said softly, “The Tongye Sect still has that sword immortal by its side.” 

The Yuguizong cultivators had a decent impression of the second disciple from the Confucian School. 

A flying sword for sending messages hovered at the entrance of the ancestral hall. The patriarch stretched out his hand to grab it, and after reading the confidential letter, his expression darkened. 

Liu Huamao asked anxiously, “What’s wrong?” 

The patriarch spoke in a deep voice, “Zhou Mi has personally appeared in the Tongye Sect’s territory and made a huge promise. As long as the Tongye Sect removes the protective formation of the Wutong Tiansan, they will be allowed to establish their own dominion. Not only that, but he will also provide them with a thousand years of protection from him and the Tuo Moon Mountain. Furthermore, the new sect master of the Tongye Sect will become the lord of a new military camp. The Tongye Sect will only nominally become a vassal of the future master of the entire continent, while everything else will remain the same. The wild world is even willing to send two great sword immortals, including Shoucheng, to serve as patrons and guest officials for the Tongye Sect. Moreover, these two will have no say in the ancestral hall discussions and must strike for the Tongye Sect three times instead.” 

Liu Huamao asked, “What about the sword immortal by their side?” 

The patriarch of the law replied helplessly, “Tongye Sect cultivators need not feel pressured; there’s no need to drive the sword immortal away from the sect. As long as they remove the mountain water formation, they can choose to observe when the sword immortal strikes.” 

Liu Huamao frowned, “But that would isolate the sword immortal!” 

To the Tongye Sect, the sword immortal was already an outsider; previously, they had relied on the sword to protect the sect, which had helped unify the hearts of the cultivators, making them willing to lay down their lives. 

Zhou Mi's actions clearly aimed to turn the sword immortal against the entire Tongye Sect. 

Should they protect the Tongye Sect? If not, the mountains and waters’ fortune would be absorbed by the wild world. If they did protect it, and the Wutong Tiansan was removed, every time the sword immortal struck, it would stir unrest among the sect’s cultivators. 

Song Shengtang stroked his beard and squinted, “This is troublesome. A huge dilemma.” 

If it were them, it would indeed leave everyone feeling conflicted. 

Liu Huamao asked, “Who conveyed this information?” 

The patriarch of the law destroyed the confidential letter and said, “A young female cultivator named Yu Xin.” 

For a moment, the atmosphere in the Yuguizong ancestral hall lightened a bit. The patriarch laughed, “She is the reincarnation of our great ancestor who revitalized the sect.” 

Jiang Shangzhen was known for saying strange things, describing Du Mao as “a prodigal son of Tongye Continent and half the revitalizer of Yuguizong.” 

This remark became widely circulated in the Divine Inscription Peak’s ancestral hall, a well-accepted joke. 

After all, the animosity between the Yuguizong and the Tongye Sect was not a matter of one or two thousand years. It didn’t hurt to add one more grievance. 

If it had not been for this great upheaval, the Divine Inscription Peak’s ancestral hall would have discussed a plan to strike down the Tongye Sect, systematically eroding its foundation. This would align with Confucian principles while secretly harming them. 

Liu Huamao sighed, “If we’re not careful, this matter alone could bring her calamity.” 

The patriarch of the law said, “Then we’ll pretend we never saw this information. This is a matter of principle; no matter how the fates of the two sects unfold later, we should speak and act kindly regarding this Yu Xin, and if we have the chance, we can lend her a hand.” 

The old patriarch repeated, “If we have the chance.” 

Suddenly, the old man stood up, and soon everyone followed suit, walking out of the ancestral hall. Outside, they saw a young woman in a cotton coat, speaking in the refined dialect of Tongye Continent she had just learned, slowly saying that the Yuguizong need not surrender their sect, and that cultivators need not leave the mountain, only needing to hand over a Cloud Cave blessed land. 

A blue-robed swordsman named Chen Yin, tall and holding his sword at his back, had bought a black boat at the Peach Leaf Crossing. The usually graceful boatman, as adept in poetry as any scholar, had long since scattered and fled. 

The blue-robed swordsman had to row the boat himself. 

Now, among the cultured literati and dignitaries of the capital of the Great Qian Dynasty, who had the leisure to enjoy the scenery on a boat? 

Thus, this man was undoubtedly a foreign celestial master. 

The black boat at Peach Leaf Crossing was not the kind of small boat used in common water towns; it had a decoration resembling a stork carved on the prow, which piqued the blue-robed swordsman’s interest in rowing. 

He wore a jade pendant from the ancestral hall that read, “Ancestral Hall Continues the Incense,” and “Taiping Mountain Cultivator I.” 

This jade pendant was merely a trophy from a military camp, which he had taken. 

Feiran had a good impression of the Great Qian Dynasty, as it was replete with scenic spots and talented people, especially the elite cavalry and military strength stationed in various regions, which caught the attention of several military camps in central Tongye Continent. 

The overall situation in the lower regions of Tongye Continent was actually much better than the Jiazhi camp had anticipated. In short, the performance of the secular dynasty of Tongye Continent on the battlefield could be summed up in two words: terrible. 

The strong wind revealed the strength of the qing grass, further highlighting the excellence of the Great Qian Dynasty. However, wild grass was still wild grass; no matter how resilient, a great fire could reduce it to ashes. 

After all, the “timing” of Tongye Continent was now controlled by the Tuo Moon Mountain of the wild world. 

Feiran tossed away the bamboo stalk, and the black boat drifted forward by itself. 

However, today, the military camp in the southern capital was embroiled in fierce debates regarding the survival of the Liu clan of the Great Qian. One faction insisted on annihilating Shinjing City, slaughtering the city and establishing a capital, providing a warning to all the vassal states of Tongye Continent. They aimed to behead the princes and ministers, hanging their heads at the gates of every small nation to show the consequences of resisting. 

Another faction believed that the literati and martial artists of the Great Qian had many usable talents and the capital to support them. As long as they operated properly and established a puppet emperor, they would become a significant aid to the military camp. After all, the young emperor had abandoned his kingdom and emptied the treasury, fleeing to the Fifth Continent, which could be used to spread the news widely. 

All major cities in the Great Qian had already been placed under martial law, allowing only entry but no exit, to prevent civilians from fleeing, being secretly guided and exploited by the demon clan to break through defenses, potentially leading to national catastrophe. 

However, Feiran was not here to enjoy the mountains and rivers but to meet someone. 

The head of the Golden Summit Temple, Du Hanling, a cultivator of low realm, an Earth Immortal, was not a sword cultivator but had a sharp mind. 

The young boy at the Water Platform of the Yuanju School, when meeting Feiran, found his fate intertwined at that moment, originally hoping to follow Feiran to the mountains for cultivation, yet inexplicably ended up dead. 

In the former North Jin state, Lu Jianxin, who ultimately died at the hands of “himself,” encountered Yu Si, and if it weren’t for Jiang Shangzhen’s intervention, he would have had the opportunity to undergo a transformation, becoming the lord of a city; instead, he was attached to Yu Si, plus a pair of wooden clogs from his Daoist path, making them the two greatest protective charms, leaving him almost impossible to die. 

Feiran had been mulling over Zhou Mi’s words repeatedly: the Confucian academies and schools had given too much power to the secular dynasties, unwilling to use an iron fist to unify and restrain the hearts of the people. 

The three Confucian academies and seventy-two schools sounded numerous, but in the vast Tongye Continent, they were only three schools, including the Great Fu Academy. 

In the end, the Confucian temple still wanted to restrain the scholars and sages of the schools, forbidding them from interfering too much in court matters, and absolutely not allowing the scholars to act as the shadow emperors of various nations. 

As a result, each acted independently, with the mountains above being a world apart, the reclusive high beings disdaining the world, and many ministers and officials being nothing more than fame-seeking individuals, using false scholarship to crowd out true sages. The mountains above and below, various nations and places, were like scattered sand. 

Yet, Feiran was very curious about Zhou Mi’s founding teachings and their fundamental principles. 

How could one fundamentally change this predicament? 

The coexistence of the demon and human clans in the future was a monumental challenge. 

As for Zhou Mi’s true identity, Feiran had heard some rumors. 

Zhou Mi was indeed a pseudonym; he had once been a genuine scholar of the vast world. 

According to his senior brother Qie Yun, Zhou Mi had been a prodigy in his youth, with great knowledge. 

However, his learning had never been accepted by the Confucian temple. After a debate with someone, he became disheartened and chose to travel the wild world. 

This scholar had proposed a set of “Twelve Policies for Taiping” to the Confucian temple. 

First, a set of personal cultivation guidelines for all scholars should be established, roughly corresponding scholars, gentlemen, and sages to family, country, and world. 

All emperors and rulers of secular dynasties and vassal states must be disciples of Confucian academies; non-scholars cannot be national rulers. 

Every head of a school should be a royal tutor! 

Scholars and gentlemen should serve as national instructors. 

Whether it’s the Three Dukes and Nine Ministers or the Three Provinces and Six Ministries, these central and important officials should also be disciples of the academies. 

Every court should establish a position capable of ignoring palace constraints and responsible for documenting the merits and demerits of a nation’s rulers and ministers, serving as the academy’s three-year major evaluation. 

Second, all upper-level demon cultivators in the vast world should be exterminated; earth immortal demons should be expelled to the continent, with strict regulations. 

Once any demon cultivator enters the Dragon Gate realm, they must proactively report to the Confucian temple and各地書院, with their “true names” recorded in the files. 

These demon cultivators, upon entering the Golden Core realm, must assist local mountain and water deities, ensuring good weather for a century within their jurisdiction, particularly in eliminating mischievous creatures, similar to the role of a “county magistrate.” The academy would then evaluate their merits to see if they can be granted titles such as mountain chief or water fairy, or whether they must work for another century. Once promoted to mountain chief or water fairy, it would be akin to shifting from muddy waters to clear ones in the human realm, and their subsequent paths of promotion would be comparable to those of river water deities and mountain spirits. 

Third, three locations near the Suspended Mountain should be chosen to connect the southern Pusa Continent, southwestern Fuyun, and southeastern Tongye Continent, for example, the territory of the former Yu Long Sect. 

They should gradually station troops at the Sword Qi Great Wall, first relocating unsuitable mundane scholars among the local populace to the Yu Long Sect’s islands. Afterward, they should draw sword cultivators from Beiju Lu Continent to be stationed at the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

All cultivators who have committed grave crimes in the vast world can redeem their lives on the battlefield with their contributions. 

All mountain and wild cultivators can purchase mountain elixirs, manuals, and treasures with their war merits. They need not leave the city to fight; they can defend the walls during wars and work behind the scenes afterward, using the Sword Qi Great Wall as a fundamental base to continuously build cities towards the south, forcing the wild world to dispatch troops every thirty years. 

The Sword Qi Great Wall has unique geography, and the Qi cultivators are naturally oppressed compared to sword cultivators. Thus, a sufficient number of pure warriors should be cultivated. Although they are similarly suppressed by the Dao and pure sword intent, they differ from Qi cultivators; warriors can temper their bodies through this, and the threshold for warriors is lower than that for Qi cultivators. Ultimately, the Sword Qi Great Wall will have this kind of warring pattern: if you are not a sword cultivator, everyone else is a warrior. 

Apart from sword cultivators and pure warriors, many Qi cultivators will act more as assistants. 

Fourth, all celestial and Ascension realm great cultivators will be granted extra freedoms. 

These mountaintop figures need to contribute, but each type of contribution will yield greater returns. 

The Confucian temple will acknowledge their “superiority.” 

For instance, when heading to the Sword Qi Great Wall, the Confucian temple promises they need not fight to the death, and their fundamental principles won’t be harmed. They only need to do some embellishing things, such as expanding advantages in advantageous situations, or using non-essential items to defend against the great demon’s attacks, or setting up mountain and water formations to protect cities, city heads, and sword cultivators and warriors. 

Fifth, the Confucian temple will establish seventy-two Daoist schools in addition to the seventy-two academies across various continents and nations. 

Besides actively inspecting cultivation qualifications and accepting “tributes” from various nations’ courts each year, collecting seeds of cultivation from different regions, these Confucian scholars will primarily focus on military affairs, not engaging in superficial discussions but deeply understanding all historical contexts. 

The final assessment will be conducted in the constantly smoke-filled Sword Qi Great Wall. 

Sixth, the various teachings of the Hundred Schools of Thought will be divided into nine ranks, with both upward and downward adjustments, similar to official ranks. 

Those who refuse to comply will be expelled from the ranks, forbidden from studying, and all their books destroyed. The head of any family, the ancestor, will be imprisoned in the Confucian temple’s merit grove. 

Seventh, breaking the barriers between the mountain and the mundane world, one suggestion is to facilitate and entice them with benefits, promoting mountain cultivators to become celestial couples. 

Eighth, marginalizing the teachings of Buddhism and Daoism, banning all temples and monasteries, ensuring that Confucianism achieves true supremacy in the vast world. 

Ninth, focusing on supporting military, commerce, and arts. 

In addition, there are three more policies specifically targeting the distant neighboring worlds and ancient deities. 

Feiran sighed, gathering his complicated thoughts, muttering to himself, “Ultimately, Master Zhou proposed these twelve policies to consolidate power for the Confucian temple. To grant scholars greater freedom, paving the way for lasting peace.” 

At a ferry near Peach Leaf Crossing, two black boats met. 

Feiran frowned. It seemed that Du Hanling was not coming alone. 

The Earth Immortal cultivator was accompanied by a young Golden Core cultivator and a city god dressed in formal attire. 

Feiran merely frowned, while Du Hanling, along with his disciple Shao Yuanran and the city god of Qiche City, wore expressions as if they had seen a ghost in broad daylight. Even Du Hanling, a person of his fierce nature, was shaken at the sight of Feiran, dressed in blue robes with a sword at his back and the jade pendant from Taiping Mountain hanging from his waist. He felt a sense of dread wash over him; could this truly be a coincidence? 

Two figures approached from the opposite side—Liu Cong of the Great Qian clan and Duke Gao Shizhen. Upon seeing “Feiran,” they nearly turned to flee. 

Feiran understood instantly and smiled. 

It seemed they all recognized the Hidden Official, and from the looks of it, their past interactions had not been pleasant. 

Thus, Feiran smiled and said, “The mountains and waters reunite; it’s been a long time.” 

White clouds drifted past the peak of the Languishing Mountain. The little girl in black, upon seeing them, waved her golden backpack and green bamboo staff vigorously, greeting them as a way of being hospitable. 

“Hey, hey, hey! I’m the right protector here, the water monster of the Mute Lake. I have two friends, one named Pei Qian and the other named Nuan Shu. Do you know them? Have you heard of them?” 

Today, the right protector of Languishing Mountain accompanied the left protector of Qilong Alley, who had never been promoted, one crouching and the other lying down, waiting together by the cliff for the white clouds to pass. 

The left protector of Qilong Alley was a small official, not comparable to his own big official. 

Haha, white clouds and azure skies. 

In the mountains, they feared Ruan Xiu, while on Languishing Mountain, they feared Pei Qian, but they really liked this little simpleton. 

He once accompanied Zhou Mi Li, squatting at the entrance of the school run by the Chen family in Longwei Creek, waiting for that “the most heroic” Pei Qian to finish classes and go home, often waiting for half a day. The little girl would chat with him for a long time. She would never be like Pei Qian, who would grab his mouth for no reason and twist it, asking what was going on. 

Little Mi Li longed for the white clouds to visit Languishing Mountain. 

She frowned, growing increasingly sad, thinking, what if when Pei Qian returns home, he’s already as tall as she and Sister Nuan Shu combined? What if one day the mountain master climbs the mountain with a basket, and in that basket stands a strange little girl? 

Mi Yu sat down beside the little girl. 

Zhou Mi Li clapped her hands and laughed as the white clouds passed through the valley. 

However, just as Mi Yu sat down, he immediately stood up, communicating with Wei Ban silently, then Mi Yu summoned his life-bound flying sword, “Xia Mantian,” and rode the sword toward the Ancestral Hall at Jise Peak. 

Eventually, at the entrance, Mi Yu encountered a scholar and a tall man. 

The sword-wielding scholar smiled slightly at Mi Yu, then vanished without a sound, crossing continents on a journey. 

His trip to Baoping Continent was merely to cover for a friend; otherwise, his friend’s presence would be too noticeable. The old scholar had appeared briefly in Fuyun Continent before quickly slipping away without a trace. 

Only the tall man remained. 

He said to Mi Yu, “You can call me Liu Sixteen. I’ve just returned to the vast world to pay my respects. If I can’t meet the master, I’ll at least see the portrait of the master. If I end up crying with a snotty face, just pretend you didn’t see.” 

Mi Yu was at a loss for words. 

Having stabilized his mind, Mi Yu said, “The key to the ancestral hall is with Nuan Shu.” 

The man nodded, “Then I’ll trouble the sword immortal to make a trip; I’ll wait here.” 

Wei Ban soon brought Nuan Shu and Little Mi Li to this place. 

The two little girls respectfully bowed to Wei Shan Jun, the so-called “mountain master senior brother.” 

Upon seeing the two girls, the man’s expression softened, realizing that his little junior brother wasn’t bad after all. 

After Chen Nuan Shu opened the door of the ancestral hall, the tall man stood outside, his expression solemn as he straightened his robe and then stepped over the threshold. 

Just as the sword-wielding scholar was about to cross continents. 

He encountered that sneaky old scholar. 

He asked, “Why didn’t you show up earlier?” 

The old scholar confidently replied, “I was waiting for that big dumb guy to finish crying.” 

The scholar glanced up at the sky. 

The old scholar asked, “Brother Bai, don’t miss this chance; why not just strike a few swords? What does it mean to be a sword immortal? Isn’t it about cutting down the serpentine spirits in the wind? Those ancient deities who visit without warning are no better than serpents; they should be struck first. Previously, when Xiao Qian drew her sword in Tongye Continent, it was such an astonishing sight. A mere girl has that sword intent, and you, Bai, stand at eight feet tall holding a celestial sword. How could you endure? Just let go! If you’re polite with me, I’ll get angry… To put it frankly, I’m good at cleaning up messes, but let’s agree first—three to five swords are enough; any more, and I can’t handle it. If you really feel unsatisfied, at most, seven or eight swords…” 

The scholar ignored the old scholar and vanished in a flash. 

The old scholar stomped his feet in frustration. 

He then looked towards Languishing Mountain. 

Recalling the past, Bai had once sent Liu Sixteen back to the mountains with the song of white clouds. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 832: Driving Away Dragons and Snakes, Not Mosquitoes

In the ancestral hall of Clear Sky Peak, Liu Sixteen quietly gazed up at the three portraits of the fallen heroes of Lopan Mountain, lost in thought.
