Chen Nuanshu picked up a bamboo incense holder and raised it high, prompting Liu Sixteen to express his gratitude with a nod. He bent down to pluck three sticks of incense from the holder.

Zhou Mili told the burly man that she was feeling tired and would like to take a break, offering him her chair.

The little girl in black pointed to a chair that had a palm-sized note stuck on the back, which read “Right Guardian, Zhou Mili.”

Liu Sixteen nodded in understanding.

Chen Nuanshu tugged at Mili’s sleeve, and the two left the ancestral hall together, leaving Liu Sixteen alone.

As they exited the hall and walked past the outer door, they saw a poised swordsman in a simple blue gown, standing alongside Wei Shanjun, who was adorned in a flowing white robe with golden earrings. Together, they looked like a pair of exquisite orchids in a courtyard.

Mi Yu used his heart voice to inquire about Wei Bo, “How did you know the identity of that person? The Hidden Official never mentioned it.”

Wei Bo explained, “Earlier, when Mr. Bai approached the borders of North Yue, he introduced himself to the people of Piyun Mountain, saying, ‘Bai Ye is visiting Lopan Mountain with my friend Liu Sixteen.’ Liu Sixteen then claimed to be half a senior brother of Chen Ping’an and came here to pay respects to the portrait of his teacher.”

Mi Yu teased, “Speaking of Bai Ye, why is Wei Brother so excited?”

Wei Bo chuckled, “Who wouldn’t be fascinated by a sword immortal who isn’t a sword cultivator?”

There weren’t many people worthy of Wei Bo’s admiration—just Bai Ye, the inscription of A Liang on the Sword Qi Great Wall, and the great deity of Suishan in the Middle Lands.

Mi Yu shook his head. “In my hometown, people don’t speak much of him.”

It wasn’t that they thought the scholar’s reputation was undeserved, but rather that Bai Ye drew his sword so rarely that there wasn’t much to say. Excluding the year he cut through the Yellow River’s waterfall, he seemed to have no notable achievements in the long years that followed.

Until this time, when he appeared in the wild lands of Fuyou Prefecture, slaying a great demon with three strikes.

Actually, between his two sword strikes, the Fire Dragon Real Man visited a solitary island far from land, and later, Bai Ye quietly wielded his sword to slay a transcended great demon in the Middle Land’s Divine Continent.

Mi Yu glanced inside the door. The tall figure from afar lit three incense sticks but stood for a long time without placing them in the incense burner, likely muttering to himself.

Mi Yu couldn't help but feel envious of Liu Sixteen, who could burn incense and pay respects upon arriving at Lopan Mountain.

The sword immortal, known as Yu Mi, had been at Lopan Mountain for quite a while but had yet to pay his respects in the Clear Sky Peak’s ancestral hall. Yet, it wasn’t entirely his fault; he had said he would wait until the Hidden Official returned to his hometown, hoping to record “Mi Yu” in the ancestral hall’s genealogy when more people were present. As a result, he had postponed this for several years. Mi Yu was genuinely somewhat vexed, as there were many things happening at Lopan Mountain. Spending time with little Mili, eating melon seeds while watching the clouds drift by, or strolling along the white jade railing outside the Mountain God’s temple was simply too dull. He often found himself chatting with Liu Xianyang at the blacksmith shop by Longxu River, discussing the mysteries and knowledge of the celestial sect regarding the ephemeral nature of dreams, hoping to eventually invite Wei Shanjun, the guardian Zhou Fei, and that young man in white to seek fortune for Lopan Mountain and gather some spiritual energy.

However, while these activities were enjoyable and comforting, opportunities for serious matters were still far too few.

Mi Yu had a strong desire to meet the embroidered river goddess and find an opportunity to test her bravery with a sword strike.

In his hometown, opportunities to interact with gods of rivers and mountains were few and far between. He hadn’t expected that in this Baoping Continent, there would be shrines and deities everywhere.

He had long wanted to visit the fox nation in Clear Wind City. As for the city lord, Xu Hun, Mi Yu regarded him as a kindred spirit, seeing as Xu Hun was said to be a man who rolled in the world of cosmetics. Mi Yu was particularly eager to confirm whether, after all these years, the infamous “mole armor” that once belonged to Liu Xianyang’s family still fit him well.

As for the so-called “Ten Sword Immortals of the Ten Peaks” near Zhengyang Mountain, a recently emerged old ancestor sword immortal had just come out of seclusion. At that time, Mi Yu was dozing off at the riverside shop with Liu Xianyang when he heard Liu Xianyang mention the term “old sword immortal,” startling Mi Yu. He was weighing whether his jade purity realm in the Sword Qi Great Wall had a chance to exchange his life for that of the immortal realm in Baoping Continent when Liu Xianyang handed him a mountain water report, a special congratulatory letter from the mountain, with mud-gold characters on a blue background page.

Looking at the report filled with flattery, Mi Yu felt as if the old guy hadn’t merely entered the jade purity realm but had ascended to the transcendental realm. Mi Yu was baffled. Did he really need to remain in the jade purity realm for a hundred years? The reason he was honored as the “Embroidered Sword Immortal” in the Sword Qi Great Wall and gained the reputation of being among the “Top Ten in Jade Purity” was largely due to a six-month extended seclusion.

Mi Yu felt as though his beloved sword was rusting. If it weren’t for Bai Ye’s visit with Liu Sixteen, he might have almost forgotten that his life sword was named “Xia Mantian.”

Ordinary cultivators or mountain spirits, like the black snake from Qidun Mountain or the massive python in Huanghu Mountain, wouldn’t feel the passage of time too acutely. However, who was Mi Yu? He was someone who could doze off in the clouds of the Sword Qi Great Wall, unconcerned about sword refining. After arriving at Baoping Continent, especially after parting ways with Wei Jin at the Wind and Snow Temple, Mi Yu increasingly felt distanced from the Sword Qi Great Wall. He dared not even dream of becoming a great sword immortal, especially since he didn’t even know where the jade purity realm’s bottleneck lay.

In truth, according to Mi Yu’s own character, not knowing was fine; he didn’t care. Whether or not he became an immortal was left to fate; if heaven chose to give him a chance, he would accept it; if not, he wouldn’t seek it.

However, upon arriving at Lopan Mountain, without the Hidden Official at the mountain peak, the steward Zhu Lian also absent, and even Zheng Dafeng, who guarded the gate, far away, only Nuanshu and little Mili remained, along with a few children who had just begun practicing martial arts, or some spirits and ghosts that Mi Yu was not fond of dealing with. Thus, he inexplicably became the temporary backbone of Lopan Mountain, which felt rather strange.

After all, back in his hometown at the Sword Qi Great Wall, he was used to the presence of so many old and great sword immortals. Even if the sky were to fall, he wouldn’t fear it, especially since he had a brother, Mi Hu, who was a talented sword cultivator with the potential to rank among the top ten sword immortals in the Sword Qi Great Wall. Mi Yu was accustomed to being carefree and indifferent to everything, which made him nostalgic for the days at the Summer Resort and Spring Fan Studio, when the young Hidden Official would tell him what to do, and every time he did something, he would receive some form of reward afterward.

Suddenly, Mi Yu exclaimed, “If this continues, I’ll truly just be waiting to eat and die. Sunbathing and snacking on melon seeds is far too addictive.”

For some reason, on Lopan Mountain, perhaps it was too easy to adapt to this environment, Mi Yu felt he had fallen victim to a saying in a book: he was experiencing spring drowsiness.

Especially the daily routine of patrolling the mountain with Zhou Mili twice a day was the most enjoyable thing.

Wei Bo hesitated and asked, “Are you planning to visit Old Dragon City?”

Mi Yu glanced at the sky and shook his head. “I wanted to take a look before, but now I genuinely can’t leave Lopan Mountain unattended. It’s too close to Piyun Mountain and could easily attract those ancient remnants.”

Wei Bo nodded. “My North Yue is the only territory that hasn’t been invaded by ancient gods. We must be cautious.”

Inside the ancestral hall, after Liu Sixteen honored the incense, he closed his eyes and murmured once more.

Zhou Mili, with a golden shoulder pole and a green bamboo staff, said earnestly to Sister Nuanshu, “The mountain master’s half-brother is quite tall and seems very strong. And that’s only half! If he were a full brother, wouldn’t that be something?!”

Chen Nuanshu, with several keys hanging from her waist, sighed, “Half a brother doesn’t mean what you think it does.”

The little girl in black raised her eyebrows, clearly amused. “Sister Nuanshu, I was just joking. Didn’t you get that? It’s like I spoke for nothing.”

Chen Nuanshu smiled, narrowing her eyes, and patted the smaller Mili affectionately. “You’ve become a bit sharper today, Mili. Keep it up tomorrow.”

Zhou Mili nodded vigorously. “Yes, yes! Pei Qian always says that ambition isn’t bound by age, and cleverness isn’t measured by height.”

Liu Sixteen left the ancestral hall, crossed two thresholds, and smiled at Chen Nuanshu. “You can lock the door now.”

The girl in the pink skirt nodded and went to shut the inner door. After hesitating for a moment, Mili followed Sister Nuanshu to handle some tasks, pondering how to properly entertain their esteemed guest Liu Sixteen.

Liu Sixteen clasped his fist in gratitude towards Mi Yu and Wei Bo, saying, “Junior brother has been away from the mountain for many years, and I appreciate the care from you, Sword Immortal and Mountain Monarch.”

Mi Yu replied, “There’s no need for formalities, Mr. Liu. I am merely a worshipper of Lopan Mountain.”

Wei Bo added, “I owe my position as the Mountain Monarch of North Yue to A Liang and my friendship with Chen Ping’an. It’s only right to lend a hand in small matters.”

Liu Sixteen said, “No need to call me Mr. Liu; I don’t deserve it. Just call me Jun Qian. Although it’s also a pseudonym, I’ve always used this name publicly in the Haoran world.”

In the backyard of Yang’s pharmacy, smoke wafted around.

The old man Yang tucked his old smoking pipe into his belt and stood to greet them.

It was the old scholar and Bai Ye who had come together.

Previously, Bai Ye had already left the continent for the sea, but the persistent old scholar had stopped him, insisting they sit together for a while.

Bai Ye remembered the fate from the end of the Yuanbao years at the Spring Ming Gate in his homeland and accepted the old scholar’s invitation without refusal.

If Chen Chunan from South Posa Continent monopolized the term “refined scholar,” then Bai Ye singularly embodied the concept of “immortal.”

His swordsmanship was extraordinary, his talent in poetry unmatched, and although he had no rivals in verse, his lyrics and music circulated widely, leaving later generations astonished. They often suspected it was a false claim, but they dared not confirm it, resulting in many unsolved mysteries. In the end, there was only one explanation: as an immortal, what couldn’t he accomplish?

As the old scholar entered the courtyard, he immediately raised his fists high, shaking them vigorously, a radiant smile on his face. “Today, I finally have the honor to meet the Heavenly Lord Qing Tong. I’ve lived a full life, and it’s not been in vain!”

Old man Yang, rarely smiling, replied, “Mr. Wensheng, your demeanor is as impressive as ever.”

The union of a cultivator of the fourteenth realm with the Dao of Heaven and Earth was not trivial; it wasn’t merely about seeking greatness.

The former literary sage, who had once impressed old man Yang, now had his domain encompass South Posa Continent, Tongye Continent, and Fuyou Continent, rather than the more stable Middle Land Divine Continent, Aiai Continent, or Liuxia Continent.

Now that both continents had fallen, the old scholar was not in a relaxed position.

Bai Ye merely nodded in acknowledgment to old man Yang.

The old scholar, however, had no intention of letting Bai Ye off the hook. He pulled out a long-preserved document from his sleeve and handed it to old man Yang, cheerfully saying, “This is the ‘Yuanbao End Year’ piece, also known as the ‘Delightful Tablet,’ an authentic piece, absolutely genuine. It wouldn’t do to visit without a gift. The gift may not be light, but the sentiment is weightier.”

Old man Yang opened the document, revealing the piece from the end of the Yuanbao years, where Bai Ye, intoxicated by wine, had fallen asleep by the Spring Ming Gate, dreaming of riding on a raft with the Heavenly Lord Qing Tong across the starry river. Upon waking from his drunken dream, inspired, he composed the poem.

Old man Yang rolled up the document and tucked it into his sleeve.

This was originally a mutual understanding between Bai Ye and old man Yang, needing no words. However, the old scholar’s antics had robbed it of its lingering charm.

Unexpectedly, the old scholar boasted shamelessly, “Heavenly Lord Qing Tong, you might as well take a look. The beauty of this piece lies in the back. In addition to Cui Zhan’s embroidered tiger seal, there’s also Xiao Qi’s ‘Spring Breeze’ book seal, and the slightly incongruous characters ‘Jun Qian’ at the end, along with the seal that reads, ‘Look around; understanding is not far away.’”

Old man Yang did not take the document back out, understanding its significance.

Old man Yang remarked, “After the sage created characters, aside from the eight who contributed to the opening, there are no great masters in the world of calligraphy. They are the lowest of the low.”

It was evident that the old man did not recognize the calligrapher’s ability to rank among the top nine schools and even believed they lacked the qualifications to stand among the various scholars.

The old scholar was famously adept at keeping conversations going, eagerly nodding, “That’s not a pleasant thing to say, but it is a great truth. Cui Zhan expressed similar sentiments earlier, feeling that the so-called masters of calligraphy today are just scribblers. It’s like a snail shell trying to flip over the ocean; what else could it be but mischief?”

Bai Ye was well aware that the old scholar had good relations with several pioneering calligraphers. Cui Zhan’s worth a thousand pieces of gold didn’t come from thin air; it was the result of the old scholar traveling with him across the world, collecting autumn winds. Fine as any stone tablet or inscription might be, they still lacked the authentic spirit and intent. Yet, Cui Zhan had the opportunity to witness the original works of those calligraphy ancestors, thanks to the old scholar’s assistance.

“Brother, if you write a few more pieces, riding this wave of inspiration, just write whatever comes to mind. The more relatable the content, the more delightful it is. Whether you bought a few pounds of oranges or had a couple of meals today—whether it rained or shone, feel free to write about it. If all else fails, just say you met me today, an old friend with a kind heart, and sent you a basket of pears, causing you to shed tears…”

This must be treated as a family heirloom and treasured. “Brother, what kind of look is that? Am I the kind of person who sells out at the first opportunity? Do you think I have such friends?”

“I write; you write. We’re a perfect match. We just need a big vendor to help us publish the books, and then we’ll be unbeatable together.”

As for the so-called eight founders that the Heavenly Lord Qing Tong mentioned, Bai Ye had a rough idea: the Great Seal Taishi Zhou, the Small Seal Li Tonggu, the Clerical Script Yuan Cen, the Regular Script Shi Jiujiu, the Modern Cursive Zhang Chunhua, the Wild Cursive Zhang Huai, the Standard Regular Wang Zhong, and the Small Regular Script Zhong Yao. Only Cui Zhan was “not diligent,” just casually writing, but his cursive script was the most renowned. In reality, Cui Zhan’s small regular script was extremely exquisite, and the sutras he copied were treasures held by many great Buddhist temples in the Middle Lands.

The old scholar turned to sit on the long bench under the eaves, reaching out to pat it, “Sturdy.”

Old man Yang asked, “Mr. Wensheng, apart from having me send the calligraphy to Lopan Mountain and stamping more seals, what else do you need?”

The old scholar replied, “Nothing else, just a simple thank you to my predecessor.”

Old man Yang certainly didn’t believe that.

The old scholar wasn’t in a hurry to slap his own face; he looked left and right. 

Perhaps in the past, Xiao Qi and Xiao Ping An had both sat here. Without their teacher by his side, the student felt lonely and uneasy sitting alone, making it rather challenging.

The three of them almost simultaneously looked up.

In the sky of Baoping Continent, a massive hole appeared, with a golden-bodied spirit slowly peering out. Within thousands of miles of the sky, countless golden lightning bolts intertwined like a net, appearing to fall upon the North Yue’s Piyun Mountain.

The old scholar exclaimed, “Bai Brother, this is a provocation! Do you need me to shout ‘Bai Ye is here’ for you?”

Bai Ye’s expression remained calm. “With Liu Sixteen here, there’s no need.”

The old scholar stood up, rubbing his hands together. “That silly giant is always at a disadvantage in fights. He’s much worse than his junior brother. But that relentless momentum of his is still impressive.”

In the sky above Baoping Continent, the enormous remnant of the ancient divine being was merely brushed aside by what appeared to be a tiny figure. That minuscule person relentlessly struck at the towering spirit, creating an immense thunderclap. In the end, the uninvited guest, along with his hand, arm, and head, was shattered in an instant.

The high sky, spanning almost half a continent, rained down countless golden droplets. Before they could touch the earth, the majority of the golden fragments had already disappeared, melting into the heavens and earth. Guided by an unseen force, the remaining golden rain almost entirely fell within a thousand miles around Piyun Mountain. Just as they were about to land and merge into the mountain waters, a flash of golden light vanished, leaving many mountain spirits and celestial dwellings stunned. Had they been robbed by the Mountain Monarch Wei? Some enlightened beings immediately gazed upon the mountain range, only to find the spiritual energy of Piyun Mountain had not increased much—strange indeed.

On the steps of Qilong Alley, a smiling woman shook her sleeves, which sparkled with golden light, but the phenomenon quickly dissipated.

The old scholar remarked, “I’ll trouble the elder to lead the way.”

Old man Yang nodded.

Liu Sixteen felt a shift in his thoughts. In a sudden swoop, he descended towards the earth, abruptly shrinking the mountains and rivers by thousands of miles until he arrived in the backyard of the small town’s pharmacy.

Seeing the old scholar already standing on the bench, Liu Sixteen’s eyes turned red. Fortunately, he had already cried in the ancestral hall at Clear Sky Peak; otherwise, he would have been even more embarrassed.

The old scholar stood on the bench, stroking his beard with a smile.

Liu Sixteen quickly approached, his eyes brimming with tears, and bowed deeply, exclaiming, “Jun Qian pays respects to the teacher!”

Among his four former students, Cui Zhan was reserved, hiding his brilliance; Qi Jingchun learned the true teachings of the literary sage; Liu Sixteen was the most awkward yet also the most sincere.

The old scholar patted the sturdy man’s shoulder before jumping down from the bench. Then, stroking his beard, he laughed, “You truly are a good brother of Bai Ye, my excellent disciple. What a fine saying: ‘Driving away dragons and snakes, not mosquitoes!’”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 832: The Dragon and Snake Drive Away the Mosquitoes

Inside the Ancestral Hall of Jisi Peak, Liu Sixteen gazed silently at the three paintings that bore the incense offerings of the Lost Fortune Mountain, his head tilted back.

Chen Nuanshu walked over with a bamboo incense holder, raising it high with both hands. Liu Sixteen thanked her, bowing his head to pull out three incense sticks from the holder.

Zhou Milie told the burly man that she was tired and would rest, offering him her chair.

The little girl in black pointed to a chair, where a palm-sized note read, “Right Protector, Zhou Milie.”

Liu Sixteen nodded.

Chen Nuanshu tugged at Milie's sleeve, and together they left the Ancestral Hall, leaving Liu Sixteen alone.

As they stepped out of the shrine's main door and walked past the entrance to the Ancestral Hall, they saw Mi Jianxian, dressed in a simple green robe, and Wei Shanjun, draped in a snow-white gown with golden earrings, standing side by side at the entrance like fragrant orchids beside a jade tree.

Mi Yu sent a mental inquiry to Wei Ban: “How did you know the identity of the other person? The Hidden Official never mentioned it.”

Wei Ban explained that when Mr. Bai approached the borders of the North Mountain, he proactively introduced himself, saying, “Bai Ye visits Lost Fortune Mountain with my friend Liu Sixteen,” while Liu Sixteen claimed to be a half-brother of Chen Ping’an and came to pay his respects to the teacher's portrait.

Mi Yu teased, “Speaking of Bai Ye, are you that excited, Wei Brother?”

Wei Ban chuckled, “Who wouldn’t be in awe of a sword immortal who isn’t a sword cultivator?”

There were few people who could earn Wei Ban's admiration—Bai Ye, that calligrapher A Liang who carved inscriptions on the Sword Qi Great Wall, and the great deity of the Central Plains, Suishan.

Mi Yu shook his head. “In my hometown, there isn’t much talk about this person.”

It wasn’t that he thought the scholar’s fame was exaggerated, but Bai Ye had fought too few times to warrant much discussion. Aside from that one time he summoned the Yellow River's waterfall with a single sword strike, he seemed to have no accomplishments in the long years that followed.

Until this time, when he appeared on the rugged continent of Fuyouzhou, slashing down a major demon with three strikes.

In fact, between those two sword strikes, the Fire Dragon True Person visited a solitary island suspended over the sea, and after that, Bai Ye quietly set off on a distant journey, slaying a transcendent demon from the Central Plains with a single sword strike.

Mi Yu glanced back at the tall figure inside the hall. After lighting the three incense sticks, he towered over them, yet he hadn’t placed them in the incense burner for a long while, likely murmuring to himself.

Mi Yu envied Liu Sixteen, who could burn incense and pay respects as soon as he arrived at Lost Fortune Mountain.

Disguised as Yu Mi, the Jade Purity Realm Sword Immortal had been at Lost Fortune Mountain for quite some time but had never paid respects in this Ancestral Hall. It wasn’t anyone’s fault, as Mi Yu himself had said he would wait for the Hidden Official to return to his hometown and for more people to gather at Lost Fortune Mountain before registering “Mi Yu” in the ancestral records, which had dragged on for several years. Mi Yu was indeed getting a bit impatient, as there were many things to do on Lost Fortune Mountain. Spending time with Zhou Milie, eating sunflower seeds while watching the clouds drift, or strolling by the white jade railing outside the mountain god's temple was simply boring. So, he would go to the blacksmith shop by Longxu River to chat with Liu Xianyang, the equally lazy man, discussing the teachings and knowledge of the celestial sect regarding illusions, hoping to one day involve Wei Shanjun, the worshipful Zhou Fei, and that white-clad youth to seek a prosperous start, ultimately earning some divine money for Lost Fortune Mountain and enriching its spiritual energy.

However, while these activities were enjoyable and comforting, serious opportunities were too few.

Mi Yu was quite eager to meet the Embroidered River Water Deity, hoping to find a chance to sneak up and test her courage with a single sword strike.

In his hometown, Mi Yu had very few opportunities to interact with the gods of mountains and rivers. He never expected that in this Baoping Continent, shrines and deities were everywhere.

He had long wanted to visit the Fox Kingdom in Qingfeng City. As for the city lord, Xu Hun, Mi Yu regarded him as a kindred spirit since Xu Hun was rumored to be a man who rolled in makeup. Mi Yu wanted to confirm whether the city lord, who was contending with Huang He from Fenglei Garden for the title of “the first person under the realm of the five greats” in Baoping Continent, still fit into the inherited “mole armor” that belonged to Liu Xianyang’s family.

As for the so-called “Sword Paths Connecting to the Mountain Peaks, Ten Sword Immortals on Ten Peaks” of Zhengyang Mountain in Baoping Continent, there had just been a venerable sword immortal who emerged from seclusion. At that time, Mi Yu was dozing off with Liu Xianyang at the riverside shop, and when he heard Liu Xianyang mention “old sword immortal,” he was taken aback, contemplating whether his Jade Purity Realm from the Sword Qi Great Wall had a chance to exchange lives with the immortals of Baoping Continent. Liu Xianyang handed him a mountain and river bulletin—a congratulatory letter exclusive to the mountain, with mud-gold characters on a blue background.

Looking at that bulletin, Mi Yu noted that the flattering words made it seem like the old fellow had not just entered the Jade Purity Realm but had ascended to the Transcendent Realm. He wondered, how could someone merely at the Jade Purity Realm need to retreat for a hundred years? The reason why he was respected as the Embroidered Sword Immortal and earned the title of “First of the Jade Purity” was largely due to the fact that he had stayed in seclusion for half a year longer than expected.

Mi Yu felt that his treasured sword was about to rust. If it weren’t for this visit from Bai Ye and Liu Sixteen, he might have forgotten that his personal flying sword was called Xiamantian.

Ordinary cultivators or mountain spirits, like the black serpent from Chess Mountain or the great python in Huanghu Mountain, wouldn’t feel time passing too long. But who was Mi Yu? A person who could lounge in the clouds and mist in the Sword Qi Great Wall, relaxed and carefree, and upon arriving at Baoping Continent, especially after parting ways with Wei Jin at the Wind and Snow Temple, Mi Yu felt increasingly distant from the Sword Qi Great Wall, no longer dreaming of becoming a great sword immortal, as he didn’t even know where his Jade Purity Realm bottleneck lay.

In fact, according to Mi Yu’s nature, not knowing was just fine. Whether or not he became an immortal was left to fate; if Heaven chose to grant him that, he wouldn’t seek it, and if it was given, he would accept it.

However, upon arriving at Lost Fortune Mountain, with the Hidden Official not present at the mountain top, the chief steward Zhu Lian also absent, and even Zheng Dafeng, who watched the gate, having gone far away, it left only Nuanshu and Milie, along with some children who had only recently begun practicing their punches, or some spirits and demons Mi Yu was reluctant to interact with. Thus, Mi Yu inexplicably became the temporary backbone of Lost Fortune Mountain, which felt a bit strange.

After all, back in his hometown at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Mi Yu was already accustomed to the presence of many old sword immortals and great sword immortals. He wouldn’t fear even if the sky fell, especially since he had an elder brother, Mi Hu, a talented sword cultivator who originally had the chance to rank among the top ten sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall. Mi Yu had grown used to being carefree, accustomed to not caring about everything, so he missed those years at the Summer Resort Palace and Spring Banner Pavilion when the young Hidden Official would tell him what to do, and the key was that whatever he did would yield rewards afterwards.

Suddenly, Mi Yu sighed, “If things keep going like this, I’ll truly just be waiting to eat and die. Sunbathing and eating sunflower seeds are just too addictive.”

For some reason, at Lost Fortune Mountain, perhaps because he had adapted too well to this environment, Mi Yu felt that he had fallen victim to a certain saying in a book—spring drowsiness.

Especially the most interesting thing was the twice-daily mountain patrols with Zhou Milie.

Wei Ban hesitated a moment and asked, “Are you planning to check out Lao Long City?”

Mi Yu glanced at the sky and shook his head. “I wanted to see it before, but now I really can’t leave Lost Fortune Mountain. It's too close to Piyun Mountain; it’s easy to attract those remnants of ancient times.”

Wei Ban nodded. “My North Mountain is the only territory that hasn’t been invaded by ancient deities. We must be very careful.”

Inside the Ancestral Hall, after Liu Sixteen paid his respects, he closed his eyes once more, murmuring softly.

Zhou Milie, shouldering a golden shoulder pole and holding a green bamboo staff, turned seriously to Sister Nuanshu and said, “The half-brother of the Mountain Lord is really tall and looks strong. And that’s only half! If he were a whole one, what would happen?!”

Chen Nuanshu, who had several keys hanging from her waist, helplessly replied, “Half or whole, it doesn’t mean the same thing.”

The little girl in black raised her brows in delight. “Sister Nuanshu, I was just joking! Didn’t you get it? It’s like I said nothing at all.”

Chen Nuanshu smiled, her eyes narrowing, and patted the slightly shorter Zhou Milie, gently saying, “Milie, you’ve become a bit more clever today than yesterday. Keep it up tomorrow.”

Zhou Milie nodded vigorously. “Right, right! Pei Qian said before, ambition doesn’t depend on age, and cleverness doesn’t depend on height.”

Liu Sixteen left the Ancestral Hall, stepping over two thresholds, and smiled at Chen Nuanshu, saying, “We can lock the door now.”

The girl in a pink skirt nodded and went to close the inner door. Zhou Milie hesitated for a moment but decided to follow Sister Nuanshu to handle serious matters. As for how to properly entertain the esteemed guest Liu Sixteen, she would need to think it over carefully.

Liu Sixteen clasped his hands in salute to Mi Yu and Wei Ban, expressing his gratitude, “Junior Brother hasn’t been at the mountain for many years. Thank you, Sword Immortal and Mountain Lord, for your care.”

Mi Yu replied, “There’s no need for formalities, Mr. Liu. I am but a servant of Lost Fortune Mountain.”

Wei Ban added, “I owe my position as the Mountain Lord of the North to A Liang, and I am also a close friend of Chen Ping’an. We are closer than distant relatives; it’s only a small matter, it’s only right.”

Liu Sixteen said, “No need to call me Mr. Liu; I can’t bear it. Just call me Jun Qian. Though it’s also a pseudonym, I’ve always used this name in the Haoran world.”

In the backyard of Yang’s Medicine Shop, smoke curled in the air.

Old Yang tucked his old smoking pipe into his waist and stood up to greet them.

It was the old scholar who had come together with Bai Ye.

Earlier, Bai Ye had already left the continent and entered the sea, but he was stopped by the persistent old scholar, who insisted on coming here to sit for a while.

Bai Ye remembered the fateful encounter at Chunming Gate in his homeland at the end of the Yuanbao era and did not refuse the old scholar’s invitation.

If Chen Chunan from South Posa Continent monopolized the term “cultured gentleman,” then Bai Ye singularly monopolized the term “immortal.”

With unparalleled swordsmanship and dual mastery of poetry and prose, he was indeed unmatched in poetry. Yet, songs and melodies spread, leaving later generations astonished, feeling they were mere forgeries, but they couldn’t confirm it, resulting in numerous mysteries.

In the end, there was only one explanation—immortals can accomplish anything.

Upon entering the courtyard, the old scholar immediately raised his fists high and shook them vigorously with a radiant smile. “Today, I finally have the honor of meeting the Heavenly Lord Qing Tong! I thought I had lived a wasted life, but it seems I haven’t died in vain!”

Old Yang, rarely smiling, responded, “Mr. Wen Sheng, your demeanor remains as magnificent as it was back in the day.”

The union of the Fourteenth Realm cultivators with heaven and earth is not simple; it’s not merely about seeking greatness.

What truly made Old Yang regard this former Wen Sheng with esteem was that the place of his union was in South Posa Continent, Tongye Continent, and Fuyou Continent, rather than the stable territories of Central Plains, Aiai Continent, and Liuxia Continent.

Now that the two continents had fallen, this old scholar was undoubtedly not at ease.

Bai Ye merely nodded in greeting to Old Yang.

Old Yang didn’t exchange pleasantries with Bai Ye either.

However, the old scholar had no intention of letting Bai Ye off easily. He fished out a long-preserved letter from his sleeve and handed it to Old Yang with a grin. “This is the ‘Yuanbao End of Year’ letter, also known as the ‘De Yi Letter,’ an authentic piece of writing. It wouldn’t be right to visit without bringing a gift. The gift may not be light, but the sentiment is heavier.”

Old Yang unfolded it, revealing a letter from the end of the Yuanbao era, where Bai Ye drunkenly slept under Chunming Gate, dreaming of traveling the stars with Heavenly Lord Qing Tong. Upon waking from his dream, inspired, he composed this poem.

He rolled up the letter and tucked it into his sleeve.

Originally, it was an understanding between Bai Ye and Old Yang that required no words.

But with the old scholar stirring it up like this, the moment was devoid of lingering charm.

Unexpectedly, the old scholar boasted shamelessly, “Heavenly Lord Qing Tong, feel free to open it and take a look. The beauty lies in the back. Apart from Cui Zhan’s embroidered tiger seal, there’s Little Qi’s ‘Spring Breeze’藏书印, and the somewhat abrupt ‘Jun Qian’ at the end, finished with the seal ‘Look to the left and right, and the heart shall not be far.’”

Old Yang, however, did not take out the letter again, merely acknowledging it with a nod.

Old Yang remarked, “After the sage created characters, apart from the eight who also made significant contributions, there hasn’t been a single master in the world of calligraphy who hasn’t attained the Dao. The lowest of the lowest.”

It was evident that the old man did not recognize the calligrapher’s ability to rank among the top nine schools, even feeling that calligraphers didn’t deserve a place among the hundred schools of thought.

The old scholar was known for being able to follow up on anything said, always able to smooth things over, nodding vigorously, “That may not sound pleasant, but it’s the truth. Cui Zhan once had this sentiment early on, feeling that the so-called masters of calligraphy in the current age are merely scribblers. They’re all just empty shells that want to turn the tide—what else could it be but mischief?”

Bai Ye was well aware that several pioneering ancestors of the calligraphy school had good relations with the old scholar. Cui Zhan’s reputation for writing gold was not earned from thin air; it was due to the old scholar traveling the world with him during his early years, gathering autumn wind. No matter how good the stele and letters in the world were, they ultimately were separated from the true essence of authentic writing by a layer of paper. Cui Zhan, however, was able to see the original works of those calligraphy ancestors with the old scholar’s assistance.

“Old brother, you should write a few more letters, taking advantage of this inspiration from wine. Write down whatever comes to mind. The more down-to-earth the content, the more likable it will be. How many oranges did you buy? What meals did you eat today? Did the wind blow or rain? Did you enjoy yourself on the balcony? Did the bamboo shoots turn out a bit bitter today? Just write freely. If that doesn’t work, say you met me today, and your old friend was so generous, he sent you a basket of pears, making you cry uncontrollably…”

It would need to be treated as a family heirloom. “Old brother, what kind of expression is that? Am I the kind of person who sells things the moment I step out? You think I’d have friends like that?”

“I write, you write. We're a perfect match. We just need a big business tycoon to help with the printing and selling of books. Otherwise, the three of us together would be unbeatable in the world.”

As for the so-called eight founding figures of the Heavenly Lord Qing Tong, Bai Ye had a rough idea: Da Zhuang Taishi, Li Tonggu of the small seal script, Yuan Cen of the clerical script, Shi Jiujiu of the regular script, Zhang Chunhua of the running script, Zhang Huai of the wild cursive script, Wang Zhong of the standard script, and Zhong Yao of the small regular script. Only Cui Zhan was “not diligent in his craft,” just casual about it. In fact, Cui Zhan’s small regular script was exceptionally exquisite; the sutras he copied were treasures in many major Buddhist temples in Central Plains.

The old scholar turned and sat on the long bench beneath the eaves, patting the bench with his hand. “Sturdy.”

Old Yang asked, “Mr. Wen Sheng, aside from having me pass on the letter to Lost Fortune Mountain and seal it with more stamps, what else do you wish for?”

The old scholar replied, “Nothing else. Just to thank the senior.”

Old Yang certainly didn’t believe it.

The old scholar wasn’t in a hurry to slap his own face, glancing left and right.

Perhaps in the past, Little Qi and Little Ping’an had also sat here. Without the teacher nearby, the student felt lonely sitting there, unable to rest comfortably, which was somewhat exhausting.

The three of them almost simultaneously looked up.

In the sky of Baoping Continent, a massive hole appeared, with a golden-skinned deity slowly poking its head out. Countless golden lightning bolts intertwined like a web across thousands of miles around the vicinity, and its gaze seemed to have landed on the area around North Mountain and Piyun Mountain.

The old scholar stomped his foot. “Bai Brother! This guy is definitely provoking you! Do you need me to shout ‘Bai Ye is here’ for you?”

Bai Ye’s expression remained calm. “With Liu Sixteen here.”

The old scholar stood up, rubbing his hands. “That big guy, fighting bare-handed, would suffer losses. It’s better that Bai Brother has a celestial sword…”

Yet, in the middle of the old scholar’s words.

A robust figure, originally at Jisi Peak of Lost Fortune Mountain, was first sent by Mountain Lord Wei Ban to a secluded edge of North Mountain territory. Then, within a radius of a hundred miles, there was the sound of the earth rumbling, and the figure shot straight up into the sky.

Wei Ban wiped the sweat from his forehead. Sending this person who called himself “Jun Qian” to the boundary of his jurisdiction was such a laborious task. He was no longer the land deity of Chess Mountain, but the Mountain Lord of the North. If it was this difficult, was Liu Sixteen’s “way” too exaggerated?

That figure transformed into a rainbow of light, soaring into the highest point of the sky.

Since that ancient deity was still far from the ground while in the sky, it had not yet been suppressed too much by the Great Dao. It was an undeniable colossal being, like a great mountain suspended in the air.

The old scholar laughed and scolded, “That foolish giant always suffers in fights. He’s far behind his junior disciple. But his unwavering momentum is still quite impressive.”

At that moment in the sky of Baoping Continent, the deity, as large as a mountain, was abruptly struck aside by a figure as small as a mustard seed. This infinitesimal being continuously punched at the towering deity, and in an instant, the sky reverberated with thunder. Eventually, the unexpected guest's hand, arm, and head shattered instantly.

In the high sky spanning nearly half a continent, countless golden droplets fell. Before they could land, the vast majority of the golden fragments had already vanished, dissolving into the world. It was as if they were drawn by the mysterious Great Dao, with the remaining golden rain almost entirely falling within a thousand miles around Piyun Mountain. Just as they were about to merge with the mountains and waters, the golden light flickered and vanished, leaving many mountain spirits and celestial dwellings stunned. Could it be that Mountain Lord Wei intercepted them? Several enlightened beings immediately observed the mountains and rivers, looking at Piyun Mountain, but it seemed that the spiritual energy in the mountains and waters had not increased too much—what a strange occurrence.

On the steps of Qilong Alley, a smiling woman shook the golden light flowing from her sleeves, but the anomaly disappeared in an instant.

The old scholar said, “I’ll trouble the senior to lead the way.”

Old Yang nodded.

Liu Sixteen felt a shift in his thoughts and swiftly descended. Approaching the earthly ground, he suddenly shrank the mountains and rivers by thousands of miles, arriving at the backyard of a small town’s medicine shop.

Seeing the old scholar already standing on the long bench, Liu Sixteen’s eyes turned red. Thankfully, he had already cried in the Ancestral Hall; otherwise, it would be even more embarrassing now.

The old scholar stood on the bench, stroking his beard and smiling.

Liu Sixteen walked over quickly, tears brimming in his eyes, and bowed deeply, calling out, “Jun Qian pays respects to the teacher!”

Among the four students of the past, Cui Zhan was reserved, with a sharp edge; Qi Jingchun received the true teachings of the Wen Sheng, while Liu Sixteen was the most awkward but also the most sincere.

The old scholar patted the broad-shouldered man’s shoulder, jumped down from the long bench, and nodded with a smile, “As expected, you’re a good brother of Bai Ye; my good disciple, what a great ‘only drives away dragons and snakes, not mosquitoes!’”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 833: Riddles

The old scholar took Liu Sixteen to explore the town of Huaihuang County together. Liu Sixteen had never traveled to Lihuzhou Cave, so he couldn't feel any sense of nostalgia or change. 

The tall man only felt sentimental. This was the place where Xiao Qi, although far from home, found peace in his heart. For true scholars, it's easy to feel lost when gazing into the distance; the hardest part is finding a sense of belonging, a "hometown" where they can truly relax along the endless path of learning.

Liu Sixteen regretted his "return to the mountains" journey, thinking he should have waited a bit longer. Even if he couldn't change the outcome of Lihuzhou Cave, it would have let Xiao Qi know that during his solitary journey, he had a fellow disciple watching him from behind. That way, he wouldn’t feel so isolated, as if he were at odds with the whole world, which could seem pitiful, laughable, and incomprehensible to others.

The old scholar said softly, "Silly tall one, there's no need to be too sad. We scholars, when we read and seek knowledge, are in tune with the sages of the past, becoming their neighbors and friends. Once we put aside the texts of the sages, we should take the initiative, claiming, 'Who else but me?'"

The old scholar murmured the phrase "Who else but me?" again.

Liu Sixteen nodded but still felt somewhat downcast. Restraining his nature and true self was indeed something he excelled at.

Time passed slowly, and as the years rolled on, if considered by actual age, not to mention a few senior brothers, even the teacher and close friend Bai Ye could be said to be "younger" than him—far from it. 

But wisdom comes with experience. 

Thus, the old scholar, who was not tall and had a thin frame, was referred to as "old" scholar.

Huaihuang County was now a top-tier county in the Great Li Dynasty.

The townsfolk, who once made their living by firing ceramics, relying on mountains and rivers, had almost all left the town and the dragon kiln. They sold their ancestral homes and moved to the state capital to enjoy a better life. The biggest and only official in the town back then was the supervising official, but now officials of all ranks could be seen everywhere. Each year, the peach blossoms bloomed on time, and though the old porcelain mountain and the immortal's tomb were gone, the incense at the civil and military temples flourished. At the peaks of the mountains and the banks of the rivers, there were now numerous temples that attracted throngs of worshippers.

In the past, the town lacked a county government but had an old locust tree that provided shade for the fields. Under that tree, every dusk, old men would gather to share tales of the past, while children, tired of listening to stories, would play among themselves. During the summer heat, when the children were worn out, they would run to the Iron Chain Well, eagerly awaiting their elders to pull up the basket and slice the melons and fruits chilled by natural ice. Despite the heat of the day, the water, the melons, and even the knife felt cool, as if their eyes were cooled too.

The old scholar arrived at the site of the Iron Chain Well, where the well still stood even without the iron chains, but its mysteries had vanished. Today, the county's officials had lifted the restrictions, but the number of people coming to draw water had greatly decreased. This small county town was filled with all kinds of people, many of whom were cultivators seeking the dragon's energy, spiritual energy, and the energy of immortals. As a result, the market atmosphere in the town was not as lively as that in the northern state capital, where the smoke from cooking fires and the sounds of roosters and dogs filled the air.

The old scholar suddenly smiled and said, "Your little junior brother was once an apprentice kiln worker and was very skilled. However, he traveled far as a youth, believing he hadn’t truly graduated, so he never easily put his skills to use. If you see your junior brother in the future, you can ask him to help you burn some scholar’s supplies, like the Four Treasures of the Study, or some small items. Just tell him directly; there’s no need to be too formal. Your junior brother is never stingy."

Liu Sixteen responded with an "mm." 

This time, reuniting with the teacher after a long time, the teacher had mentioned his junior brother in every sentence. Liu Sixteen listened and remembered every word without feeling the slightest jealousy; he was only happy because the teacher's mindset had seemed so relaxed for a long time.

The old scholar certainly meant something by his words, but after waiting for a long time without any realization from the silly tall one, he kicked Liu Sixteen lightly on the calf.

The teacher felt guilty towards his little disciple and couldn’t bear to ask for items himself. Did the other students not know to ease the teacher’s burden a little? The silly tall one was clearly not as clever as his junior brother.

Liu Sixteen immediately understood and said, "Student will also ask for a few items for the teacher."

The old scholar pretended to be troubled, rubbing his hands. "What kind of propriety is that, what kind of propriety?"

Liu Sixteen replied, "The teacher hasn’t said anything. Your junior brother is so clever; he will naturally understand."

The old scholar immediately changed his expression, stroking his beard with a laugh, "Of course, your junior brother is the best at drawing connections, especially between the characters 'ten thousand' and 'one.' The teacher hasn’t taught him much, yet he has learned extremely well on his own. Now, everyone says my ability to take disciples is unparalleled; in fact, it’s quite embarrassing for me."

In reality, the matter of taking Chen Ping’an as a closed-door disciple had never been mentioned by the great deity Suishan, and neither had Chen Chun’an, Bai Ze, or later Bai Ye ever agreed with a word.

So who exactly the "everyone" the old scholar referred to was, who knows?

Liu Sixteen nodded. "I only heard some rumors from Bai Ye and the teacher, which confirmed that your junior brother is indeed very clever."

The old scholar chuckled heartily. 

It had been a long time since he felt so refreshed.

The silly tall one praised his teacher, recognizing his foresight and the cleverness of his junior brother, which made the elder brother confident and pleased. 

Good, good, very kind, very kind.

In terms of worldly knowledge, among the four direct disciples, Cui Zhan was undoubtedly the best. In fact, the silly tall one could rank second, but he just didn't like to talk and often kept to himself. When he did speak, it was often in a straightforward manner, like when he once chased after A Liang to play a game.

Among the four brothers, there was no distinction between closeness or distance. While Xiao Qi and his peer sometimes had conflicts, their relationship was actually closer. Cui Zhan and Liu Sixteen had a decent relationship; one thought too much, while the other spoke too little, so they got along well.

As Liu Sixteen walked through the town, besides strolling with the teacher, he paid attention to many details—the presence or absence of the door gods at each household, the size of the incense offerings at the civil and military temples, and whether the aura of the mountains and rivers in the county flowed steadily and harmoniously... All these were part of his senior brother Cui Zhan's increasingly refined achievements, revealing an invisible manifestation of the "Great Way" in the Great Li Dynasty.

One must understand that "the human heart is indeed precarious, and the way of the Dao is subtle," which is precisely the first eight characters of the Confucian "heart transmission."

In Liu Sixteen’s eyes, Cui Zhan's meticulous cultivation over the past century or so in both the Great Li and Baoping Continent was indeed a remarkable feat, balancing the heavy and the light with ease.

In his early years, Cui Zhan was not a grand master of the Great Li; he was merely an heir of the Literary Sage. He had so much to say about the state of the world, but as his knowledge grew, his naturally proud temperament meant that in his life, there seemed to be only one person willing to listen: Liu Sixteen, this silent and reticent junior brother, whom Cui Zhan deemed worthy to speak to.

Liu Sixteen said, "Earlier, when the ancient remnant's golden body shattered, my intention was to gift it to the North岳 region, as a token of gratitude to Lord Wei of Piyun Mountain. I didn’t expect there to be a strange presence in Qilong Lane that could actually cast a spell and gather all the body fragments. It seems Lord Wei wasn’t surprised at all; he looked entirely unbothered."

The old scholar nodded. "That long-lived friend in Qilong Lane has an impressive background; she is the incarnation of the ancient gold essence copper coin. She currently serves as a temporary unmarked worshipper of the Fallen Mountain. When she comes to gather the golden body fragments, the Great Way aligns perfectly, so it’s a matter of course. Besides Lord Wei, the cultivators in the North岳 region would only be left in the dark. Lord Wei is used to taking the blame for Fallen Mountain, as debts do not weigh one down. So, when you meet Lord Wei in the future, be extra courteous and observe how magnanimous he is; he has hosted numerous night feasts without batting an eye."

Liu Sixteen replied, "Then I will seek out Brother Zuo later and break a few remnants of those golden bodies that covet the North岳 mountains and rivers. I’ll also remind the long-lived friend to ensure she gives five shares to Piyun Mountain."

The old scholar nodded in satisfaction, saying, "Helping others is helping oneself; it is indeed a good habit."

For now, the silly tall one wouldn’t have major issues. 

Even if some accidents occurred, as the teacher, he wouldn’t simply be idle.

Moreover, Liu Sixteen’s words were equally ineffective with Brother Zuo. 

Brother Zuo had always liked to put on airs as an elder brother. Back in the tavern at the Sword Qi Great Wall, he was a bit shy and didn’t act right.

In the past, whenever the old scholar wanted to drink more or host a small banquet for the Five Zang Temple, he would urge the silly tall one to manage the funds with Brother Zuo, suggesting they spend what they had today and borrow if they lacked money tomorrow. Yet, not once did it ever work out. Xiao Qi was much more considerate, knowing to take the opportunity to set up stalls and help write letters and Spring Festival couplets. Each time he earned some pocket money, he never let Brother Zuo handle it, and then the teacher and a few students would secretly leave Brother Zuo behind, first finishing their drinks and burping in the yard before entering the house, leaving Brother Zuo out of the loop.

Liu Sixteen asked, "On the way here, Bai Ye mentioned to me that the previous Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Xiao Zhen, should have integrated with the barbaric world."

The old scholar replied, "Xiao Zhen is a sword cultivator and has indeed integrated with the world, so he shouldn’t be underestimated. However, if Brother Zuo is pushed too hard, he doesn’t necessarily need to integrate with the world to reach the Fourteenth Stage..."

At this point, the old scholar looked worried and shook his head. "It’s best if he doesn’t; which Fourteenth Stage cultivator can be considered free? Moreover, your Brother Zuo is the most taboo sword cultivator. It’s a tremendous trouble; you know that well enough. When Brother Zuo is stubborn, even if it’s just you few junior brothers, it’s not easy for me as the teacher to influence him. I was never willing for Brother Zuo to learn swordsmanship."

Liu Sixteen remarked, "Brother Zuo started practicing swordsmanship quite late, yet he can make the 'Sword Immortal embryo' a topic of discussion on the mountain. Even Bai Ye believes Brother Zuo’s path is substantial, and his swordsmanship will be high."

The old scholar sighed, "The path of gains and losses cannot be overlooked."

As they strolled, many passersby in the streets noticed the tall Liu Sixteen, but it was fortunate that Longzhou had grown accustomed to the presence of mountain deities, so they didn’t find the tall man frightening.

Because of the relationship between the closed-door disciple Chen Ping’an and the child-like Guige, the Great Li Dynasty, in return, left behind only a "falsehood" of the ancient well that resembled a small cave heaven, while the "truth" was moved behind the bamboo houses of the Fallen Mountain to the pond’s edge, where there was another hidden world. Though the Song family of the Great Li recognized the value of the well and its many secrets, they remained unable to fully develop the small cave heaven on their own. There were simply too few sword immortals in Baoping Continent; otherwise, the small cave heaven in the well, albeit small, was a remarkable cultivation site, particularly suitable for those associated with dragons and water spirits. It was also possible that Cui Dongshan deliberately kept it hidden, having long considered the well to be his own property.

The old scholar sat for a while by the well, contemplating how to connect the lotus root blessed land with the small cave heaven. After thinking it over, he considered seeking help, which was manageable since he had built some connections in the Haoran world. Sadly, money was hard to come by, so he could only sigh, "A penny can defeat a hero, and a poor scholar dies of worry," to which Liu Sixteen offered to borrow money from Bai Ye. However, the old scholar shook his head, saying it wasn't good to borrow money from friends, as it would damage their relationship. Then the old man looked up at the silly tall one, and after thinking for a moment, Liu Sixteen said it wouldn’t count as borrowing money from Bai Ye.

It is said that the first time Bai Ye sent Jun Qian back to the mountains, he drunkenly wrote the word "magnificent," and deliberately wrote the "magnificent" character a bit bigger.

It implied that his friend Jun Qian's grand demeanor was not limited to just a bit, viewing the rivers and mountains of the world over countless years.

Recalling the past, that person who was hailed as the most accomplished scholar in the world, could write such a work and have such aspirations, indeed had no regrets.

After sending his friend back to the mountains, Bai Ye descended the mountain alone, wielding his sword among mortals. With a single strike, he split the Yellow River's cave heaven, allowing the scholar to resist the heavenly will with his own strength, ensuring that the central land would never again worry about drought.

This single act significantly boosted the water transport of the Haoran world by a tenth.

What a spirited display!

Thus, Wei Ban, who hailed from the ancient Divine Water Kingdom, naturally held Bai Ye in high esteem.

As for those who could be so unrestrained and casual with Bai Ye, there was probably only this "Jun Qian brother," who had once accompanied Bai Ye to visit the immortals.

At this moment, the old scholar smiled broadly, standing up and heavily patting the silly tall one's arm, praising, "Sixteen, you’ve made progress."

In this world, how could there be a senior brother who doesn’t look after his junior brother? In the lineage of the Wensheng, there certainly wasn’t.

The old scholar wasn’t without the means to acquire some money himself. In the vast Haoran world, even the most deeply hidden heavenly materials and earthly treasures couldn’t escape his discerning eye. However, it was a matter of knowing what to do and what not to do; he felt it was crucial to talk about the rules of earning money, especially since the Great Way had its own order. Earning something unjustly today would inevitably lead to loss tomorrow; it wasn’t worth it. As a teacher, he wouldn’t want to complicate matters for the youngest and most promising disciple.

Bringing Liu Sixteen to the place popularly known as the Crab Workshop, the old scholar stopped and said, "This is where the Ascension Platform is guarded by the Qingtong Tianjun; it has ended up looking like this."

With one hand behind him and the other pointing to the sky, he continued, "Once, a heavenly general was responsible for guiding earth immortals to ascend. At that time, the so-called earth immortals were known for their 'truth,' which was comparatively valuable compared to 'heavenly immortals,' who lived long and roamed the land, referred to as terrestrial immortals. As for the current Nascent Soul and Golden Core cultivators, being called earth immortals, they are simply incomparable. The 'seeking truth' of immortals is mainly about understanding the heavenly way, achieving liberation, and ultimately ascending. During that tumultuous and grand battle, this heavenly general, adorned in 'Great Frost' armor, was the only one to choose to fight to the death, and he was pinned to the door by a certain elder... no, it was by a not-so-elderly predecessor with a single sword."

The last true dragon in the world, after enduring countless hardships, had to escape here for a reason. As long as the Qingtong Tianjun was willing to reopen the Ascension Platform, there would be a glimmer of hope. Though the heavens had perished, there was still no talk of ascension. However, escaping to a secret realm of shattered mountains and rivers wouldn’t be difficult. At that point, it would be a true case of being far and wide.

However, as one of the greatest criminals in heaven and earth, Qingtong Tianjun's situation was precarious, akin to a mud bodhisattva crossing a river; self-preservation wasn’t hard, but she seemed to need to hold incense high over her head every day to prevent the incense from ceasing, naturally reluctant to ruin the rules set by the three individuals at the Fifteenth Stage for the sake of a little true dragon.

The Lihuzhou Cave was a series of interconnected truths set up by Yang Laotou, obscuring the shallow illusions visible to the world, in fact, to hide the greatest truth, which was the true illusion.

The old scholar lingered at the archway for a long time, gazing up at one of the tablets.

Liu Sixteen asked, "That fellow who entered the Haoran world from the barbaric world, using the name Zhou Mi, has many tricks. Do you know what his background is, teacher?"

Due to his status, Liu Sixteen had never been very interested in worldly affairs.

The old scholar's expression grew serious as he slowly replied, "His surname is Jia; I won't say his full name to avoid attracting his scrutiny. He was once a genuine student of our Confucian school, so we can call him Jia Sheng."

Liu Sixteen immediately understood, “So it’s him.”

Upon reflection, he felt it was unexpected yet within reason.

Historically, many scholars after Jia Sheng's death had defended him and cried injustice, with some even stating, "In one generation, the great Confucian is none other than Jia Sheng." Those who said this were not ordinary people.

The so-called great Confucian praised Jia Sheng for his talent, charisma, and literary prowess. It was evident that within the Confucian lineage, there was no disagreement regarding the current rules. In the Western Buddhist nations, and even in the Qīng Míng world, there was no such thing as a hundred schools contending.

Liu Sixteen asked, "What do you think of Jia Sheng’s Twelve Policies for Peace?"

"A powerful remedy, one that can indeed bring peace." 

The old scholar smiled, "But there is a problem with it: Jia Sheng is solely focused on treatment. Even if he saves someone, the power of the medicine is too strong. For example, in this market below the mountains surrounding us, no matter how good the medicine is, after several years or ten years, most people would just become a medicine jar. How can one not worry about that? 

These are just superficial issues; there is a deeper root cause: the knowledge of Jia Sheng diverges fundamentally from the Confucian teachings."

Liu Sixteen softly asked, "So, is that why you resolutely denied the achievements of the eldest senior brother back then?"

The old scholar hesitated for a moment, then shook his head. "His achievements are somewhat better than Jia Sheng’s because it isn’t about starting from scratch, rebuilding a house and nailing shut the windows, leaving only one door. Your senior brother’s achievements are far from being as extreme as Jia Sheng’s."

The old scholar pointed to the now faded tablets and asked, "Why are the tablets hung high while the couplets are often posted wide?"

Liu Sixteen followed the teacher's finger and answered, "Only by walking on a wide path can one steadily ascend to greater heights."

The old scholar nodded in approval and then led Liu Sixteen around the archway, sharing some insights in a whisper.

The four tablets read: "Taking the Initiative," "Seek Nature," "Do Not Seek Outside," and "Energy Shocking the Bull."

After circling around, they returned to the tablet that read "Taking the Initiative."

The old scholar emphasized the Daoist aspect.

The Daoist tablet’s "Seek Nature" praises the individual who is the first disciple of the Dao ancestor, Bai Yujing. He ultimately transformed into the Three Pure Ones. On the street of blessings in Lihuzhou Cave, the scholar Li Xisheng, who was stuck in the peach and plum blossoms, belonged to the Confucian lineage, while the one in the Daoist sect was enveloped in the Dao. There was still another, even the old scholar himself didn’t know for the time being, but it was presumed to be a disciple of the Buddhist sect.

The struggle among the three teachings resides within me.

I discuss the Dao with myself, living in the world while being at odds with it, as if a ghost ship brushes against the vessel; even if there are those with malicious hearts, they remain calm.

This is the true greatness of the Dao ancestor’s method.

Compared to the mixed praises and criticisms of Bai Yujing's other two headmasters, this Dao ancestor's first disciple has an excellent reputation outside the Qīng Míng world in several realms.

Moreover, both Dao's second and Lu Chen were his disciples, but only the Dao ancestor's closed-door disciple was replaced with Lu Chen as his apprentice.

Liu Sixteen furrowed his brow slightly.

The old scholar patted his arm, "No need to think too much. Although in the Lihuzhou Cave, Li Xisheng, one of the three, is a latecomer, in the Haoran world, Xiao Qi is the one who arrived last. Moreover, the Dao ancestor himself has no intention of targeting Xiao Qi; it’s more about the methods of the other two lineages from Bai Yujing. Li Xisheng has always been somewhat out of control. If it weren’t for Lu Chen’s plotting, the kind of grand competition between Xiao Qi and Li Xisheng would have been as fierce as the waves clashing, creating towering waves with a magnificent spirit. Regardless of victory or defeat, it would never have been a matter of lowly actions. Perhaps..."

Even as the old scholar spoke to his disciple in a whisper, he still didn’t express his feelings.

Originally, the old scholar wanted to say, "As fellow practitioners, we should establish our teachings and recognize our ancestors. One is a primary disciple while the other is a secondary disciple, and the Great Way benefits each other."

Whether it was Li Xisheng, the Dao ancestor, or Xiao Qi, once both sides truly began to debate the Dao, they would surely have this broad-mindedness.

But they had not been able to reach that point.

Now that things had reached this stage, the situation was already set; it was pointless to say more.

However, the old scholar’s reluctance to speak excessively on this matter did not mean he was indifferent.

The old scholar never endorsed the unprincipled notion of repaying kindness with vengeance; that was not a broad-minded attitude but rather ignorance.

Liu Sixteen turned his head, having to lower it to see the teacher's profile.

The teacher was gazing up at the four characters with a hint of sadness.

It was just that the teacher felt too lonely. There were very few who could share a drink with him and allow him to speak his mind freely.

The plaque read: "Taking the Initiative."

The old scholar had not withdrawn his gaze for a long time.

"Who else but me?"

In the Confucian lineage, there was Qi Jingchun of the Lihuzhou Cave, Cui Zhan of the Baoping Continent, and Brother Zuo of the Tongye Continent, as well as Chen Ping’an of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Now, there was also Liu Sixteen, who had returned to the Haoran world.

A gentle breeze brushed his face; the old scholar looked around and smiled, raising his hand to scratch his head, murmuring, "The spring breeze knows my intentions, sending dreams back to past years. There are many in the world who are improper; many injustices exist, but they cannot extinguish the beauty in my heart."

Liu Sixteen echoed softly.

The past is gone, and the future has yet to come. Time is forever the past, and every moment has a future. The past once was the future, and the future will become the past.

In the end, he was kicked by the teacher, who jokingly scolded him to stop it. The Confucian lineage was fortunate to have his little junior brother, or else they would be laughed at for being a group of hermits.

Liu Sixteen grinned, mimicking the teacher's head-scratching gesture, glad he still had plenty of hair. 

But when he looked at the teacher’s thin figure, he couldn't help but feel sad and nearly shed tears.

When Liu Sixteen raised his head, he wondered why no one was coming yet. Why was there no movement in the sky? Feeling discontent, he prepared to throw a punch to vent his frustrations.

The old scholar chuckled, "Silly tall one, look forward to something good. Fighting and killing is too un-scholarly."

After that, the old scholar took Liu Sixteen to the old academy. Though it had fallen into disrepair, there was no sign of decay; everywhere was clean and organized.

It was said that a young girl named Warm Tree would come down regularly to clean the academy and the ancestral home in Mud Bottle Lane.

They then visited the new academy established by the Chen family at Longwei Creek, where the sound of reading echoed.

The old scholar particularly enjoyed watching the little children shake their heads as they learned; some recited fluently while others stumbled over their words, but all were quite good.

While visiting the academy, the old scholar also observed the teaching methods of the instructors, their demeanor, and their tones.

In truth, true Buddhas merely speak ordinary words.

In official circles, using bureaucratic language is unavoidable, yet one must not speak only in officialese; remember, all official language derives from human language.

Even as a deity on the mountain, one cannot only possess the aura of immortals with sleeves full of clouds and wind; there must also be some human warmth.

Having read too many texts from the sages, people differ, and their reasoning varies. Ultimately, one must hope for improvements in the world; otherwise, constantly lamenting and speaking strange words while dragging others into disappointment and despair is not virtuous.

After leaving the academy, as they walked through the Apricot Blossom Lane, the old scholar casually said to Liu Sixteen, "Back then, Xiao Qi accompanied Brother Zuo on a journey through the mountains and rivers, while you visited Baidi City with Cui Zhan."

Liu Sixteen nodded. "After Cui Shixiong finished the Cloud Color Chess game with the lord of Baidi City, he wrote a cursive couplet for Zheng's family: 'No ancients before, no successors after; standing right in the middle.'"

The old scholar laughed, "Is that so?"

Liu Sixteen continued, "In the end, he lost the game, so Cui Shixiong didn’t want to say much more."

It was a homophone for "Zheng."

See, disciples of the Confucian lineage treat others with sincerity.

Then, as they walked along the road, they encountered a handsome young drunkard, who was the supervising official Cao Gengxin, along with the county magistrate Yuan Zhengding, both prominent scions of the Great Li.

Cao, the supervising official, had just finished drinking, with a full wine jar hanging from his waist, swaying as he made his way to the official residence for roll call.

Sometimes, when he was too drunk to walk, he would give a handful of coins to a familiar young worker or call out to a well-known child on the street, paying them to take the wine jar to the supervising official's office and place it on the table, which would count as helping him check in.

The old scholar looked at the young man with a smile.

Cao Gengxin noticed the short elder in a Confucian robe surveying him, but he didn’t greet him and instead turned to the side, swaggering down the street with a laugh, giving a nod of respect to the unfamiliar old gentleman.

The old scholar returned the gesture with a nod.

In this world, not all scholarly officials can be so free-spirited and unrestrained, but at the same time, it is absolutely necessary to have a few like them.

As for the county magistrate Yuan Zhengding, the more, the better.

In the old scholar's eyes, there was no distinction between the two; they were both exceptional young men.

After wandering through many streets of the small town, passing through the somewhat desolate Mud Bottle Lane, they returned to Qilong Lane, where a tall, white-clad figure awaited them on the steps.

The long-lived friend had been waiting for a long time and greeted the old scholar without a word.

The old scholar smiled broadly, and the long-lived friend led them into the auspicious shop, where the old scholar sampled some pastries, and Liu Sixteen also tried a few, although he didn’t dare to overindulge. The previous shopkeeper, Shi Rou, was startled and was about to offer a grand greeting to the "Wensheng Laoye" who seemed to have stepped out from the portrait, but the old scholar waved his hand with a smile, telling her not to bother.

Liu Sixteen spoke with the long-lived friend about some serious matters, and she naturally had no objections. If a few more golden raindrops fell in the North岳 region, the lotus root blessed land's empty seat for the mountain spirit would emerge like bamboo shoots after a rain. Moreover, as the lotus root blessed land had not long been promoted to a medium blessed land, it would soon be able to match the top medium blessed lands in terms of both the number of spirits and the quality of their golden bodies.

Money falling from the sky is indeed a rare occurrence, and if it all fell into one person’s pocket, it would be even more exceptional.

With the long-lived friend overseeing the mountain at Fallen Mountain, the influx of wealth would be unstoppable.

Thus, both before entering and after exiting the Qilong Lane, the old scholar cheerfully expressed his gratitude to her.

The long-lived friend initially cited her responsibilities, but the second time, she habitually accepted it with a smile.

After leaving Qilong Lane, the old scholar said, "Since your little junior brother isn’t around, let’s go meet your little junior brother's close friend. He is certainly one of the ones who protects Chen Ping’an the most."

At the blacksmith shop by the Longxu River, Liu Sixteen met Liu Xianyang, who was lounging on a bamboo chair, soaking up the sun.

After Liu Sixteen introduced himself, Liu Xianyang urged the old scholar to sit quickly while bending over to help the old scholar rub his shoulders, asking whether the pressure was too light or too heavy, all while chatting with Liu Sixteen, saying he and the elder were kin.

The old scholar couldn’t help but chuckle, not specifying what kind of kinship they shared.

Liu Sixteen also found it amusing, not revealing the truth, thus acknowledging the young man’s claim of kinship.

The old scholar squinted his eyes in satisfaction, enjoying the moment, and said to the young man that the pressure felt just right, very comfortable, then the old man imitated the children reading, swaying leisurely as he recited, "In the world, pearls and jade are nothing to be taken; how could they compare to the soil at the head of Yangxian Creek?"

Liu Xianyang gasped, "The poem just bought for our local county records, the elder already knows? It seems your learning is so vast that even the entire Haoran world cannot contain it; at the very least, it must include the fifth realm."

Since he was Chen Ping’an's teacher, he could be considered half a teacher to Liu Xianyang.

Flattery overstepped. 

Liu Sixteen, being tall, could only sit on the steps, his fists resting lightly on his knees, staring ahead as if he hadn’t heard.

However, the old scholar took it seriously, saying, "Such words are best kept among kin; they should not be widely shared, lest they invite envy and resentment."

Liu Xianyang, sitting on the adjacent bamboo chair, declared solemnly, "If the elder says so, it must be that clear and bright character. But we, your student disciples, should seize every opportunity to speak fairly for the elder. Good words are never too many!"

Liu Sixteen couldn’t help but glance at Liu Xianyang, whose face was full of sincerity. This young man had studied under the Confucian Chen family for many years in the Southern Poxing Continent. Reflecting on the scenes at Fallen Mountain, with Wei Shan Jun, the sword immortal, and the girl in the pink skirt named Chen Warm Tree, as well as the little girl in black named Zhou Milin, all seemed well-educated. He felt relieved. As long as his junior brother didn’t pick up Liu Xianyang’s way of speaking, everything would be fine.

The old scholar chatted with Liu Xianyang about some serious academic matters.

Through a question-and-answer format, the old scholar was very pleased. The depth of study and diligence indeed depend on innate talent, yet sincerity and effort do not rely on talent.

Afterward, the old scholar had Liu Xianyang ask questions, leading into another question-and-answer session.

From start to finish, Liu Xianyang sat up straight.

At the end, the old scholar said to the young man, "Xianyang, consider this a lesson for you—think carefully about how to harmonize your foundation for standing and the methods for dealing with the world."

After Liu Xianyang nodded, he stood up, stepping back a few paces, bowing respectfully to the old scholar as a disciple of the Confucian lineage.

The old scholar stood up, smiling and nodding, "I won't return the bow like those later Daoists because I have a question for you, and you haven’t answered. Whatever you gain from now on, I will return the favor later."

As if stepping out of a small world of the Confucian lineage, Liu Xianyang immediately revealed his true self, standing up straight and laughing heartily, "Elder, you flatter me."

Liu Sixteen understood even more than Liu Xianyang.

The teacher's question was a big one.

In fact, the essence of the three teachings of Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism shares many similarities in higher and broader contexts.

For example, there was a question in the "Transmission of the Lamp": "What should learners do if they don’t adhere to the earth?" The master replied, "Where do you intend to establish your life?"

The old scholar said, "Let’s go, let’s go."

Liu Sixteen quickly stood up and bowed, "Jun Qian bids farewell to the elder."

The old scholar said, "The emperor loves the eldest son, the common people love the youngest. As your teacher, I cannot help but favor my closed-door disciple a bit more. Jun Qian, do not think too much about it; after all, Chen Ping’an is different from you; he has spent the least time by my side, relies on himself the most, and is still the youngest...”

At this point, the old scholar halted his words, suddenly realizing that even his own closed-door disciple was not so young anymore.

That once-clear-eyed youth, who couldn’t even drink and walked across mountains and rivers in straw shoes, had actually passed his thirties and was now approaching forty.

The old scholar sighed, stamping his foot, and his figure vanished.

Liu Xianyang then offered a handful of sunflower seeds, while Liu Sixteen returned to the steps, shaking his head.

Liu Xianyang took the initiative to say a few words, to which Liu Sixteen nodded or replied concisely with a few words. The two "kin" who had met for the first time began to fall silent, each lost in their thoughts, yet neither felt awkward.

Finally, Liu Sixteen asked, "Earlier, when you were dozing off, I noticed your sword intent flowing through your form. Were you practicing swordsmanship in your dreams?"

Liu Xianyang nodded, casually saying, "There’s an ancestral sword manual with a rather peculiar method of practice; it’s a pity it’s not suitable for Chen Ping’an."
