Liu Sixteen said, "I’m friends with Bai Ye. His swordsmanship is quite good. If you encounter a significant bottleneck in your sword cultivation in the future, you can seek him out for sparring. Although Bai Ye has a cold demeanor, he’s actually warm-hearted. When he meets a junior like you, he’ll definitely take notice."

Liu Xianyang turned and clasped his fists with a beaming smile, "Alright, even if the bottleneck isn’t too severe, as long as Bai Ye is willing to teach, I’m eager to learn!"

Liu Sixteen nodded. The young man was not small-minded; he had a big heart. He wouldn’t think he was receiving charity from someone above him, which was excellent.

No wonder he could be friends with his junior brother.

Just like himself and Bai Ye?

Liu Sixteen stood up and bid farewell to Liu Xianyang. He was not one to enjoy talking, especially not polite talk.

Liu Sixteen asked Wei Shan Jun to help conceal his presence as he returned to Fallen Mountain.

He planned to stay here for a while, waiting for the door to the sky to open again, so he could entertain guests.

Having spent a long time at Fallen Mountain, he had become familiar with Wei Ban and even with Mi Yu, who came from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Liu Sixteen inquired about his junior brother’s hidden official matters from the sword immortal Mi Yu.

He felt greatly relieved.

Now, Liu Sixteen was quite knowledgeable about Fallen Mountain.

Although his junior brother often traveled far and rarely stayed in his hometown, he spent more time in foreign lands.

Yet he had still accumulated a vast foundation, which was truly not easy.

Currently, Fallen Mountain's resources, apart from the incense connection with Piyun Mountain’s Wei Shan Jun, purely from the business at the Niu Jiao Mountain ferry, generated quite a bit of income.

It was a pity Liu Sixteen could not meet Zhu Lian, the one nicknamed the Old Chef.

Moreover, the teacher said that his junior brother’s first disciple, Pei Qian, would sooner or later astonish the entire world, which made Liu Sixteen quite curious.

The sword immortal Mi Yu, who went by the alias Yu Mi, had yet to pay respects at the Zushi Hall of the Jisefeng, but in Baoping Continent, a sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall at the Jade Purity level held considerable weight.

However, this sword cultivator was indeed quite lazy.

It was said that through his own ferry, he had purchased many mountain artifacts used to appreciate the mirror flowers and water moons, including white bowls, paintings, inkstones, and letters, gathering more than twenty items for Mi Yu, spending money like water. When Zhou Milin spoke to Liu Sixteen about this, the girl felt heartbroken for Yu Mi, saying that at this rate, it was clear he was heading for a life of celibacy.

The doorkeeper Zheng Dafu, born a pure martial artist, had gone to the fifth realm.

Cen Yuanji, born from the Zushi Hall of Fallen Mountain, was also an unnamed disciple of Zhu Lian. The young girl practiced her punches sincerely, walking back and forth along the road from the mountain top to the foot every day.

Seeing this, Liu Sixteen planned to find an opportunity to discreetly guide her on some boxing techniques in accordance with the mountain’s rules.

The siblings Yuan Bao and Yuan Lai were the direct disciples of Lu Baixiang and had just left Fallen Mountain not long ago. 

Thus, Fallen Mountain became even quieter.

As for the Bai Jian Tai, the Golden Core bottleneck Cui Wei had turned into a Qi Practitioner, and he was now following the path of talismans.

The old man Huan Yun, who wandered here from North Ju Lu Continent, had stayed at Fallen Mountain for a year to teach Cui Wei talisman techniques.

Because Cui Wei was not yet a direct disciple of Fallen Mountain’s Zushi Hall, there were few taboos regarding transmitting teachings. Although there was no formal teacher-student relationship, there was a practical one.

Another peer, Zhang Jiazheng, had not been discouraged by his lack of cultivation aptitude. Instead, he chose to follow the reclusive accountant from the Upside-Down Mountain, Wei Wenlong, to learn about financial calculations.

In the auspicious shop of Qilong Lane, the female ghost Shi Rou wore the skin shed by a powerful ascendant.

As for the long-lived friend, she was even more so.

At the grass-roots shop, the blind Daoist Jia Sheng, Zhao Denggao, and Tian Jiu’er were a trio of master and disciples. That girl, Jiu’er, had blood that made her a natural "symbol spring." Had she not entered Fallen Mountain, her fate would not have been good; it was easy for her to become a cash cow for the mountain deities.

A black snake that migrated from Fallen Mountain to the Grey Mist Mountain for cultivation came from Qizhu Mountain and was now at the Dragon Gate level. 

After transforming into human form, he appeared as a pale-faced youth dressed in a "crow blue" robe, a garment made from snake shedding. 

Going by the name of Yun Zi, his true name was "De Zhang."

Regarding the "true name," which was equivalent to half a life, Liu Milin had said it was the "order" of that big white goose, and Yun Zi dared not disobey.

Fortunately, beyond the bestowed name, that Cui Dongshan had also granted a precious treasure suitable for dragon-type cultivators.

As a mountain spirit-water monster, Yun Zi's rapid breakthrough was related to his innate aptitude, but not significantly; it was mainly thanks to the snake gall stone gifted by Chen Lingjun.

As for the deep-hidden great python from Huanghu Mountain, it was already at the Golden Core bottleneck but had always been unwilling to leave the river.

Wei Ban had revealed to Liu Sixteen that it originally hoped to compete with a certain "little loach" for an opportunity in the Great Way of the Five Elements. Unfortunately, it lost and ultimately could not leave Lihuzhou Cave.

The great python's cultivation aptitude was naturally not poor. It had already been able to transform into human form. However, it seldom revealed itself; when it occasionally appeared in the world, it would show its true form, preferring to lurk at the bottom of the great lake, quietly establishing its own aquatic cave.

The former owner of Huanghu Mountain, who had bought the mountaintop with gold essence copper coins, had no idea that a water monster was lurking at the lake's bottom because the great python had never appeared on land in human form. However, it was unaware of its cultivation level, nor did it comprehend the grand opportunity related to the flow of luck in Lihuzhou Cave. Otherwise, they would never have half-sold and half-given Huanghu Mountain to Fallen Mountain.

The great python now went by the name of Huang Shan Nv, with its true name also gifted by Cui Dongshan, recorded in the genealogy as "Buddha Song." She would occasionally leave the water's edge to meet Zhou Milin.

Zhou Milin still dared not descend the mountain alone, relying on bags of sunflower seeds to trade with Wei Shan Jun, and she was thrown by him to the water's edge of Huanghu Mountain every month.

The Huang Shan Nv, with her eyes like water in the autumn, would leave the water’s edge occasionally. When she did, a faint natural aura of vastness surrounded her.

By the lake stood an old pine tree, also hiding mysteries, with a reclusive aura that had not yet caused any disturbances in the mountains and rivers.

What an old python lying still for a thousand years; when would that old pine not meditate?

Contrasted with Yun Zi, who had a naturally imposing presence, the true form of Huang Shan Nv preferred tranquility over movement. The latter's lair was named Qingni Slope, located in Grey Mist Mountain, meaning "fog poisoning the soaring kite and wind carrying the giant python."

The young man in white had once brought the left protector from Qilong Lane to travel through Huanghu Mountain, and when they reached the water, he laughed, saying a literary master once had a poem: "Leave the dragon beneath the lake; do not test the dog on the street."

Hearing that the great python was lurking underwater, its true head pressed against the mud, the earth dog behind the young man trembled in fear, lying flat and unable to rise.

The vassal Huangting Kingdom and the old Divine Water Kingdom, including Hongzhu Town and Qizhu Mountain, historically belonged to the ancient Shu region, where it was said that the cave of the dragon was endless, attracting sword immortals to appear in the waters, with sword light descending to slay dragons. 

However, Liu Sixteen had no intention of visiting Yun Zi and Huang Shan Nv, not wanting to disturb their cultivation, or rather, not wanting to disrupt their resolve in the Dao. 

After all, among the water spirits in the world, encountering Liu Sixteen was not a good thing for them.

Only that little Milin, who carried a golden shoulder pole and a green bamboo staff, patrolling the mountain morning and night without complaint, even when she spent time with Liu Sixteen each day, seemed to have no issues.

Firstly, this "mute lake great water monster" had a low cultivation level, and secondly, Zhou Milin's heart was clear and pure, hence her lack of trouble.

In addition, some of the figures from Fallen Mountain's Zushi Hall were also not on the mountain.

After Liu Sixteen became familiar with Fallen Mountain, he noticed that from the young mountain lord to the student disciples, and even to the direct disciples of the Zushi Hall and the worshippers, it seemed they were all traveling far and wide.

The atmosphere felt strange.

Ordinary mountains would not be like this.

Martial artists, sword cultivators, Confucian scholars, Daoist qi practitioners, various mountain and marsh spirits, and female ghosts.

Not to mention that special long-lived friend.

But they all got along harmoniously.

How strange. 

Today, Zhou Milin dragged the tall Liu Sixteen to sit on the mountain peak, watching as the clumsy Cen sister practiced her punches down the mountain. Her figure seemed to grow smaller and smaller, which made Milin burst into laughter, covering her mouth with both hands, "Hahaha!"

After laughing, Zhou Milin, without waiting for Pei Qian’s reminder to be more ladylike, felt a bit sad, so she decided to say something cheerful and turned to Liu Sixteen, quietly asking, "Half the mountain lord senior brother, let’s guess some riddles! I know a big basket of them. Not to mention Warm Tree sister, even Pei Qian can’t compare to me; she always can’t figure out the answers and ends up spinning around in a hurry." 

Liu Sixteen smiled, "You ask."

Zhou Milin cleared her throat, "In the sky, there is a drum hidden deep within the clouds. When struck, it thunders; when struck again, it rumbles. What is it?"

Liu Sixteen replied, "It’s thunder."

Zhou Milin gave a thumbs up, then the little girl began to ponder.

Oh dear, she had encountered a master.

Originally planning to remind the tall one, Zhou Milin asked, "There’s a grass on the mountain, and it has plenty of pearls. If I don’t take it with me, you’ll also run in vain..." 

Liu Sixteen chuckled, "It’s dew, right?"

There’s a saying in the books about morning dew, that the past is bitter and lengthy.

Still, there’s luck in being safe, seeing the light again; what wrongs remain, if only morning dew.

Zhou Milin crossed her arms, furrowing her brow, thinking of a more challenging riddle, "There are many chess pieces, and the chessboard is large. We can only watch but can’t play. I ask you, what are the chess pieces?"

Liu Sixteen smiled and shook his head.

He had once traveled beyond the heavens alone, witnessing the form of the Literary Sage, plucking those "chess pieces" to block ancient existences.

Zhou Milin shook her head, grinning, "Is it difficult? If you don’t know, just look up at night, and you’ll know the answer."

Then the little girl looked at the tall one, seemingly a bit forlorn. She said, "Little stone tablet, one by one, standing at the door in two rows." She opened her mouth slightly, chuckling.

Liu Sixteen laughed as he rubbed the little girl’s head, "Got it."

"Being tall and close to the sky, I really envy that." 

Zhou Milin propped her chin, gazing into the distance, her little worries were genuine, "Half the mountain lord senior brother, I’ll tell you a big secret. I actually don’t like patrolling the mountain that much, but every day on the mountain, chewing sunflower seeds with nothing to do, I can’t help. What do you think? So every time I patrol, I run really fast; I’m secretly slacking off."

Liu Sixteen nodded, "I’ll help you keep it a secret."

Zhou Milin moved closer and whispered, "Then I’ll tell you a colossal secret. Back when I traveled the rivers with the good mountain lord in the North Ju Lu Continent..."

The little girl set her green bamboo staff and golden shoulder pole aside, then stood up, saying, "I was standing in a big backpack, whacking Pei Qian’s head with all my might. Chen the good man said one snowflake coin is worth one chestnut, and I didn’t even blink."

Liu Sixteen chuckled knowingly, saying earnestly, "Then you’re truly impressive; being able to hit my junior brother’s chestnut, if that gets out, the reputation of the mute lake great water monster will indeed be as big as the sky."

Originally spirited Zhou Milin’s expression dimmed suddenly, "Those riddles were all taught to me by him. If he doesn’t come home soon, I might forget one or two."

Liu Sixteen suddenly wanted to stretch his legs and take a trip to the barbaric world, to see that junior brother who could make the teacher laugh, and then just say he passed through here from Baoping Continent.

So on the city wall, would his junior brother inquire with his gaze, "You come from your hometown; you should know the affairs of your hometown"?

Liu Sixteen sighed heavily, wishing he had asked the teacher whether it was feasible. 

In an instant, Liu Sixteen vanished from where he stood.

Zhou Milin blinked vigorously. Where had the tall one run off to? She had no harder riddles left.

Liu Sixteen stood on a golden arched bridge, slightly furrowing his brow.

Then he saw a tall woman in white, leaning on her sword, slowly turning to look at him.

She had a pair of the most exquisite golden eyes in the world.

Liu Sixteen remained silent for a moment, puzzled, "Why are you still here?"

The fearless Liu Sixteen did not take a step forward.

The reason was simple: when Liu Sixteen was young, he had dealt with her and suffered greatly. 

He glanced at the long sword in her hand and continued to ask, "Aren’t you without a sword attendant anymore?"

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 834: When the Time Comes, Heaven and Earth Will Move Together

Liu Sixteen didn’t find his time on the mountain particularly boring. In this dilapidated place, where the mountain lord was temporarily absent, it was like a gentleman hiding his talents, waiting for the right moment to act.

If there is a way in the world, it will be seen; if there is no way, it will be hidden. As far as this saying goes, it seemed that in this dilapidated mountain, the way had not yet appeared. When the world was in turmoil, no one wanted to remain here, preferring to descend the mountain instead. However, not everything had been revealed yet, and Liu Sixteen was in no rush. Besides, with his little junior brother's choices and actions, as an older brother, he could not demand much more.

Thus, as an outsider to the dilapidated mountain, Liu Sixteen's impression of it continued to improve.

Yet, Liu Sixteen harbored a great doubt in his heart. The person he had encountered before—was she the sword attendant who had once followed that supreme existence to conquer the realms, now known in later generations as the Spirit of the Immortal Sword? Or was she actually the true master of that sword attendant, having intentionally changed her appearance to deceive future generations? Because in Liu Sixteen’s view, sword attendants, or sword spirits, did not exist, at least not as complete beings.

He had asked her, but unfortunately, she did not provide an answer.

Her gaze remained as indifferent as ever, showing no trace of disdain.

Today, Mi Yu did not accompany Xiao Mi Li on her patrol of the mountain. Instead, he went to the top of the steps and found Liu Sixteen sitting on the ground.

Mi Yu sat beside him and said, “With you here at the peak of the dilapidated mountain, I can relax.”

Mi Yu was planning to take a trip to Old Dragon City with his sword.

He took the sword nurturing gourd “Hao Liang” from his waist and smiled, “I’m not seeking death, but just in case, I’d like to trouble Liu Sixteen to pass it on to my long-life friend. I won’t go to Qi Long Lane and end up with nothing.”

Liu Sixteen shook his head, “I won’t stay too long.”

Suddenly reminded of something, he thought of that existence from the Yang family pharmacy, the proximity of the dilapidated mountain to the Cloud-Piercing Mountain, as well as that woman from the Longquan Sword Sect.

Liu Sixteen changed his mind. “Sword Immortal, be extra cautious. When I head south and reach Old Dragon City, I’ll make sure to support you. Then you can return to the dilapidated mountain.”

Mi Yu felt a bit helpless. Being referred to as "Sword Immortal" by Liu Sixteen felt more like an insult than a compliment.

What troubled Mi Yu more was that he had to remind Liu Sixteen once again, “My surname is Mi.”

Would it be too much to ask to call me Mi Sword Immortal instead? 

Liu Sixteen laughed heartily, “Alright, Mi Sword Immortal.”

Feeling somewhat relieved, Mi Yu gazed into the distance at the scenery beyond the mountain and smiled, “Then I will shamelessly accept your kindness. At the battlefield in Old Dragon City, I will count the days and wait for your arrival.”

Liu Sixteen inexplicably recalled the young man he had seen practicing swordsmanship in his dreams.

The man was increasingly worried. It seemed that everyone around his little junior brother had thick skins. Familiarity among acquaintances was a good thing, but this level of being overly familiar was rather rare, wasn’t it?

According to his teacher, his little junior brother’s character was one of gentleness, propriety, thrift, and humility, never missing a single word. He was the most able to adhere to etiquette; when there were few people, he felt free in the heart, and when there were many, he became even more cautious. He pursued a refined scholarly demeanor, striving to become a great scholar, and displayed the charisma of a hero...

His teacher’s words were always to the point during their four years of studying together and would never exaggerate his disciples. Just like back then, when faced with the tidal wave of praise from the outside world for the three disciples of the Literary Sage, his teacher merely said, “My little Qi’s scholarship is alright, but he is still far from being a true sage. Don’t push him too hard, old folks.”

He would say that Cui Zhan’s calligraphy was acceptable, and his chess skills were mediocre; he never managed to win against the city lord of White Emperor City.

As for the swordsmanship of the senior brother on the left, he learned it late, and the reason he had some skills was merely due to luck. A guy who couldn’t even be considered a sword master wouldn’t have much future, would he?

After the senior brother on the left got into trouble, his teacher had even more to say. “You all have higher status; there’s no need to be angry with a junior. I’ll deal with him when I return. Why glare? He doesn’t understand etiquette at all. Quickly apologize to the seniors, be sincere, and bow your head a little more…”

Mi Yu understood in his heart, but he was also too lazy to mend the fence; it could easily backfire.

The tall and robust Liu Sixteen sitting next to him looked simple and honest, but he definitely could not be regarded as someone without a heart.

Although Mi Yu was a sword cultivator born and raised in the Sword Qi Long Wall, he had seen quite a few gentlemen and sages and thus found it embarrassing to say some of the strange phrases from the Sword Qi Long Wall, such as “From afar, it looks like A Liang; up close, it’s the Hidden Official.”

While it was true that in his hometown, the Hidden Official had never lost a debate, whether inside or outside the summer palace of the Sword Qi Long Wall or in the Upside-Down Mountain at Spring Fan Studio, he could not control what others said behind his back.

Moreover, countless hired hands from those wine shops and gambling dens openly criticized the second manager who was responsible for delivering money, as if they were fiercer than anyone else.

After all, Liu Sixteen was the senior brother of the Hidden Official. Some things were not suitable for Mi Yu, an outsider from the literary faction, to comment on.

If Mi Yu were truly foolish, would he still be the Mi Sword Immortal capable of provoking countless romantic entanglements?

Liu Sixteen said, “You should be able to guess, I come from a demonic lineage.”

Mi Yu nodded, “I’ve seen a lot; it’s not surprising.”

In discussing this matter, Mi Yu seemed quite the sword immortal.

Liu Sixteen fell silent.

On the dilapidated mountain, a small girl in black, bouncing and skipping, first accompanied Sister Nuan Shu to clean up the Ancestor Hall at the Misty Peak and then set off on her own to patrol the mountain. Today she was in a good mood, probably because she had made new friends; she wasn’t running as fast as usual. Right now, she was happily calling out to a little girl sitting in the water. Dressed in a red outfit, she was in a boat but not rowing. It was hard to tell what she was, a little red altar filled with red dumplings. It was all too puzzling...

Liu Sixteen rested his hands on his knees. “Sword Immortal, I won’t see you off. In the future, when we meet again in Old Dragon City, we won’t have need for farewells after drinking.”

Mi Yu smiled bitterly, “My surname is Mi.”

Then he broke into a smile, “Little Nuan Shu and Xiao Mi Li, please take care of them, Liu Sixteen.”

“Rest assured, Sword Immortal, with me around, there’s no need to worry.”

Liu Sixteen’s promise was made with a carefree demeanor.

He then laughed and patted Mi Yu on the shoulder, “You’re a good person!”

Mi Yu no longer cared about being called Sword Immortal without the character for Mi, realizing it was futile to fuss over it.

The Sword Immortal in the green robe rose gracefully, clasped his fists with Liu Sixteen, and then flew away on his sword, instantly vanishing into the southern horizon. He was worried that Xiao Mi Li might see him and be sad; knowing too soon would only lead to sadness. So Mi Yu deliberately restrained his aura and the spectacle of sword flight, letting the light of the sword vanish in a flash.

Yet Mi Yu did not yet know how Liu Sixteen’s “a good person” would be evaluated.

Earlier, Liu Sixteen had spoken with Liu Xianyang about his friend Bai Ye.

That “friend Bai Ye, skilled in swordsmanship”...

Liu Sixteen continued to bide his time, waiting for the heavens to open up again.

Mountain Lord Wei Ba had a strong sense of justice. As the older brother of the mountain lord, Liu Sixteen was bound to help his little junior brother exchange some favors.

Otherwise, he wouldn’t be able to face his teacher again.

Liu Sixteen suddenly laughed, “Little junior brother, you’re truly hiding your talents too much. Have you already been looked down upon by many people?”

The few night banquets at Cloud-Piercing Mountain, the steward of the dilapidated mountain, Zhu Lian, and the Chen Ling who came from Yujiang had all made appearances. As for Pei Qian, Chen Nuan Shu, and Zhou Mi Li, when they went to Cloud-Piercing Mountain, they stayed far away, merely there for the excitement. At the night banquets crowded with immortal masters, city gods, and mountain deities, the three little girls did not attract much attention.

In the realm of Beiyue, the impression of the dilapidated mountain, which had opened its doors after Longquan Sword Sect, was still quite deep, aside from the fact that the young mountain lord hailed from the shabby Li Zhu Cave Heaven, it was more so due to the admiration from the Northern Mountain Lord Wei Ba. This made it quite enviable. Beyond that, the relationship between the dilapidated mountain and Longquan Sword Sect was well-known, as they had rented three mountain peaks. This was an acknowledged fact. The key was the rumor that the young mountain lord, who had risen from the bottom of society, had a close affinity with the only daughter of the Saint, Ruan Xiu. This matter circulated with some credibility, and since neither the Saint Ruan Qiong nor the daughter Ruan Xiu had ever seriously denied it, it became quite intriguing.

With the backing of Ruan Qiong and the protection of Wei Ba, the young man with the surname Chen from the dilapidated mountain, who had always remained hidden, was able to soar to great heights, rapidly rising to become a notable immortal sect within the old territory of Dali.

Possessing half of the Niujiao Mountain ferry and occupying all the ruins left behind by the Bagua Pavilion, he had even appointed the Golden Core female immortal Liu Chongrun to personally manage the ferry “Fan Mo.”

It’s just a pity that this dilapidated mountain was a mere facade, lacking any capable cultivator to represent it.

It was said that the young man named Chen Ping An was still just a pure martial artist, not even someone who practiced cultivation.

The territory was not small, but there were too few people. As the largest landlord in the territory of Li Zhu Cave Heaven back in the day, there never was a unique figure who could stabilize the situation.

For the past twenty-plus years, they had been hiding under the shade of Cloud-Piercing Mountain and Longquan Sword Sect, like an old lute half concealed.

Being looked down upon by outsiders seemed to be a matter of course.

Liu Sixteen chuckled as a small girl in black quickly ran up the steps to the mountain peak, stopping to pretend to be out of breath.

Liu Sixteen was tall enough to lightly pat Xiao Mi Li’s back while sitting.

Zhou Mi Li sat beside him and asked, “Want some sunflower seeds?”

Liu Sixteen shook his head.

Zhou Mi Li sighed, “Then I won’t eat them either.” 

After sitting with the tall figure for a long while, Zhou Mi Li said she was going to see a friend and excused herself, running off.

She took out three small bags of sunflower seeds and gently called out, “Lord Wei, Lord Wei!”

Wei Ba appeared near the mountain god temple, received the three bags of seeds, and smiled, “Are you heading to Huanghu Mountain or Huimeng Mountain?”

Zhou Mi Li felt a bit guilty today, holding her green bamboo staff and golden small shoulder pole together, extending a palm as she said, “Lord Wei, I know you’re busy with important matters. Today is the last time, I promise!”

Wei Ba put the seeds into his sleeve and smiled, “For now, there’s no need for that. If something really happens, calling won’t be of much use. So whether there’s something or not, shouting at the dilapidated mountain is all the same.”

Zhou Mi Li shook her head, “I said this is the last time I’m troubling you, Lord Wei. It must count. Today I’m going to Huanghu Mountain to visit Sister Hongxia.”

Wei Ba could only nod and “sent” the little girl toward Huanghu Mountain.

That great python, known as the Lady in Yellow, whose real name was Fo Song, preferred to call herself “Hongxia” only in front of Zhou Mi Li.

Zhou Mi Li set down her shoulder pole and bamboo staff, needing to take a few deep breaths as before to muster the courage to lean over the water. The little girl dipped her head into the water, eyes wide open.

After a long while, she still couldn’t see Sister Hongxia.

In a light yellow dress, Sister Hongxia was actually smiling and standing on the shore, crouching down beside Zhou Mi Li, gently patting her head.

Poor little Mi Li was so startled that she dove into the water, flailing her hands randomly, instantly disappearing dozens of feet underwater.

Sister Hongxia felt a bit guilty for a moment.

After a while, when she surfaced, her eyes were watery from crying because her belongings were left on the shore. But soon the little girl grinned and burst into laughter.

She was here, grinning widely, completely unconcerned.

Zhou Mi Li bounced out of the water, splashing as she walked, crouched down, and seriously comforted her, “Don’t be scared, don’t be scared, I was just teasing you.”

Sister Hongxia thought for a moment but still didn’t ask Zhou Mi Li about the faint, terrifying aura from the dilapidated mountain.

Involving the Dao, such matters were of utmost importance, and she shouldn’t pull the little girl into it.

So Sister Hongxia simply smiled and said, “Which martial arts story do you want to tell me today?”

Zhou Mi Li chuckled, “With a shout, the mountains and waters turn green. I don’t know, have you heard it?”

Sister Hongxia laughed, “I’ve heard of it.”

Zhou Mi Li froze for a moment, realizing she hadn’t opened the door to good fortune today.

Sister Hongxia suddenly felt a great fear. This was the first time the culprit who made her not dare to think about the journey of the rivers and lakes had come to Huanghu Mountain.

Longquan Sword Sect, the woman Ruan Xiu.

This was someone who seemed to have “ascended” to the heavenly realm of Baopingzhou and had personally killed an ancient deity.

Fortunately, there was still a clueless Zhou Mi Li who saw the very lovable Sister Xiu and waved vigorously, “Sister Xiu, want some sunflower seeds!”

Ruan Xiu smiled and slowly walked to Xiao Mi Li’s side, bending down to rub the little girl’s head, taking a big handful of seeds from her.

Ruan Xiu shot a sidelong glance at the trembling Sister Hongxia and asked in mind voice: “You’re just going to remain a part of the dilapidated mountain, living off others? Aren’t you planning to leave the lake and go explore the rivers? Do you plan on waiting for me to die first?”

Sister Hongxia turned pale.

How could she dare to have such thoughts?

It would be a great injustice to her.

Ruan Xiu said, “After I leave, you should go explore the rivers immediately.”

Sister Hongxia’s teeth chattered, and she could only nod gently.

In fact, she wasn’t even sure if she genuinely nodded.

Zhou Mi Li blinked and looked at Sister Xiu munching on sunflower seeds, then looked back at Sister Hongxia, softly asking, “Sister Xiu, why does Sister Hongxia seem a bit afraid of you?”

Ruan Xiu laughed, “She’s timid. Even more so than Mi Li.”

Zhou Mi Li wanted to laugh, but since Sister Xiu was talking about Sister Hongxia, she couldn’t laugh and didn’t forget to wave her hand in front of Sister Hongxia, signaling that nothing was wrong.

Ruan Xiu said, “Shall we go play at Divine Show Mountain?”

Zhou Mi Li hesitated, “I just got here, and I haven’t chatted with Sister Hongxia much yet.”

Ruan Xiu said, “Then you talk first; I’ll sit nearby.”

In the end, the little girl in black sat in the middle.

Sister Hongxia wouldn’t dare sit beside Ruan Xiu.

After hearing a story about a mute lake, Ruan Xiu opened her handkerchief, took a piece of pastry, and handed it to Xiao Mi Li.

Zhou Mi Li immediately understood, shook her head, and began to eat the pastry.

Then she would tell a story about the good mountain lord!

There were plenty of stories; she had a huge basket full.

Like the last time she talked about how Chen Haoren encountered a mountain spirit and failed to compose poetry, resulting in them being driven out of the cave, Sister Xiu would be very happy, as it was the first time Zhou Mi Li had seen her smile like that.

At that time, Sister Xiu went from beautiful to breathtaking.

---

Yang’s Pharmacy. Liu Sixteen was invited to help guard the formation.

Old Yang had also called for Ruan Xiu.

Liu Sixteen was genuinely feeling a bit helpless.

It was one thing not to run into them before, but now facing them, it was indeed strange.

Not to mention the addition of that “Li Liu,” with whom they had a significant past but ended up on opposing paths due to the Dao.

What’s going on in this place where his little junior brother has grown up?

Old Yang tucked his old smoking pipe into his waistband and suddenly looked at Ruan Xiu, taking off the pipe and saying, “Here, help me pass this to him.”

Ruan Xiu nodded and took the old smoking pipe that Old Yang tossed over.

Liu Sixteen’s eyes lit up, a smile appearing on his face.

In the past, among their literary lineage, Liu Sixteen’s three senior brothers were all exceptional individuals, yet each had guarded their integrity as if it were precious. Many women admired them, both on the mountain and below. While it might not be said that there were as many as there are fish crossing the river, there were certainly quite a few.

It was just that the eldest brother, Cui Zhan, was ambitious and focused, and although he would never deliberately alienate or reject women, he would only treat them with courtesy at most.

The other senior brother thought women were annoying and would often wonder why they liked him. “You all like Cui Zhan or Qi Jingchun, go after them instead.”

Little Qi was simply clueless.

After Liu Sixteen and Ruan Xiu, Mountain Lord Wei Ba was also called over. This Northern Mountain landlord had a serious expression.

Wei Ba stood beside Liu Sixteen, who had cast an illusion, and previously, he had occasionally inquired. Wei Ba had publicly claimed that he was just an old friend from Cloud-Piercing Mountain.

As for whether anyone believed it, Wei Ba didn’t care.

After all, he wasn’t saying to outsiders that he wouldn’t hold any more night banquets.

Wei Ba asked, “Is there a need for the younger generation to move the mountains and rivers?”

Old Yang shook his head, “I know a thing or two about divine powers.”

Wei Ba was speechless.

Liu Sixteen smiled. This old man, who had never been one to joke around, was getting better at chatting.

The world had not been idle for ten thousand years.

In an instant, the entire Northern Mountain realm appeared shrouded in white mist in the eyes of cultivators. As for ordinary folks, they remained oblivious.

Today was a momentous day, unprecedented in ten thousand years.

Because this old Yang, who had been guarding the human realm for ten thousand years, was about to reopen the Ascension Platform for the ancient Qing Tong Heavenly Lord in the human realm.

Still, it was unclear how Old Yang would operate his divine powers. The celestial beings who quietly rushed to various places in Longzhou instantly felt as if they were standing on a high platform.

It was too bizarre, to the point that many Nascent Soul and Golden Core cultivators exchanged glances, but soon stabilized their minds and steadied their Dao hearts.

On the high platform, there were old men dwelling in the mountains and exceptional young people from the mountains.

This large group of Golden Core and Nascent Soul immortals from Baopingzhou, who had previously received a secret order from the Dali Criminal Department, contained shocking content. The last line of the secret letter was extremely stern, forbidding them from leaking a word and only allowing them to secretly head to Longzhou in Dali.

The Taoist priests from the Divine Revelation Sect, the martial cultivators from Zhenwu Mountain and the Wind and Snow Temple, Jiang Yun from the Jiang family, the two old sword cultivators from Zhengyang Mountain, and the head of the Xu family from Qingfeng City...

The eldest disciple of Longquan Sword Sect, Dong Gu, and Xie Ling. The Golden Core swordsman Cui Wei from the dilapidated mountain, the Golden Core cultivator Cai Jin Jian from Yunxia Mountain...

There was even a sword cultivator from Fenglei Garden, Liu Baqiao, returning to Longzhou.

The master of the garden, Huang He, even after receiving the order from Dali, directly gave up this opportunity for a great Dao fortune, only allowing Liu Baqiao to set off, saying to his disciple, “In my life, I only practice the sword alone, without accepting the favors of anyone other than my master.”

Liu Baqiao advised him a few times, but Huang He finally said to him, “You’re not as talented as I am. For the next hundreds of years, I want to focus on sword cultivation, and if you, the new garden master, fall short in realm, you’ll embarrass my master and Fenglei Garden. You don’t have the right to bargain with me, so hurry up and get to Longzhou in Dali.”

Earlier, the direct disciple of the Zhengyang Mountain ancestor, Yuan Bai, had asked the garden master of Fenglei Garden, Huang He, for a duel. Yuan Bai summoned his life sword jade stone, turning it into ashes.

As a result, even though Huang He did not fall in rank to the Golden Core, it was undeniable that his Dao was damaged. Even so, as long as he arrived in Longzhou, he had a chance to recover his Nascent Soul’s fullness. Given Huang He’s natural talent, perhaps he could even step into the upper five realms.

But Huang He still refused to come here.

The lower sect of the Yuanguang Sect, the true realm sect, had just broken through the bottleneck of the Dragon Gate realm, including the sword cultivator Sui You, totaling three people.

In a chaotic world, there will be countless heroes and tyrants rising to the occasion, each displaying their talents.

In the backyard of the pharmacy, Liu Sixteen said, “I’ll just go to the heavenly realm first, to avoid getting flustered and not receiving guests properly. Welcoming guests at the door is more sincere.”

Ruan Xiu had just finished her pastry, clapped her hands, and said, “Likewise.”

Old Yang nodded.

---

The National Master of Dali, the Confucian scholar Cui Zhan, supported the White Jade Capital, with the body of a celestial being seated in heaven.

Cui Zhan lightly uttered a word.

“Sever.”

In an instant, the sword light reached every corner within Cui Zhan’s sight.

He severed the head of a great demon in the realm of the celestial.

In the realm of the Five Mountains, all the borders of rivers and mountains, all the counties, towns, and cities far from the battlefield of Dali, had numerous incense burners set up to worship the Five Mountains, led by local civil and military officials along with the common people, who would offer incense day and night. The local city gods and auxiliary officials, along with the spirits of heroes from civil and military backgrounds, and the deities of mountains and rivers, were responsible for examining and weighing the essence of the incense, reporting it to the Ministry of Rites and compiling it.

At this moment, countless poems and songs arose from Baopingzhou, called Five Mountain Poems, with a hundred selected and compiled into a book, distributed to various academies and village schools across the continent, allowing children everywhere to sing them in the streets.

With the Five Mountain Lords, the essence of incense continuously flowed into the Great Mountain, half of which was intercepted to maintain the towering golden body of the divine form, while the remaining two-fifths were given to the Mountain of the Crown Prince, and the remaining three-fifths were distributed to many mountain and river shrines within the borders, providing sustenance to the fortune of various vassal states, boosting the national fortune, extending the nation's longevity, and ultimately enhancing the national power, which in turn fed back into the Dali Dynasty and the greater fortunes of the continent.

The Tongye Continent was where the emperor fled, and the immortals escaped.

But in Baopingzhou, even the children in the streets and rural areas could contribute silently to the stability of the continent’s fortunes through their innocent singing.

Dali had changed its laws, allowing each vassal state to select two or four spirits, to post “family” door gods on their doors, reconstructing the golden bodies to protect their regions, preventing the sporadic invasions from the demonic tribes, and working together with local immortal cultivators and the national clan offerings to jointly layout defenses against the disturbances of the demonic tribes.

At a mountain peak, far from Cui Zhan's divine form in the middle of Baopingzhou, a dozen people looked down at the rivers and mountains.

Leading them was Mr. Fan, the founder of the merchant family, guiding a group of ancestral masters of merchants who had come to Baopingzhou.

Despite not being too young in appearance, after Cui Zhan drew his sword, the merchant ancestor withdrew his gaze and sighed, “Distant waters seek distant mountains. Old friends leave behind stories.”

After reflecting on the world for a moment, this “Mr. Fan” turned to the point, smiling, “Everyone says water follows the mountains, and the flow of rivers in the world is unpredictable, while only mountains remain still. Is it really just the water that moves and not the mountains?”

An old man who had accompanied him for many years laughed, “Lack of money, right?”

This person was the one who had once beset A Liang and managed to escape, cheerfully giving himself the nickname “Half Peak.”

This group of merchants, who were rich enough to rival nations, burst into hearty laughter upon hearing this.

Indeed, they didn’t lack anything but money.

The merchants had already spent a substantial sum to relocate inland mountains to the coast, creating strongholds, or moving some coastal mountains that posed an inconvenience to the Dali cavalry inland, forming what appeared to be “naturally formed yet actually artificially created” formidable battle lines!

Next, they would have to spend even more! Money from the immortals, money from the Grain Rain! 

Snowflake money, Lesser Heat money? There certainly wasn’t a single one; too shabby!

In summary, the merchants needed to ensure that the vassal troops of Baopingzhou, lacking cavalry, could hold the strongholds.

Moreover, they needed to clear out space for Dali’s unstoppable iron cavalry to gallop freely across the vast plains.

Mr. Fan smiled and said, “Everyone, hurry up and scatter money across the continent.”

One by one, they obediently followed the ancestor’s order, disappearing into the world like the wind.

On the battlefield of Old Dragon City, several divine beings had descended, unstoppable.

Ma Kuxuan had merely returned to Zhenwu Mountain, one of the ancestral homes of the martial family in Baopingzhou. Shortly after returning to Old Dragon City, he encountered celestial beings descending from the heavens, visiting Baopingzhou.

As one of the ten young candidates of the world, Ma Kuxuan, he was also commanding a dozen ancient divine beings to reciprocate, attacking the heavens.

Moreover, there was the Southern Mountain Lord, the only female mountain lord, Fan Junmao, whose golden body was over a thousand feet tall. She held a portion of the ancient moon “Truth” as a bow, a gift from the Lady Gui, using the essence of the sun and moon as arrows and bowstring.

When an arrow was shot, whether it was aimed at the heavens to slay ancient gods or to strike great demons at sea, it carried earth-shattering might.

On the Dragon-Ascending Platform near Old Dragon City, there was a young girl, Zhi Gui, whose golden eyes were fixed on a great demon far out at sea.

The demon was also staring back at Zhi Gui.

Zhi Gui grinned and slowly raised a hand, making a gesture of breaking the neck toward that scarlet concubine.

---

At Shujian Lake.

A refined old man in a tall crown and flowing robe stood at the water’s edge on an island.

The patriarch of the True Realm Sect, Wei Ying, felt something stir within him but refrained from using his powers to peer into the distance.

Hundreds of strange spirits, without exception, were all grievances of those who had died violently, still retaining a hint of true spirit even after a hundred or a thousand years. They surged out of the lake and returned to the human realm.

In their lifetimes, they were all individuals who had died tragically in this lawless land of Shujian Lake, their souls lingering due to various injustices. Some were innocent, some deserved their fates, and some had died unfairly even though their crimes did not merit death, and now they gathered around the old man, watching the bustling world of Shujian Lake, year after year, as life and death remained uncertain, the strong violently killing the weak, and the weak not knowing what they had done wrong, simply feeling that their cultivation was too low, and nothing more.

Ultimately, all these spirits shared a common confusion: which was the mortal realm, and which was the realm of the dead?

Finally, a weary young man from another land arrived here, answering the question lingering in the hearts of countless restless spirits.

Gu Can’s killing was wrong, and not killing Gu Can was also wrong. This custom of Shujian Lake, which would still be wrong a thousand or ten thousand years later, was indeed incorrect. Some wrongdoings and the discomfort in one’s heart must cause one to suffer for a lifetime.

Because in this world, wrong is wrong. If there is a wrong, one must correct it. This has always been the case, right? Should we let generations of future people continue to question this? Surely not, that wouldn’t do.

Those wronged spirits, who had also offered their answers, bid farewell to the young man one by one.

They, along with that young man, provided Shujian Lake with an answer, a response that would still be filled with sorrow and regret.

“Skinny as a bamboo pole, how will you ever find a wife in the future? Once you leave this ghostly place, remember to eat plenty of fish and meat! I’m not bragging; my cooking is excellent. I’m known for my messy stew that can make the Buddha jump the wall; too bad you don’t have that luck.”

“Chen Ping An, take it easy; let’s not reunite too early. Also, you, this useless accountant, remember to slap Gu Can a few times to vent your frustration. You’ve gotten yourself into trouble with this Gu Can, you’ve really hit rock bottom. In the future, mind your own business; it’s not worth it.”

“Mr. Chen, I still feel the world isn’t too beautiful, but… it seems there’s still a bit of hope. I’ll take my leave now, and do take care, Mr. Chen.”

The young man, who had only just started to leave his youth behind, smiled and waved goodbye to them, hoarsely uttering a few words of well-wishing. When he could not speak, he would lightly knock his chest with a fist or clasp his hands in farewell.

After those spirits vanished, the young man fell into deeper silence.

The old man was not only acknowledging the young man’s troubles and efforts to make amends but also felt gratified that the parting was filled with regret yet not completely hopeless.

The old man collected his thoughts, smiling, “Since you can still hold onto a spark of spirit, it means you’re not completely numb. That’s why you’re being held here and unable to be released. This time, your souls will dissipate completely, and I’ll accumulate some merit for you. For every wrong, a right will counterbalance it, and as for your fortune, accumulate it.”

With the old man’s words, those spirits felt a sense of great relief, as if they had received a pardon, transforming into golden-bodied water deities.

Before this, Dali had already laid down a land route for these spirits, allowing them to travel like the righteous deities of the lake, heading towards the center of Baopingzhou.

The old man smiled again, “All the spirits of mountains and rivers in the world are my friends, aren’t they?”

The old man asked himself and answered, “If not, then so be it!”

Countless mountain spirits suddenly condensed their forms across the mountains and peaks of the continent.

The old man lifted one hand, “Heaven is showing signs.”

From all corners of the continent, there were a total of twenty-four peaks, where a young man in white had buried twenty-four bamboo slips in advance.

The spirit army surged forth, like an unprecedented ghost army crossing the borders, riding the winds toward those twenty-four peaks.

The old man finally approached the ferry at Qingxia Island, looking down.

After that young man had fallen into a deep sleep, Ruan Xiu and Zhong Kui had come to visit him, who was snoring thunderously on the ground. 

In fact, it was not just the two of them.

The old man chuckled, what a world full of wonders.

When he looked up again, he saw that Baopingzhou had no grand formations of the Three Altars and Four Symbols, but it did have this even more magnificent and more aligned with the Dao’s grand formation of the Twenty-Four Heavenly Seasons.

The great formation followed the cycles of the heavens and protected the entire continent without any gaps.

A middle-aged monk, wandering with a begging bowl, had traveled around this continent year after year.

He began to chant. 

Wherever he had stepped in the past, in the cities, between the mountains and rivers, in bustling places and secluded spots, the lotus flowers began to bloom.

In the end, across the continent, Baopingzhou resembled a beautiful flower vase on some table, with a large golden lotus blooming within.

Twelve massive sword boats hovered at the forefront of the battlefield, suspended behind Old Dragon City.

Countless martial forces used secret methods to beat drums, amplifying the momentum, adding a mysterious celestial time to the flying swords.

On the flying swords, there were already talismanic cultivators pouring their hearts and souls into inscribing intricate cloud patterns onto every single sword, sparing no expense in both immortal money and spiritual essence.

In an instant, the flying swords clustered together densely like a torrential rain, directed toward the demonic army attacking the city at sea.

The smallest region of the vast territory, Baopingzhou, was the only one that not only maintained a solid defense but also had the strength to engage in grand offensives against the barbaric world.

Prince Song Jixin did not station at the grand Dali capital of Baopingzhou, nor did he move his residence to the comparatively stable Southern Mountain. He remained in Old Dragon City, acting as one of the pillars of the southern battlefield alongside the two highest-ranking military officials of Dali, Inspector Cao Ping and General Su Gaoshan. However, the two generals were not inside the city but rather on the land outside Old Dragon City, waiting in full battle formation.

And the once noble son of the Dali family, Song Mu, who was no longer the pampered young man from Mud Bottle Lane, was now clenching his fists, his eyes red. The war had continued for a year, and the prince showed no signs of retreating, having heard that the barbaric world had once challenged the Sword Qi Long Wall with tens of thousands of sword cultivators.

Standing at the top of the prince’s estate, Song Jixin pressed his hands against the railing, the veins on his hands bulging, and laughed angrily, “Come! Let’s fight another round with the Dali!”

A gentleman from the Guankong Academy arrived in Old Dragon City and, before departing, exchanged bows with the headmaster of the academy, preparing to head to the front lines.

The gentleman held a jade porcelain bottle, crystal clear, seemingly filled with thunder and lightning, resembling a small thunder pool.

In fact, the thunder within the bottle was a manifestation of his scholarly Dao’s subtle essence.

After saying farewell to the headmaster, he shared a light-hearted remark with a younger disciple from the same hometown.

“Next year when the flowers bloom in our hometown, be sure to take a few more glances for me.”

A scholar from the academy, with whom he had previously had disputes and even fierce arguments, happened to be traveling to the battlefield with him.

It turned out that the disputes over knowledge among scholars were truly just the disputes of gentlemen.

Gentlemen and sages, the two exchanged smiles, sharing an unspoken understanding.

The chief offering of the Fu family in Old Dragon City, an old swordsman who had practiced for many years near the Dragon Ascending Platform, walked alongside a woodsman from the Sun family, both taking leave from their respective lords to rush to the most perilous areas of the battlefield.

As the two rode the wind, the woodsman, who had once read the sacred texts but had never become a disciple of the academy, remarked with a hint of a smile, “The green mud is winding, twisting and turning a hundred steps, it doesn’t matter if my heart is full of mud and mire; that isn’t a reason for you beasts to barge in.”

The old swordsman laughed, “You’re too pretentious, I can’t say it, so I’ll just follow your words. Let’s say it’s a dying wish: to cross this road, to enter the family gates, I must die first.”

An old cultivator who had safely left Tongye Continent, an old Nascent Soul who had once struck a big deal with the young man from another land and Jiang Shangzhen, gathered all the cultivators of his sect.

The old man’s sect was located in the northern part of Tongye Continent, known as the Qinghu Palace of Tianque Peak, and the old man himself was the master alchemist, Lu Yong.

Before the barbaric world’s demons had even landed, the well-informed and self-preserving Master Lu had already led his disciples onto the immortal ferry, escaping to Baopingzhou ahead of time. If they had waited another ten days, they would have faced a closed door.

However, like all the other clever people, even after entering the territory of Old Dragon City, they hadn’t been able to secure refuge in the city, so they had to gather with other foreign cultivators, as if they were prisoners.

But they had saved their lives, although life was still not easy.

The military cultivators of the Dali Dynasty never spoke a word to them; they either killed those who didn’t follow the rules or coldly watched these Tongye Continent refugees from a distance.

The different military cultivators shared the same gaze.

No sympathy, only the innate coldness brought by the battlefield, and the ridicule of looking at something that wasn’t exactly human.

However, in the high buildings of the “cage,” there was leisure to observe the battlefield without obstruction, which was not hindered by Dali.

After the old man witnessed the daily brutal battles outside Old Dragon City, he gradually spoke less. Until today, Lu Yong suddenly became furious, his beard standing on end, “How dare you uproot my family’s thousand-year-old tree?!”

Finally, the old Nascent Soul smiled sadly, leaving his disciples with the words to live well in this foreign land. After all, they had just barely made it here; they shouldn’t die easily, no matter how embarrassing it was. They should focus on their cultivation and refine better pills.

In the end, the old cultivator looked at the youngest children among them, his expression becoming relaxed.

With my death, there would be fewer of you Tongye Continent cultivators living as stray dogs.

As for the younger generations to stand firm on Baopingzhou, it would be much easier.

A monk from a great temple arrived at the battlefield of Old Dragon City, sweeping his staff in the air, creating ripples.

The monk finally sat in mid-air, hands clasped together.

Bodhisattva hooks and locks, all bones resonating together.

His body was like a spiritual tower, glowing like fire.

An unknown Taoist master stepped onto a treasure boat, leisurely arriving as if he were on a scenic tour.

The old man unleashed a method of summoning soldiers like beans, scattering talismans like the common folk scattering paper money.

Hundreds of puppet figures, each standing several feet tall, appeared in the cloud seas.

In the vast expanse of land between Old Dragon City and Southern Mountain, the earth was remarkably flat.

Two regiments of Dali cavalry were stationed here, lined up like a tide, motionless.

They awaited the enemy.

An unarmored general, patrolling the front lines on horseback, held a sword and spear out of habit.

This high-ranking Dali inspector suddenly stopped his horse, facing south alone.

I, the Dali cavalry, shall charge from north to south, piercing through the continent!

The skill of killing, how could it be unknown? Not to mention the continent, the entire world was well aware!

Now, where the hooves stood, they would kill countless demons!

General Su Gaoshan raised his iron spear and pointed south, “Dare to come here? Grind them all to dust!”

---

The Emperor of Dali, Song He, remained in the northern capital.

After the court session, he allowed the officials in dragon robes to retreat for the time being and walked alone along the base of a tall red wall.

At the suggestion of the National Master, he had issued identical edicts to the vassal lords of the continent.

If Dali lost this grand battle, the continent would be annihilated, and everyone would have no country or home to speak of.

But if Dali won this battle, the three vassal states with the highest death toll could recover their nations, breaking free from the Dali Song family’s territory. Even if only one person remained, the Dali dynasty would actively assist in their recovery, and within a hundred years, they would surely become one of the strong nations of Baoping.

The Emperor of Dali personally swore an oath with the Five Mountains. Should he breach this covenant, both humans and gods would be enraged, and the Song family’s dynasty would be severed.

Before the edict was issued, there had been a question and answer session between monarch and subject, teacher and student.

Cui Zhan asked Song He.

The National Master questioned the Emperor.

The teacher asked the student.

“Your Majesty, if it comes to this, Dali may not even be able to maintain its position among the top ten dynasties in the future.”

“But if it comes to this, you, Song He, as a descendant of the Dali Song family, will undoubtedly become a renowned sage for millennia.”

“How to choose is up to you, Song He.”

Song He smiled and said, “The National Master underestimates the ambitions of this student. In the vast world of righteousness, how many emperors among the top ten dynasties could be worthy of being remembered for millennia in history?”

“Song He, you want your descendants to stand before their ancestors’ portraits and linger the longest beneath mine!”

The embroidered tiger nodded after hearing the answer.

Song He had a question he couldn’t help but ask, “What if I don’t agree, and I don’t let the National Master fulfill his wish?”

Cui Zhan laughed at the time, “Your Majesty, you know the answer well.”

The Emperor of Dali laughed heartily, “What an embroidered tiger.”

Finally, the Emperor glanced at the National Master, who had overstepped far too much.

Cui Zhan nodded.

The Emperor’s face bore a look of sorrow, and with the embroidered tiger by his side, it inevitably gave the feeling of being restrained.

But if Dali truly lost this calculating embroidered tiger, how could Song He not feel a bit anxious?

Cui Zhan slowly said, “I, along with Qi Jingchun, have left so many seeds of knowledge that are different from others for your Dali Dynasty. Even if Dali loses half its territory in the future, there will still be great opportunities for a resurgence. It’s just a pity that you may not witness it in your lifetime. In this matter, your fate is similar to that of the previous emperor. It is indeed a significant regret. Hence, having me as your National Master is a blessing for Dali, but it may not be a blessing for you two emperors.”

“A minor misfortune, but Dali and Song He have both been fortunate, having this opportunity and undertaking under the guidance of the National Master.”

The Emperor bowed respectfully to the old man, softly saying, “In that case, this student bids farewell to the National Master.”

At this moment, Song He let out a heavy breath, slammed his hand against the wall, and then firmly pressed against it, speaking in a deep voice, “Let’s hold up the sky together!”

A courtier in a dragon robe suddenly stepped forward, then quietly halted, whispering, “Your Majesty, someone’s coming from the north.”

Song He’s spirits lifted, and he quickly walked to the space between the two walls, looking up. Although he knew he wouldn’t see them, those people wouldn’t arrive so soon above Dali’s capital, but he couldn’t help but take a glance.

Now, the eastern Baopingzhou and northern Juluozhou were forming a continent under that grand plan!

The Fire Dragon True Man, along with Li Liu and the corpulent woman from Lushui Pit who had ascended, were still responsible for guarding this sea route.

One on the left, one on the right, safeguarding the “bridge” connecting the two continents.

A large group of sword cultivators from the northern Juluozhou were flying south toward Baopingzhou along that route.

The first sword immortal of the north, Bai Chang, the master of the Taihui Sword Sect, Huang Tong, and Li Cai from Floating Lake...

Besides the sword cultivators, there were also two high disciples of the Fire Dragon True Man, Yuan Lingdian from the Zhixuan lineage, and also from the Baiyun lineage.

A group of Daoist masters from the Da Yuan Dynasty’s Chongxuan Office, the master of the Pima Sect, Zhu Quan, as well as the bone sword cultivator, the female spirit Pu Rang from the Bone Swamp.

Jinguan City’s Gao Cheng had previously opened the restrictions of the world, allowing Pu Rang to summon her sword.

Now, Gao Cheng had already left Bone Swamp, and the Pima Sect cultivators had nothing to do, while Pu Rang, who had died in that ancient battlefield, chose to go to another battlefield, as if silently bidding farewell to that man who she could never be with. Since she had no hope of becoming a celestial couple with him, why should she burden him from becoming a human Buddha? 

Liking someone should not be like this.

As they traveled southward, whether they were sword cultivators or not, everyone lacked the spirit of heroism or the exuberance of youth.

Their hearts were calm.

It was just like doing something completely natural.

We, the sword cultivators from northern Juluozhou, quietly closed our doors. Regardless of how we fought and schemed against one another, using flying swords, cultivators, and martial artists, we often turned against our own kind.

But with the tide rising, any cultivator could be absent, but we could not afford to lose any from northern Juluozhou!

Those going south were even more heroic.

---

Liu Sixteen had just shared a drink with Mi Yu at the Dusty Pharmacy, but Mi Yu, who was supposed to go north, said he would return to the dilapidated mountain a little later.

So Liu Sixteen drank another pot of wine with this Sword Immortal.

That day, Lady Gui, the patron of the Fan family, suddenly arrived at the Dusty Pharmacy.

Liu Sixteen said, “I’m rather surprised you would do this.”

Both Liu Sixteen and the most authentic “Moon Palace Seed” Lady Gui could be considered remnants of ancient times. 

In later generations, people loved to talk about bizarre tales of immortals, saying there were ancient beings over the vast seas, who with just a finger could fill ten rooms.

In truth, for the two of them, it wasn’t anything extraordinary.

They, or rather “they,” had once looked down from the heavens at the earth, witnessing the rise of the human race, observing their ascent to the mountains, and finally their ascent to the heavens.

In the center of Baopingzhou. 

A great river, calm and quiet under the night sky. 

A small boat, with a child struggling to pole it.

But there was a lazy young man in white, lying at the bow of the boat, his white sleeves trailing in the water. 

The moonlight reflected off the water, making the white sleeves look even whiter. 

The young man closed his eyes and loudly sang, “Spring waters carry boats, boats carry people, the boat moves with the spring waters in the sky.”

Suddenly, the young man sat up, complaining bitterly, “Heaven doesn’t cherish the suffering of this singer.”

Cui Dongshan used his fingers to rub the corners of his eyes, trying to feign tears of sorrow.

But before he could squeeze out a tear, he saw two figures coming towards him; one from the Bone Swamp of northern Juluozhou and the other from even farther away.

At Jinguan City, Gao Cheng had once opened the barriers of heaven and earth, allowing Pu Rang to summon her sword.

Now that Gao Cheng had already left the Bone Swamp, the Pima Sect cultivators had nothing to do, while the spirit Pu Rang, who had died in that ancient battlefield, chose to go to another battlefield, silently bidding farewell to that man she could never be with. 

As they traveled southward, whether they were sword cultivators or not, everyone lacked the spirit of heroism or the exuberance of youth.

Their hearts were calm.

---

In the bustling and lively Qingfeng City, as the dusk fell, a shop was closing.

A man sat in the backyard of his shop on a rattan chair, holding a charcoal basket, quietly enjoying the snow.

He wore a long blue robe, cloth shoes, and white socks, looking somewhat shabby yet clean.

He resembled a fallen son of a once-prosperous family in a market.

And the ruler of the fox country was actually serving him wine like a maid.

Lord Xu, the city lord of Qingfeng, had recently left the city, so as the last remaining Nascent Soul in the city, she was free to act.

She remembered many years ago during a journey through the world, it was an autumn day when Zhu Lian covered his face and went to meet a so-called martial arts master, a legendary figure.

The young Zhu Lian, while wandering the rivers and lakes, passed through a small village where there was a large persimmon tree towering over many rooftops. At the highest point of the tree, many ripe persimmons hung unpicked, falling and colliding with the cooking smoke. 

Some daring children climbed onto the rooftops to poke the persimmons down, hoping for a meal and a scolding, which was worth it.

Young Zhu Lian hailed from a family of great renown, a lineage of scholars.

He waited for a bowl of warm wine for winter, his thoughts drifting far away, recalling memories tied to wine.

That journey had been Zhu Lian’s first real venture into the rivers and lakes. Although he had made some progress in martial arts, he still felt uncertain about his own skills. In his family and even in the capital, where everyone regarded him as a transcendent being, he had never had the opportunity to strike out.

Moreover, Zhu Lian had never seen martial arts as a proper career, casually taking a few precious martial arts manuals from his home just for fun.

So that journey was actually the first time Zhu Lian earnestly appreciated the landscapes of the world.

Then at a village tavern selling loose wine, a man, dressed in a wrinkled thick cotton coat, wearing cotton shoes padded with cotton, and a sickly cotton hat, stooped over the threshold of the tavern, trying to straighten up as he spoke, raising his voice to ask for two taels of warmed wine and a plate of fennel beans.

However, after pulling out a few copper coins to settle the bill, the man seemed to have run out of courage. Occasionally, when he chatted with people, the smile on his face seemed not too confident, and his shoulders were tense, always slanting, one high and one low.

At that time, Zhu Lian had asked the tavern owner for a pound of the locally brewed wine. That man probably felt embarrassed for having drunk two taels while others were having a pound, so he pointed at the children playing nearby and asked if they knew how many ways the character for “fennel” could be written.

The children ignored the man, only enjoying their own play.

Zhu Lian then changed his mind, ordering another bowl of wine and asking that scruffy man how many ways the character for “fennel” could be written.

That man wiped off the wine stains on the counter, and Zhu Lian ordered another bowl of two-tael wine, handing it to the man who might have read books or might not have.

In the end, after the man drank the two taels of wine he paid for and the two taels of free wine, he suddenly broke down, saying that on the road here, a dog had looked at him, as if it was talking to him, which was terrifying.

The owner and customers in the tavern all burst into laughter.

But Zhu Lian didn’t say anything nor did he laugh.

This was a trivial matter from the old hometown.

There were also some stories in the new hometown.

For instance, in the Dusty Pharmacy in Old Dragon City, there was a senior with a one-foot spear who had formed a bond with both Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafu.

In fact, Xun Yuan had considerable grievances with the dilapidated mountain, and they weren’t minor. However, before the mountain lord and Zhu Lian could discuss how to resolve their grievances, Xun Yuan had already died.

Thus, the world lost a lover of reading celestial texts and an even fonder admirer of watching the fleeting beauty of nature, who would splurge without hesitation.

The dilapidated mountain lost a grievance, and the human world lost much of its interest.

Zhu Lian leaned over to set the charcoal basket down at his feet, leaning back in the chair.

How many true friends are there in the world? Yet they are all slowly leaving.

The woman gently asked, “Yan Fang, are you lost in thought?”

She still preferred to call him Yan Fang; if there were outsiders in the shop, she would call him Shopkeeper Yan.

Zhu Lian, Yan Fang.

Zhu Lian didn’t turn his head, casually saying, “Once a person ages, they easily recall old friends and old affairs. Others’ trivial matters are my fond memories.”

The woman covered her mouth and laughed.

For Zhu Lian to say such a thing was truly a huge joke.

Unexpectedly, next, Zhu Lian suddenly said a few words that brought a somber atmosphere.

“There’s a lot of self-deception in the world, which seems tragic and laughable to outsiders.”

“But for those involved, it is a fortunate beauty and a necessity.”

“For example, you might feel that Qingfeng City isn’t a place to entrust your life, but you increasingly find that I’m far better than Xu Huan and that woman. Really, don’t do this. Rely on yourself, don’t depend on anyone, not even me, Zhu Lian, or my dilapidated mountain; you must not rely completely on anyone.”

That made her frown.

But Zhu Lian added, “All women in the world should not be like grass that bends in the wind. I have always believed that every woman has her own charm that is no less than a man’s.”

She was initially shocked, then suddenly laughed, nodding, “I know, I know, you always have the most profound principles.”

Zhu Lian turned to look at her, smiling, “I’m a mirror; if you don’t believe it, look at whether I have you in my eyes?”

She playfully rolled her eyes at him, not looking.

Zhu Lian bent down to pick up the charcoal basket, standing up and joking, “I see myself in your eyes, so you must be my mirror. Of course, I need to take you home.”

At first, she felt a twinge of fear, but then her gaze turned resolute as she asked, “Is it today?!”

Zhu Lian nodded, “I can’t openly strike out; there’s no need to deliberately cause a scene here.”

She hesitated for a moment and quietly asked, “Don’t blame me for being indecisive. This kind of commotion cannot be hidden, and if Lord Xu pursues after the fact? Are we truly fine?”

It was “we,” not just “me.”

She didn’t mean to say it that way, but her heart had a mind of its own, leading her to speak this way.

Zhu Lian smiled warmly and gently pinched her cheek before lifting the charcoal basket in his hand, “One stream of urine can ruin Lord Xu’s plans.”

She turned her head away, shooting him an annoyed glare.

Other men could say such things, but only you, Zhu Lian, could not.

Zhu Lian muttered to himself, “Taking you and the fox country back to our homeland, I must descend the mountain.”

She was increasingly worried, “Are you going south?”

Zhu Lian didn’t provide an answer.

She became even more anxious. If she had just gone to the dilapidated mountain and Zhu Lian went to the battlefield, how would she manage in that unfamiliar foreign place? What would happen to her fox country?

Zhu Lian handed the charcoal basket to her, “Warm your hands. Rest assured, my young master hasn’t returned to his homeland yet; I wouldn’t want to die early.”

She looked at him with a strange expression, “You call Chen Ping An young master?”

Zhu Lian gently patted her cheek, laughing, “How bold, little maid, truly outrageous!”

She was not only not angry but instead smiled charmingly.

She raised her hand, gently covering his hand.

In the night, few knew the elegance of the night traveler.

Among all the people in the world, Zhu Yi Lang.

---

In the heavens of the barbaric world, due to Dong Sangeng, a moon had forever vanished. 

Today, the entire world plunged into panic, for inexplicably, a second moon had also vanished.

At the Sword Qi Long Wall, a round-faced girl in a cotton coat “unexpectedly” landed on the heavily restricted city walls.

The Dragon Lord was also an exception; he did not obstruct her actions.

A young man in a bright red robe, with a saber at his side, was slowly walking through his stances, then finished his movements and approached her, clasping his hands to stand still, smiling as he asked, “Is that Liu Cai? You’ve kept me waiting a bit too long.”

The round-faced girl was astonished, but deep down, she sighed softly.

While it might not be the truth, this guy was truly impressive.

When faced with matters, always think of the worst.

Chen Ping An smiled brightly, “One of the ten, still a sword immortal, quite impressive. When asking for strikes, please go easy; I’m quite afraid of dying.”

Finally, someone came to the city walls for a visit, and he could chat a few words with him.

Feeling great, he even treated the beasts of the barbaric world as humans for the time being.

After all, you’ll die soon!

In this vast world, the wife is the greatest.

So aside from Ning Yao.

No matter who you are, if you challenge me, you will die!

The round-faced girl said, “I’m not Liu Cai. I did go to Tongye Continent to look for him, but I couldn’t find him.”

Chen Ping An squinted, a sincere expression on his face, tentatively saying, “Since you’ve been to the realm of righteousness, why don’t you pretend to be Liu Cai for a brief moment? Just a stick of incense will do.”

She couldn’t help but laugh, “You’re sure you can kill me in just a stick of incense? By the way, my name is She Yue.”

Chen Ping An nodded, “I have a good eye for people; She Yue isn’t Liu Cai but is still one of the ten.”

Not only did Chen Ping An not draw his narrow knife, but he even took it off and casually tossed it far away.

Instead, from both sleeves, two short knives slid down.

He slightly bent over, wearing a bright smile, holding the knives in both hands.

She Yue patted her cheek.

Suddenly, the two short knives spun rapidly, creating a dazzling display, and the atmosphere on both sides became extremely chaotic.

Like countless fine sword energies crisscrossing the heavens and the earth.

Finally, when the short knives were firmly grasped by that man, all anomalies disappeared, and his smile became increasingly radiant, yet his eyes grew more and more insane. Then that man spoke in the elegant tongue of the barbaric world, saying something she completely couldn’t understand, “I’ve made up my mind; from now on, I’ll travel the world under the name Cao Mo!”

Having never intended to strike first, She Yue once again patted her cheek. After putting her hands down, she said, “Then I’ll give it a try?”

Chen Ping An laughed heartily, “Give it a try!”

---

(End of Chapter)
 

 **Chapter 835: Chen Shiyi**

Chen Ping'an held his double knives firmly, not rushing to make a move.

Facing a "peer" who was among the top ten young talents, there was some strategy to consider in how to approach this fight. After all, the top ten were not ranked by any particular order. And he was currently in the eleventh position.

The true identity, background, and lineage of the round-faced girl before him remained shrouded in mystery, like a moon hidden behind clouds. Since she dared to show up here, she must have been confident in her ability to leave alive; otherwise, that old dog, the Dragon Monarch, wouldn’t have allowed her to act on impulse.

Therefore, it was crucial not to scare her off. He needed to make her feel at ease, allowing her to go all out against him.

Besides, being in the top ten, it would be unreasonable if she couldn’t take down someone ranked eleventh; it would sound bad if it got out.

Chen Ping'an slowly approached her, spinning his twin knives rapidly between his fingers and the backs of his hands. The intertwining blades flickered like fireflies, moving so quickly that their light seemed to wrap around and dance, ultimately resembling two adorable miniature moons resting in Chen Ping'an's hands.

Seeing that the young man wasn’t hastily attacking, She Yue patiently awaited his move. She was quite curious about how he would open the engagement—would it be an illusionary talisman, or perhaps a flying sword technique that would give the sword cultivator a hard time? Or was it merely the brute force of a martial artist at the peak of the mountain?

She Yue had heard many legendary tales about this last hidden official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, especially two accounts that she, who usually didn’t care much for external matters, had surprisingly remembered clearly. Within and beyond the Sword Qi Great Wall, there were stories of the distant A Liang and the hidden officials of the south and north.

As for Chen Ping'an's flamboyant movements, She Yue chose to ignore them. When it came to the art of "playing with the moon," no one could hold a candle to her. Even the major demon, the Lotus Temple Master, who had been a neighbor in years past, had only gained a slight advantage due to age.

Her gaze shifted left and right, and she still felt that this well-known young hidden official of the wild world was merely decent-looking, not better than Jiang Shangzhen. Of course, whether a man was handsome or not didn't matter; the same could be said for women.

Once, a neighbor in the heavens had said that if one met the right person, they would see the most beautiful scenery in each other's eyes, as if they were two distant lands, with the sun and moon far apart, yet their gazes remained unchanged throughout time.

Unfortunately, She Yue had no interest in love affairs. The idea of being deeply infatuated was something she couldn’t even begin to imagine.

Chen Ping'an continued to approach slowly, tentatively asking, a puzzled expression on his face, “Earlier, there was an unusual phenomenon in the heavens—a moon was missing, and I could feel it here. Could it have been captured by Miss She Yue? If that’s the case, how can we fight? I’m just a small being on the city walls, while you’re in the vast realm of the bright moon… Moreover, I’m only ranked eleventh, a world apart from the top ten. I’m quite aware of this.”

The round-faced girl didn’t mention the whereabouts of the missing moon. Instead, she replied, “If you don’t want to fight, that’s fine with me. I came here just to enjoy the scenery, yet you insisted on being aggressive and challenging me.”

It was no wonder she and Jiang Shangzhen from Tongyezhou were such good friends; both were quite shameless.

When a man decided to be shameless, age didn’t seem to matter at all.
