The two were still about thirty paces apart, but in terms of their realms, they felt as if they were only a hair's breadth away.

Chen Ping'an stopped about twenty paces away, suddenly retracting his knives, holding their tips backward, as if trying to show goodwill. He smiled and asked, “Miss She Yue, as the guest, how do you propose we fight? Let’s agree on some rules first; I’ll defer to your judgment. Otherwise, we might end up injuring each other.”

She Yue feigned disinterest, glancing at his dual knives and stating, “Good knives, unmatched sharpness, yet deeply concealed. What are their names?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, smiling, “I found them by the roadside; they’re not worth mentioning. They can’t compare to Miss She Yue’s grand skills of encompassing the great moon and refining heavenly luck. It’s a pity that the Dragon Monarch was worried I wouldn’t focus on my training and isolated me from the world; I regret not being able to witness such extraordinary sights.”

She Yue replied, “Although you’ve been deliberately downplaying your abilities, you can’t hide your murderous intent when it arises. You shouldn’t have accidentally shaped your blade light into a moon. Of course, I suspect you did it on purpose. You, the hidden official, have likely documented all the details of the battles you’ve faced outside the city wall; I could read them if I wished. That Feiran loves to peruse such records while enjoying wine.”

Chen Ping'an paused again, speaking helplessly, “Is it truly the case that holding a weapon incites a murderous heart? It’s my fault for not cultivating my mind enough; I admire Miss She Yue’s keen insight. As for that Feiran, if he admires me so much, after our spar, please tell him he can simply take on the surname Chen.”

She Yue’s expression became slightly strange.

Chen Ping'an realized, “Has that shameless Feiran taken on the Chen surname as a pseudonym? He didn’t even inform me before visiting! To take without asking is the act of a thief, utterly disgraceful!”

It had been many years since he had spoken with anyone.

He felt nostalgic.

Thus, Chen Ping'an was more than willing to make an exception for her. 

Today’s fight would involve more conversation. The more, the merrier—every additional sentence could help him pass a lot of time.

The agonizing stagnation of time felt unbearable, and Chen Ping'an truly wished to avoid experiencing it a second time.

The short knives in his hands, narrow as daggers, were acquired from a valley battle in the North Ju Lu Continent, where he had been ambushed by a group of assassins from the Cutting Deer Mountain.

In a narrow encounter, following a dangerous skirmish, Chen Ping'an, who didn’t believe in his own luck, had let Sui Jingcheng help collect the spoils of war, during which she had found these twin knives. They were inscribed with the words “Morning Dew” and “Evening Glow.” In truth, not only did Chen Ping'an and Sui Jingcheng initially fail to recognize their value, thinking them ordinary, but even the female assassin from Cutting Deer Mountain, the previous owner of the knives, had not recognized their significance. It was only when he encountered his close friend Liu Jinglong, who had read countless books, that he learned of their true nature. Liu Jinglong not only taught him the methods of refinement according to the texts but also revealed the true identity of one of the knives, inscribed with “Hunting the Deer,” which was the famed “Caozi Dagger” recorded in history. That Caozi was the name Chen Ping'an planned to use as he traversed the world in the future.

In the future, whether he ventured into the wild world or returned to his homeland, against any cultivator below the fifth realm, Chen Ping'an would ensure they wouldn’t know how they died.

As for those who died, whether they could see his true appearance or know his real name would depend on his mood.

Of course, this was all contingent on whether he could leave the Sword Qi Great Wall.

“Caozi” Cao Mo was the first assassin recorded in the grand history.

And with that place of three defeats, it was ultimately regained by Cao Mo.

What a good omen!

It should be noted that atop the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Ping'an had indeed lost three matches.

He thought of it as a way for him to share a bit of glory with that senior Cao.

In short, Chen Ping'an promised he would never let the “Hunting the Deer” in his hands gather dust.

At this moment, with one of his Caozi daggers in hand, known in the historical records as “Hunting the Deer,” the remaining knife, since it wasn’t recorded in history, Chen Ping'an decided to name it “Cutting the Deer,” following the name of Cutting Deer Mountain.

First, hunt the deer, then cut the deer!

He had a talent for naming things.

She Yue asked, “So, are we fighting or not?”

In the past, when she was in Tongyezhou, facing Jiang Shangzhen, who was known for “slaying immortals with a single willow leaf,” she seemed utterly defenseless. Besides her temporary lack of strength and realm in comparison, the round-faced girl had never intended to engage with Jiang Shangzhen. To her, pursuing the Dao and fighting with others seemed meaningless, and a battle she was destined to lose only served to annoy her; if she could avoid it, she would.

Yet today, facing this “eleventh hidden official” among the young talents, She Yue felt a bit selfish.

During the relentless pursuit of Jiang Shangzhen across ten thousand miles, he had indeed failed to kill her. Before he left, he had benevolently shared his thoughts with her, touching upon the essence of her Dao. It felt as though it was meant to happen, as if she were destined to hear Jiang Shangzhen’s words when she arrived in Tongyezhou.

She Yue was not one for many words, but she was far from foolish. When Jiang Shangzhen spoke, at first, she didn’t take it seriously, but after hearing him, she felt a stirring in her Dao heart. Undoubtedly, it pointed toward something profound.

Jiang Shangzhen’s words were like a poem of immortals traveling through the vast world, akin to a fragmented verse of stepping into the void. 

To sail to the azure heavens, one must have the means to perfect the missing pieces; in the five lakes, She Yue sold wine at the edge of white clouds.

At the time, Jiang Shangzhen had said little more, but he had frequently mentioned the hidden official Chen Ping'an, appearing to jest, which had piqued She Yue’s interest. Otherwise, given her temperament, why would she be so unusually patient with this hidden official?

She would either have left early or engaged in battle and left swiftly afterward.

However, if She Yue were to discover the truth later, she might wish to smash that Jiang fellow with a round moon.

Because the opportunity for enlightenment lay with the hidden official, it was purely Jiang Shangzhen’s nonsense. He merely wanted to use Chen Ping'an’s identity as a “close friend and brother” alongside his role as a disciple of the Falling Ruins Mountain to play matchmaker for himself.

Thus, he deliberately linked these two “peers” who were worlds apart.

But what made Jiang Shangzhen most formidable was that the prophecy was indeed true; it involved a significant secret in Tongyezhou, known only to the old sect leader of the Yuguizong, Xun Yuan, and half of the ancestor of the Yuguizong, Du Mao.

Tongyezhou was said to have once had a heavenly phoenix tree.

With such a tall tree, naturally, there would be a moon hanging from the sparse branches.

The tree was close to the heavens, and the moon came to the mortal realm; the tree and moon were intertwined, half in the mortal world, half in the heavens.

She Yue’s choice to disembark in Tongyezhou, rather than heading to Fuyiao or Posuo, was a meticulous decision. After the Lotus Temple Master’s death, another figure emerged out of the blue. As for Zhou Mi asking She Yue to help find Liu Cai, that was merely a side matter.

But the problem lay in Jiang Shangzhen hinting at a connection between the Dao and Chen Ping'an was absolutely false; it was a complete fabrication.

When dealing with women, Jiang Shangzhen seemed to weave a web of truth and falsehood, leaving all women convinced of one truth.

So in reality, after distancing himself from She Yue, Jiang Shangzhen was laughing heartily. “My good brother, Zhou Fei, I can only help you this far. Consider it a chance for you to find a round-faced girl to chat with in a foreign land.”

As for whether She Yue would seize this opportunity and whether she would truly complete her Dao, Jiang Shangzhen scoffed. “What does that have to do with me?”

Even with my slender arms and legs, I’ve already done this much; those who are merely spectators should roll up their sleeves and join the fray!

Moreover, would a wild world like the Moon Mountain turn into a fruitless endeavor, dressing up the moon for someone else? Whether the round-faced girl would find fulfillment was uncertain.

After all, during Xun’s time, he had once speculated that this prophecy might have something to do with the world’s most favored Bai Ye.

Was She Yue looking for Bai Ye? 

Or was Zhou Mi bargaining with Bai Ye?

Jiang Shangzhen found the thought amusing.

Regardless, even if the young girl couldn’t attain her Dao, what did it matter to me? I, Jiang Shangzhen, am so generous that I have gifted you a friend, Brother Chen. Shouldn’t that be enough to satisfy you?

Chen Ping'an had no idea about the twists and turns here.

If She Yue had mentioned Jiang Shangzhen, even just a word or two, Chen Ping'an might have been able to guess at least something.

But unfortunately, the round-faced girl was reluctant to bring up that “sister-in-law” Jiang Shangzhen, as she found his words rather distasteful.

At that moment, Chen Ping'an, looking troubled, stopped ten steps away and asked again, “Can we not discuss the rules before we start? It’s our first meeting, and there’s no enmity between us. Lighter punches are meaningless, while heavier techniques could lead to injuries.”

She Yue curiously asked, “Do you always like to chatter before a fight?”

“I don’t enjoy it; I used to dislike it very much.” 

Chen Ping'an suppressed his smile, holding the knives with their tips pointed forward.

Regarding this matter, Chen Ping'an had once taught someone how to conduct themselves while risking his life against Ma Kuxuan in a foreign land.

The two wide sleeves of his bright red robe seemed to tie themselves into a knot, binding the cuffs. The young man slightly bent at the waist, his posture slightly hunched, and his gaze turned upward a bit. “But you all keep making me dislike it. What can I do?! Miss She Yue, why don’t you teach me how to act according to my own preferences?!”

She Yue looked at the young man’s expression and gaze, “Less nonsense. One incense stick’s time; just come to kill me.”

She Yue raised her wrist, her two fingers together, with moonlight condensing like a lamp. She gently waved, and the moonlight dispersed across the Sword Qi Great Wall, marking the time for both sides with a stick of incense. In an instant, the moonlight filled the city walls, gradually dimming at a speed both sides could clearly perceive, as if the moonlight were slowly departing from the mortal realm, undetected by mortals yet observable by immortals.

Chen Ping'an squinted his eyes, now standing upright again, “When a guest comes from afar with a request, the host cannot refuse.”

Even with She Yue’s good temper, she was somewhat annoyed with this person. Despite his efforts to conceal his great murderous intent and heavy malice, he still insisted on speaking so jovially, as if they were old friends catching up.

She coldly said, “With the intent to kill, yet trying to fool me into holding back? You, sir, are lacking in principles.”

Chen Ping'an’s demeanor shifted entirely, no longer displaying even a hint of anger. He nodded gently, his face filled with sincere understanding, carrying a hint of guilt as he spoke, “I come from a humble background, while you hail from the bright moon above. Miss She Yue is a transcendent being from books—what do we need to fuss about? Isn’t that bullying? That wouldn’t be nice; perhaps you should change your ways in the future.”

It turned out that being able to converse with anyone was indeed a delightful thing.

It was enough to bring tears of joy to the hidden official.

He remembered reading in a book about someone who joyfully drank alone while others wept in despair.

At that time, he felt the realm of sages was too high, and his vision too narrow, so he couldn’t understand why they cried. Back then, he thought that traveling far or reading more would help him understand.

Once he knew why the ancients cried, he realized that it was better not to know.

When the ancient travelers found themselves at dead ends, they could still turn back.

Thus, Chen Ping'an, holding the twin knives, imitated the girl’s habit of lightly slapping her cheek when she was about to act.

Whenever She Yue got angry, before making a move, she would habitually raise her hands and slap her cheeks hard.

After accompanying this guy in endless chatter for so long, only to find that the opportunity for enlightenment wasn’t with him, and still being subjected to his strange comments, it truly irritated her.

Now he dares to mimic me?!

After slapping her cheek hard, a clear radiance scattered from her face, transforming into countless beams of light, the moonlight she had refined flowing like water, disregarding the restrictions of the Sword Qi Great Wall and the realms of the Ji Zhi account. The delicate, fragmented moonlight spread throughout half of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The “She Yue” standing at the city wall was struck by the twin blades—one severing her neck, the other piercing her heart.

Of course, it was merely an illusion created by She Yue. It was meant to test Chen Ping'an’s speed of attack and the sharpness of his blades.

Her inherent divine ability allowed her to reveal her true body even to Jiang Shangzhen, a sword cultivator of the immortal realm, requiring him to summon his own flying sword to find her true form. Though this hidden official was allied with the Sword Qi Great Wall, he was still merely at the Jade Purity realm.

She Yue could dodge and evade, and she could also deliver her own “flying sword” like an immortal, summoning countless techniques./n/nIf Sha Yue wanted to learn magic, no matter how unique or closely-guarded the teachings were, as long as it was under the light of the moon and there wasn’t a significant difference in their realms, all she needed was to have "seen" it once, and she would grasp at least seventy to eighty percent of the essence within. 

This wasn't to say that Sha Yue looked down upon the renowned Hidden Official, known for his myriad of techniques. In the wild, untamed world, when it came to combat methods, she was undoubtedly the best among her peers. Thus, in the secret records of the Jiazi Bureau, this round-faced girl in a cotton robe earned the title of the "Treasure House of the World."

Talismans, flying swords, golden body avatars, mechanism puppets, the true forms of great demons, celestial armor, devastating weapons… whatever was in her heart could manifest, all materialized by her moonlight. She could even possess the physique of an ordinary warrior at the Mountain Peak realm if she wished.

Unfortunately, due to her current cultivation level, she was limited to the resilience of the ninth stage, and Sha Yue didn’t particularly enjoy close-quarters combat techniques. It was akin to moonlight lingering on the earth, while the moon itself hung high in the sky.

The first Sha Yue, who had received two knife strikes, was merely an illusion she had crafted with the intent of forming a physique suitable for the Wandering Realm. Thus, her demise was expected, resulting in her immediate death. The round-faced girl in the cotton robe shattered, her moonlit form vanishing without a trace.

Chen Ping'an, although he had followed another manifestation of Sha Yue, had already sensed an anomaly near the city walls before he drew his blades. A hand appeared, radiating an unusual light, revealing a flawless magical seal that emerged from thin air, commanding the five laws of thunder in the palm of his hand.

This spontaneous five-thunder technique was not meant to kill Sha Yue’s illusion; there was no need to mobilize such force against a warrior at the Wandering Realm. Instead, the thunder blazed brightly, illuminating dozens of feet around him, seeking clues for the dissipating moonlight. If the two were to clash, even the slightest collision could give Chen Ping'an a sliver of advantage, transforming that sliver into ten thousand opportunities for slaughter on the mountainside.

For every minuscule chance his opponent possessed, he would return it tenfold.

Treat others with sincerity and hospitality, wishing for mutual benefit.

Unfortunately, that girl, Sha Yue, was too cautious, leaving no openings.

And that was fine.

Otherwise, how could the so-called ten best young talents of the world not disappoint?

Why would they have any right to stand alongside her?!

Chen Ping'an, at the small world’s sky curtain, shattered a large mass of moonlight with his dual blades, then rode the wind to hover above the city walls.

Sha Yue’s form split into three, each one spaced far apart.

In addition to the two true flying swords belonging to him, the Bird in the Cage and the Moon in the Well, he also had two flying swords meant for Qi practitioners, the New Moon and Full Moon, along with two imitation swords from the Sword Immortal of the Hate Sword Mountain, the Thunder Cough and Pine Needle.

Chen Ping'an’s heart stirred, sending the Thunder Cough and Pine Needle darting toward the two girls.

He himself executed the technique of shrinking the earth to travel thousands of miles, appearing before one of the Sha Yues who faced him, striking a fighting pose.

The previous Wandering Realm physique had been too weak; now, she had switched to a Mountain Peak physique, seeking to test how heavy her fists were.

Did she think she was as fearsome as Xiao Qian when throwing punches?!

As Sha Yue struck first, even Chen Ping'an, who was meticulous in assessing his opponents, couldn’t help but think her technique was crude, her intent weak, and her foundation lacking.

Perhaps the only thing commendable about this warrior version of Sha Yue was her speed, reminiscent of the sensation from when that brooding man had once sparred with him.

Clad in bright red, sleeves swirling, wielding dual blades, she darted and danced, chasing her enemy while cleaving through the air.

However, this warrior version of Sha Yue, with her Mountain Peak physique and learned boxing techniques, could only retreat repeatedly, evading attack after attack.

Even though her speed was slightly superior, Chen Ping'an miraculously appeared at her escape points time and again, putting her in peril.

She intended to test the resilience of her opponent's physique, but with both sides asking questions, how could she succeed?

Though they were both at the Mountain Peak realm, the gap in pure martial prowess was still too great.

Just as his blade was about to pierce her shoulder, Chen Ping'an unexpectedly twisted his body, delivering a light elbow strike to her forehead.

Sha Yue slipped back for over ten feet, her moonlight-formed cloth shoes shattering into pieces. As she halted her retreat, she "put on" a new pair of shoes.

The young man, slightly leaning back, casually offered his back to the Mountain Peak warrior Sha Yue, smiling lazily as he asked, “Was it not fun at all?”

The warrior version of Sha Yue, expressionless, had transformed the round-faced girl in a cotton robe into one clad in a magnificent robe imbued with celestial energy. Over the robe, she wore a set of dazzling battle armor, its radiant glow shimmering with colors.

Though he couldn’t identify the robe, Chen Ping'an recognized the armor. His eyes widened in surprise as he curiously asked, “Miss Sha Yue, is that transforming armor you’re wearing called the ‘Rainbow Dew Armor’? Ah, indeed, the vast wilderness has a rich history that rivals others, and you hail from the Moon, a celestial being I can only envy. Have you, besides the Rainbow, also seen the ‘Cloud Sea’ and ‘Radiant Glow’ armors?”

His friend, Zhong Kui, well-read and knowledgeable, had once immediately recognized the origins of the armor worn by Wei Xian.

The Buddhist Kingdom, Flower Bud, Mountain Ghost, Water Fairy, Radiant Glow, Colorful Robe, Cloud Sea, Western Peak.

In total, there were seven of the earliest “ancestral” Rainbow Armors. Besides the one Chen Ping'an had acquired and lent to Wei Xian, according to Zhong Kui, it was said that only the Mountain Ghost and Colorful Robe remained, with records of their existence in the current world; the rest had long since vanished.

The warrior version of Sha Yue remained silent, raising her fist once more, beckoning the infuriating young man with a curl of her finger.

No matter how hard her fists were, and despite her dual blades being elusive, did she truly believe she could kill him?

Her gaze seemed to convey a message: if you can completely shatter this warrior physique, perhaps we could exchange a few words.

Chen Ping'an recalled the fortunate acquisition of the Western Peak Rainbow Armor, making it hard not to think of certain people and events.

Sometimes, one had to admit that the more one saw and knew, the more burdensome it became; it wasn't always a blessing.

Because it made acceptance easier.

Fortunately, Chen Ping'an had always embraced fate, so he could choose not to accept it at certain moments.

Otherwise, if one inadvertently connected joy and sorrow in the affairs of the world, it would be particularly difficult for those who were usually the most cautious to endure.

Since that girl, Sha Yue, was seeking a fight, he might as well show some sincerity.

As a pure warrior, he should be less concerned about the propriety of gender interactions; after all, that wasn't the mark of a true hero!

Chen Ping'an turned around, utilizing the top-tier techniques from his sleeve to store away the dual magical blades that felt like extensions of his very being.

In the matter of sparring, he sought it but could not attain it.

He wished she would throw out a thousand punches, with her pinnacle martial intent as a Mountain Peak warrior landing upon him.

However, even as Chen Ping'an suppressed his own Mountain Peak realm to its lowest point, the warrior Sha Yue showed no intention of striking first. It was clear she wanted either to land a blow on him or to take a hit while encased in her armor and the Rainbow Dew Armor.

If Chen Ping'an were to treat this lightly, Sha Yue wouldn’t mind, knowing she only had a short incense stick's time before she would leave the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Thus, Chen Ping'an had no choice but to let go of his reservations, feeling a bit guilty. Not only did he strike with more force, but he also accelerated slightly, first shattering the ambiguous Rainbow Armor, then the unknown robe, and finally, with a decisive blow, shattering the warrior Sha Yue's head.

All dissolved into moonlight.

Sha Yue realized that testing the young Hidden Official's ninth stage further was pointless. Her form dissipated in place, splitting from one into ten, scattering across half of the Sword Qi Great Wall, with two appearing at the cliff edge and the city walls.

No longer was there that amiable round-faced girl; instead, there were various forms, some with golden body avatars, some as sword-wielding immortals, and others as true demons.

Even though she was aligned with the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Ping'an still found it difficult to pinpoint the real Sha Yue among the myriad illusions. One was genuine, or they could all be false.

These uncertain existences all asked in unison, “Why don’t you employ those sword immortals that stepped out from the scrolls? Wouldn’t that save time and effort?”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “A stick of incense’s worth of time is actually quite long. It’s just that I’m someone with nothing to do, so I cherish every moment.”

As he spoke, Chen Ping'an stepped on something, slowly ascending. Beneath his feet appeared a colossal imitation of the White Jade Capital, gradually revealing itself as if water had receded to reveal stones, until finally, the pinnacle of the White Jade Capital soared high, almost touching the sky.

The young Hidden Official, clad in the Daoist "Crimson Purple" heavenly attire, resembled a true immortal of the White Jade Capital, his methods transcending the heavens, allowing him to stroll leisurely.

He stepped atop the peak of the White Jade Capital, eventually reaching a particularly intricate eave.

Chen Ping'an reached out, grasping a sword immortal flag, lightly tapping the empty space beside him. Rings of ripples spread out, endlessly overlapping.

Sha Yue suddenly asked, “I'm not Liu Cai; you seem a bit... angry? Are you suspecting Liu Cai? Because I’m not Liu Cai, does that confirm some of your thoughts?”

Chen Ping'an maintained his usual demeanor, smiling casually as he replied, “How could that be? Miss Sha Yue, don’t be so suspicious. How could I guess the identity of someone who has allowed you to see all the moonlight across the world, someone who has made you wear out countless pairs of cotton shoes in search of them?”

Half the incense stick had passed.

Chen Ping'an suddenly focused his mind, plunging into a tranquil state as if sinking to the bottom of an ancient well. His spirit felt light, as if wandering freely, his thoughts drifting with the ripples, smiling as he said, “Miss Sha Yue, as a demonic cultivator, you should be cautious when naming yourself in the future. Otherwise, you might inadvertently leak the roots of your Dao. That’s a major taboo in the martial world, so do remember. ‘Sha Yue’ is too obvious. Why not learn from Fei Ran, whose name is elegant and sounds like a cultured scholar? After acknowledging your ancestry as Chen, it would be even better.”

The ten Sha Yues seemed to share a competitive spirit, morphing from ten to hundreds, then thousands, filling the city walls.

Among them, one Sha Yue revealed her true form, looking up at the towering structure, smiling as she said, “But I’ve already named myself; everyone knows it, so how can it be ‘in the future’? Besides, I don’t want to change my name.”

A gentle breeze blew down from the heights, rustling the young man’s garments and hair.

He smiled and answered, “In the next life.”

Sha Yue was then struck by the realization that he was the eleventh?!

The one standing at the highest point of the imitation White Jade Capital seemed to have seen through Sha Yue’s thoughts, saying, “If it weren’t for being here and taking advantage of some favorable timing and geography, I wouldn’t even rank as the eleventh.”

Sha Yue suddenly felt the urge to engage with him seriously, no longer merely testing the waters.

Chen Ping'an refrained from elaborating further, merely tugging at the corner of his mouth, a fleeting look of amusement that was perfectly visible to Sha Yue.

It seemed to say, I can't kill you, and you can’t kill me either, so let’s both take this seriously and give it another go.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 836: Two Strikes

Chen Ping'an stood atop the highest and most perilous point of the replica White Jade Capital, wielding a fully repaired sword immortal flag. 

In his own world, every detail came into focus, as if he were a common man closely examining an inscription carved into a cliff. 

The celestial maiden, She Yue, seemed infatuated with the seven-colored dew armor. 

On the city wall, the only “cultivator She Yue” to show her true form channeled the moonlight through her innate divine abilities, adorning herself once more with the extraordinary armor that resembled an ancient rainbow. She looked up at the young hidden official clad in what appeared to be a Daoist robe. 

The colors of her armor flowed like the ethereal ribbons of a “Wu family” celestial maiden from Buddhist temple murals. 

She Yue quietly awaited the dispersal of the sword Qi ripples, confronting her luminous moonlight at every turn, as if two armies were clashing, each with millions of troops ready for battle. 

Beneath her feet, the white jade replica of the White Jade Capital towered, akin to the “highest peak in the heavens.” This celestial treasure was familiar to She Yue, having originated from the adjacent moon of the Lotus Blossom Abbot. It was an ancient relic that the old demon Daoist gifted to a secluded disciple of the Lotus Blossom Mountain to curry favor. After Li Zhen's defeat and demise, it was picked up by Chen Ping'an, who had not yet assumed the role of a hidden official, evidently guided by a master, allowing him to refine it completely. 

Was it the Taoist sage who once guarded the sword Qi Great Wall’s sky? Yet, would it be appropriate for a Taoist to guide a Confucian disciple in refining an object shaped like a replica White Jade Capital? 

She Yue understood that the other party was still searching for her true form, and her mind wandered, making her realize why Mr. Zhou would say she was too lackadaisical. 

However, today, She Yue intended to take things more seriously, as she was indeed a bit angry. 

On the city wall, She Yue’s numerous moonlight avatars were bizarre and diverse. Sword immortals summoned flying swords, martial artists hurled punches toward the White Jade Capital, and great demons soared up, crashing into the White Jade Capital with their immense bodies. As they advanced, the sword Qi ripples from the sword immortal flag suddenly knotted in various places, forming a vast net woven from countless strands of sword Qi from the half-completed Great Wall of Sword Qi. It was evident that to shake the White Jade Capital, they would first need to break through the omnipresent, overwhelming sword Qi with their physical bodies, flying swords, martial techniques, or divine abilities. 

The momentum was fierce, and it was no mere trickery. Thus, She Yue alone launched an attack as if a great army had assembled to assault the White Jade Capital. 

As for the original form of "She Yue," she rode the wind, her seven-colored armor smashing through the sword Qi net, making her way toward Chen Ping'an’s vicinity. 

In the realm of “Jade Purity,” Chen Ping'an smiled casually, raising one hand to officially summon an ethereal and extraordinary five-thunder talisman. Instantly, it expanded to the size of a mountain peak, then suddenly descended, perfectly overlapping with the high point of the White Jade Capital. 

This put Chen Ping'an at the summit of the White Jade Capital while standing atop the talisman. 

The tall building, like a journey through the mortal realm, featured a scholar riding a white ox, hanging books from the ox's horns. 

All laws converged, and the flickering lightning intertwined, as if a heavenly tribulation were gathering in the sky. 

If this were not at the Sword Qi Great Wall, but rather in any other realm, perhaps these creatures beneath the Earth Immortals, specters, and entities of the mountains and rivers would collapse in fear upon seeing the White Jade Capital, the thunderous heavenly tribulation, and this godly figure in the sky, their hearts and minds shattered. 

Chen Ping'an, who resembled both the immortal of the White Jade Capital and a “godly being,” although his gaze was fixed solely on the colorful-armored “She Yue,” was already surveying the heavens and earth. 

Holding the sword immortal flag, Chen Ping'an stepped forward, firmly planting his foot on the talisman, left hand holding the flag, right hand pinched into a gesture, facing the ground as he lightly inscribed characters. 

Though it was a thunder law talisman, it could be regarded as the pinnacle of all laws in thunder, deserving of its reputation for creating myriad beauties. Once this talisman emerged, it hung high in the sky, and the scene manifested through the technique was far from limited to thunder and lightning. 

From the seal of the inscription, bolts of lightning burst forth like the combined might of sixteen heavenly thunder generals wielding whips, striking down to the mortal realm. 

Strands of golden lightning descended from all directions, rapidly plunging to the ground, turning sharply to finally strike the great demons that were crashing into the White Jade Capital, shattering the moonlight into dust, leaving no trace. 

The five-thunder talisman that Chen Ping'an had manifested from his palm was previously guided by the outer celestial demon Frostfall in the prison, and the tailor had assisted in relocating the five-thunder talisman to the “mountain peak” pattern on the palm of Chen Ping'an. 

The talisman consisted of a total of six faces, referred to by Frostfall as the “Six Full Talismans,” also known as the “Moon Full Talisman.” Aside from the top's heavenly inscription being incomplete, one face was blank, and the base featured the sixteen-character inscription in insect-bird script: 

“Gathering the five thunders, encompassing all laws. Severing the five leaks, the pivot of heaven and earth.” 

Thus, the sixteen bolts that resembled ancient divine “thunder whips” originated from these sixteen ancient inscriptions, with each insect-bird script character at the base of the talisman appearing as the core of the thunder department. 

The remaining four faces were inscribed with a total of thirty-six deities who had yet to be “awakened,” depicted with closed eyes. The significance of the number nine was immense, and thus the engravings portrayed figures of thunder lords, wind masters, rain teachers, cloud officials, and celestial maidens, all resonating with a profound ancient aura. 

The endless transformations of yin and yang, all within this talisman of mountains, all contained within the grasp of the holder. 

The characters that Chen Ping'an currently inscribed were meant to “unauthorized” engrave the heavenly inscription onto the talisman. 

The study room below was stocked with ancient inkstones from the world of heaven and earth. This five-thunder talisman, which fell into Chen Ping'an's hands due to a fortuitous encounter, was supposed to have dual inscriptions from heaven and earth. 

Chen Ping'an aimed to fill the gaps in the talisman, completing the last blank inscription with his own. 

The second-hand bookstore owner was not well-read but had a fair amount of experience in engraving seals. 

What if the moon waxes and wanes again? With a heart as bright as the moon, even if it wanes, it will return to fullness. The cycle of the Dao rotates between gain and loss. 

I have stood atop this city wall for many years; I have not complained daily about heaven and earth, nor have I neglected my sword refinement, talisman painting, or martial arts training. 

I even managed to compile three hundred thousand words. Even if that book of travelogues only contained this little content, I would refine it just the same, whether it be three million words or ten million—Chen Ping'an would refine it all! 

In the future, when the opportunity arises, I shall wander the world under the pseudonym Cao Mo. 

As for the path of talismans, I am also an adept in this craft. 

On the city wall, surrounding the replica White Jade Capital, great demons rampaged, shaking this magnificent structure that resonated with the Sword Qi Great Wall, allowing the thunder whips to strike down upon them with overwhelming force. The moonlight shattered and reformed tirelessly, as if they had suffered no damage at all, suggesting that even the slightest tremor of the White Jade Capital would disturb Chen Ping'an's soul and Dao heart. 

Moreover, a number of golden-bodied martial artists, She Yue, ascended the great towers and walls of the White Jade Capital with astonishing speed, moving like apes climbing cliffs. 

There were also golden-bodied manifestations of martial artists whose identities Chen Ping'an did not even know, towering at a hundred feet, wielding divine weapons, smashing relentlessly into the White Jade Capital. 

Chen Ping'an's heart stirred slightly, unable to help but frown. Did She Yue's backing seem excessive? She was not very old, yet had so many tricks up her sleeve. A girl like her, appearing foolish yet cunning, would surely have no friends wandering the rivers and lakes. 

You have your myriad techniques and divine powers, while I possess my little expertise. 

Chen Ping'an drove the sword immortal flag forcefully into the ground, racing like the wind and lightning, falling from the White Jade Capital to the mortal realm. Both the flag and the talisman were refined objects, so naturally, there was no hindrance. The flag pierced through and vanished in an instant. 

It landed in a replica great city within the White Jade Capital. 

After the sword immortal flag was driven into the central ground of the city, the great banner stood tall, and troops assembled. 

The sword immortals contained within the flag subsequently emerged one by one, shooting out like meteors, some flying with swords and others wielding them, tasked with eliminating the martial artists She Yue that clung to the White Jade Capital. 

This display of sword immortals was, indeed, more impressive than when Li Zhen first summoned them. 

Chen Ping'an's mind was primarily focused on this matter of completing the inscription. 

He had already inscribed four characters on the talisman as the heavenly inscription. 

However, he had never truly poured his heart into it or executed the foundational method above “Dan Shu Zhen Ji.” 

Thus, the act of writing was the first complete manifestation of the “Five Thunder Talismans.” 

As Chen Ping'an inscribed the characters, his thoughts directed the talisman, and the fragments of the inscription scattered like shimmering snowflakes until they finally formed four characters: “Water Dew Stone Emerges.” 

The characters emerged, initially appearing small, only the size of a palm, so insignificant compared to the talisman’s mountain-sized surface that they could be overlooked. Chen Ping'an looked down at the four characters. The first strange thing about this inscription was that after suffering hardships and losses in the past, he decided to write the characters backward this time. Coupled with the borrowed cultivation of the Jade Purity realm, this allowed the inscription to be completed effortlessly, almost seamlessly. 

Upon seeing those four characters, Chen Ping'an's eyes crinkled into a smile of genuine delight. 

It felt as if the Dao was lofty, distant from certain high and mighty beings, but today, since he could write those four characters, it proved that continuing on this path for another ten, hundred, or thousand years would only bring him closer to those heights than the youthful swordsman who once drifted on a single leaf boat. He was getting closer every day. One day, he would wander the world on a sword, visiting the realm of heaven and earth, standing at the same height as the summit of the White Jade Capital. 

One day, he would soar away on a sword, visiting the azure realm, equal to the pinnacle of the White Jade Capital. 

The colorful She Yue, who had originally flown toward Chen Ping'an and the Five Thunder Talisman, suddenly changed her mind, shrinking the mountains and rivers to take a shot at the sword immortal flag at the heart of the formation. 

Having completed the inscription, Chen Ping'an smiled and, mimicking She Yue, let his mind wander. 

Choosing to align with the Dao, although losing his yin and yang spirits and heavily damaging the Dao, he did not feel much disappointment about it. 

I am still me. 

Chen Ping'an remains Chen Ping'an. 

In my heart, I dwell for a long time, always residing in my hometown. 

The cultivator She Yue, clad in armor akin to the essence of military ancestors, caught Chen Ping'an’s attention, increasing his unexpected joy. Zhong Kui had once mentioned that the seven pieces of dew armor, including those in the Western Peaks, were most enigmatic because they possessed certain innate abilities similar to those of sword cultivators. 

As She Yue neared the city where the sword immortal flag stood, seven celestial maidens materialized from seven ribbons, ultimately forming a rainbow that hung in the air, starting from where She Yue rode the wind and landing on the sword immortal flag above. As it struck down, the rainbow light collided with the flag, dazzlingly shining, sending sparks flying, yet the momentum flowed like a river into the sea, endlessly surging. The aura around the flag stirred violently, as if great waves were crashing against rocks, with spiritual and sword energy merging, causing the sword immortal flag to begin to tremble. 

After following She Yue's lead, another “Chen Ping'an” stood atop the flag, one hand resting behind him while the other formed a gesture in front, smiling as he gazed through the rainbow at the woman approaching on the wind, saying, “This little White Jade Capital of mine, with five cities and twelve towers, has only this one door closed. Miss She Yue, please go elsewhere to enjoy the scenery.” 

It was unexpectedly a “Chen Ping'an” clad in a blue Daoist robe. 

His face appeared slightly older than the real Chen Ping'an. 

This scene, these words, were likely not received warmly by all the Daoist immortals in the azure realm. 

She Yue was unaware of the true identity of that “middle-aged Daoist,” but it didn't matter to her. 

As for overstepping one’s bounds, she had done it plenty. 

For example, as she reached the top of the rainbow arc, she transformed into the likeness of the Lotus Blossom Abbot, reaching out to press down. 

Above the grand city, the cloud sea condensed into a pristine white hand, within the palm were lotus leaves, radiant in moonlight, intertwining with green lotus under the moon's glow, and then in a flash, the palm's lotus pool blossomed with countless snow-white lotus flowers. 

The middle-aged Daoist Chen Ping'an glanced at the descending hand and the blooming lotus pool, smiling, “The Dao is vast, yet it is not defined by the magnitude of forms. Smallness remains small.” 

The Daoist stood with one hand behind him, performing a gesture, flicking his fingers. 

A golden light slowly ascended. 

The might of the thunder crashing down toward the lotus pool was overwhelming, and with every flower that bloomed, a pillar of pure white light descended. 

That golden light from the middle-aged Daoist, swaying like a bird's wings in a storm, first welcomed the deluge of snow-white rain. 

Daoist Chen Ping'an smiled, “Quickly, as per the command, go!” 

The golden light abruptly vanished, appearing on the back of that palm facing downward. 

A dragonfly had already perched on it. 

Be it the clash of rainbow light and the sword immortal flag or the oppressive might of that great hand, the emergence of this golden light bore no signs of earthly phenomena; logically, it wouldn’t make a difference. 

Yet, when the golden light lingered on the back of the hand, it caused the torrential white rain to reverse course, causing flowers to bloom and then retract, the palm descending and then retracting. 

Time flowed backward. 

It resembled a contest of Daoist techniques between the middle-aged Daoist and the Lotus Blossom Abbot. 

She Yue shook her wrist, recalling the rudimentary techniques she had observed, and the great hand dissipated. 

She still focused her thoughts on shaking the sword immortal flag, proving that not just martial artists but cultivators could also overpower myriad opponents through sheer strength. 

This cultivator, She Yue, stopped, glancing around. 

How precarious it was, towering high, five cities and twelve towers. 

A wave of thunder and lightning surged, enveloping the mighty might of the heavenly Dao, crashing down upon the earth ruled by the White Jade Capital, shattering the moonlight of the great demons again and again. 

However, the sword immortal flag was suppressed by the rainbow light, and the number of sword immortals that had emerged earlier was too few, allowing the climbing martial artists of She Yue to advance with their sword light, cutting through them endlessly, while the sword immortals could not completely sever them. The martial artists’ ascent toward heaven had already progressed significantly. 

Then, She Yue sensed something unusual. 

It was the first time she had this feeling. 

That Chen Ping'an had finally begun to use his ultimate techniques! 

If She Yue had not guessed wrong, he was using one of his innate items! 

Within the White Jade Capital, five tall martial artists resembling Chen Ping'an appeared, either wearing straw sandals and carrying a sabre, or sheathed swords on their backs, or with wine flasks hanging from their waists, or adorned with jade hairpins, or dressed as scholarly figures in blue robes. 

They simultaneously emerged from various heights of the White Jade Capital, each wearing one of the five-colored outfits. 

They swiftly dispatched the She Yue martial artists who lacked sufficient cultivation. 

“Too slow! Your strikes are too slow!” 

“Like paper!” 

“When martial artists question each other, strikes must land on the enemy. Don’t hold back!” 

The five martial artists resembling Chen Ping'an threw unceasing punches, shattering the bodies of the She Yue martial artists, twisting their heads off, or delivering straight hand chops that cleaved She Yue in two. 

What a pity for the compassionate and protective second-hand bookstore owner. 

Another gentle voice fell upon She Yue’s heart like a whisper from the heavens. 

“Miss She Yue, you have lived next to the Lotus Blossom Abbot for a long time, yet I have never exchanged a word with that Taoist sage of the sky. Why is it that your Daoist techniques seem so light, so easily broken?” 

“So, you see, seeking a teacher in scripture is not as good as finding a wise mentor. Why don’t you and I become disciples together? I have always set a high bar for accepting students. As for my teachings, they are quite commendable.” 

“Your techniques are merely a reflection of the vast moon's essence, treating the main body as the host and dividing it for guests. The fundamental Dao is to return to unity; it would be better if Miss She Yue were sincere, bringing out your true divine abilities as a visiting gift?” 

She Yue found this person quite bothersome. While he had considerable skills, he spoke far too much nonsense. 

She had never found anyone so irksome. 

Perhaps even two Jiang Shangzhen pursuing her for miles couldn’t compare to how annoying this Chen Ping'an was. 

Standing at the pinnacle, Chen Ping'an suddenly stepped on the last characters of the heavenly inscription inscribed earlier, which belonged to the initial part of the talisman. 

The characters written earlier were “Land,” “Sink,” “Decree,” and “Order.” 

Thus, the complete talisman was “Land Sink Decree.” 

So, when Chen Ping'an stepped heavily on the characters “Land Sink,” with a wave of his hand, he laughed loudly, “Go!” 

The characters Land and Sink moved to the upper left and lower right corners of the talisman, while the characters Decree and Order followed to the remaining corners. 

A six-faced five-thunder talisman was finally completed without any gaps. 

She Yue’s heart trembled slightly, sensing something was wrong. 

That five-thunder talisman, akin to the heavenly thunder department opening its doors, radiated light as it rapidly descended, aligning with the city wall and the heavenly Dao. 

This caused nearly half of She Yue’s illusions to find themselves within the realm of the “Land Sink Decree” in an instant. 

Standing at the top of the rainbow, the cultivator She Yue realized that only now did Chen Ping'an employ the fundamental techniques of the Sword Qi Great Wall to separate heaven and earth. 

At the same time, he summoned those two yet-unknown but evidently powerful innate flying swords. 

In the three realms of heaven and earth, half of She Yue was restrained. 

She Yue sighed softly, clearly realizing that this bothersome person had even more troublesome techniques. 

Regarding the heavenly restrictions of the Sword Qi Great Wall and the young hidden official’s innate flying swords, she was already aware and had prepared for the worst. 

It was just that she didn’t expect that this talisman, which could be used to enhance offensive power, would be transformed into a cage by Chen Ping'an with just a few strokes. 

One of the martial artists She Yue had just begun to attach to the White Jade Capital, rather than the cultivator She Yue clad in seven-colored armor, had the responsibility of gathering all moonlight, transforming back into a young woman with a round face in cotton clothing. 

She had already entered the small realm of the flying sword cage. 

As the talisman hit the ground, the thunder light vanished, and the world turned dim. 

It was as if in the chaotic void before the heavens and earth had opened. 

Even the towering White Jade Capital, the sword immortal flag, the middle-aged Daoist, and the five martial artists resembling Chen Ping'an all vanished without a trace. 

The young man clad in a crimson Daoist robe, holding a narrow blade, gently tapped his shoulder, slowly descending from the sky to the city wall, his smile radiant. “Even if I cannot completely vanquish Miss She Yue, I must at least keep a presence of her atop the city.” 

The young hidden official spoke polite words. 

Yet within this small realm of the cage filled with dense sword energy, apart from the path Chen Ping'an had taken, the flying swords dissipated on their own, making way for the crimson-robed figure, while all around the realm, flying swords gathered densely, forming circles and layers, their tips aimed straight at She Yue. 

Within ten feet around She Yue, the moonlight flowed like water, blocking those flying swords from entering. 

She Yue asked in confusion, “You altered the purpose of that five-thunder talisman without permission? Do you not care that this will diminish its potential as an immortal weapon, robbing it of the chance to become a talisman of a sect?” 

Chen Ping'an blinked, seemingly at a loss for words, as if to say, “Miss She Yue, your question is too overwhelming and difficult to answer.” 

She Yue curiously asked, “Isn’t that so?” 

Chen Ping'an stopped tapping the blade, resting the narrow knife at his waist, complaining, “Miss She Yue, you and I have a connection. I cannot allow you to belittle yourself. Even half of She Yue, or a small portion, should still be worth a sect’s talisman.” 

She Yue felt a little guilty and replied, “It’s just that your talisman techniques are too strange; I can’t predict how a single talisman could be so enigmatic.” 

Chen Ping'an suddenly posed an even stranger question, “Can one’s guilt lead to death?” 

Here we go again! 

She Yue raised both hands and slapped her cheeks heavily. 

Without Chen Qingdu stationed at half the Sword Qi Great Wall, no matter how strange the techniques of the Jade Purity realm Chen Ping'an were, how could they possibly stop a moon’s far journey? 

Chen Ping'an hung the narrow knife at his waist, suppressing his smile, hovering in midair, left hand’s fingers brought together, gently pressing against the void. 

Finally, a flickering light appeared in the air. 

Chen Ping'an’s fingers slowly swept from right to left. 

His eyes squinted, fixated on that speck of light, which transformed into a bright glow and gradually into a sword. 

In his small personal realm, a golden figure gently grasped the sword hilt, riding a fire dragon, heading toward Chen Ping'an’s heart lake, looking up at the sky where a moon hung. 

Behind Chen Ping'an stood a towering golden deity, his golden-body manifestation, yet clad in a Daoist robe, appearing middle-aged. 

In the realms of heaven and earth, the four characters converged into one place. 

The boy with the jade hairpin stood atop the characters, confidently smiling, almost smug, exuding the righteous spirit of a scholar. 

The boy in straw sandals stood on the characters “Land” and “Sink,” wearing a jade hairpin, his waist adorned with a water talisman. 

Initially, utilizing the Dao of the aligned realms, he thought alone, murmuring to himself, and wandered alone. 

With a golden elixir attained at the mountain peak, he would ultimately be recognized as one of those young swordsmen in the eyes of the gods atop the mountains. 

He would also master a fist technique, “Mountain Shaking Blueprint,” a talisman technique, “True Records of Dan Writing,” and a straightforward book titled “Sword Technique Canon,” all committed to memory. 

There remained a threshold for establishing a residence, yet no major talismans had yet been set aside. 

He still had a path back to his hometown. 

As the setting sun slowly departed, flowers bloomed along the path home. 

The moonlight around She Yue grew increasingly resplendent, the moon's essence growing denser. 

Layers of flying sword formations, formed from the innate divine abilities of the well at the bottom of the well, shattered instantly after being coated with a layer of moonlight, enveloping She Yue in moonlight, growing larger as a petite moon before ascending into a great moon. 

Yet, She Yue suddenly furrowed her brow, as countless flying swords were broken, but mysteriously, while the opponent’s flying swords dissipated, the true “only” flying sword seemed to silently refine itself through this innate moonlight! 

She Yue promptly halted her thoughts, abandoning the idea of using moonlight to forcefully break the formation and leave. 

Even though Chen Ping'an was now a sword cultivator of the Jade Purity realm, how much stronger could a single sword be? In reality, these myriad flying swords pointed directly at the true essence of “She Yue”? 

She began to gather the moonlight, condensing it increasingly thickly around her. 

Shall I give it a try? Let’s see! 

Chen Ping'an suddenly grasped the sword hilt, holding it horizontally in front of him. 

The golden deity behind him mirrored his actions, moving in perfect unison. 

She Yue, do you truly believe I do not know where you are hiding? 

I regard you as a beast of the wild realm. 

You should not regard me as a mere human. 

Come before me, and let us be enemies. Be cautious. 

One sword to sever the moon in my heart. 

Please reveal yourself. 

Another sword to cleave your true form. 

Please die. 

I have a sword to question, let heaven and earth answer, starting from the bright moon. 

That She Yue, who had plucked the moon from the sky to return to the mortal realm, ran headlong toward the opposite city wall, displeasing Li Zhen. Now, she could not fight that girl. The key was that when it came to origins and backgrounds, the other party was not lacking. 

Li Zhen could only exchange lives with She Yue at her peak, but now, her round face was less charming, her demeanor indifferent, her expression one that conveyed “don’t bother me,” which had once made Li Zhen envious to the point of jealousy. 

Li Zhen flew to the edge of the cliff, near a gray-robed figure, complaining endlessly, “Why didn’t you stop She Yue? Isn’t it impressive to have the heavens on your side? Can plucking a moon from the sky allow one to break the rules of the heavenly cycle? Let our hidden official capture her for a chat, wouldn’t that ruin all our hard work in an instant?” 

Now, on this half city wall where Li Zhen and the Dragon Lord stood, the hundred sword immortals of the Lotus Blossom Mountain had almost all rushed to the world of righteousness. Yet here Li Zhen lingered, as the direct successor of the Lotus Blossom Mountain's great ancestor, truly losing face for the sect. Even one of Li Zhen’s senior brothers passed by the Sword Qi Great Wall without greeting her, directly flying over the city wall. 

The Dragon Lord, gathering countless strands of sword Qi, formed a vague shape. The old man raised his sleeve, pointing at the last remaining bright moon in the sky, saying, “Isn’t there one left? If you have the ability to pluck it, I’ll let you wander over to the opposite city wall. Do as you please.” 

The hundred sword immortals of the Lotus Blossom Mountain were indeed the proud sons of the heavens in the wild realm, but above them was still a small handful of hidden figures, not very old yet with extraordinary status, unrecorded in the heavenly cycle. 

Aside from that round-faced girl who had been bothering Li Zhen, the mistress of that bright moon was actually also Fei Ran, Yu Si, Tan, and Dou Kou. 

Li Zhen sighed, “Dragon Lord, oh Dragon Lord, our friendship spans thousands of years, and we should cherish it more. Not only do you not protect my path, but you also say things that hurt feelings. Can this jar of old wine withstand your few hearty swigs? Always leave a line for others, there’s no absolute genius.” 

Plucking the bright moon down to the mortal realm. 

In the past, the Lotus Blossom Abbot could manage to refine half of a moon’s essence, but due to the presence of the Lotus Blossom Mountain, they didn’t dare proceed. Of course, doing so would also be meaningless. The moon not in the sky, exchanging earthly advantages for heavenly timing, was still a losing deal, detrimental to the practice of the Dao. 

The world of righteousness has many blessed lands, surpassing several realms. The Lotus Blossom Abbot, full of ambition, tried to unify the moons from various places, and when that happened, the old demon Daoist, along with some heavenly timing, would become the embodiment of the “Dao,” not merely a divine being, but surpassing one. 

It is said that before the great war, Zhou Mi once went to the heavens to discuss the Dao with the Lotus Blossom Abbot. Zhou Mi laughed amidst the moonlight, saying, “Why must we lose to the past this year? Why must contemporary people lose to ancient ones?” 

It’s a pity that flamboyance is often swept away by the wind and rain. The unfortunate Lotus Blossom Abbot even failed to catch a glimpse of the bright moon of the world of righteousness. It cannot be said that the Lotus Blossom Abbot was ambitious yet incompetent; it was simply that Dong San’s sword strikes were too domineering. 

Dong's bold act was not only in slaying the Lotus Blossom Abbot, a demon seated on a throne but also in completely ruining a portion of the heavenly timing and fortune of the wild realm. 

It was like taking a grain of rice and turning it into a pile of snowflakes; even if all the snowflakes landed in the pockets of the Lotus Blossom Mountain, the price difference was indeed a genuine loss for the wild realm. 

The Lotus Blossom Mountain would need to expend a considerable amount of resources to reconstruct a complete moon and hang it back in the sky. 

Though the Dragon Lord allowed that round-faced girl to land on the opposite city wall, he had been keeping an eye on the situation there. If She Yue made any move beyond the bounds, he wouldn’t hesitate to strike down mercilessly. 

Among the young generation, one of the top ten in the realm, destined for greatness, was indeed extraordinary, but in the eyes of an ancient sword immortal like the Dragon Lord, the young successors were merely reflections of his former self, nothing more. 

Compared to the lackadaisical Li Zhen, who was distracted by swordplay, She Yue's realm was sufficient, and with her unique divine abilities, she could break through numerous restrictions as if entering a no-man's land to meet the young hidden official. 

One had just returned from the other’s hometown, while the other enjoyed being a watchdog for someone else's house. 

Two young individuals of similar ages, hailing from different hometowns, fortuitously found themselves among the young ten. 

Li Zhen inquired, “Are they chatting or fighting?” 

The Dragon Lord replied, “A lone man and a lone woman, kindling a fire, do you believe it?” 

Li Zhen grinned, “Hurry and lift the restrictions, let me have a look. Seeing is believing. If they really ignite the thunder and fire, I’ll paint a divine scroll and ask someone to deliver it to Ning Yao. Who knows, perhaps Chen Ping'an will not be slain by Liu Cha but will be cut down by Ning Yao first. Wouldn’t that be splendid? When Ning Yao strikes at him, the hidden official certainly wouldn’t dare fart, only obediently stretching out his neck. That’s what I admire most about the hidden official.” 

The Dragon Lord cast a glance at this increasingly unfamiliar “observer,” shaking his head, “With this reunion, I admit you’re right— you are indeed more pitiful than Chen Ping'an. You are no longer an observer. At least Chen Ping'an stays here as a watchdog; no one finds it ridiculous. Perhaps even Fei Ran and the likes would respect him a bit.” 

The Dragon Lord gazed skyward. 

In the past, the three of them practiced swordsmanship together, climbed mountains, and questioned the sword of the heavens. 

In the end, the Dao diverged at that high mountain in the wild realm. 

He, the Dragon Lord, didn’t die at the Lotus Blossom Mountain but rather lost his heart at the moment when Chen Qingdu decided to visit the Lotus Blossom Mountain. 

Although he still willingly wielded his sword toward the Lotus Blossom Mountain, it was merely to provide an explanation to all his fellow practitioners who had become prisoners. 

Chen Qingdu had died once during the battle at the Lotus Blossom Mountain and ultimately died again here. 

So what about this observer? Having also perished once at the Lotus Blossom Mountain, and afterwards, lost to Chen Ping'an outside the city wall, the last trace of the Dao heart and the observer’s spirit within Li Zhen had likely vanished completely. 

The Dragon Lord rarely asked the same question twice, but today he made an exception for She Yue and another for Li Zhen, “In your final battle with Chen Ping'an, relying on the innate abilities of that flying sword, what exactly did you see?” 

Li Zhen laughed, “One is not an observer, and one doesn’t resemble the Dragon Lord. How dare you pity me.” 

The Dragon Lord switched to another question, “Did the one from the Lotus Blossom Mountain, like you, see that outcome?” 

Li Zhen pondered, “I wonder if my master knows about it. Because I don’t truly know anything.” 

The Dragon Lord ceased speaking. 

This Li Zhen was truly troublesome. 

Let’s just assume she would be sent off by the observer one last time. 

Li Zhen was either completely oblivious to the Dragon Lord’s intentions or knew and simply didn’t care, but she continued to plead, “Dragon Lord, please lift the restrictions. Practicing swordsmanship is so dull.” 

Unexpectedly, the Dragon Lord did indeed lift the restrictions of the heavenly cycle. 

Li Zhen exclaimed, “Oh no! The White Jade Capital is quite impressive; the hidden official seems to harbor quite a bit of resentment toward the azure realm. This Jade Purity realm of techniques and divine powers is indeed remarkable; I certainly can’t provoke it.” 

“Look, the hidden official is starting to stir the hearts of others. If it had been Sister Liu Bai, she’d have been in serious trouble.” 

“Dragon Lord, you’re of high rank and wide experience. Do you know where the true form of She Yue is? Can the hidden official’s keen nose catch a whiff?” 

Listening to Li Zhen’s incessant chatter, the Dragon Lord couldn’t help but recall some old matters he preferred not to think about. 

Chen Qingdu’s innate flying sword, Floating Duckweed, had long shattered at the Lotus Blossom Mountain. 

Thus, later generations came to have the saying that “the wind rises at the end of the green duckweed” and “a single floating duckweed returns to the ocean.” 

The Dragon Lord’s innate flying sword, the Immortal Tomb of the Great Ruins. 

The observer’s innate flying sword, the River of Time. 

Hence, within an ancient history that spanned thousands of years, the front page of the old history recorded “Sword Cultivator Observer,” whose way was the most arduous, targeted the most by those ancient deities. 

Friends Chen Qingdu and the Dragon Lord had been the longest guardians of the observer, merely for the longest time. 

Because the sword cultivators who guarded the Dao the most were those who had perished in the dust of history. 

There had once been several sword cultivators of incredibly high achievement, their sword techniques splendid and their sword intent vigorous, manifesting sword scenes of grandeur that could even stir the long-dead heart of the Dragon Lord millions of years later. 

It is hard for future generations to imagine that Chen Qingdu’s talent, back when he first started practicing swordplay, was not the best amid a tumultuous rise like comets falling. 

In fact, it could be said to be ordinary. 

Only due to fortunate circumstances did Chen Qingdu manage to seize the opportunity and hold on tightly to it, gripping that chance as if it were a sword. 

Yet, with Chen Qingdu’s stubborn nature, for thousands of years, he likely would not wish to confess this matter to anyone. 

The tides of time have changed, and the world has grown forgetful. 

Li Zhen stood on tiptoe, gazing toward the battlefield in the distance, exclaiming, “These two are truly fierce fighters, with all kinds of techniques; it’s dazzling!” 

An endless array of techniques and chaotic methods clashed on the battlefield. 

Li Zhen suddenly asked, “Chen Ping'an seems to have utilized his Jade Purity cultivation from the very start, unlike our hidden official’s usual style. This battle, could it end up being thunderous yet with little rain?” 

The thunder roaring was indeed quite significant. 

Suspended high above the White Jade Capital, that five-thunder talisman, inscribed with sixteen characters, each containing the true meanings of the Dao, was held by divine beings wielding thunder, fiercely striking down upon the earth. 

This left Li Zhen feeling somewhat dazed, as if the sword cultivator observer had returned to the ancient battlefield. 

Li Zhen shook her head, dispelling those meaningless thoughts. 

With a face full of regret, Li Zhen lamented, “What a pity it isn’t Liu Cai. If it were Liu Cai, with those two innate flying swords, if paired with a certain treasure borrowed from the Lotus Blossom Mountain, no matter how cautious our hidden official was, he would still end up losing completely.” 

The Dragon Lord mocked, “Hoping for others to come to your aid is no longer an observer. Do you no longer wish to be a sword cultivator?” 

Li Zhen sighed, “Dragon Lord, what’s wrong with you? Why are you always so sarcastic when speaking with me? Why don’t you challenge the hidden official to an arm-wrestling match?” 

The Dragon Lord continued focusing on the battlefield, casually replying, “No use arguing with him. Why humiliate myself?” 

Li Zhen had no retort. 

On the opposite city wall, the figures of the two suddenly vanished. 

Li Zhen laughed heartily, “The hidden official has finally revealed his killer move! Miss She Yue has truly overstepped; once caught, escaping will be difficult.” 

The Dragon Lord remarked, “That five-thunder talisman was sent out by you.” 

Li Zhen smiled, “If Miss She Yue wants to hold me accountable, she must survive to leave!” 

The Dragon Lord said, “Having once peered at the heavens, why must you return to being a frog at the bottom of a well? Observers are indeed just as foolish as your friend Chen Qingdu.” 

Li Zhen’s expression suddenly changed, and she lost all desire to bicker with the Dragon Lord. 

The Dragon Lord had sensed something was amiss even before Li Zhen did. 

Li Zhen was suddenly knocked off the city wall by the impact of sword energy. 

First stunned, she then hugged her head with both hands, letting her body drift as she fell to the ground, laughing heartily, “The Dragon Lord helping others with his sword; it’s truly a rare sight!” 

The Dragon Lord extended his hand, revealing his sword form, summoning the phenomena of heaven and earth, sweeping through the clouds, and obliterating everything in sight. 

The Dragon Lord’s sword Qi clashed with many ancient sword intents, like the grand contest of the Dao. 

Li Zhen, no longer daring to casually land, found herself in a predicament. In a hurry, she summoned a protective treasure, striving to resist the sword intents and energies that didn’t recognize any of the Lotus Blossom Mountain’s direct successors. 

The sword lord struck forcefully toward the opposite city wall, holding nothing back. 

If not, She Yue would severely damage the foundations of the Dao, for which the Dragon Lord had no concern; it was her own doing. However, the Dragon Lord would never allow Chen Ping'an to gain any benefits from the Dao! 

Earlier, allowing She Yue to approach the city wall for a chat, whether to discuss the Dao or spar, was merely the Dragon Lord throwing a stray bone to a lost dog. 

In Chen Ping'an’s heart, a single sword was all he needed to shatter the bright moon. 

She Yue’s form drifted within the earthly cage, though not entirely She Yue, she was still a caged bird. 

With another strike, 

Chen Ping'an’s true self fell alongside his golden deity. 

Heaven and earth shared a sword. 

That form rapidly consolidated into a part of She Yue’s essence, cleaved apart, and shattered again and again, pulverizing her essence and Dao techniques. 

Chen Ping'an looked up, scoffing. 

The Dragon Lord’s previous strike, it seemed, wasn’t too swift after all. 

Above half of the Sword Qi Great Wall, heaven and earth returned to clarity. 

The Dragon Lord swept through the chaotic sword energy and fragmented moonlight, then grasped it again. 

A pale-faced girl with a round face stood beside the Dragon Lord, hoarsely saying, “She Yue thanks the Dragon Lord.” 

The Dragon Lord glanced at She Yue’s aura and remarked, “Fortunately, the foundations of the Dao were not heavily damaged. Take this opportunity to correct your temperament, diligently practice in the world of righteousness for a period, and you should be able to make it up.” 

She Yue silently nodded. 

A figure in a bright red robe stood opposite, gazing at She Yue, grinning, “Just a small mistake; I didn’t grasp the measure well, Miss She Yue, please forgive me.” 

She Yue had a lingering doubt in her heart but kept it hidden, not voicing it. Currently, with the foundations of the Dao damaged, it was not easy. If not for her peculiar true form, indeed as Li Zhen said, she had a unique advantage, then an ordinary martial artist would be writhing in pain, and those cultivators would be in a state of panic, their futures within the Dao appearing bleak. 

Li Zhen, standing slightly farther from the Dragon Lord and She Yue, peeked toward the opposite side, only to see the hidden official raise a hand, revealing the most pure and compact moon in the world. 

It was likely to rival even the purest moon of the scholarly Chen Chun'an. 

Chen Ping'an’s palm moved slightly, the moon gently swaying as if atop the peaks of the patterned mountains on his palm. 

This was to compensate for the loss of that shattered moon in his heart, far exceeding what could be described as merely adequate. 

She Yue said, “Today’s conflict will surely be repaid.” 

Chen Ping'an nodded, “Come again when you have the chance. You are always welcome.” 

Chen Ping'an shifted his gaze towards the sneaky Li Zhen in the distance, smiling, “Look at Miss She Yue’s visiting gift, and then look at your meager demeanor. If I were you, I would have headbutted a wall and died.” 

Li Zhen, propping herself on the city wall, hung precariously in midair, her head peeking out, wearing a pitiful expression without uttering a word. 

Even though She Yue had suffered so terribly, it was wiser to keep a low profile around the hidden official. 

For on the record of the heavenly cycle, She Yue was the type of cultivator who could run away even if she couldn’t win; moreover, she was praised as the arsenal of the world, with countless divine techniques. Thus, she would have a significant advantage in battles at the same level. 

Yet, She Yue’s loss this time fundamentally stemmed from her not bringing her entire true form to this city wall. 

Li Zhen sighed deeply, realizing that this deal with the hidden official had not only yielded no loss but a considerable gain, which was quite disheartening. 

The Dragon Lord reopened the restrictions, and Chen Ping'an still held his hands in his sleeves, slightly nodding, his gaze lifted as he smiled at She Yue, saying, “Miss She Yue, I cannot see you off.” 

Chen Ping'an also found it peculiar that this round-faced girl, upon arriving in the world of righteousness, was so lackadaisical, not even killing anyone? 

Li Zhen jumped onto the city wall, but by then, She Yue had transformed into moonlight, vanishing in an instant, passing through the gates at the remnants of the Inverted Mountain, traveling thousands of miles, ultimately merging with most of her true self in Tongye Prefecture. 

Now, as the world of righteousness and the wild realm continually clashed, especially with Tongye Prefecture and Fuyun Prefecture gradually merging into the Dao, the heavenly timing was becoming increasingly aligned. 

It was no longer a sight of day and night divided by a single door. 

She Yue had a riddle in her heart: why did it seem that Chen Ping'an’s second strike was not his all-out effort? 

Otherwise, even with the Dragon Lord’s assistance, She Yue should have retained more of her moon essence. 

Yet, with a heart as large as her round face, she could not help but feel dismal; half of her moon essence had just been lost! 

On a mountain peak, the round-faced girl scrunched her face tightly and then slowly squatted down, gently patting her cheeks, comforting herself, saying, “It’s fine, it’s fine, don’t cry, don’t cry.” 

Chen Ping'an turned to leave. 

Unbeknownst to him, the Dragon Lord struck again. 

It seemed the Dragon Lord was genuinely enraged this time. 

His form dissipated, then reformed ahead. Chen Ping'an burst into laughter. 

On the opposite city wall, Li Zhen stealthily approached the gray-robed figure, “This time, She Yue returned home, not bringing her entire true form.” 

The hidden official truly spared no effort, betting big for big gains, which was quite impressive. 

The Dragon Lord ignored Li Zhen and, to himself, coldly laughed, “Daring to openly step on that name, you have no fear that the three leaders in the White Jade Capital will sense it.” 

Meanwhile, in the azure realm’s true White Jade Capital, a young Daoist with a lotus crown on his head walked along the railing, raising his hand to observe from afar, laughing, “What a good character, what a good name.” 

Chen Ping'an sat atop a city wall, his feet dangling, gently swinging. 

One hand cradled a small, pure moon, while the other flipped the short knife, which had been recklessly embellished with inscriptions in later generations. 

This dagger from Cutting Deer Mountain, later inscribed with the characters “Morning Dew,” eventually fell into the hands of the young man named Chen Ping'an. 

Chen Ping'an glanced at the miniature bright moon, smiled, and tucked it into his sleeve. 

In the future, when he gifted it to his first disciple, it would serve as a token for breaking through from the fifth realm to the sixth. 

If they had already entered the sixth realm and broken through to the seventh, it would present quite a challenge for the master. 

The dagger spun in Chen Ping'an's fingertips and on the back of his hand. 

Chen Ping'an suddenly came to a halt, sheathing the short knife, leaning against the city wall, and murmured quietly to himself. 

Fortunately, peace prevails, and the sun returns to the sky. What other grievance could there be, but the morning dew first? 

A Liang, upon returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall from the azure realm, had once shared a drink with Chen Ping'an, saying, “It’s truly a pity. 

You’ve never witnessed the three teachings debating, the old scholar who seems to have won even before he speaks, nor have you seen that spirited, vibrant sage of literature. 

You’ve never encountered that man whose hair has begun to gray slightly yet doesn't appear too aged. 

You’ve never seen the young Cui Zhan, dressed in white, plucking black seeds above the clouds. 

You’ve never seen the boy holding his head high after making a mistake. 

You’ve never seen the young Qi, who furrows his brow slightly while reading. 

You’ve never seen Liu Sixteen, who presses down on two heads to prevent the two brothers from fighting, grinning, then, at the master’s glance, slightly loosening one head so that the younger brother can gently kick the unreasonable elder brother. Eventually, the master plays the mediator, saying it’s enough, it’s enough. 

Little Qi crosses his arms, exuding an air of confidence, resembling the master during his teaching moments. 

The tall elder brother Cui Zhan gently rests his chin on the annoyed younger brother’s head, saying, “Alright, you’re the elder brother; let the younger brother have his way.” The younger Qi would take advantage of this, shaking his head at the elder brother, saying, “Do I need him to let me?” 

When both sides glared fiercely, the younger brother would scurry behind the older brother. But once the elder brother let go of the younger brother’s shoulders, Little Qi would feel something was amiss, promptly hiding behind the master, who would spread wide his arms, shielding the younger disciple, stepping left and right to intercept the fuming elder disciple named Zuo. 

Yes. 

Chen Ping'an had never witnessed these scenes. 

At that time, Chen Ping'an chuckled, raising his cup, drinking deeply, saying, “I have only heard you speak of them. Even merely hearing about them and imagining them brings me great joy.” 

Ah Liang observed the sorrow that seemed to escape from the smile of a young man, a sorrow that could not be easily hidden even through his empty cup. 

Sorrow is always so stubborn and cannot be contained by wine. 

So, in the end, Ah Liang drank up the last cup of wine, both lamenting and comforting, saying, “Since leaving the Sword Qi Great Wall, it feels like I have aged. One day, a dark, skinny boy in straw sandals, accompanied by a little girl in a red cotton coat, walked toward me.” 

At that moment, atop the city wall, Chen Ping'an also longed to return to his hometown, to quickly walk toward many cherished individuals. 

The road home is long; even if I encounter many strangers along the way, I must earnestly behold them all. 

Chen Ping'an hugged his head with both hands, standing tall as he gazed toward the empty distance. 

The couplets and spring couplets at the ancestral home in Mud Bottle Alley must surely be replaced anew every year. 

As a traveler from afar, enduring the longing for home, it is certainly because I miss my hometown dearly. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 837: The Heart of a Swordsman Is Hard to Connect

Chen Ping'an suddenly stood up, his vision clearing as he respectfully clasped his fists towards a distant guest. With the Grand Sword Immortal no longer present, he found himself half a guest and half a host at the Sword Qi Great Wall, so it was only natural for him to assist in receiving visitors.

As his gaze swept across the vast expanse of land to the south, he spotted an unexpected elder.
