Chen Ping'an had no idea what kind of divine ability the elder had employed to render the carefully arranged mountain and water restrictions of the Epoch Account completely ineffective. When the gap in realms was too great, thinking too much was pointless.

He truly envied that elder who had gouged out his own eyes and thrown them across two worlds. With the vastness of heaven and earth at his disposal, where could he not wander? If he wished to return home, who could stop him? If he chose to close his doors to guests, who would dare to visit him?

It was indeed the way of cultivation to reach such heights.

Upon seeing the elder's abrupt appearance, the Dragon Lord tensed, his mood growing heavier. Clad in a flowing gray robe, the elder's sword aura formed a vague silhouette atop the southern city wall. The Dragon Lord remained silent, fixated on the sole great exception in the barren world.

This eccentric old blind man had, over the millennia, more or less adhered to the rules, merely guarding his own small patch of land. He took pleasure in commanding forbidden great demons and golden-armored deities, moving mountains by the hundred thousand to create a pristine, unblemished landscape.

The Dragon Lord harbored a sense of trepidation towards this man, yet he felt no awe. In fact, the Dragon Lord had known the old blind man for quite some time; they were familiar with each other, having once been on good terms. However, as the years passed, they had ultimately failed to become close friends.

Li Zhen, ever perceptive, sensed the situation was dire. Fearing that the divine beings would fight and the mortals would suffer, he wasted no time in taking to the skies on his sword, heading north. He even went as far as to hide by the main gate, exchanging quips with the sword-wielding man before finally asking Zhang Lu if he had any wine.

Zhang Lu, the Grand Sword Immortal, who was seated cross-legged by the tethering post, tossed a jar of Rain Dragon Sect's immortal brew to Li Zhen, saying it was sent by Xiao Xian. "Save some for yourself; I’m just like a swallow collecting mud now, with over two hundred jars piled up."

Li Zhen couldn't help but lament how the customs and atmosphere of the later generations at the Sword Qi Great Wall had been thoroughly spoiled by outsiders like A Liang and the Hidden Official. Nowadays, while swordsmanship might not be impressive, they all seemed to be talented conversationalists.

Sipping his wine leisurely, Li Zhen curved his fingers, lightly tapping the tethering post's cylindrical top. "There are four posts in total, two in front and two behind. Historically, they’ve tethered dragons, cattle, horses, and monkeys. It’s a pity we need to suppress this main gate for now; otherwise, that old Yuan Shou would be green with envy. If he passed by here again, he’d surely smash one post and take the other three for himself."

Zhang Lu chuckled. "In the end, it's still that womanizer who can’t beat your master."

Yuan Shou was one of the great demons of the throne, wielding a sword while brandishing a long staff on the battlefield. His arms were long like a monkey's, and in his hand was a rough stone string, made from the magnificent mountains that had vanished throughout the history of the barren world, initially relocated by the demon who called himself Yuan Shou using his innate powers, then carefully refined into a rosary.

This time, Yuan Shou had already visited the regions of Haoran and the southeast of Tongye Island and the southwest of Fuyiao Island. Wherever he went, he smashed any mountain peaks that had ancestor halls, regardless of size.

Li Zhen jumped onto another tethering post for cattle at the gate, imitating Zhang Lu’s cross-legged seated position, sipping wine while contemplating how to trick a second jar out of him.

Zhang Lu asked, "Your family's Great Moon has lost another phase. Previously, she made a round trip to the Cursed Moon, and her aura seems to have changed. Did she have a confrontation with Chen Ping'an? She looks quite injured."

Li Zhen nodded, expressing regret. "Just suffered a minor setback. Sister Cursed Moon is quite formidable; even landing in the eleventh position isn’t a challenge for her. When she gets truly angry, she can easily make the Hidden Official kneel and beg for mercy. A lifetime of reputation ruined in an instant. Thankfully, not many witnessed this, just me and the Dragon Lord. And I’m the kind of person who keeps my mouth shut, preferring to bury my thoughts unless... someone offers me a drink, then I might chat a bit more."

Zhang Lu laughed. "You shouldn't be getting any wine."

Li Zhen remarked, "I heard you and Chen Ping'an are old acquaintances? You’ve crossed paths many times?"

Zhang Lu patted the tethering post beneath him. "As a gatekeeper, I have to engage with all the outsiders coming and going."

During the Thirteen Conflict, Zhang Lu had lost and was demoted here to guard the gate.

Li Zhen looked up at the sky, gently placing his wine jug on top of the post. Suddenly, he chuckled inwardly. "Guarding the gate, as Zhang Lu said, is true, but not entirely. A sword of justice ultimately left a mark in your homeland for a reason. That little Taoist boy seems to casually toss a mat, spending his days sitting near this tethering post, passing the time, but there’s surely a principle and method to it."

Turning to Zhang Lu, he said with a hint of pity, "You seem to always be so anxious, which is why your outcome doesn’t seem to be so favorable."

Zhang Lu surprisingly tossed a jug of Lu Hua Island's stored immortal brew to Li Zhen.

Li Zhen exclaimed in delight, "I thought I’d never drink the Grand Sword Immortal's brew again."

Zhang Lu replied, "It’s rare for you to speak the truth, so you ought to have some wine."

Li Zhen placed the full jug of wine next to the empty one, one on the left and one on the right, unexpectedly feeling a touch of melancholy, murmuring, "Remembering is not as good as forgetting, knowing is not as good as not knowing."

Only true wise men, those who have attained the Dao, genuinely fear the impermanence of the grand path.

Zhang Lu smiled. "Looks like Chen Ping'an winning against Cursed Moon has put you in a sour mood."

Li Zhen extended his hand towards the Grand Sword Immortal, who was drinking, and said, "In the past, I wandered by the osmanthus tree, dropping my poetic hooks into the mortal realm. Today, I raise my head to gaze at the bright moon, while the Earthly Swordsman drinks heavenly blessings. Quite fitting. Allow me to offer a couplet in exchange for a jug of wine. Don’t let an old friend be left empty-handed."

Zhang Lu waved him off. "Scram."

With a sigh, Li Zhen could only uncork the jug and silently converse with Huan Bo.

He pondered what that old blind man was doing at the Sword Qi Great Wall. If the old blind man and the Dragon Lord engaged in a life-or-death struggle, the riverbed would surely shift, adding more chaos to the mix.

Li Zhen laughed, "What does it have to do with me?" 

Then he cried, "Why am I here?"

Zhang Lu cast a glance at the young sword cultivator, noticing that it seemed Chen Ping'an hadn’t managed to gain any advantage.

The young Hidden Official, trapped in one place for too long, hadn’t lost his mind, while the disciples of the freely wandering Moon-Treading Mountain were nearing insanity.

Chen Ping'an didn’t remain standing on the high city wall for long; stepping forward, he plunged downward, intending to land straight on his feet. However, before his feet could touch the ground, he was unexpectedly met with a sword strike from the Dragon Lord without warning.

The Dragon Lord held a grudge.

Chen Ping'an could only slightly alter his intentions, appearing on a brushstroke of the city wall that was closest to the ground.

He made an effort to stay as close to that elder as possible. Speaking with an elder at the highest point would be too disrespectful. Whether the elder took offense was a matter of his own temperament; whether the younger one cared was a matter of upbringing and etiquette.

This wasn’t only true for the Grand Sword Immortal and the old blind man; it was a principle Chen Ping'an adhered to throughout his journeys, traversing countless mountains and rivers.

At the old blind man's feet lay a listless old dog, bored out of its mind, who lifted a paw and lightly scratched at the ground.

If only Chen Ping'an could break through the restrictions of the Epoch Account, he would surely call out to the Dragon Lord, urging him to come quickly to see a relative down below.

The old blind man first spoke to the Dragon Lord, "As long as we don’t fight, I’ll chat with the Hidden Official for a few moments."

The Dragon Lord nodded.

Though the old blind man had a foul temper, he always spoke candidly and could be trusted.

Then the old blind man turned his head, "Which dialect of the Sword Qi Great Wall is more familiar, and which is more refined for the barren world?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "It's all up to you, elder."

The old blind man chuckled. Chen Qingdu truly favored this kind of straightforward yet subtly refined younger generation.

Chen Qingdu had never liked to share his innermost thoughts; he had been like that since ancient times.

Just like A Liang, who had once crawled and snuck up the mountain, showing off at his own doorstep, saying that a man who only enjoyed drinking alone must have many stories to tell.

Of course, A Liang, apart from boasting and flattering, claimed that both hosts and guests were men with stories. He also wanted to trick the old blind man into sharing some ancient tales.

The old blind man had not granted him that wish, but he saw no reason not to drink the wine A Liang brought.

Suddenly, the old blind man kicked the lazy dog, barking, "You’re a flying ascendant! Haven’t you seen money before?! Or do you think there’s shit on the ground to eat?"

The old dog nearly managed to unearth a somewhat valuable lost treasure from the depths of this battlefield site.

After a few rolls, it let out a whimper and simply laid down, refusing to move.

Chen Ping'an maintained his usual smile. Indeed, a dignified ascendant should have some pride and not compete with a mere Nascent Soul junior over what little treasures the heavens offered.

The sickly old dog opened its eyes, glancing at the young Hidden Official in a bright red robe. Hearing the sword immortals who were guests of the mountain, it realized that this young man was indeed a master of picking up money. Old blind man, you truly are blind; you scold your own dog instead of the outsiders.

The old blind man asked the young man in the barren tongue, "How did you know of Cursed Moon’s hiding place? Cursed Moon has only been in this world for a few years, and even over at Moon-Treading Mountain, they keep things hidden. There shouldn’t be any records of her at the summer palace."

"I’m just gambling on a slight chance!" 

Chen Ping'an didn’t even bother using his heart voice and spoke directly: "I almost simultaneously summoned three formations, and Cursed Moon remained calm and collected, even choosing not to rely on her innate moon spirit to break through and swap her loss for my gain. So she practically handed me the answer. She was also gambling, betting whether I could find her. Maintaining three great formations requires a drain of spiritual energy, while she could observe from her heart’s moon wall. Why wouldn’t she want to?"

Gently, Chen Ping'an knocked his fist against his chest and smiled, "Far away in the heavens or close at hand, what's even closer is the inner state of us cultivators. Having seen the bright moon, we all carry it within ourselves, whether bright or dim. Even if it's just a reflection in our heart lake, it could serve as the best hiding place for Cursed Moon. Of course, this is predicated on the fact that her realm isn’t too far apart from mine; otherwise, it would just be a trap for her. Meeting a junior like me, she could afford to be so reckless, but if she were to encounter an elder, she wouldn’t dare act so recklessly."

As for some truths that teetered on the edge of exaggeration, Chen Ping'an didn’t feel comfortable voicing them in front of the elder.

What of Cursed Moon? In my realm, I still manage to gain the upper hand, successfully dealing out two strikes before she needs the Dragon Lord’s intervention to stop my second strike.

The old blind man nodded.

Compared to when Chen Qingdu was young, he had become far more meticulous.

Back then, among the many sword cultivators in the world, those who pondered the most acted with careful consideration. The Dragon Lord would simply shout and strike, his sharpness fully displayed. Meanwhile, Chen Qingdu, amid wielding his sword, preferred to observe everything—studying the world and the heavens, seeking to learn from all. As for brains and perception, at a similar age, he truly had less than this Hidden Official.

Thus, it was said that scholars were never good people.

The old blind man inquired again, "If Cursed Moon is willing to sacrifice even a bit of her innate moon spirit to shatter your peculiar flying sword, what would you do?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head and finally spoke with his heart voice, "She can't do that. If she tries, I'll let her go. I would remove that caged bird and maintain only the Wellspring Moon. At most, I could shatter it using a Thunder Seal to exchange for her moon spirit to help refine my flying sword, Wellspring Moon. Even so, the deal would still be profitable."

Using the essence of the bright moon to refine the Wellspring Moon, sharpening its edge, even now, just thinking about it, Chen Ping'an felt that if he ever had the chance to reunite with Cursed Moon, they could still give it a try.

In truth, whether he could retain Cursed Moon wasn’t something Chen Ping'an was particularly attached to.

Especially after realizing that Cursed Moon, during her time in the Haoran realm, had hardly killed anyone, his murderous intent was even less pronounced.

Earlier, upon her arrival at the city wall, he had regarded her as a demon of the barren world.

Chen Ping'an, of course, had initially been ready to cut down anyone who dared to cross him, thinking he was still on a battlefield facing the entire demonic army of the barren world.

Yet when it turned into a genuine confrontation, his mindset immediately shifted.

Moreover, Chen Ping'an worried that Cursed Moon might return in a fit of rage, fully restored, to the Sword Qi Great Wall, ready to engage him in a do-or-die showdown.

Thus, he ultimately withdrew, only seizing half of her moon spirit.

As he thought of this, he raised his head to the heavens. The sun, moon, and stars operated regularly, there was originally a void that counted as Cursed Moon’s cultivation ground. She plucked the moon from the heavens to the mortal realm, with one full moon divided, I received one piece. Quite satisfactory.

If he were back in his hometown, a moderately ranked lotus root blessed land would present an exceptionally bright suspended moon—an all-inclusive reunion on the Mid-Autumn Festival, where families gather under the full moon.

Every year on the fifteenth day of the eighth month, the full moon shone like a great mirror, and everyone in the blessed lands could see all those they wished to see, except themselves.

Of course, he had promised to gift it to his eldest disciple as a breakthrough in martial arts, and Chen Ping'an felt no reluctance.

Outside the city on the vast land, the old blind man continued to nod gently.

Though the Hidden Official’s scholarly identity was somewhat eye-catching, a young man who was clever enough was surely no mistake. If he could also hope for better times ahead, that would be even better.

Historically, there had been a scholar from the Haoran realm who was a novelist. He first traveled to the Sword Qi Great Wall, then to the Hundred Thousand Great Mountains, not low in rank and reasonably skilled. After finding the old blind man, he spoke with conviction, saying, "Us literati, when we write on paper, only write about how true the world is. We only need to write about the tragic events and the pitiable people in the world, and how the readers feel, without taking responsibility. It’s up to the readers whether they grow more desperate and numb. We just want everyone to know how unbearable and intolerable this world is..."

In the end, he was met with the old blind man’s annoyance. Regardless of how many paths there were in the grand Dao, you could walk whichever you wished. It wasn’t his son or disciple, so the old blind man couldn't be bothered.

But coming to his doorstep, ruining the rules, and daring to come empty-handed, he had to leave something behind.

The reason he was only half-dead wasn't because the old blind man had shown mercy, but because the novelist’s ancestor had hurriedly arrived and rescued the remnants of his soul, taking him back to the Haoran realm.

A Liang, who stood by, wore an expression of amusement, as if to say, "I didn’t do anything at all."

Later, A Liang returned, unexpectedly sober. He said a few words of reason, suggesting that no matter how good a classic work was, it still wasn’t good enough. He was just a coward, trying to share the burdens of his heart with readers.

Even if a piece was well-written, it wasn’t the best. It still divided thoughts. Was it heartfelt writing cold words, or merely writing with a cold heart? 

Was it lamenting the heavens for great sorrow, or merely lamenting that the world’s beings did not share in his sorrow? There was a world of difference.

The same writing, the same tragic prose, yet with warm and cold hearts alike. Ordinary people might casually flip through a book, unaware of the depths, but a scholar seeking to cultivate peace could not remain oblivious.

The old blind man then asked him why he didn’t write himself.

That good-for-nothing merely leaned against the wooden gate, running a hand through his hair, saying, "I’ve seen too many novelists who don’t need pens to write. They write with their lives in the mortal realm, shining brightly, whether in lengthy tomes that span millennia or short tales that last decades. 

Some are intoxicating to read, while others break the heart upon sight. But all are the true good writings in A Liang's heart."

Seeing that the old elder had been silent for a long while, Chen Ping'an couldn't help but ask, "Elder, have you come this time with something for me to do?"

The old blind man collected his thoughts and shook his head. "Just came to have a look."

The old dog dared only to mutter complaints in its heart; the old blind man had lost both eyes, and it felt contempt for him.

It somewhat missed that good-for-nothing A Liang; only when the old blind man encountered him would he find himself at a loss.

Suddenly, Chen Ping'an bowed deeply.

The old blind man laughed, saying, "What’s this? Are you trying to urge me to exert myself more?"

Chen Ping'an straightened his back. "I’m merely expressing my gratitude that the elder’s disillusionment could allow me to be disappointed for ten thousand years."

As the ancient saying goes, mountains rise majestically, born of heaven’s inequity.

This elder, having been trapped like a painting for ten thousand years, harbored more grievances in his heart.

The old blind man nodded, raising a skeletal hand to scratch at his cheek, unexpectedly smiling a little. "Very well; I almost couldn’t help but beat you half to death. You’re indeed clever and know how to cherish your blessings. Otherwise, I suppose the Dragon Lord and Liu Cha wouldn’t have come looking for trouble with you."

Chen Ping'an could only bitterly smile.

This elder, who had made the Grand Sword Immortal visit him twice, didn’t seem like someone who would joke around.

The old blind man turned to leave.

He truly only came to take a look and chat casually.

As for the Dragon Lord, the old blind man had nothing much to say, and it seemed the same for the Dragon Lord. Old friends from the past had become like strangers.

The ascendant old dog scurried after the old blind man.

The Dragon Lord too dissipated, returning to a flowing gray robe.

Chen Ping'an suddenly called out, "Old elder, how is A Liang doing?"

The old blind man did not turn back but replied, "Just a turtle at the mountain, that good-for-nothing is quite happy."

Chen Ping'an felt both worried and relieved; it seemed he wouldn’t have to worry about A Liang visiting anytime soon.

As Chen Ping'an took one last look, he saw that the mountain and water restrictions had reopened, but what he saw in his heart was the Moon-Treading Mountain and the Sword Qi Great Wall, standing in stark contrast. The mountains and rivers were different, but old friends were safe and sound.

He felt the urge to drink again.

Chen Ping'an stealthily pulled out a jug of wine from the fifteenth flying sword and then moved it into his sleeve's small world. Just as he took it out to have a sip, the Dragon Lord struck the jug and the wine shattered into pieces.

Chen Ping'an had grown used to this; his figure flickered and vanished, returning to the city wall, walking like a student, shoulders swaying with his big sleeves, loudly proclaiming how delicious the stinky tofu was. Paired with the stewed old dog meat, it had to be a unique delicacy.

Unbeknownst to him, he couldn’t bear to see the world outside the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The old blind man, however, clearly "saw" the scenery atop the city wall.

The old dog, seizing the moment while the old blind man was in a good mood, grumbled, "I didn’t provoke him; we’ve only met once, and he’s already thinking about my flesh. How infuriating."

The old blind man scoffed, "Who do you think you are to provoke the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall? Whose courage borrowed yours?"

The old dog didn’t dare to argue back, only submissively wagging its tail in supplication.

Far away, a great land beyond a thousand miles from Moon-Treading Mountain had been temporarily designated as a forbidden area.

A jug of fine wine was set there, deliberately left behind by the old blind man.

The powerful demons stationed at Moon-Treading Mountain didn’t dare to move the jug, turning a blind eye to its solitary presence on the ground.

Even though it was confirmed that the jug contained no abnormalities, merely ordinary wine, the great demons still refrained from touching it.

In the barren world, where the strong were revered for ten thousand years, the old blind man, holding sway over a territory, was one of the few at the peak of fourteen realms.

Now, in the barren world, after Xiao Xian had visited the ancient well’s abyss, another had emerged. However, she achieved her status through the fate of the barren world rather than simply through her innate flying sword.

The fourteen realms were far too profound and unpredictable; no one could inquire about the differences between them.

In fact, A Liang could have answered those questions, but who would dare to provoke, adding fuel to the fire and snow to the frost? Did they truly think he couldn’t leave Moon-Treading Mountain?

Moon-Treading Mountain and A Liang were both suppressive forces, yet they also maintained a subtly delicate balance of non-interference. 

After all, A Liang himself was unwilling to relinquish that path to seek a sword at Moon-Treading Mountain.

A great demoness, who could be considered Li Zhen's senior, with the beauty and grace of the Haoran realm, arrived at the chaotic void beneath Moon-Treading Mountain.

From a distance, she gazed at the scholar sitting cross-legged, surrounded by a multitude of golden characters that served as a mat, looking much like an outsider who had come to borrow the mountain for cultivation.

She couldn’t understand why this man would choose such a path. The renowned Mr. Wen from the Sea of Literature had once explained the great truth of "If a man does not act for himself, heaven will punish him."

Thus, she found it even harder to comprehend A Liang's self-destructive path.

The scruffy man noticed the Moon-Treading Mountain woman cultivator and immediately straightened up. "Sister New Makeup, why do you still wear the same old guise as when we first met? Meeting old friends in old attire is truly poetic."

The woman demoness, known as New Makeup, recalled their past meeting and frowned, "Shut your mouth!"

Had her own nonsense hit a wall?

A Liang was not one to fear such situations, wearing a deeply affectionate expression. "It seems sister New Makeup still remembers our first encounter well, which comforts my heart. There are few good men worth a hundred years of memory for you."

New Makeup scoffed, "If you had made a different choice, how many swords would you have used to cut me down?"

A Liang felt a bit embarrassed; this woman truly knew how to strike hard. 

New Makeup, not understanding the deeper meaning, thought he was merely lost in thought, distractedly navigating the sword intent while suppressing the void beneath them.

A Liang figured this was a rare opportunity and would have to pull out all the stops.

Having reconnected, he still looked handsome, and with a higher level of swordsmanship, he was sure this sister had grown used to it. So, he decided to bring a touch of poetic romance.

A Liang cleared his throat and moistened his vocal cords.

Unexpectedly, New Makeup coldly laughed, "Shut up."

This man, who had once traveled the barren world on his sword, because of continuous troubles, his sword-wielding demeanor had been witnessed by many great demons.

While leaning on his waist with both hands, he loudly recited poetry, claiming it was the style of both sword immortals and poets. It was worth noting he was still being pursued by the great demons attacking with techniques.

A Liang sighed, feeling that beautiful women lacked appreciation for romance; they were the most unflattering when they disappointed good men.

New Makeup asked, "With your cultivation, why don't you cherish it properly?"

A Liang responded, "I can answer sincerely, but sister New Makeup must first listen to a few words from me."

New Makeup nodded.

As expected, there were no surprises.

The man clapped his knees, smiling and reciting poetry.

Not much smile, but loud enough, "This is my A Liang's original creation, the Three Farewell Song."

"Shu Road is difficult, let’s drink, dreaming of the heavenly maid, bidding farewell."

"Pipa Song, Long Regret Song, an ancient wild grass to send off."

"Ah, Wang Sun, no home to part from, a painted calligraphy gift to General Cao."

"If it weren’t for the exam topic, it could be changed to that Mud Skill Mountain, carrying firewood, a hundred and fifty nights against the moon, that would also be quite nice."

"Washing the soldiers’ horses, gifting flowers, walking alone by the river seeking a perfect couplet. Hmm, if replaced with the Three Rivers watching the rising water's ten verses, it seems even better."

"What a fine fellow! Such a stream of literary thought flows like a rushing spring, like a wheel that can’t be stopped, impressive, truly impressive."

New Makeup said, "Are you done babbling?"

Finally, A Liang nodded, his expression a mix of amusement and seriousness, resting his fists on his knees, speaking to himself, "What a scene where Jia Sheng weeps, and no one remains. What a sight to behold, drunk as a horse falls, no need to laugh at people; I invite all to drink and watch."

New Makeup remained silent, waiting for the answer.

Why was A Liang so careless with a sword cultivator of the fourteenth realm?

"Because I cherish this hard-earned fourteenth realm."

A Liang didn’t play the rogue, smiling and saying, "It’s a pity sister New Makeup, you’re not young anymore and have traveled too little, so you don’t understand. After all, it’s hard for the heart of a swordsman to connect." 

New Makeup fell silent.

Whether swordsman or sword cultivator, the entire realm acknowledged it.

Only this man, who acted overly "refined," was truly off-putting; it made one feel that there was no need to be so pretentious; simply be your sword immortal.

New Makeup had once asked Mr. Zhou what he would choose if the Haoran realm was filled with people like A Liang.

Mr. Zhou had smiled, saying that he wouldn’t come to their hometown, and that A Liang was A Liang precisely because there was only one A Liang.

It was said that A Liang had roamed the barren world alone with his sword multiple times, seeking Zhou Mi, who had once been disheartened in the Haoran realm, only to weep with ghosts and gods.

But Zhou Mi had always been unwilling to meet him.

Suddenly, A Liang stood, his expression solemn, and recited the wise words he had read in his youth, words imbued with the divine meaning he grasped early on.

"Eyes reach for miles, heart wanders the vast wilds, spirit breaking the ground, heaven rises in response."

"Clouds churn and dragons change, spring brings tree blossoms. Is creation in my heart or my hands?"

All of A Liang's words transformed into massive golden characters, slamming into the abyss beneath the golden mat.

The characters further manifested into a golden dragon, spring winds and tree blossoms, appearing amidst the white clouds, suppressing the soaring malevolence.

Confucian sages exuded righteousness. With heaven's mandate in their mouths, their words followed the law.

Deep beneath, there were tremors like the heavens collapsing and the earth splitting, as if roads were blocked, having to retreat temporarily, but the residual momentum still slowly reached the golden mat.

Making New Makeup feel utterly astounded.

The man rubbed his head and cheerfully asked the Moon-Treading Mountain demoness, "Are scholars fierce?!"

(End of Chapter)

 

 **Chapter 838: Jia Sheng's Disappointment (Part 1)**

Before Liu Sixteen left the Desolate Mountain (Luoposhan) to head towards the Old Dragon City (Laolongcheng) battlefield, the burly man who called himself "Jun Qian" paid a visit to the Master Hall at the Jise Peak (Jise Feng) to pay his respects. He also made a trip to the first floor of the bamboo building at Desolate Mountain. Aside from a wooden plank bed placed in the corner, the rest of the space resembled a study.

The little steward, Nuan Shu, unlocked the door with a key, and Shumi Li stood at the threshold, holding a green bamboo staff and a golden shoulder pole, acting as a guardian with his chest puffed out and standing straight.

Liu Sixteen opened several neatly arranged books on the table. Most of the pages were filled with densely packed annotations written in small script. If the writing truly conveyed the author's thoughts, then the younger disciple must have been a serious and meticulous scholar. After all, Master Brother Cui Shan’s treasured collection was just like this; whenever he encountered different interpretations in books, he would have Little Qi transcribe them, resulting in dozens of notes written in the margins of a single book.

Liu Sixteen returned the books to their places and glanced up, noticing a pair of couplets hanging on the wall, featuring a blue background with golden characters depicting cloud bats. According to Shumi Li, these were scavenged by the younger disciple from Beiju Luzhou.

*Three feet of sword amidst the storm outside the mountain, when there's a matter, draw the sword and descend the mountain.*

*In a room filled with flowers and birds, without worries, read the sages and the wise.*

Liu Sixteen, who appeared rugged, was actually quite observant. He quickly noticed a seal in the corner of the couplets that read “Chen Shiyi.”

With both literary and martial prowess, he cultivated strength and heart.

Before returning to the mountain, Liu Sixteen first went to Yang's shop to guard the formation for the Eastern Duke, then accompanied Ruan Xiu to the Celestial Canopy to host guests. Their wishes fulfilled, they smashed two enemies with their fists, and two golden rains fell upon the northern region of the continent, with half of the golden body fragments collected by the long-lived friend and the other half gifted to Cloud-Piercing Mountain.

That little girl, Ruan Xiu, was even bolder, directly crossing the threshold and venturing into the sky. One wondered if she had managed to meet the Sage of Rites.

After returning to the mountain, Liu Sixteen received a minor official position from the right protector of the Desolate Mountain, titled "Mountain Patrol Envoy." Shumi Li remarked that the position was not significant, so he shouldn’t complain.

While patrolling the mountain, the man stretched out his arms, one holding a little girl in a pink skirt, the other a girl in black, as they walked together in the morning light.

Once during a patrol, a little lotus fairy sat on his head, admiring the moonlight together.

The Azure Youth Heavenly Sovereign reopened the Ascension Platform in the mortal realm, which was a tremendous blessing for many earth immortals and practitioners in the continent.

An Ascension Platform.

A genuine ascent to an ancient ruin, eventually leading to a dilapidated heavenly gate towering above the sea of clouds.

Throughout this process of the heavenly platform rising, it served as a kind of tempering of the Great Way.

Any earth immortal practitioner who could maintain their Dao heart and keep their soul intact could reach the summit. Although they would inevitably be unable to cross the severely restricted ancient gate, simply standing outside the heavenly gate amidst the clouds was already a fulfillment of merit.

Many practitioners fell from the Ascension Platform, returning to the mortal world with varying degrees of success, depending on how high they ascended.

Seventy to eighty percent experienced significant gains. Xu Hun, the lord of Qingfeng City, donned his wart-covered armor and stood firm as a mountain on the Ascension Platform. He finally broke through the bottleneck of the Nascent Soul realm and entered the upper five realms.

Liu Baqiao, a swordsman from the Wind and Thunder Garden, was relatively unfortunate. Due to a flaw in his sword heart, he remained stuck in the Nascent Soul stage. He had nearly grasped a hint of the Great Way, but it seemed that inner demons had plagued him, causing significant injury. After taking a major step forward, he found himself unable to take a second step and even slightly retreated. However, even just transitioning from the Golden Core stage to the genuine Nascent Soul stage, Liu Baqiao had a decent report for his senior brother, Huang He, who was about to relinquish his title as the garden lord. Otherwise, if Liu Baqiao returned empty-handed, he felt that with his senior brother's temperament, he might be sent away and confined to the mountain for a hundred years—never to descend again until he achieved the Nascent Soul.

Liu Baqiao, like Xu Hun, reached the summit above the sea of clouds but soon found himself unavoidably returning to the mortal realm. He revisited the small town and went to the construction office, where he had a pleasant reunion with Supervisor Cao, whom he met for the first time, over drinks.

Cai Jinjian, a female Golden Core immortal from Yunxia Mountain, was a bit of a surprise. Given her talent, several masters on the mountain had not anticipated that she would reach the Nascent Soul stage in this lifetime. Yet, she managed to hold on until the end, even catching a glimpse of the heavenly gate, which was quite an accomplishment.

This time, Cai Jinjian's ascent could be considered a leap to the heavens. If all goes well, upon her return to her sect, in addition to the master chair she had previously been given, she would likely become the youngest female master in Yunxia Mountain's history.

Many immortal residences in Baoping Continent often saw practitioners become Golden Core guests. Besides being able to open their own peaks and announce their presence across the continent, they could also elevate their standing in the sect's hierarchy. If fortunate enough to reach the Nascent Soul stage, they would ascend even higher.

As for the upper five realms, they could easily establish their own sects.

After exiting the Ascension Platform, Cai Jinjian found herself alone outside an old academy. She gazed at the empty classroom, lost in thought.

Jiang Yun, a dark-clothed man from the Jiang family of Yunlin, did not immediately rush to the Eastern Sea front to join his master and the Grand General Wei Liang. Instead, he lingered for a moment, mirroring Liu Baqiao and Cai Jinjian's choices, revisiting the familiar Lihuzhou town.

However, when he arrived at the iron lock well, he felt somewhat disappointed. The iron chain that once hung down into the well had long been refined into his life-bound object. This allowed him to successfully refine a small personal realm into the long-lost "Iron Mountain Jungle" and "Crystal Clear Dojo," and he now possessed a treasure that was both offensive and defensive.

This time, Jiang Yun also ascended to the Nascent Soul realm.

Other earth immortals experienced varying degrees of advancement in their realms. Those fortunate enough to see the heavenly gate's ancient visage were still in the minority.

Out of the earth immortals who secretly came to this place, only about twenty to thirty percent left empty-handed and returned, having gained nothing, quickly falling off the Ascension Platform.

However, they dared not show any change in expression.

The only "compensation" was that they did not break their mirrors here; the earth immortals would not need to accumulate too much merit for the upcoming battles in Old Dragon City.

Sui Youbiao, within the True Realm Sect at Shujian Lake, had recently broken through the bottleneck of the Dragon Gate realm, making her the least experienced Golden Core earth immortal among this group.

However, Sui Youbiao's transition from a pure martial artist to a sword practitioner was already a remarkable feat. In just over a decade, she had become a Golden Core sword practitioner, astonishing many. Yet, both Yuguizong and the True Realm Sect had concealed a lot about her.

If it weren't for Sui Youbiao's identity as a direct disciple of the sub-sect of Yuguizong, during this gathering at the Ascension Platform, all the earth immortals from Baoping Continent, who were all sharp-minded individuals, would surely have raised suspicions about her.

Unfortunately, Sui Youbiao was unable to break through this time and only reached the bottleneck of the Golden Core stage.

She merely glimpsed more heavenly scenery than the average earth immortal.

*I wish to follow the master to the heavenly platform, casually sweeping away fallen flowers with the immortals.*

It's a pity that there was no master beside her, and no immortals in the sky.

In truth, Sui Youbiao had a certain opportunity to ascend to the Nascent Soul stage. However, for reasons unknown, she deliberately suppressed her eager sword during a crucial moment when the long sword she carried was willing to protect her path.

Because she did not draw her sword and refused to resist the heavenly winds with her sword intent, relying solely on her solid practitioner’s physique and focused spirit, she lost an even greater opportunity.

After exiting the Ascension Platform, Sui Youbiao's sword heart was clear. Not only did she not show any signs of dejection, but her Dao heart also grew more resolute. She bought some pastries at the New Year's shop on Qilong Alley and then rode the wind towards the state city.

Along with Sui Youbiao, leaving Shujian Lake were two direct disciples of the True Realm Sect brought by Sect Master Wei Ying from the Upper Sect's Jiu Yi Peak to Baoping Continent. Both companions of Sui Youbiao traveling north were also sword practitioners and direct disciples of Wei Ying. The young woman, named Sui Yu, was particularly eager to visit the Sword Qi Great Wall to verify whether the sword immortal Mi Yu was as handsome as her master.

A young man named Nian Jiu seemed to be completely oblivious to worldly affairs beyond cultivating and practicing swordsmanship. His only task was to stop his beloved senior sister from going to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

However, their names recorded in the True Realm Sect's mountain and water register were Wei Gusu and Wei Xianyou.

Their life-bound swords were called "Fish Dragon" and "Wine Pot," both named by their master, Wei Ying. Sui Yu liked hers, and Nian Jiu liked his because the wine pot contained a hidden world.

They exited the Ascension Platform slightly earlier than Sui Youbiao.

Previously, they had temporarily stayed at an immortal guesthouse in the state city, owned by a young man named Dong, who was renowned in the North Mountain region for his beauty, earning him the nickname "Half a City."

Even with the discerning tastes of Sui Yu and Nian Jiu, they found the guesthouse's environment serene and exceptional, making it their top choice for future visits.

Sui Yu remarked telepathically, "Sui Youbiao is so attractive; even Master likes her. Why don't you like her?"

Nian Jiu replied earnestly, "I only like those who like themselves."

Sui Yu grew furious, calling her thick-headed junior brother a fool and shouted, "Drop dead!"

Sui Youbiao landed outside the guesthouse. The Dong Water Well's immortal guesthouse was not large but had strict rules; even guests could not casually ride the wind to enter or exit, only able to walk through the door.

Sui Youbiao found Wei Gusu and Wei Xianyou and simply said, "To the Niujiao Ferry."

Wei Xianyou looked at Sui Youbiao and after a long gaze, he still felt a sense of amazement. The young man thought to himself that if his senior sister continued to be so unreasonable, he might just start liking someone else.

Sui Youbiao and the two direct disciples of the True Realm Sect had sword talismans, allowing them to ride the wind freely in the Longzhou region. As a direct disciple of the Desolate Mountain, Sui Youbiao naturally already possessed a Dragon Spring Sword Sect’s talisman sword, but spending True Realm Sect's money for an extra one was no trouble.

With her sword on her back, Sui Youbiao rode the wind towards the Niujiao ferry.

The long sword, once lost and then found, was both infatuated and hungry.

It was just unclear who was infatuated with whom and who was the master and who was the heartbreaker.

A man and a woman left the Qingfeng City region under the cover of night, carefully concealing their appearances and traces. Once they entered the North Mountain region, it felt as if they were simply enjoying a scenic tour. The age difference between the elderly man and the young girl was stark; the old man was hunched, while the young girl had a lovely complexion, not overly striking. Occasionally, the old man would take out a branch of pear blossoms and gently twirl it, which the young girl did not find embarrassing at all. If the beautiful innkeeper truly dared to do this, it would be a toss-up as to who would benefit.

The old man was somewhat excessive, teasing her about how she now resembled a rustic girl from the countryside.

It was none other than Zhu Lian and the Fox Kingdom's lord from Qingfeng City, one returning to his hometown while the other traveled far from home.

The current Qingfeng City must be in turmoil.

The lord of the Fox Kingdom, under the alias Pei Xiang, was a Nascent Soul practitioner with seven fox tails.

As for whether to place the Fox Kingdom in a lotus root blessed land, relatively isolated from the world, or to set it on a certain mountain peak of a vassal state, Zhu Lian primarily deferred to Pei Xiang’s wishes.

However, Pei Xiang still found it hard to believe that a Desolate Mountain could possess a medium-sized blessed land. After all, she trusted Zhu Lian but held doubts about the Desolate Mountain.

Zhu Lian chuckled, "I forgot to remind you, once we reach my home on the Mountain of Young Master, you must remember one principle: treat people with sincerity."

Pei Xiang felt somewhat anxious, her demeanor growing increasingly delicate. With charm surrounding her, she bit her lip, "You should be more specific. I have a good memory and am used to bowing my head and obeying others."

This was primarily due to her long dealings with the Xu family of Qingfeng City, where she feared the phrase "up the mountain."

Zhu Lian shook his head, "If I say too much, you will become complacent. Moreover, I don’t need to elaborate. My Desolate Mountain is quite pleasant; the storms outside are merely for sightseeing. Other mountain peaks, like Qingfeng City, have people bickering over silver coins. Desolate Mountain is different."

She then asked, "Are there any particularly petty women on Desolate Mountain? I'm quite afraid of that."

The Xu family woman still made Pei Xiang wary to this day.

Just thinking about the awkward situation that woman was in now made Pei Xiang unable to suppress a laugh. Women often enjoyed putting other women in difficult positions. That woman probably felt that her looks couldn't compare, so she enjoyed putting subtle jabs in her embroidered shoes, and now she was facing her retribution, wasn't she?

As the innkeeper said, Xu Hun had just entered the upper five realms and was just right for a celebratory occasion for Qingfeng City.

Indeed, Qingfeng City excelled at creating a buzz. First, the legitimate daughter married the commoner's son of the Yuan family, and then there were whispers of the Xu family seemingly using their cunning legitimate son to form a marriage alliance with the old sword immortal of the Tao family from Zhengyang Mountain. Now that Xu Hun had crossed the great threshold of the heavenly gate and entered the upper five realms, given Qingfeng City's temperament, unless a Fox Kingdom disappeared into thin air, not to mention Beiju Luzhou, the news would probably spread even to Aiai Continent.

Zhu Lian chuckled about how one could easily become complacent and suffer the consequences, which Pei Xiang wholeheartedly agreed with, feeling quite satisfied. At that moment, she received a gentle slap from Zhu Lian, who said, "And you?"

In the dusk, the two passed through the bustling Red Candle Town. As long as they crossed Qi Dune Mountain, the Desolate Mountain would be just ahead.

Pei Xiang felt a weight lift off her shoulders as she looked up to clearly see the cloud-wreathed Cloud-Piercing Mountain, giving her another boost of reassurance.

Zhu Lian bought a lot of sunflower seeds at a market stall and then led Pei Xiang down a street.

Pei Xiang softly asked, "Who are we going to see?"

Zhu Lian replied as they walked through the crowded street, "To meet the Water God of Danjiang, Li Jin."

Zhu Lian added, "He sells books, and we've always had a good relationship. After all, distant relatives are not as good as close neighbors."

Previously, due to the matter involving the Water Goddess of Yuyue River, it was inevitable that there would be some tension between the brothers Li Jin, after all, it's human nature to feel sorrow for another's misfortune.

This time, they would take the opportunity to help resolve the innkeeper's worries.

After all, Zhu Lian was never good at dealing with women.

Did women really need to be dealt with? 

In any case, Zhu Lian never needed to.

Pei Xiang understood this and knew that this bustling Red Candle Town, located at the confluence of three rivers, had three Water Gods, among which Li Jin had only been sealed by the Great Li for a few years, and the temple's incense was still quite good.

The Fox Kingdom was a place where all sorts of people mixed together, and news circulated quickly among the mountains, so Pei Xiang was well aware of many secrets and confidential matters in the continent.

As for Zhu Lian's acquaintance with Li Jin, Pei Xiang was not surprised. After all, although Li Jin held a significant position, he was still a newcomer in the "mountain and water bureaucracy" of the Great Li. He likely needed to establish a good rapport with the Desolate Mountain, and getting close to Desolate Mountain was almost equivalent to getting acquainted with the Mountain Lord Wei of Cloud-Piercing Mountain.

The Nascent Soul fox enchantress, "Pei Xiang," while only a realm apart from Wei Ban, differed vastly in both identity and true cultivation.

Now, a piece of news began to spread, stating that Lord Wei would soon advance to the next level, thanks to the three golden rains' nurturing and tempering. He would soon reach a state equivalent to that of an immortal, becoming one of the most refined mountain lords among the five peaks of the continent once again.

The innkeeper was a handsome young man in black, reclining in a wicker chair, sipping tea while reading.

However, Pei Xiang did not pay much attention to Li Jin's appearance; comparing looks was the least of her concerns./n/nLi Jin recognized Zhu Lian almost immediately after seeing him draped in a thin veil. There was no mistaking it; Zhu Lian was far too familiar with the place. Within moments, he had picked up the few books on the shelf that were related to the world of seduction—books he had often admired but had never dared to purchase. Today, however, he seemed to be in a lavish mood, exuding an air of “I’m a scholar, and even just glancing at the price of a book is an affront to the sages.” It appeared that Zhu Lian had made quite a fortune on his recent excursion.

Li Jin glanced at the “young lady” beside him. As the Water God of the river trade, he could sense something amiss, though he couldn’t pinpoint the exact nature of her realm. No matter; this was already an answer in itself—was she perhaps at the Nascent Soul stage? Ah, yes, the Xu family in Qingfeng City had a well-known fox kingdom, famous for its fox-fur beauties that were exported across the continent. What a fascinating little enchantress! Had she fallen into Zhu Lian’s trap? Was Falling Cliff Mountain planning to completely sever ties with Qingfeng City? Zhu Lian was indeed a pivotal figure in Falling Cliff Mountain; even in the absence of the young mountain lord, he could make such decisive moves.

Li Jin’s mind was abuzz with speculations, yet he pretended not to recognize Zhu Lian. He returned to sipping his tea and reading, content to let the shopkeeper do the talking—buy if you wish, but if you want to bargain, then you can leave.

Perhaps the true wise person was someone like Li Jin, who saw through the facade but chose to keep silent, playing the fool.

Whether born as fortunate humans or as rare spirits that had finally learned to speak, they all had to learn the wisdom of silence in this world.

Zhu Lian snapped his fingers, and Pei Xiang immediately produced a small inkstone, engraved with the words “Mountain Lord.”

Then, Zhu Lian inscribed a series of characters and a seal in small seal script. 

“May stone endure ten thousand years, paper a thousand, human lives a hundred, but sincere hearts only a few.”

Zhu Lian’s personal seal bore the inscription “Silent Marquis.”

He took the inkstone and, having been fully briefed by Pei Xiang about how to unlock its spatial restrictions, felt confident. 

She also possessed another treasured item, a rare keepsake from the fox kingdom, considered her secret stash. Yet, Zhu Lian had no interest in it.

When a woman reveals her heart to a man, he should bear some responsibility if he has any decency. 

But Zhu Lian was precisely the kind of person who feared such obligations.

So, he felt no romantic inclinations towards this fox kingdom’s ruler.

Zhu Lian retrieved two meticulously painted scrolls and spread one of them on the counter. He turned to the Water God with a smile. “Shopkeeper, care to take a look?”

Li Jin rose at this, placing his teapot and books aside. The tea table already sported an exquisite bronze vase adorned with cloud and dragon motifs, its details rendered beautifully. 

Inside the bronze vase, a few branches of peach blossoms were arranged. 

Li Jin approached the counter with a knowing smile. “Dear guest, I’d rather not be mundane and buy this with money. How about we trade a book for a painting?”

Pei Xiang was seeing this painting for the first time, likely having seen it in a spice shop in Qingfeng City, casually crafted by “Manager Yan” during his leisure time.

She glanced at Zhu Lian.

Her bright eyes sparkled, filled with curiosity. 

Zhu Lian remained noncommittal to Li Jin’s suggestion and opened the second scroll.

The first scroll depicted a scholar riding a large carp, the fish barely showing its head and tail, while its massive body was enveloped in swirling clouds.

Zhu Lian had sealed it with small characters reading, “My heart is profound, a realm of Daming.” 

The other scroll was titled “Dragon Gate Overlooking the Rapid Stream,” featuring the scholar propping himself against a grand pillar of Dragon Gate, with characters stating, “Fish and dragon transform, out of this world.”

Li Jin’s smile grew wider. “Zhu Lian, my old friend, this is a masterful work.”

Zhu Lian nodded with a smile. “Li Jin, brother, you have a keen eye.”

Li Jin did not linger on the paintings for long and leaned against the counter. “Let’s get to the point—what’s the price? A good omen is worth its weight in gold. Just say the word, and I’ll negotiate.” 

Using the name Li Jin, he was truly the “Golden Carp.”

Zhu Lian patted Pei Xiang’s hand, signaling her to roll up the scroll carefully and tie it securely.

With a cheerful grin, Zhu Lian said, “We’ve done business for a long time, so today let’s trade a painting for a book, how does that sound?”

Li Jin glanced at the two scrolls, withdrew his gaze, and shook his head with a smile. “Let’s stick to the old rules; it’s best to keep things clear among close friends.”

Zhu Lian laughed heartily. “Then consider this a gift for my brother Li Jin!”

Only then did Li Jin nod, placing his hand on the scroll. “Thank you. From now on, your shop will offer a special discount of twenty percent on books for you, Zhu Lian.”

Pei Xiang, sharp as ever, immediately understood the deeper implications of their exchange.

Zhu Lian, acting as the chief steward, hoped to foster closer ties between Falling Cliff Mountain and the Water God of Chongdan River, mutual benefit through friendship.

However, Li Jin, in his role as the Water God, politely declined Zhu Lian’s proposal for an alliance.

Zhu Lian took a step back, and the two maintained their brotherly friendship, enjoying each other’s company without any ulterior motives.

It was a pleasant gathering, and they parted amicably.

Zhu Lian took Pei Xiang to Qidun Mountain, which lay adjacent to the scenic Red Candle Town.

While walking, Zhu Lian picked up a branch as a makeshift walking stick, resembling an old man more and more.

Pei Xiang casually asked, “If it weren’t for the ink outline, wouldn’t it be more fitting to paint that carp in a bright red color?”

Zhu Lian shook his head. “To put it this way, I know Pei Xiang is a fox spirit, but would it be appropriate to call you a ‘fox seductress’ right in front of you? Certainly not. If all goes well, Li Jin will add color to the painting himself—no need for anyone else to do it.”

Zhu Lian smiled and said, “Don’t believe me? Let’s make a bet. A small wager, a snowflake coin.”

Pei Xiang, uninterested in gambling, thought it pointless to wager on an outcome.

As they walked, not only Pei Xiang, as a Nascent Soul fox spirit, but all the earthly immortals of Baoping Continent could see the majestic golden lotus that covered the continent.

Baoping Continent resembled a treasure vase, blossoming a single lotus flower.

Swaying gently in the spring breeze.

Such a spectacle was astonishing, even for Pei Xiang.

However, as time passed, it became less surprising to her, merely a rare beauty of the human world to admire.

On this journey home, Zhu Lian rarely took the time to appreciate the breathtaking scenery around him.

He simply inquired about the Flower God Temple and its officer, whether he truly managed the fragrance of flowers.

Pei Xiang dismissed the matter, seeing him merely as a martial arts master. 

Zhu Lian was reluctant to share any deeper insights, knowing that a pleasant gathering does not guarantee a pleasant farewell. Whether it ends well or poorly is not solely his concern; human hearts are as fragile as shattered glass.

Unless the young master is at the mountain top.

Zhu Lian chose a secluded path on Qidun Mountain, remembering how Pei Qian and Zhou Milu often took this route when waiting for the young master. He believed that during that time, Pei Qian had frequently practiced her crazy sword techniques here.

Years away from home had brought significant changes.

For instance, he learned in Red Candle Town that a new mountain god temple had been established at Qidun Mountain, while Falling Cliff Mountain had lost one mountain god in return.

The mountain god temple on Falling Cliff Mountain had been relocated to Qidun Mountain, maintaining its rank, appearing to be an official transfer, but it was essentially a demotion.

Without a plaque or deity statue, the structure remained intact.

This move indicated a tacit understanding between Mountain Lord Wei Ban and the Great Li Dynasty.

Mountain God Song Yuzhang showed no resentment, as if he had anticipated this day. 

In fact, before the relocation, he had taken his first stroll outside the temple, which had long been devoid of incense offerings, exploring Falling Cliff Mountain. He seemed to embrace a sense of lightness, as if he had shed all burdens.

Zhu Lian could empathize with Song Yuzhang. But since each served their own master, there was no need for friendship. Yet, Zhu Lian never hindered Pei Qian and the others from visiting the mountain-top temple.

Aside from the matter of the mountain god temple, Zhu Lian received congratulations from Li Jin, the Water God of Chongdan River.

The great python from Huang Lake had actually dared to leave the mountain and enter the river. Since Li Jin offered his congratulations, it was clear that the woman in the yellow robe had successfully traversed the waters.

Li Jin had been cautious, only whispering this matter to Zhu Lian in the bookstore.

Meanwhile, Pei Xiang, as a genuine Nascent Soul cultivator, could still sense things from afar, even from the borders of Longzhou. She quickly soared to a high point, gazing at the dramatic changes in the river trade of Longzhou, asserting that a great creature was indeed moving through the water.

Feeling the journey was dull, Zhu Lian decided to share this information with Pei Xiang, providing her with a clearer picture than her wild guesses about the water dragon’s origins. Pei Xiang, soaring in the skies, had utilized her ability to observe the mountains and rivers. Even though the confluence of three rivers was teeming with energy and spirits employing illusion techniques obscured her vision, she determined that the impressive creature moving through the water must be a revered guardian of Longquan Sword Sect, otherwise, how could it navigate the waters so smoothly? The floods were raging, yet it seemed as if local water gods were aiding in its passage to avoid flooding the shores and harming the people.

For ordinary scholars on the ground, the torrential rains in the expansive territory of Longzhou merely made the daytime appear dark as night, with rivers surging violently.

But for the cultivators on the mountain, it was a grand spectacle of a water dragon transformation.

Since Pei Xiang had already mentioned it and they were nearing home, Zhu Lian no longer concealed the truth. “Her name is Hongxia; she has been cultivating on a subordinate mountain of Falling Cliff for quite some time now, so she’s practically family to you. Since you are both women, if you get along, you can visit each other often. Falling Cliff Mountain has no taboos about small mountains; everything is laid bare on the table—there are simply distinctions in closeness.”

After all, the mountain rules were few, and even Milu could recite them fluently.

Pei Xiang was slightly taken aback and complained, “You didn’t think to mention such a significant ally beforehand?”

A Nascent Soul water dragon! 

She could easily be regarded as a half-Yu Pu realm Qi practitioner! 

This powerful water dragon, born with a resilient body and innate abilities, who among the Nascent Soul cultivators, aside from sword cultivators, would dare to provoke her?! Especially those celestial sects near large rivers; if enmity arose, it would be like receiving an invitation from the King of Hell—accepting would lead to death, refusing might lead to the same outcome.

If Xu Hun of Qingfeng City hadn’t already ascended to the fifth realm and was a formidable warrior renowned across the continent, Falling Cliff Mountain, with just this water dragon as their support and Zhu Lian, could have gone head-to-head with Qingfeng City.

“Hongxia can ease Pei Xiang’s worries a bit, at least.” 

Zhu Lian smiled, merely mentioning it to Pei Xiang without elaborating further.

Coincidentally, back home, Hongxia wouldn’t even dare to speak a word at Falling Cliff Mountain.

If Zhu Lian remembered correctly, Hongxia hadn’t even seen the Hall of Ancestors on Jisefeng.

What worried Zhu Lian the most was actually Chen Lingjun wandering in the North Julu Continent.

Since no definite news had reached Baoping Continent yet, it meant that Chen Lingjun had not yet crossed the waters.

He didn’t care too much about the exaggerated outcome of Chen Lingjun’s journey compared to Hongxia; he was merely concerned that Chen Lingjun’s impulsive nature could lead to trouble while traveling alone. With her temperament, things wouldn’t be too bad back home, as she had already accepted her fate and would never cling to pride again, calling it “a matter of grievances in the world.” But out in the world, she would likely try to save face again.

Pei Xiang was in a good mood as she plucked a flower from a tree and handed it to Zhu Lian.

Zhu Lian waved his hand, chuckling, “The uglier the person, the more they love flowers. You keep it.”

In the past, it was customary for men to adorn themselves with flowers in the Lotus Flower blessed land. Otherwise, the practice would have faded with only the flower-adorned Zhou Shi remaining.

Pei Xiang shot him a glare but still pinned the flower in her hair.

Zhu Lian could fly with the wind, and Pei Xiang, being a Nascent Soul Earth Immortal, followed suit, paying no mind to the road beneath them. Zhu Lian led them to a secluded ridge on Qidun Mountain, already a distance away from the mountain temple where Song Yuzhang resided.

With his hands clasped behind him, Zhu Lian stood atop an ancient pine tree, a knowing smile gracing his lips.

He could see Falling Cliff Mountain.

Pei Xiang sat on a branch, gently holding the flower to her temple.

Zhu Lian sighed, “Which family dares hang a placard of ‘No Trouble’? As long as there’s tofu and vegetables in peace, one can eat and wear warmly, sleep soundly today, and rise easily tomorrow. That is peace in our mundane world.”

Pei Xiang teased, “It’s not that I’m boasting, but how can we consider ourselves mundane scholars?”

Zhu Lian looked up at the sky and murmured, “Even if only one is beneath another, everyone else is still mundane.”

In Zhu Lian’s old hometown, even if the younger Ding Ying had a slightly higher martial arts realm, in terms of mindset, it was another matter entirely. Ding Ying was born of a moment, rising with the tide; whether his fist techniques were good or not, in Zhu Lian’s eyes, they were mere trifles.

According to Pei Qian’s later accounts, Ding Ying couldn’t even compare to what Zhu Lian had achieved back in the day. Moreover, the path that the later demon Ding Ying took was essentially the one paved by the martial arts-obsessed Zhu Lian.

That high immortal crown was something Zhu Lian had casually tossed to the young Ding Ying.

Zhu Lian single-handedly defeated nine opponents, annihilating the world’s elite, none around him to contest.

Yet, he didn’t see it as any grand feat; he felt far from what he truly desired.

For instance, the elder of Falling Cliff Mountain had already reached the heights of Zhu Lian’s heart. Zhu Lian had to step forward, one step at a time, to see it clearly.

One of the three portraits hanging at Falling Cliff Mountain depicted the martial artist Cui Cheng.

And it was that same person who had brought the mad old man, who had been crazy for over a century, to Falling Cliff Mountain, stemming from that wandering monk who eventually blossomed with each step.

Pei Xiang pointed and asked, “Is that Falling Cliff Mountain?”

Zhu Lian nodded, “Water surrounds the mountains, and mountains encircle the water. Among them, the most majestic and profound is my home.”

Pei Xiang joked, “How sentimental! Are you good at making sour fish soup?”

After all, Zhu Lian had once joked, proclaiming himself the best chef, claiming his fist techniques were decent and his skills in music, chess, calligraphy, and painting were passable.

Zhu Lian laughed heartily. “Pei Xiang, you mentioned this, so let me remind you—at Falling Cliff Mountain, aside from the young master, no one should discuss sour fish soup, or it might get recorded in the accounts.”

Under the splendid starry night, the two resumed their journey along the path of Qidun Mountain. Zhu Lian moved slowly, practicing his stances, while Pei Xiang, with nothing to do, gazed at the scenery.

They finally reached the last high slope of Qidun Mountain, where Zhu Lian stopped, looking into the distance, feeling suddenly contemplative. “Awakening from a dream is like jumping off a cliff.”

Pei Xiang asked with a smile, “Why’s that?”

Zhu Lian shook his head. “No answer.”

Pei Xiang didn’t ponder this remark deeply.

Zhu Lian’s occasional words were often peculiar, leaving others puzzled.

She couldn’t help but recall the water dragon now sharing her realm. “That great python’s journey is remarkable. Is it because your Longzhou has a good name?”

Zhu Lian replied, “No matter how good the name Longzhou is, it pales in comparison to my young master’s name.”

Pei Xiang raised a finger, gently rubbing her forehead, feeling a headache coming on.

Zhu Lian, oh Zhu Lian, if you keep this up, I might start to suspect something.

Zhu Lian muttered to himself, “The dog looked at him, he looked at me, I looked at the heavens—could this really be? I’m becoming increasingly uncertain.”

Quickly, he added, “Just a fool’s musing, Pei Xiang need not mind.”

Pei Xiang asked, “If I ask you and you answer, wouldn’t that be a confirmation of your truth?”

Zhu Lian shook his head, expressing his feelings. “How could I know whether you’re true or not? Asking is pointless, and answering is just the same.”

Pei Xiang felt a flicker of annoyance.

Yet, she also felt a sense of relief; Zhu Lian’s candidness showed he no longer regarded her as an outsider.

Pei Xiang inquired, “Then who can provide you with an answer?”

Zhu Lian raised a hand to the heavens and pointed into the distance, finally clapping his hands gently. “The sun and moon in the sky, the word ‘brightness.’ My heart shines bright, a good person. If this person tells me the answer, I shall believe.”

Zhu Lian shook his sleeves and self-deprecatingly said, “Don’t worry; I seldom feel this way; it’s merely the nerves of returning home.”

Pei Xiang felt a bit flustered.

Perhaps a person who thinks this way is quite curious and very lonely.

Zhu Lian had already collected his thoughts and continued on the path.

Once, he traveled alone across his homeland, donning a starry robe. 

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 839: Jia Sheng Disappoints (Part 2)**

Under the night sky, Ruan Xiu stood by the banks of the Jade Liquid River. 

In this temporary spot for recuperation and stabilizing her cultivation, Hong Xia immediately activated her divine powers, hastily surfacing and landing to meet Ruan Xiu. 

Before her transformation into a water serpent, Hong Xia had been trembling with fear in front of Ruan Xiu. After her successful transformation, however, she was even more lost in thought, unable to control herself. 

Thus, the initial joy that had bubbled up in her heart upon successfully transforming into a serpent had at least halved. 

The water goddess of the Jade Liquid River hesitated, her demeanor timid. Moments after Hong Xia appeared, she too came to pay her respects to Ruan Xiu. 

Ruan Xiu glanced at the two of them—one a transformed water serpent, the other a formally recognized water goddess. She said nothing, simply nibbling on a piece of sweet peach blossom cake. 

The section of the Jade Liquid River had long been cleared of all river officials and water spirits by the water goddess, fearful of inadvertently offending the young woman with the ponytail standing before her. 

Previously, having received Ruan Xiu's "imperial edict," the woman in yellow had anxiously chosen a water source during the torrential rain that night, revealing her true form and beginning her journey through the waters. 

At present, the only three places in Longzhou that could be considered as celestial mountains were Longquan Sword Sect, Piyun Mountain, and Luopoc Mountain. 

Therefore, this journey through the water had gone so smoothly that the woman in yellow, now known as Hong Xia, felt as if she were dreaming. 

First, she emerged from a source stream, where the river goddess of Longxu River, the Horse Orchid, had no temple or incense offerings to honor her. The river goddess had only dared to flatter her as she helped contain the floods. Then, she passed through the Iron Talisman River, where the first-rate river deity of Great Li, Yang Hua, was stationed. Though she did not reveal herself, she still suppressed the water's momentum. After that, she traversed a short stretch of the Embroidered River, and finally, she went upstream against the treacherous and wild Chongdan River, where both river deities acted like guardians, ensuring Hong Xia's safe passage. 

Ultimately, she could reach a natural water cave rich in spiritual energy along the Jade Liquid River to heal her injuries. 

It was the water goddess herself who personally invited the "Daoist Hong Xia." 

The water goddess of the Jade Liquid River truly envied the opportunities this great serpent had. 

Conversely, she felt that, far from attaining any great fortune or blessings, she seemed to only attract calamities and misfortunes. 

The woman in green remained silent, and both Hong Xia and the water goddess fell silent as well. 

Ruan Xiu, eating her cake, glanced at Hong Xia and remarked, “Not a pretty sight. No wonder you lost to a little loach.” 

Hong Xia cautiously stole a glance at Ruan Xiu's wrist, where a fire dragon coiled like a bracelet. 

What had once been a lifeless fire dragon now moved its eyes skillfully, locking onto Hong Xia. 

Hong Xia's heart jolted, and she quickly averted her gaze, struggling to steady her mind and prevent herself from instinctively taking a step back. 

The fire dragon was at least at the upper fifth realm—definitely at the upper fifth realm! 

Ruan Xiu seemed unaware that her leisurely consumption of the cake was a great torment for the two individuals before her, like fish frying in a hot pan, subjected to intense heat. 

Even if she realized it, she likely wouldn’t care. 

Ruan Xiu had just returned to the Haoran World, aided by a middle-aged scholar who had opened the door for her. 

Fearing her father would scold her for her recklessness, she came here to hide for a while. 

In a bad mood, she naturally couldn’t muster a pleasant expression for Hong Xia. 

Ruan Xiu gently shook her wrist, the fire dragon that had emerged in the outer heavens was exceptionally docile towards its master, continuing to slumber peacefully. 

The most ordinary mountain and marsh water spirits could count themselves fortunate for successfully navigating a great river, and with a good lineage, they might just gain some auspicious trait of the water dragons, such as dragon claws, scales, or whiskers. 

Just like the great demon of the yellow eel from Tongye Island, who had attempted to navigate the waters and become a dragon. Had it not been for the water goddess's numerous interventions, it would have already transformed into a dragon long ago. 

As for the water spirits that were originally of dragon lineage, they needed to traverse at least one great river to be recognized by the heavenly principles. This would not only grant them the true form of a dragon but also allow them to nurture a dragon pearl of their own. 

However, three thousand years ago, that calamity that had befallen all water spirits was seen as the end of true dragons, leaving only many illegitimate dragon descendants. 

With the great floods of the Haoran World being so sparse, there were only a few rivers, often densely populated with sects. Who would dare to act recklessly? Not to mention traversing tens of thousands of miles, even hiding in a secluded spot at the river bottom, seeking a place with rich water flow to make a nest, simply hanging a plaque of some dragon palace or water mansion would be considered a great fortune. 

Thus, successful navigation and dragon transformation of a great serpent had not occurred in three thousand years. 

All water dragons and countless water spirits wished to transform into dragons, but who dared to? 

Because no one could assure whether that nameless sword immortal who had annihilated true dragons would strike again. 

Until there was a dragon with pure white scales in Baoping Island that navigated through a great flood, truly returning to its dragon form. 

This little serpent, Hong Xia, was leagues away from that little loach from Niping Alley. Even the small creature that followed behind Zhi Gui during its navigation was still inferior. 

Ruan Xiu lifted her chin towards the surface of the Jade Liquid River and said, “You may all leave.” 

Both the water serpent and the water goddess felt like they had received a pardon. 

They immediately submerged into the water, exchanging a distant glance at the riverbed, both too timid to communicate with their thoughts, each feeling a sense of shared suffering. 

Ruan Xiu frowned, still gazing at the flowing river, and asked, “Is it beautiful?” 

An old boatman leisurely paddled down the river. 

Even from over ten miles away, Ruan Xiu's voice was clear to him. He made no reply, simply exclaiming in wonder. 

A young woman in a Daoist robe stood at the bow of the boat, looking at Ruan Xiu with a smile, “Miss Ruan, we meet again.” 

Ruan Xiu had previously thought well of He Xiaoliang, who had traveled through the Lihuzhou Cave as a Daoist disciple of the Divine Decree Sect, but now she felt less inclined to be friendly. 

The leader of the Qingliang Sect from Beiju Lu Island, He Xiaoliang. 

Next to her was a deer-riding goddess who had emerged from the mural city of the Skeleton Beach. 

She had received instructions to stand behind her master, He Xiaoliang, because earlier, just a glance at the woman in green had left her feeling uneasy. 

Not long ago, He Xiaoliang and the old boatman, who was half her senior, had received an exceptionally cryptic instruction from their master. 

There were only two tasks: one concerned Chen Lingjun, which had already been dealt with, and the other was for He Xiaoliang to return to Baoping Island to seek out the young loach from Niping Alley and the Ma Ku Xuan from Xinghua Alley. He Xiaoliang could also conveniently meet a certain senior brother. 

As for the old boatman, compared to that junior brother, he was more eager to visit Old Lady Gui in the Old Dragon City. 

Li Xisheng crossed the Middle Land Divine Continent, arriving outside the main gate of the Fulu Street in his hometown. 

After greeting his parents, he went to the small pond where his younger sister resided. 

Looking at a small golden crab inside, he smiled, “Don't say you're not afraid of thunder and lightning, even the Dragon King of the Sea can roam freely.” 

Zhu Lian and Pei Xiang walked out of the Chess Stone Mountain, still taking their time to return. Near the entrance at the foot of Luopoc Mountain, Pei Xiang spotted a little girl in black, arms crossed, clutching a green bamboo staff and a golden shoulder pole, standing straight and wide-eyed, as if she were a little water spirit guarding the mountain gate. 

Pei Xiang couldn’t help but chuckle, “You really are...” 

Unsure of how to describe the mountain winds of Luopoc Mountain. 

Zhu Lian introduced, “She is our right protector here at Luopoc Mountain.” 

Pei Xiang laughed out loud. 

Zhu Lian added, “I’m not lying to you; Xiao Mi Li is indeed listed as our right protector in the Luopoc Mountain genealogy, sitting very close to the master’s hall on Jise Peak.” 

Pei Xiang remained skeptical, “Is that true?!” 

Zhu Lian chuckled, “By the way, when you meet Xiao Mi Li later, feel free to greet her outright with, ‘You are the legendary big water spirit of the Mute Lake,’ and she’ll be very happy.” 

He wiped away the mask on his face, returning to his usual appearance as the old cook of Luopoc Mountain. 

Pei Xiang also removed her mask, dispelling her illusion. 

Zhou Mi Li rubbed her eyes and then dashed over to Zhu Lian, her voice choked with tears, “Old Cook! I thought you were lost and didn’t know how to get home! I didn’t dare to go to Hongzhu Town to pick you up…” 

The little girl was so distressed she could hardly speak. 

She didn’t care about any semblance of pride, accidentally admitting that she was afraid to go to Hongzhu Town and the Jade Liquid River. 

Zhu Lian reached out to ruffle Xiao Mi Li's hair, shaking the large package on his back, and smiled, “Guess what’s inside.” 

Xiao Mi Li wiped away her tears, cautiously glanced at the woman next to the old cook, pursed her lips tightly, and offered a respectful bow to Pei Xiang. 

Pei Xiang nodded with a smile. 

Just now, she had been so focused on whether the old cook was fatter or thinner that she hadn’t noticed how exceptionally beautiful this sister was. 

Pei Xiang recalled Zhu Lian's reminder and smiled, “You are the big water spirit of Mute Lake?” 

Zhou Mi Li froze on the spot, unsure whether to scratch her face or her head. 

Oh? 

This sister suddenly looked even more beautiful. 

Perhaps this is what Pei Qian meant by “girls become more beautiful as they grow up”? 

Sigh, what’s so good about growing up? But Xiao Mi Li wouldn’t dare to say this to Pei Qian. 

Zhou Mi Li recalled the old cook’s question and whispered, “Is it that kind of immortal book Pei Qian mentioned? With pictures of little figures that can fight? It's a pity Pei Qian doesn’t want to say more. Can I take a look? I love reading now; I’m learning a lot. Hehe, when Pei Qian comes back home, she’ll be in for a big surprise.” 

Zhu Lian's face flushed with embarrassment, and he helplessly replied, “It’s just sunflower seeds.” 

Zhou Mi Li sighed dramatically, sounding wise beyond her years, “You’re already grown up, and you’re still munching seeds?” 

However, the little girl quickly smiled, “Well, I bought them, so let’s just go with it!” 

Zhu Lian nodded with a smile. 

The long-lost winds of home finally felt more than just a distant memory. 

I have returned home, here amidst these mountains. 

A little water spirit seemed to transform into a small yellow oriole, flitting around Zhu Lian, chattering about family matters.
