There were some things she couldn't mention, so Xiao Mi Li kept them to herself. Among the clever spirits of Luopoc Mountain, Pei Qian ranked first, and she was second; even Sister Warm Tree could only come in third! 

Pei Xiang found it utterly absurd and couldn’t help but inquire with her mind—was that little water spirit really the right protector of Luopoc Mountain? 

The protective positions for the sects and celestial caves among the mountain homes carried immense weight, recognized as half of the mountain water formation by the genealogical celestial masters. 

Pei Xiang was certain this little water spirit’s realm was not just low; it was quite absurdly low. If this little girl was already a right protector, could it be that Hong Xia was the left protector? Or perhaps the chief offering of Luopoc Mountain? 

But Zhu Lian, utterly indifferent, continued to engage in trivial talk with the little girl. 

Pei Xiang found herself both amused and frustrated. 

No wonder you’re called the old cook. 

Just as Pei Xiang felt a hint of gloom, it quickly turned to horror. 

A handsome young man in white appeared out of nowhere, smiling at Zhu Lian, “You’re really getting into the swing of things, aren’t you? How many years has it been?” 

Pei Xiang thought this person was as handsome as a jade mountain. 

In her eyes, he was only slightly less attractive than Zhu Lian. 

The Mountain Lord Wei Bo! 

Within the northern land of the continent, he was the foremost deity respected by all. 

Zhu Lian sighed, “It’s been so long since I’ve been back home; I really miss you, Wei brother.” 

Wei Bo smirked, “Oh, spare me.” 

You reap what you sow; Zhu Lian immediately rubbed his hands together, “The Mountain Lord’s abilities have skyrocketed; we should all celebrate together. Once the chaos is over, let’s have a night banquet in good order!” 

Wei Bo ignored Zhu Lian, simply nodding at the ruler of the Fox Kingdom. 

He could roughly guess Zhu Lian’s schemes. Quite the rascal. With this one move, Zhu Lian had effectively cut off half of the Xu family’s income in Qingfeng City. 

Pei Xiang hurriedly offered her respects to the Mountain Lord. 

Graceful and charming, it wasn’t that she intended to be so. 

Little Mi Li joyfully shouted, “Mountain Lord Wei! Mountain Lord Wei! Mountain Lord Wei!” Usually, she would only call out twice, but today, she was especially happy, so she shouted an extra time. 

Wei Bo understood, slightly bent down and opened his palm. 

Little Mi Li dropped a large handful of sunflower seeds. 

Wei Bo thanked her, naturally munching on the seeds while communicating serious matters with Zhu Lian through thought. 

Pei Xiang watched, her eyelids twitching. 

When Zhu Lian heard what Wei Bo had to say, he scoffed, “That little brat saved his own life.” 

The remnant of the Zhu Ying Dynasty that had come to seek refuge at Luopoc Mountain had also received a secret decree from the Great Li. However, he had not gone to the Ascension Platform, and the young sword cultivator had effectively forfeited an enormous opportunity. 

This was undoubtedly a sign from Emperor Song of the Great Li to Luopoc Mountain. We are aware of this person's origins, yet are still willing to let bygones be bygones. The pursuit by the Ministry of Justice will cease. 

Zhu Lian was quite satisfied with that stray dog’s decision, which was indeed wise. Having been granted a place to take refuge at Luopoc Mountain, one should be content. If he were to take advantage of Luopoc Mountain and mistakenly believe that a one-time life-saving talisman could serve as a permanent shield, then Zhu Lian would surely stick a death talisman on his corpse. 

Otherwise, once he returned to Luopoc Mountain, Zhu Lian’s second order of business would definitely be to question him. 

And when Zhu Lian questioned someone, it was a matter of life and death. 

As for the first order of business, it was, of course, to send sunflower seeds to Nuanshu and Mi Li, and then prepare a grand feast of seasonal mountain delicacies. After that, he would take off his apron and go question him. 

Zhu Lian raised his head. 

Then Pei Xiang saw a young man in a blue robe slowly walking down from the mountain, his smile gentle. 

Zhu Lian froze for a moment. 

He cast a glance at Wei Bo. 

Wei Bo intentionally kept quiet about this person; after all, Zhu Lian had returned home, so he might as well go see for himself. 

Having secretly plotted in Qingfeng City for all these years, Zhu Lian had refrained from any correspondence with Luopoc Mountain, just in case he lost everything at the last moment. 

After all, that Xu family woman was no easy opponent. For instance, regarding the matter of quietly gathering literary talent through the Fox Kingdom, Zhu Lian had already noticed traces of it, yet Pei Xiang still hadn’t confided in him. 

So Zhu Lian truly didn’t know this person’s identity. 

He could only tell that the other person was a sword cultivator of no low realm. 

Mi Yu communicated with Zhu Lian through thought, “I’ve met the steward. I come from the Sword Qi Great Wall, Mi Yu, with ‘Mi’ as in rice and ‘Yu’ as in wealth, a Sword Cultivator at the Jade Purity Realm. At Luopoc Mountain, Brother Zhu calls me Yu Mi.” 

Zhu Lian clasped his fists with a smile, “Brother Yu, you’re quite gallant, adding much color to Luopoc Mountain.” 

Yu Mi quickly returned the gesture, saying, “I dare not claim such praise.” 

Wei Bo smiled, amused. 

Zhou Mi Li winked at Yu Mi, then subtly leaned backward, glancing at the package on the old cook's back, signaling Yu Mi that the old cook had bought a large quantity of sunflower seeds today. 

Pei Xiang felt somewhat out of place and was shocked by the “Brother Yu.” 

The aura of sword qi was overwhelming! 

Of course, it wasn’t that Yu Mi was trying to show off his realm. 

Such things were far too trivial. 

In reality, Yu Mi had just returned from the Old Dragon City not long ago, and the residual killing intent mixed with sword qi had yet to dissipate. 

He was merely revealing his aura naturally. 

This was still the result of Yu Mi deliberately suppressing the sword intent. 

Besides Yu Mi and Zhu Lian returning to Luopoc Mountain, there were others who were on their way. 

Zhong Qiu and Cao Qinglang had finally returned from their long journey to Baoping Island, traveling from the north via the intercontinental ferry of the Pi Ma Sect. 

Returning directly from the Middle Land Divine Continent to Baoping Island was not feasible without an intercontinental ferry, and the journey was too treacherous. 

Master Zhong had taken Cao Qinglang on a detour through the White Frost Continent, heading to Beiju Lu Island, and then took the ferry south to return home. 

Another group included Sui Jingcheng and his senior brother Rong Chang from the Floating Duck Sword Lake, who were traveling back from the southern part of Baoping Island and would pass by Luopoc Mountain again. 

During their journey, they specifically ran to the Old Dragon City to find their master, Li Cai. Li Cai had not allowed his senior disciple, Rong Chang, to remain on the battlefield, stating that if she were to die, the Floating Duck Sword Lake would be bullied half to death. Thus, Rong Chang should not join the fray; anyway, the Floating Duck Sword Lake had its sect master to support them, and it was not worth bragging about; they certainly wouldn’t be humiliated. 

At this moment on the mountain, outside the bamboo tower, the sword cultivator Cui Wei, who was training at the Sword Offering Platform, was preparing to descend. 

He was going to bid farewell to his sword immortal senior brother Yu Mi and also see the one practicing talismans, Jiang Qiu. 

Cui Wei had also visited the Ascension Platform. 

He was already a Yuan Ying sword cultivator. 

Now, Wei Bo, the Mountain Lord of the North, was relatively free not because he was slacking off but because, during those recent battles after the celestial doors opened, he hadn’t needed to lift a finger, simply reaping the benefits. It was likely that upon reuniting with the Zhongyue Mountain Lord Jin Qing, the latter would have quite a few words to say. 

Zhu Lian gathered Wei Bo, Yu Mi, and the accountant Wei Wenlong together to discuss serious matters. 

There were far too many things to discuss, and not a single one was trivial. 

Even the arrangement of the Fox Kingdom was not the most important matter. 

Pei Xiang followed the little girl in a pink skirt named Chen Nuanshu, together with that strange little Mi Li, to settle into a quiet courtyard. 

Pei Xiang felt complicated emotions, unable to sleep at night, so she decided to leave her residence for a walk and sat on the steps at the mountain peak. 

She felt that her current mood was overly unreasonable. 

Before reaching Luopoc Mountain, she was afraid the family’s foundation was too thin, but after arriving, strange events unfolded one after another, leaving her dazzled and inevitably anxious. 

Then Pei Xiang noticed that Zhu Lian seemed to have finished discussing things and was currently accompanying Cen Yuanki down the mountain. 

Zhu Lian discovered that Cen Yuanki had made significant progress in her fist techniques, having learned from Liu Shiliu’s guidance. 

Zhu Lian urged Cen Yuanki to continue her training on the platform while he hurried ahead to sit next to Pei Xiang. 

Zhu Lian spoke softly, “Are you just realizing that you’ve found yourself in a foreign land? It’s all right; you’ll get used to it soon.” 

Pei Xiang quietly asked, “Yan Fang, have you been secretly mocking me in your heart as a frog in a well?” 

Zhu Lian laughed, “How did you become so sentimental? In my impression, the ruler of the Fox Kingdom in Qingfeng City is a heroic woman—clever and decisive, and quite beautiful.” 

Pei Xiang sighed, “I wish I had never met you.” 

Some women’s emotions are genuinely irrational. 

When their mood is good, everything is fine. When their mood is poor, everything is bad. 

The latter often comes suddenly, catching men off guard. 

So don’t listen to her specifics; whether they’re fragmented grievances or inexplicable angry remarks, don’t be anxious or throw yourself into chaos; just consider it an unarguable truth and listen well. 

Once you become impatient or try to reason with her, what can be done? It’s all ruined. Even if you don’t speak, you must listen carefully and pay attention to her. 

Whether a man is willing to do this often reflects the true knot in a woman’s heart. 

However, who Zhu Lian was quickly caused Pei Xiang to smile. 

Cen Yuanki had stopped halfway down the mountain, collecting her fists. Upon seeing the warm scene on the steps, she admired Zhu Lian even more. Just returning home, he was already caring for guests at Luopoc Mountain. 

If the young mountain lord were sitting beside that woman, Cen Yuanki would likely worry about Pei Xiang's situation. 

What if it was that mountain lord? With improper eyes and a penchant for drunkenly wandering at night, he loved to ignore everything and embark on solitary journeys, leaving Zhu Lian to work tirelessly. 

Meanwhile, Cen Yuanki diligently practiced her punches every day, and no one could find fault with her. Moreover, perhaps next time they crossed paths, the gap in their fist techniques would close considerably. 

In the small town under the heavy night, Yang’s pharmacy. 

The long-lived friend left the Dragon Riding Alley and came here at night, gently knocking on the door. 

Having recently returned from a place of ancient battle to temper his martial arts, Su Dian and Shi Ling Mountain had already returned from their travels, continuing as unremarkable shop assistants. However, Shi Ling Mountain resided in Peach Leaf Alley, while only Sister Su Dian stayed here. 

Su Dian had received instructions from her master to open the door for a certain woman. 

The long-lived friend went to the backyard. 

Su Dian simply moved a stool to sit at the entrance. 

In the backyard, the long-lived friend bowed deeply to the elder. 

Performing the junior's etiquette, she didn’t even sit down. 

She inquired whether the shop needed any golden coins or copper money. 

After all, the great war was in full swing. Outside the Old Dragon City, while the battles were not as fierce as in Old Dragon City, there was still smoke and chaos everywhere along the coastal battlefront. 

Old Yang shook his head, “Your good intentions are appreciated. It’s not easy for you to accumulate that little fortune, so keep it well.” 

The reason he was willing to converse with her a bit longer wasn't just due to her sincere heart but also because of their connection with the divine way. 

The long-lived friend was about to take her leave when the elder suddenly asked, “Have you noticed the hidden thread on that Shi Rou?” 

The long-lived friend shook her head, “I have not discerned it.” 

Old Yang replaced his old smoking pipe and lightly tapped the steps before packing the tobacco, “In the ancient Shu region, there are many extraordinary people. The legacy of that Shi Rou is merely one among them. At first, it wasn’t noticeable, but as time passes, it becomes more apparent.” 

The long-lived friend found the Baoping Island intriguing; Luopoc Mountain had a rich collection of books, and she often browsed through them. She recalled seeing something mentioned in a book about the eight hundred immortals of ancient Shu. 

The elder continued revealing secrets, “She has some connection with that Bai Yu Jing’s three teaching masters, a tenuous bond. As for when it might lead to the lotus flower and the root, it depends on her mood and whether she wishes to return to her true homeland to meet her senior brother.” 

The long-lived friend listened quietly, silently noting it in her heart. 

Old Yang suddenly said, “Wild cats roam freely at night.” 

The “childhood companion” of Ma Ku Xuan surely had a far more significant background than Shi Rou's little legacy. 

Old Yang pointed to the long bench under the eaves across from him, “Sit down. Let’s chat casually.” 

The long-lived friend complied and sat down. 

Old Yang fell silent for a long while before slowly speaking, “In such a small place, there’s nothing more intimidating to outsiders.” 

For the past sixty years. 

Cui Zhan and Qi Jingchun, this pair of sworn enemies for all to see. Cui Zhan’s betrayal was true, and destroying his teacher and ancestors was one thing. 

The literary saint, the old scholar, Jun Qian, and Liu Shiliu. Along with Chen Ping’an, the lineage of the literary saint is only missing one who hasn’t appeared here yet. 

The most accomplished in the world, Bai Ye. 

The three masters of Bai Yu Jing, Lu Shen, are here to set up shop for divination, while the Yin-Yang master Zou Zi is here selling candied haws. 

The Heavenly Lord Xie Shi. 

Ruan Qiong and Ruan Xiu, Li Er and Li Liu, two pairs of father and daughter. 

Cao Xi and Cao Jun, a pair of grandfather and grandson from Niping Alley. 

“Blind Daoist Jia Sheng,” Zheng Ju Zhong of Baidi City, another pair of master and disciple. 

One of the avatars of the Daoist elder, Li Xisheng. 

In the past, there was Song Changjing of the White Dragon Fish Garment. 

Mo Jia’s Xu Ruo. 

Just a few steps away from entering the town is A Liang. 

Like the maid from Niping Alley, Zhi Gui, who steals light through the wall. 

The first upper fifth realm mountain lord of Baoping Island, Wei Bo. 

Sword cultivators Jiang Shangzhen, Yu Mi, Li Cai… 

And of course, lastly, the ancient sword hanging beneath the bridge. 

For those cultivating on the mountain, sixty short years is nothing. 

Thus, if one’s luck falters slightly, regardless of who comes here, no matter how high their realm, if they act recklessly, they will find their lives hanging by a thread. 

Even if one is momentarily successful and makes an enemy here, with their lives temporarily safe, they must look ahead and be cautious. After all, the youngsters from Lihuzhou Cave, especially this generation of Chen Ping’an and Ma Ku Xuan, have ventured far, and their futures will not be small. 

Old Yang surprisingly smiled, “What an opening, truly magnificent.” 

The long-lived friend remained breathless and focused, listening but saying nothing. 

Then she turned her gaze. 

A weary young scholar appeared, carrying a bamboo box and a green bamboo staff, suddenly lifting the curtain. Upon seeing Old Yang’s rare smile, he burst into laughter, “Old man, look at you so happy, are you silly? Did you find a wife?! Old age is getting better, that’s quite something!” 

The long-lived friend was taken aback. 

The young man, unaware of her identity, could only clasp his fists and laugh, before scampering behind Old Yang and playfully wrapping his arms around the elder’s neck, “Do you miss me? Do you miss me?!” 

He had no idea that Old Yang could find such a beautiful sister. 

The long-lived friend was momentarily stunned and then suddenly laughed. 

She realized it was the famous Li Huai, who had a good relationship with his master since childhood. 

Old Yang let Li Huai act as he pleased, only saying, “You’ve come back.” 

Li Huai loosened his grip, plopping down beside him, gently patting his legs, complaining, “This trip was a good one, but it exhausted me. No fortune whatsoever.” 

Old Yang chuckled. 

The lazy Liu Xianyang rarely visited Luopoc Mountain. 

He didn’t come often. 

His riverside blacksmith shop was not close to the mountain. 

Liu Xianyang was so lazy that he hadn’t even visited the Ascension Platform. 

After all, he had been there many times in his dreams. 

Ordinary people shouldn’t bother Liu Xianyang with anything too shocking. 

Watching the little Mi Li sitting on a small stool, resembling a chick pecking at rice while dozing off, Liu Xianyang coughed lightly. 

Mi Li jolted awake, rubbing her eyes, and immediately stood up, laughing, “Old Sleepy has arrived!” 

The nickname “Old Sleepy” had been given to Liu Xianyang by Mi Li long ago. He nodded, then sat down beside her, grinning, “Little Mi Li, as the right protector, you sure are losing face by serving as a little gatekeeper.” 

Xiao Mi Li helplessly replied, “What can I do? Uncle Big Wind has gone far away, so I’m following my sister down the mountain. Sister Nuanshu is so busy every day, and I have so much free time.” 

Then the little girl quietly added, “When Pei Qian comes back and sees me guarding the gate here, I’ll get a hefty credit on the merit book, and I can’t escape it!” 

The little girl suddenly raised a fist, “Even if they run away, I’m not afraid; I can catch them in one go! Just like… Pei Qian pressing down on the left protector of Dragon Riding Alley!” 

Liu Xianyang crossed his arms. 

Xiao Mi Li asked, “What? Are you thinking of the good-natured mountain lord?” 

Think about it, think about it; it’s just right for both of us. 

Unexpectedly, Liu Xianyang smiled and shook his head, “Forget him; thinking about him is annoying.” 

Having just taken out a handful of sunflower seeds to treat Little Sleepy, the little girl silently put them back into her sleeve. 

How can you say anything? Think about it? Then just eat it. 

Little Mi Li gently shook her head. 

Liu Xianyang held back his laughter and asked, “Previously, your good-natured mountain lord often followed me like a shadow, going to the creek’s edge, looking for a narrow water surface. I would jump first, then he would follow. Whoosh, I’d leap to the opposite bank, and then splash, he’d fall into the water. I’d laugh at him from the other side.” 

The little girl’s eyes widened as she shook her head vigorously, “Old Sleepy, you’re talking nonsense without a script. The good-natured mountain lord is amazing, amazing!” 

Except for not being able to recite poetry. 

Besides, if the good-natured mountain lord was Old Sleepy’s shadow, then what would that make her relationship with Pei Qian? Wouldn’t that lower her status? 

Liu Xianyang shrugged, laughing, “Little Mi Li, oh Little Mi Li.” 

The little girl giggled, “Old Sleepy, oh Old Sleepy.” 

Liu Xianyang gazed into the distance, looking at the bright moon, joking, “You should hurry up and find a wife, then have a daughter as cute as Little Mi Li!” 

Xiao Mi Li pondered for a moment, drawing a circle with her little head, “Generally speaking, it’s very difficult. But if I eat sunflower seeds, it’s not that hard.” 

Liu Xianyang muttered, “In the short pavilion and long pavilion, the long pavilion is even shorter. The pavilions stop and pause repeatedly, but the return path seems endless.” 

Xiao Mi Li’s eyes lit up, “Old Sleepy, you can recite poetry! Can I borrow it for a few days? I want to show off to Pei Qian later. Once I’m done showing off, I’ll definitely return it to you.” 

Liu Xianyang smiled, “Of course, you can.” 

Then, the two of them, one big and one small, looked at the round moon, each thinking of someone far away. 

**In the central region of the Golden Armor Continent.** 

Pei Qian stumbled upon a mud-streaked little child on a battlefield that ended tragically. 

This child was the last elite border soldier of a great dynasty, and in an instant, the entire force of 160,000 was wiped out. 

Upon their first encounter, the child lay on the ground, first seeing a pair of tattered boots, soaked in blood, stopping not far from the child. 

Pei Qian reached out to pull the child from the heap of dead, but the child sat there, motionless, only staring intently at a young woman covered in blood, her face cracked and cheekbones exposed. 

The child’s eyes were lifeless. 

Yuan Jianfu approached Pei Qian, casting a glance at the pitifully thin child before saying to Pei Qian, “Thank you for that punch.” 

Pei Qian forced a smile and shook her head. 

Earlier on the battlefield, she had saved Yuan Jianfu from a distance with that punch, learned from the predecessor Lei Gong Temple, so Pei Qian didn’t think there was anything worth thanking for. If her master knew, wouldn’t that be a waste of a chestnut? 

A young man dressed in white, extremely eye-catching, stood alone on a hilltop. 

In the path of cultivation, there was a Daoist known as Dao Lao Er in Qingming, recognized as truly invincible across several realms. 

On the path of martial arts, this person also possessed a certain aura of invincibility. 

After all, before him, there was a master of a martial goddess waiting for him. 

Cao Ci could not only punch to kill enemies but could also strike to save others. 

Pei Qian could at most keep an eye on the safety of her sister Xi. This was still because Yuan Jianfu was fighting alongside her and not far away. 

But that Cao Ci could extend his reach to the battlefield far away. 

No wonder he was the only rival of her master in martial arts. 

When her master sought a rival, it was always formidable, just like her master. 

Even among the disciples of the foundation, it seemed he couldn’t stand out too much. 

Pei Qian spoke to the child, “Get up. When it’s time to feign death, feign death; when it’s time to rise, rise. After rising, bow your head; that’s how one can live long. If you stay here, dead means dead.” 

Pei Qian had actually noticed this strange child long ago, but she hadn’t had the chance to care for him earlier. 

This child was of the demon clan. 

However, on this battlefield, the “child” from the Golden Armor Continent had desperately protected someone. Unfortunately, that person he fought to protect was already beyond recognition. 

The child had only recently transformed into a human form, and due to a spell, he had suffered the cost of being severed from the Bridge of Eternal Life, so he hadn’t been feigning death on purpose but had fainted, waiting until he woke up to start pretending. 

In the end, the child got up and silently followed Pei Qian, limping along. 

Pei Qian walked quickly, and he kept pace; when she slowed down, he slowed down too. 

Yuan Jianfu did not hold back, speaking straightforwardly, “Pei Qian, I’ll say one more thing. You’ll have to fight by yourself and take care of a child; it won’t be easy.” 

Yuan Jianfu bore no prejudice against the child’s demon lineage. 

Pei Qian nodded, “It’s hard.” 

She turned to glance at the child, who had momentarily stopped in his tracks. 

It seemed that after the person died, the wild aura that had surrounded the child began to gather again, making him appear more like a mountain wild spirit, not very adept at concealing the essence of his demon race. 

The greatest sorrow is the death of the heart. 

Pei Qian halted, turned to face the child, and asked in the elegant language of the Golden Armor Continent, “Do you want to learn to fight?” 

The child remained unresponsive, just standing there. 

Yuan Jianfu furrowed his brow because he saw in the child’s eyes a deep-seated hatred, directed at both himself and Pei Qian. It seemed to extend towards the entire world and its laws. 

No reason, but this was the fact. 

The child gazed at Pei Qian, and finally willing to speak, extended a hand, his voice hoarse and unclear, as if he had been wounded at the roots of the great path, making it difficult to speak. 

Yuan Jianfu strained to hear, and the child said, “Lend me money, and I’ll leave. A life-buying price, I’ll pay it back later.” 

Pei Qian replied, “You can earn money by learning to fight.” 

The child’s expression remained impassive as he lowered his head. 

Yuan Jianfu felt somewhat helpless; Pei Qian and this child were on two different wavelengths altogether. 

At the Qinghu Palace on the peak of Tianque, the veteran Yuan Ying Lu Yong harbored thoughts of death and sought out the leading martial general among the accompanying soldiers, proposing to strike a deal with the Great Li Dynasty according to the mountain rules set by the national teacher. 

The robust martial general nodded, saying they could negotiate. He then immediately summoned two young secretaries from the Great Li to discuss the details with this old Yuan Ying from afar, bringing along a secret record detailing the information about the Qinghu Palace and Lu Yong. One of the secretaries advised the martial general that Lu Yong need not fight on the battlefield to earn military merits; alchemy would suffice, as it would be even more beneficial. 

The martial general frowned and asked directly the young official about how the alchemy could be converted into military merit, given that Lu Yong was putting his life on the line here to discuss this matter, so it required a detailed explanation. 

The young secretary quickly conferred with his colleague nearby and then spoke openly, providing the martial general and Lu Yong with a clear answer face to face. 

The young official spoke rapidly, his words precise, leaving no room for ambiguity. 

For instance, all the heavenly materials and earthly treasures needed for alchemy need not come from Lu Yong and the Qinghu Palace; they only asked that the Great Li not haggle over labor costs. 

For instance, if several alchemical methods from the Qinghu Palace could indeed have an immediate effect on cultivators and pure martial artists, as long as Lu Yong was willing to reveal them to the Great Li publicly, he could earn a considerable amount of military merit. 

The martial general merely interjected, assuring Lu Yong that if he was unwilling to provide the secret alchemical formulas, the Great Li would certainly not make things difficult for the Qinghu Palace and would not pursue the matter later. 

Lu Yong was overjoyed, suppressing his excitement as he agreed to everything. 

From start to finish, it took less than half an hour. Both the young secretaries provided Lu Yong with exceedingly detailed answers about where all alchemical cultivators from the Qinghu Palace should go and how to do it, the prices of various medicines, and how the conversion into military merit would be calculated. 

Once the discussions were concluded, the two young secretaries quickly departed. 

The martial general merely clasped his fists, exchanging no formalities with them. 

Lu Yong couldn’t help but feel emotional. 

The thunderous might of the Great Li border army was not only on the battlefield. 

The Great Li martial generals responsible for watching over the foreign cultivators displayed their cold eyes whenever they donned their armor and drew their swords, occasionally casting glances at those seemingly caged celestial beings. 

To negotiate a deal with this old Yuan Ying from Qinghu Palace as a Great Li martial general was merely part of his duties. 

In the Great Li border army, laws were strict; no one had the luxury to take them lightly. 

Those various rules, large and small, were ingrained in the bones of the martial men. 

The Great Li cavalry and the accompanying cultivators shared a brotherhood without distinction between those on the mountain and those off it; they were all martial men. 

However, since the deal had been struck, there was no need for much hesitation. The man revealed a smile before departing, and as he turned to the old cultivator, he solemnly clasped his fists, saying, “For an old man like you to be willing to die in a foreign land, the Tianque Peak Qinghu Palace, both I and my comrades will remember. What a few battlefield brutes remember is of little consequence, just a heartfelt word for the old man.” 

The man strode away, the sound of his armor echoing, leaving only the old man’s silhouette behind. 

Lu Yong couldn’t help but clasp his fists towards the retreating figure before reluctantly letting go, quickly turning away to attend to his duties! 

In the distance, at the Old Dragon City battlefield. 

An old monk from a large temple fought side by side with an unknown Taoist. 

The old Taoist opened a renowned work of calligraphy, “Chushi Tie,” which contained merely twenty-eight characters, yet had over one hundred seventy-two seals in later generations. 

Each character served as a talisman, launching golden-armored puppets against the demon army. 

This was indeed a genuine Jade Purity realm cultivator, yet he remained unknown in Baoping Island. 

The martial fortunes of Baoping Island were not inferior to the other seven continents outside of the Middle Land Divine Continent, and perhaps even more prosperous than the White Frost Continent. 

However, when it came to the number of local upper fifth realm cultivators, it was decidedly meager. 

The old monk hurled his monk’s staff, transforming it into a blue serpent. 

He removed his robe, which suddenly expanded like a vast cloud sea, shrouding dozens of miles of battlefield; upon that robe, it seemed there was a surface of water, lifting the wind with grace. 

The Emperor of the Great Li, during a past decree, had ordered the construction of temples across the continent. 

The Buddhist sect must reciprocate. 

Today, the old monk and the Taoist sat together on the cloud sea during a brief respite, hundreds of zhang apart, communicating through thought. The old monk chuckled, “Why have you come here?” 

“I’ve been idle in the mountains for too long, so I came down to take a look.” 

His place of cultivation was the once-mighty Bai Shuang Dynasty, similar in power to the former Zhu Ying Dynasty. 

However, during the Great Li cavalry’s invasion, the old immortal had not intervened. 

On the path of cultivation, one’s heart must be detached. 

Yet he was not a local cultivator of Baoping Island. He had traveled here and stayed for many years. 

The old Taoist finally smiled, “The grass outside the mountain grows year after year; whether I see it or not, it’s my business. Whether it flourishes or not remains my concern.” 

At the Old Dragon City battlefield, the head offering of the Fu family, sword cultivator Chu Yang, once sought assistance from Xu Ruo, only to reunite in a foreign land. 

This was to assure the wandering swordsman of the Mo family, who had long carried a sword behind him, that saving him had not been in vain. 

Hand in hand with the Sun family’s offering, 

Now the Old Dragon City has established a Fu family mountain and water formation as a barrier, and three large holes have appeared along this southern sea front. Chu Yang was responsible for blocking the invading demon army. 

Exhausted yet exhilarated, 

The mountain and water formation, acting as the core of the Old Dragon City, served not only to resist the demon army that continuously sent soldiers to their deaths, piling up corpses, but also to find those who could break through the formation independently among the upper fifth realm and earth immortals among the demon race for the Southern Mountain Lord Fan Junmao and other enlightened individuals. 

The Great Li’s airborne sword ship was tasked with an offensive against the barbaric world. 

Now, south of the Old Dragon City, it had become the barbaric world. 

In this realm, the Baoping Island blossomed with golden lotus flowers, forming a large formation. 

Moreover, the twenty-four solar term formations continued to circulate without error. 

Cui Zhan stationed at “Bai Yu Jing,” responsible for slashing the great demons. 

A woman sword immortal who had come from afar battled incessantly, wielding a sword without pause. 

Her previous sword, “,” had long since shattered and could no longer be used. The sword she held was one she had pulled from the Floating Duck Sword Lake’s treasury. 

As for the sword that served as the foundation of the mountain peak for the sword immortal, it had been damaged in two major battles in both foreign and native lands. 

This woman sword immortal, with a stunning glance, suddenly broke into a smile. 

Because a man, appearing out of thin air, sent a sword far away, slaying a Yuan Ying demon sword cultivator before fleeing, shouting back, “My lady, you’re especially beautiful tonight, most enchanting!” 

Li Cai laughed in reply, “Does the old lady need you to tell her if she’s beautiful?!” 

At the southernmost part of the Old Dragon City battlefield, Zhou Mi appeared alongside his direct disciple, the sword immortal Shou Chen, and Liu Bai, who had rushed over from the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

Along with the newly accepted disciple, who was not a sword cultivator, the wooden clogs of Jia Shen. Once a youth, now a young man. 

Shou Chen frowned, “In such a small Baoping Island, what extraordinary talents are there? The records of the past sixty years are all here; where did these unexpected occurrences come from? Did I miss something in the records?” 

Wooden clogs shook their heads, “Senior Brother did not miss any reports.” 

Zhou Mi smiled, “It’s my fault for being away from home for too long. Also, it’s Cui Zhan’s fault for plotting too much.” 

However, in his eyes, these so-called unexpected occurrences could all be traced. If an accident occurred, it could simply be smoothed over. 

In the history of the Haoran World, there was a saying: “All the schemes and strategies of the world converge upon Jia Sheng.” 

Wooden clogs were full of spirit, stating, “Xiu Hu Cui Zhan is indeed worthy of being the elder brother of the Hidden Official.” 

Zhou Mi laughed, “How much does Cui Zhan weigh? He won’t know until he dies.” 

Zhou Mi waved his hand. 

Moments later. 

On the vast and magnificent sea surface. 

The sound of thunder grew louder, shaking the heavens and the earth. 

It turned out that just outside the sea near the Old Dragon City, another layer of sea surged up to a height of over a hundred zhang. 

This was a divine water technique from the great demon, Fi Fei, who was now the ruler of the rivers in the barbaric world. 

She intended to flood the Old Dragon City! 

On the road north, numerous demon cultivators skilled in water techniques unleashed their divine powers or added spells, all contributing to the overwhelming wave. 

The monstrous wave crashed violently against the troublesome city at the southern tip of Baoping Island. 

On the Dragon Ascending Platform, Zhi Gui transformed into a beam of rainbow light, crossing the Old Dragon City formation and crashing into the sea. Before revealing her true dragon form, she had already killed countless demons within a radius of ten miles. 

Zhou Mi paid no attention to this, merely laughing with his gate-keeping disciple, wooden clogs, “Earlier, you said Cui Zhan is indeed worthy of being the elder brother of the Hidden Official; doesn’t that seem a bit off? It should be that the young Hidden Official is indeed worthy of being Cui Zhan’s junior brother.” 

Zhou Mi looked up, speaking through thought, “Does Xiu Hu agree?” 

The imposing Dharma form, high above the capital of the Great Li, with Cui Zhan cradling Bai Yu Jing, twelve flying swords hovering like sword ships in all directions, Cui Zhan replied nonchalantly, “Jia Sheng’s schemes are indeed disappointing.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 840: No Longer in a Dilemma

Zuo You arrived at a picturesque location adorned with clear mountains and flowing waters, holding a green bamboo staff as he ascended the mountain.

At the foot of the mountain stood a temple, while a Daoist temple crowned its peak, and a academy nestled halfway up the slope. Even if it wasn't within the celestial realms of the Haoran world, it was quite similar in essence.

Zuo You found himself in a foreign land known as the Feathered Ascension Paradise (Yuhua Fudi). With nothing pressing to do and feeling it inappropriate to move his physical body, he decided to send out his Yin spirit for a leisurely journey, taking the opportunity to explore the world’s scenic beauty.

The location he was exploring within this paradise was a revered site for cultivation, renowned as a celestial abode on earth, a must-visit for hermits seeking immortality, and a favored spot for good-hearted men and women to pay their respects and offer incense.

According to legend, this land was home to many immortals in ancient times. They practiced Daoist arts and magical techniques in the mountains, leading to the construction of the Emerald Pine Palace (Cu Song Gong) by imperial decree. Eventually, an immortal achieved enlightenment here, riding a blue dragon formed from an ancient pine tree, ascending to the heavens, a story known throughout the realm. Witnessing this auspicious event, the reigning monarch promptly changed the era name in accordance with heavenly will, establishing the Baoguang Temple (Baoji Guan) in the first year of Auspicious Clouds to honor the immortal's "Feathered Ascension." Over a century later, the dynasty changed, and the temple's incense offerings dwindled. The last documented return of this "immortal" to the mortal realm was when he used supreme powers to retrieve the Baoguang Temple, which had inexplicably sunk into the water, relocating it to the mountain's peak.

The subsequent emperors of the new dynasty hurriedly conferred titles upon the founder of Baoguang Temple – an immortal and true lord – bestowing ever-greater honors, further enriching the temple with plaques and Daoist scriptures, ensuring its lasting prosperity.

In later years, various theories emerged, firmly believing that this immortal, after ascension, not only joined the ranks of the celestial beings but was also granted a high rank by the Heavenly Emperor, akin to the position of the Minister in the human realm. As a result, wherever he went, the gods of mountains, lakes, and hidden sea immortals would come to pay their respects.

Zuo You was, of course, aware that these stories served to embellish the reputation of the paradise. The so-called "immortal" was merely an old cultivator from the Tongye Continent, who had served in the ancestral hall of a sect. He ultimately hit a bottleneck at the Nascent Soul stage, failing to break through for longevity. As time passed, he decayed in both body and spirit until he encountered a massive invasion from the barbaric world. Whether motivated by the belief that his time had come, or for other reasons, the old cultivator chose to die fighting on the battlefield against the demon race that invaded Tongye Continent. The Feathered Ascension Paradise did not escape its fate, falling into the hands of a military camp.

The paradise was supposed to be carried by a direct disciple of a sect to the Baoping Continent, to hand over this Feathered Ascension Paradise to the Old Dragon City, aiding their sect's cultivators in exchanging for a suitable cultivation site from the Great Li Dynasty. 

Feathered Ascension Paradise, vast yet sparsely populated, suffered from a thin spiritual energy; coupled with the sect holding the paradise being unwilling to spend money, it resulted in a historical lack of qualified cultivators. For the sect on Tongye Continent, it was merely a low-grade paradise, barely worth the effort. Spending a fortune on the paradise could disrupt the training of their own qi cultivators, ultimately proving detrimental. Moreover, a sect leader, even if already at the Jade Purity stage, could not claim to be an immortal, and with a limited lifespan, they would only see the immediate future, unable to foresee the potential benefits of enhancing the paradise in a millennium. The other elders in the ancestral hall, having even lower realms and shallower Daoist arts, would be even more short-sighted, unable to recognize the long-term advantages of improving the paradise. After all, what benefit would it be for them a thousand years hence?

However, for the Great Li Song Clan, it did solve some pressing issues, allowing for the relocation of the most southern vassal states' citizens conveniently. The low status of Feathered Ascension Paradise was actually advantageous, as it posed minimal risks; the conflicts between those on the mountain and the mundane folk below could almost be ignored. Settling the displaced persons would incur hardly any cost.

As for how the paradise ultimately fell into the hands of the demon army, Zuo You was not particularly interested. Whether driven by human greed or unforeseen events, it simply resulted in his current detention.

As a scholar-like man dressed in green with a bamboo staff, Zuo You was overlooked by the passing incense burners, as he was a common sight.

He stopped at a bustling vendor area halfway up the mountain, where a sign proclaimed, "Last Chance to Drink, Hurry Up!" 

It was a vulgar yet endearing sight. 

The vendor reminded patrons that sincerity was required when offering incense; for those who loved alcohol, it was best to quench their thirst here. Otherwise, after climbing high and drinking, if one appeared drunk to the celestial beings with opened heavenly eyes, it could invite displeasure, making one's wishes ineffective.

The path for burning incense up the mountain was filled not only with earnest worshippers but also many porters who earned their keep by carrying the incense bearers' luggage or hauling stones up the mountain to help accumulate materials for the construction of new buildings at the temple. The former made little money, while the latter earned more, but the labor was truly exhausting. Thus, some affluent incense bearers would allow the porters to rest here and treat them to a bowl of alcohol to bolster their strength and spirit.

Zuo You bought a bowl of loose wine, but the crowd at the stall took up several tables, leaving little room. Not wanting to squeeze in with others, he decided to move a bit further away.

Seeing a customer about to walk away to drink, the vendor quickly raised his voice, demanding a deposit first; otherwise, the customer couldn’t wander too far with the wine. 

If an unscrupulous drinker finished their wine and carelessly tossed the empty bowl off the cliff, it would be a headache for the vendor to seek compensation. 

Reluctantly, Zuo You returned to the vendor, paying extra before making his way to the railing at the cliff's edge, gazing at the distant mountains and waters, which undulated like a scene from a basin.

Earlier, the scholar Shoucheng "asked for the sword" at Tongye Sect, actively offering Tongye Sect a bright future. Regardless of the demon race's intentions, it was clear they aimed to turn misfortune into fortune for Tongye Sect. After all, that scholar who went by the name Zhou Mi had made his appearance; he was the second highest-ranking demon lord of the barbaric world, and his vows and promises held weight.

It should be noted that in the southernmost part of Tongye Continent, during the meeting at the Yu Gui Sect's ancestral hall, they rejected the proposal of a round-faced woman in cotton clothing, refusing to hand over the Cloud Cave Paradise controlled by the Jiang Clan. As a result, the demon army launched relentless attacks, not holding back in their efforts.

The irritable elder of the Yu Gui Sect cursed Jiang Shangzhen, calling him a harbinger of doom, while simultaneously slaughtering demon cultivators. 

He swore that if he met his demise, both Yu Gui Sect and Cloud Cave Paradise would be fortunate to survive, and Jiang Shangzhen would have to come to his grave to express gratitude, making sure to do so loudly, or he wouldn't hear it.

This seemed to be what they referred to as the cycle of fortune and misfortune. Those who enjoyed watching jokes often became the subject of such jokes.

For years, Yu Gui Sect had reveled in the grand spectacle of Tongye Sect's misfortune, and it appeared that now it was the Tongye Sect's turn to witness Yu Gui Sect's downfall. This opportunity was just within reach, enough to simply nod in agreement.

As long as the Tongye Sect's ancestral hall seized this opportunity, it was possible that in the future, they could directly swallow Yu Gui Sect, turning that rival into a subordinate sect, which was no longer a mere fantasy.

However, among the cultivators of Tongye Sect, the morale was fractured yet not shattered. The opinions within the sect were split evenly down the middle.

Zuo You was actually quite surprised; he had initially thought that the cultivators of Tongye Sect, regardless of age, would immediately turn against him, driving him out of their territory. To his astonishment, the younger cultivators, who were lower in rank and age, managed to shoulder the burden together, resolutely refusing the invitation from the barbaric world while even seeking out Zuo You, daring to say, "We sincerely ask Mr. Zuo to stay. You can leave everything behind to us."

Having lived for several more hundred or thousand years, the older cultivators still wished to prolong their lives, while the young ones, who had barely walked the path of enlightenment for a few years, were willing to face death.

In that moment, Zuo You felt as if the world was truly improving.

In the past, the circumstances rarely left Zuo You feeling unencumbered.

For instance, when encountering those arrogant sword cultivators who relied on brute strength and authority, Zuo You would feel troubled, unsure whether to kill them outright or merely incapacitate them. 

As long as Zuo You remained within Tongye Sect, with sword energy still present in Tongye Continent, he would be like a thorn in the side of the barbaric world that could not be expelled.

After Xiao Xian shattered the Flying Ascension realm and assumed the form of Xun Yuan, he went to the relatively stable Southern Posa Continent, intending to capture the sun and moon resting on Chen Chuan'an's shoulders while also stopping by to see Lu Zhi.

Therefore, the advice from the wooden clogs of Jia Shen suggested that the sword immortal Shoucheng be responsible for the implementation of plans, ultimately using a low-grade paradise with a total population of fewer than ten million to successfully detain Zuo You.

Though Shoucheng appeared to be questioning Zuo You about his sword, his true tactic was to suddenly open the heavenly restrictions of the Feathered Ascension Paradise, mercilessly crashing down upon Zuo You. At the same time, within the paradise, a despondent demon cultivator at the Jade Purity stage beckoned to Zuo You, indicating clearly that he could either join their ranks or watch helplessly as the paradise crumbled before him.

Simultaneously, Zhou Mi executed a grand plan to shift the heavens, causing Zuo You to be trapped within the paradise.

Zuo You did not allow the paradise to collapse within the territory of Tongye Sect. In addition to slashing at the demon race, he employed sword energy to traverse the celestial barriers, using his own sword energy as a great formation to protect the paradise.

Without hesitation.

Then Zhou Mi restored the original mountains and rivers, and Shoucheng immediately sealed the paradise's restrictions, isolating the large and small worlds, momentarily confining Zuo You there. He first rooted the paradise in Tongye Continent, aligning it with the overarching Dao of the barbaric world and ordered two demon lords at the celestial realm to continuously attack the paradise's barrier using spells and divine powers, collaborating with celestial arts to wear down Zuo You's sword intent and Daoist progress. They neither pursued the result of breaking the paradise nor allowed Zuo You to feel too comfortable within the Feathered Ascension Paradise.

In this way, even if Zuo You casually drew a sword, it would disturb the heavens and earth, allowing him to escape. However, if no one tended to the paradise, it would lead to chaos, resulting in countless deaths.

Once Zuo You stabilized the boundary of the heavenly barrier, he began to scrutinize the small paradise carefully.

With a body suffused with lofty sword intent, he was still far removed from the mundane world.

Zuo You wished to leave the paradise and return to the Haoran world of Tongye Continent, which was exceedingly simple; a single sword stroke could easily part the heavens, disregarding the life and death of the Feathered Ascension Paradise. It was not just Zuo You; even Jiang Shangzhen, with a single willow leaf, could achieve the same.

Thus, trapping Jiang Shangzhen in this place was utterly meaningless. Jiang Shangzhen would undoubtedly strike decisively with his sword, and once he did, not only would the paradise suffer millions of casualties, but it could even shatter completely, and millions of mundane folk would perish without a second thought. Jiang Shangzhen would not experience even a ripple in his mindset.

In the past, Jiang Shangzhen had nearly met his end in his own trap, questioning the rogue earth immortal causing trouble in the Cloud Cave Paradise; the death toll among the mountain folk and the mundane exceeded a hundred thousand.

However, Zuo You intended to remain here temporarily until he devised a solution that wouldn’t put him in a dilemma.

This left Zuo You's physical body completely immobile, as if he were in a meditative trance at his previous resting place. Zhou Mi's tactics were quite remarkable; before Shoucheng smashed through the paradise, he had long ago set a "Heavenly Edict" within the paradise, akin to "acting on behalf of heaven," specifically to suppress the sword energy of the mundane realm. Therefore, Zuo You could only send out his Yin spirit on a distant journey; otherwise, pulling a single thread would affect the entire body. The so-called heavenly laws here could not harm the sword immortal Zuo You in the slightest, yet they would cause trouble for the mortals below.

For instance, when Zuo You previously sliced through the demon race, he cleaved a massive chasm over ten thousand miles long in the sky above the paradise. This was still Zuo You exerting effort to guide his sword energy and the Dao's operation; otherwise, after slaying the demon, countless disasters would have befallen the mundane world.

That chasm, resembling a tear in the sky, hung like a long rainbow of sword energy in the eyes of the few cultivators who dared to tread the Feathered Ascension Paradise, shimmering beautifully, flowing eternally with the sword energy.

With Zuo You's overwhelming sword energy, invincible and lethal, he could only use it to maintain the boundaries of the heavens, preventing the demon cultivators' spells from recklessly breaking through the paradise's barrier.

Otherwise, if the celestial phenomena stirred even slightly, the common folk of Feathered Ascension Paradise would suffer all kinds of natural disasters, whether it be continuous torrential rain leading to floods, years of drought turning the earth barren, or heavy snow blanketing the entire winter, killing all living things.

Initially, Zuo You had suspected that within the paradise, there might be demons left behind as hidden threats, perhaps a high-ranking demon lord lying in wait. However, after several inspections of the heavens and earth, he found no such signs.

This was normal; in the face of such a great battle, if they shattered the paradise, leading to the mountains and rivers' destruction, it would mean Zuo You could completely break free from his restraints. At that point, it would not simply be a matter of Jiang Shangzhen wielding a willow leaf, poking and prodding; it would be far more complicated.

Having confirmed that there were no major hidden demons in the Feathered Ascension Paradise, Zuo You began to send out his Yin spirit on a distant journey.

Though named the Feathered Ascension Paradise, it was misnamed, merely the private property of a low-tier sect on Tongye Continent.

In ancient times, cultivators here had "ascended" after forming their Golden Core, but on the "other side of the sky" within Tongye Continent, as they navigated their cultivation paths, the sect had attracted attention. Even if the cultivators hid deeply, their homeland’s paradise was eventually noticed by the mountain's ancestors, who deduced its approximate location from various clues. After spending decades, they finally "fished" this small paradise from the long river of time.

After that, it was only natural that the gates opened wide, allowing the fallen immortals to descend, inspect the paradise, and plunder the earthly treasures that emerged, seeking suitable materials for cultivation.

Unfortunately, this paradise was too barren; the number of heavenly materials and earthly treasures that caught the eye was minimal, and so-called cultivation prodigies found themselves thin on the ground. Occasionally, one might emerge, nurtured with devotion, yet they often proved inadequate, at most achieving the Golden Core stage. For a sect of this tier, even possessing a paradise was a classic case of being unable to cover expenses.

As for the other mountain sects and affluent families, their travels through the paradise were limited by its quality and rank, ultimately leading to minimal gains. Thus, other sects on Tongye Continent deemed their investments in the Feathered Ascension Paradise a loss, and over time, it remained a low-grade paradise. All the sects aspired to upgrade their medium-grade paradises to high-grade ones, tirelessly spending heavenly resources, but upgrading low-grade paradises to medium-grade ones was not something they readily desired. Hence, there arose the saying, "A low-grade paradise is worse than having none."

In the hands of major sects, investments could yield long-term returns, turning losses into profits. However, many smaller sects with insufficient resources often suffered as a result, typically choosing to sell their paradises to wealthier sects.

The quality of a paradise was determined not only by its land and population but also by the amount of spiritual energy contained within. Otherwise, no matter how vast the territory or how populous it was, if the mundane folk were unsuitable for climbing the mountain to cultivate, and if the thresholds for cultivation were too high with significant bottlenecks, the cultivators would all remain at the lower realms, with even the Cave Dwelling realm being a luxury. Thus, the so-called "achieving Dao and becoming immortal" would merely be the first layer of the lower level, and the paradise would inevitably be rated as "low grade."

The Feathered Ascension Paradise's 36th generation Daoist at the Emerald Pine Palace and the first abbot of Baoguang Temple was a cultivation genius who gathered the world’s spiritual energy and merits in a low-grade paradise. Not only did he attain the unprecedented Dragon Gate realm, but he also successfully formed a Golden Core, thus gaining favor from the Dao of heaven and earth, allowing him to break through the skies and journey far.

Regrettably, the world is ever-changing.

For those born in a paradise, some fortunate individuals carrying the fate of heaven and earth, the rise of one immortal could spell the onset of calamities for the world.

This Feathered Ascension Paradise, fortunate among misfortunes, preserved itself and has yet to be destroyed. Many paradises in the history of the Haoran world have faced tragic fates due to someone “ascending” and inadvertently revealing their roots, failing to be taken in by a major sect, ultimately leading to the paradise's destruction and the extinction of its inhabitants. Many low-grade paradises have been thoroughly depleted by cultivators, completely severing the path for local cultivators to ascend.

Of course, low-grade paradises often flourished thanks to a single individual, rising amidst the Haoran world.

A beautifully dressed young woman, while her elders rested, took her maid beside her and, under the pretense of enjoying the scenery, approached the scholar in green who sat alone drinking wine. She lifted her veil slightly, revealing a rosy face, and softly asked, “May I ask where this young master is from?”

Zuo You turned to reply, “From a place that a young lady has never heard of.”

The young woman blushed even more, as red as rouge, and smiled, “If you say so, I would still know.”

Zuo You shook his head and replied, “Even if I told you, young lady, you still wouldn't know.”

In the past, Zuo You either ignored such encounters or merely answered a question.

However, after reuniting and parting with his teacher last time, Zuo You felt that perhaps he needed to change his temperament.

For instance, could he treat a young woman’s flirting as a serious "sword question"?

So today, Zuo You spoke a few more words than usual.

For some reason, the young woman felt embarrassed and annoyed, turning to leave. The girl beside her was even more furious, feeling that this scholar was too dull, wasting his good looks.

Well, that was the end of the "sword question."

Clean and straightforward, without dragging things out.

Zuo You turned and walked away, returning the empty bowl to the vendor, who muttered a few complaints about how a bowl of wine took forever to drink, wondering whether the scholar had come to burn incense or to swindle wealthy women.

Fueled by resentment, the vendor quietly grumbled, “You hear me, but no one else does. If you don’t have a broad mind, you’ll be ruining your own reputation. If it comes to fighting, you think you can handle me?!”

Ordinary scholars would simply let it slide, heading up the mountain to burn incense and avoiding trouble.

However, that scholar suddenly stopped and said, “Say that again.”

The vendor’s anger flared up, but after taking another look at the tall scholar before him, he reluctantly turned his gaze away, not daring to meet the fierce-looking man’s eyes, muttering, “Nothing, nothing, sir must have misheard.”

Zuo You extended his hand.

The vendor paused for a moment before remembering to return the coins Zuo You had previously advanced. After handing over the money, he continued to grumble, thinking, “What a miser!”

Zuo You continued his ascent towards the Emerald Pine Palace. The battle death of an old Nascent Soul cultivator in a foreign land seemed like a mere drop in the bucket against the grand tide of the Haoran world, but Zuo You did not share that sentiment.

In the past, the Confucian Sage's four direct disciples would ponder over seemingly trivial matters like this; Cui Chen would explore the subtleties of human nature, perhaps gleaning insights into someone or something, consuming months of time.

The large fellow was indifferent; when greater matters loomed, he felt that if he were to be provoked, one must be capable enough to do so, or it would all be meaningless. Xiao Qi might think more about local customs, yet Zuo You was determined to confront others directly, unwilling to relent until things were clarified. 

In his youth, Zuo You had suffered greatly because of this, leading his teacher to frequently leave the study, preoccupied with resolving the troubles he had caused. Especially after Zuo You turned to sword training, this tendency only intensified.

Whenever his teacher pulled Zuo You aside to apologize face-to-face, the old scholar would often lose his temper at his stubborn student, sometimes even delivering a slap to the back of his head, pressing him to lower his head and apologize!

Yet after each reluctant apology, once out of others' sight, his teacher would delve into greater principles and clarify where true right and wrong lay. The principles discussed would gradually distance Zuo You from petty conflicts, ultimately lifting his head higher and higher!

“Study more, read more! Don’t just practice swordsmanship; that will only lead to trouble! You must understand the teachings of the sages. In the future, when you draw your sword to pierce the sky, your teacher will help mend the heavens!” But until that day, he had to read more and use the Dao and the suffering of the world as a sheath for his sword; otherwise, how could his teacher trust him to train in swordsmanship without studying?

Upon reaching the summit, Zuo You beheld the Emerald Pine Palace, its green glazed tiles shimmering. However, this glaze was not made from celestial materials; it merely represented the favor of earthly emperors.

Zuo You did not approach the temple filled with incense offerings, instead choosing a quieter spot higher up to gaze into the distance.

It would only worry his teacher; he would not be the one to alleviate his teacher's concerns.

In this regard, it was clear that the large, foolish fellow performed best; not to mention Zuo You, even Xiao Qi could not match him. 

Not retaliating when scolded, nor striking back when hit, he remained close to his teacher, nearly never causing trouble.

Zuo You looked up, first frowning, then relaxing, stifling a laugh.

Someone had broken through the heavenly restrictions with a punch, scattering the sword energy barrier casually, leading Zuo You to initially think that a high-ranking demon from the Flying Ascension realm had arrived, naturally worrying for the safety of the paradise.

However, once Zuo You recognized the unexpected visitor’s appearance, his mood brightened. He subtly revealed a bit of his sword intent for the other party to see at a glance, simultaneously guiding the sword energy to obscure their presence, ensuring that they did not draw too much attention while traversing the Feathered Ascension Paradise.

Noticing Zuo You's sword intent, the visitor promptly restrained their aura and approached the mountain Zuo You occupied. Yet, even so, the ground trembled slightly beneath the heavy-set figure's feet, sending ripples through the pine trees, leading the incense bearers to mistakenly think an immortal had manifested. Many patrons, who had already left the Emerald Pine Palace, hurried back to offer their prayers.

Liu Shili smiled widely, “It took me a while to find you.”

Before coming here, Liu Shili had journeyed across continents to Tongye, first visiting the northernmost Tongye Sect without involving himself in their matters, only inquiring about Zuo You’s whereabouts. He then traveled south, learning from a sword cultivator named Zhou Fei, who called himself a disciple of the Fallen Mountain, that Zuo You was precisely detained within Tongye Continent. Prior to breaking down the door, he indeed encountered the so-called terrifying celestial "great demons" mentioned by Zhou Fei. Zhou Fei had advised Liu Shili to be cautious, as he had a good impression of Liu Shili; the reputation of Jiang Shangzhen, who wielded the willow leaf to slay demons on Tongye Continent, was already widespread, and now even Baoping Continent was discussing the new Yu Gui Sect leader's combat style with great admiration.

At the same time, the entire True Realm Sect's reputation was also rising alongside Jiang Shangzhen.

Liu Shili's only unfavorable impression of this individual was their incessant chatter. Traveling alongside Liu Shili for thousands of miles, the incessant questions were ones Liu Shili found impossible to answer, such as whether he would ever have the chance to become the first disciple of the Fallen Mountain or whether the child he was raising with Liu Shili's junior was being mischievous at the Book Lake.

Thus, after parting ways with Jiang Shangzhen, Liu Shili inadvertently flicked his fingers, destroying the body of a demon cultivator at the celestial realm.

The demon’s body shattered like a cicada’s molt.

The Dao was damaged, causing a slight descent in rank.

Liu Shili did not pursue the escaping demon cultivator, instead focusing on the task at hand.

Zuo You remained silent.

Liu Shili, accustomed to this, began discussing the recent happenings regarding their teacher and the situation in Baoping Continent.

After Zuo You listened, his face remained expressionless.

Liu Shili sighed, “That’s all I know; I can’t provide any more details.”

Only then did Zuo You say, “Call for the senior brother.”

The large fool remained oblivious.

Liu Shili had no choice but to call out, “Left Senior Brother.”

Among their peers, the highest rank belonged to Senior Brother Zuo You.

Only then did Zuo You say, “Thank you for your hard work.”

Liu Shili tentatively suggested, “How about we switch places? I can handle dealing with a few ancient gods that have traveled far to Haoran, but the rest is not suited for me.”

After pondering for a moment, Zuo You nodded, “That’s fine.”

With his junior brother Jun Qian, there was no need for any formalities.

Liu Shili hesitated.

Zuo You frowned, “Jun Qian, speak your mind.”

Liu Shili said, “While I was heading south to Baoping Continent, I spoke with the eldest senior brother. It seems he is already aware of your situation. Therefore, I came this time to allow you to cross the continent directly to the Great Li capital. Of course, if you are unwilling, you can remain in Tongye Continent. However, here, you will only be able to go to Yu Gui Sect, as the Tongye Sect you previously protected has severely fractured. One faction of young people has been detained by several of the ancestors and their cultivators. But fret not; those captives are temporarily safe.”

Zuo You replied, “Then I will go to Yu Gui Sect.”

He did not hesitate at all.

Liu Shili sighed, as expected. Thus, he relayed the words his eldest senior brother had prepared for him, “Left Senior Brother, you have yet to visit Fallen Mountain, right? There’s a hope for each chair outside the Zhise Peak Ancestral Hall to be occupied by someone truly sitting there, or that someone has indeed sat there. Ultimately, all of them will come together to complete a painting. Our teacher, before his departure, sat in the center, and I moved a chair to a certain spot when I left Fallen Mountain… Of course, whether you go or not, whether there is a genuine Left Senior Brother seated outside, the painting can still be completed later. After all, Fallen Mountain today is not lacking in celestial arts.”

Zuo You paused for a moment before nodding, “Then let’s first visit Fallen Mountain. I will then head to Old Dragon City to see if there have been any improvements in Wei Jin swordsmanship. The Great Sword Immortal once had high hopes for this person.”

After that, he planned to visit Tongye Sect to let certain people understand just how troublesome the sword cultivator Zuo You could be.

Just as Liu Shili’s mouth began to curve into a smile, he suddenly noticed Zuo You's icy gaze, causing him to suppress his smile immediately. He first enveloped the surroundings with his aura, plus Zuo You's sword energy, creating a second barrier of heaven and earth before pulling out a map displaying the Central Mountain, Great Ravine, and Great Li capital. He tossed it on the ground, allowing Zuo You to step onto it and cross the two continents.

In truth, the eldest senior brother had previously cheerfully mentioned allowing those from afar to cross continents on their own; this was no ordinary matter. His esteemed self, Cui Chen, was also creating a path for the first time. Regardless, even if it didn’t work out, Zuo You was a great sword immortal and wouldn’t fear any accidents.

However, Liu Shili was not foolish enough to share this with Zuo You. The latter already had a contentious relationship with the eldest senior brother; if they truly clashed, it would not bode well.

When the junior brother complained, the senior brother suffered. When the senior brother fought, the junior brother bore the brunt. This was an old tradition among the disciples of the Confucian Sage.

The first junior brother was Xiao Qi, and the second unfortunate one was Jun Qian.

Especially when some unwarranted disaster struck, their teacher would heartily comfort the younger disciples, saying, “Xiao Qi, this time it was indeed your fault. Your senior brother Zuo You was actually being reasonable! It’s fine; if you are truly upset, just hit Jun Qian. Remember not to hurt yourself too much; it would be a shame to delay reading and writing tomorrow. Jun Qian, come here! Why are you just standing there like a wooden statue?”

Fortunately, such instances were rare. Their teacher would often give a knowing glance, and Xiao Qi would never retaliate, quickly calming down and instead lecturing the teacher for being biased and that he should adhere to the principles of right and wrong. The old scholar would then realize, clapping his hands, pledging to rectify his behavior next time. Such scenes frequently led two heads to peek around corners: the lower one belonged to Zuo You, while the taller one rested gently on Zuo You’s head, that of the eldest senior brother Cui Chen.

Thus, Liu Shili couldn’t help but feel a sense of regret, as if those beautiful times had vanished without a trace.

That was why Liu Shili agreed to Cui Chen's suggestion for Zuo You to visit Fallen Mountain, allowing the remaining three direct disciples of the Confucian Sage lineage to rekindle some semblance of beauty in their hearts, even as time passed and the world changed.

Before Zuo You moved, he solemnly stated, “Jun Qian, regardless of the reasons, my visit here has brought about certain celestial phenomena. Previously, I supported the heavens and earth with my sword energy, and there are calamities brewing in the shadows, which will eventually strike here.”

Liu Shili seemed not to understand.

Zuo You spoke sternly, “Junior Brother Jun Qian!”

The one who most loved to assert his seniority was at it again.

There was no helping it; the senior brother was the senior brother, and the junior brother remained a junior.

Liu Shili sighed, saying, “I understand. Not only will I ensure the stability of the heaven and earth here, but I will also be responsible for compensating the paradise.”

Zuo You lightly tossed the staff he was using to Liu Shili, saying, “Jun Qian, this is for you.”

Liu Shili broke into a smile as he caught the common staff. In the past, obtaining anything extra from the money-managing Left Senior Brother had been as difficult as ascending to the sky. 

The brothers could not manage it, and neither could their teacher.

Then Zuo You performed a formal farewell gesture to his junior brother.

Liu Shili returned the gesture respectfully.

Zuo You stepped onto the painted scroll, his physical body instantly merging with his Yin spirit.

The sword immortal and the scroll vanished in a flash.

In this small paradise, Liu Shili, relieved of the burdens of suppressing the sword energy, faced fewer restrictions than Zuo You. However, Liu Shili had little interest in exploring the world; while dispelling the celestial phenomena triggered by Zuo You's physical body, he rode the winds across the skies, ultimately seeking out a desolate mountain, preparing to follow his master's orders to take in a qualified disciple. Whether it be talent or aptitude, it was all part of the equation; teaching them the principles of the sages and instilling a few key phrases would be sufficient for the disciple to practice.

Thus, on that lonely mountain peak, Liu Shili observed a small demon yet to fully manifest its human form. The little demon stood on two feet outside its cave, struggling to use chopsticks to eat a bowl of soup dumplings, which had gone cold and mushy. Each time it attempted to grab the dumplings, they would slip from its grip and fall back into the bowl. Frustrated, the little creature eventually threw the chopsticks back into the bowl, raising its claws to curse the tableware, “Eat, eat, eat! You eat your dumplings!”

The little demon had fetched the dumplings from a distant village with great effort, not wanting them to be ruined by the messy creatures of the mountain. It was startled when it suddenly caught sight of the burly lumberjack, worried he had come to collect debts. The little demon was genuinely frightened. Seeing such a muscular figure, it doubted he would be reasonable.

Realizing that it had learned only a few superficial celestial arts from the books, it felt inadequate to confront the lumberjack. 

The little demon, filled with indignation, thought, “I paid for that bowl of dumplings! Not only did I give a few coins, but I even tossed in some wild game I found in the mountains! If I hadn’t read those few sage books in the cave, I would have been an old scholar by now. Just think about it! Not only would I have stolen your dumpling, but I could have taken the entire pot you used to cook them!”

What an outrageous act! After paying, he had the audacity to come to my home and shout? This is simply unreasonable! The little demon lingered at the cave entrance, feeling that the lumberjack must be a brutish man who had never read a book; there was no need to argue. It reluctantly ate the bowl of cold dumplings.

As this thought crossed its mind, the little demon sighed, steeling its courage to hide beside the cave without showing itself, deliberately making noise to scare off the hungry lumberjack. It feared that if it stayed too long, it might attract a glutton and bring bad luck upon itself.

It wouldn’t heal others, as the books had taught it nothing of the sort. The Daoist scriptures only contained illustrations of refining a human form by worshiping the sun and moon, and it had only skimmed through them, barely grasping the basics.

A self-styled whirlwind king was no true king; it was merely a source of amusement for itself.

Liu Shili suddenly remembered that shortly after arriving in the paradise, he had neither spoken the official language nor understood any dialect, leaving him feeling somewhat awkward as he gazed towards the cave entrance. He scratched his head.

The little demon, upon seeing Liu Shili, nearly burst into tears. Oh boy, the lumberjack who had eaten his fill now seemed ready to beat someone up! Unable to restrain itself, it trembled all over, thinking, “Don’t hit me! I’m not human…”

These lumberjack hunters who liked climbing mountains were all fierce individuals. As long as this man remained indifferent, they could pack their bags and move away. Moving far away would be just fine!

Liu Shili devised a plan to fetch a half-baked cultivator to learn the language first, so they could converse. Even if it was merely a temporary arrangement, securing two unnamed disciples in one go would be a good outcome. Whether he could ultimately take them as disciples or if they would become his true disciples or simply remain unnamed, that would all depend on their fortunes. Liu Shili was not one to indiscriminately accept disciples. 

His teacher had reminded these students numerous times: never view accepting disciples as a form of charity. Bringing disciples into his fold, whether as a schoolteacher or a mountain master, if a preacher views his knowledge as something to be thrown down from a high position, the hearts of the people will only drift away.

The little demon, seeing the lumberjack walk away, breathed a sigh of relief, mustering courage as if tidying up the mountains and rivers, swaggering out of the cave, feeling self-important. The whirlwind king would scare away a burly man; he would not need to move his home. 

Thinking grandly, the little demon hurriedly gathered its belongings, quickly stashing the few books away, and finally knelt respectfully at a small grave, bowing its head and reciting a few words. It promised to return and visit the old deity again. After finishing its bow, the little demon slipped away.

Liu Shili had not genuinely left; instead, he used a technique to conceal himself and stayed closely behind the little demon.

In ancient times, Liu Shili had learned some heavenly arts that revealed the true nature of the human heart, and he was quite pleased with this observation. 

Just like himself, the little demon appeared quite perceptive.

Above the central area of Baoping Continent, amidst the sea of clouds, the physical manifestation of Cui Chen, the national teacher of the Great Li, was seen as he imparted knowledge to numerous young scholars from various countries. However, none of the students, even those from the Guanhu Academy and Shanyan Academy, had received the title of gentleman or sage.

A slender figure in a green robe appeared at the edge of the sea of clouds, yet Cui Chen remained focused, continuing to elucidate the intricate philosophies of the Hundred Schools to the young scholars.

Many scholars noticed the anomaly, particularly those from the Guanhu Academy who had cultivated the Haoran Qi, becoming acutely aware, prompting most to turn and look toward that person.

Zuo You, however, did not glance toward Cui Chen, but instead focused on those turning to look at him, frowning as he admonished, “Entering the Seventy-Two Academies doesn’t mean you’re to become celestial beings?!”

Zuo You then transformed into a majestic beam of sword light, heading straight for the northern region, parting the sea of clouds near the Baiyu Capital with his sword energy, which took a long time to converge again.

Cui Chen continued his lecture, neither addressing the traveling sword immortal Zuo You nor obstructing the young scholars from momentarily losing focus, allowing them to revel in their excitement and speculate about the identity of the sword immortal.

Zuo You hovered momentarily at the entrance to the Northern Mountain region, before finally landing at the Fallen Mountain. Chen Nuanshu helped him open the door, and Zuo You first offered incense within the Zhise Peak Ancestral Hall. Meanwhile, Zhou Milin had already set up chairs outside, placing them in a position that seemed meticulously arranged; not a single detail could go wrong. The little girl in black had even knelt on the ground, looking up to ensure everything was perfectly aligned.

Finally, Zuo You took his seat on the chair, dressed in green, observing the scene before him.

It felt as if his teacher was seated centrally, alongside his junior brother Jun Qian, junior brother Qi Jingchun, and junior brother Chen Ping'an. The eldest senior brother… Cui Chen.

They all surrounded Zuo You.

It felt as if there were many other disciples and students of Fallen Mountain behind him.

The lineage of the Confucian Sage was branching out, flourishing.

Lively and no longer solitary.

Zuo You adjusted his collar, sitting upright, both fists resting lightly on his knees, gazing forward with a smile.

After Zuo You stood, he became the sword immortal Zuo You. From now on, he would no longer be in a dilemma when drawing his sword.

(End of Chapter)
